# Igros Kodesh

## Volume 7

In response to your letter, in which you write about the state of your avodah and your hiskashrus to the Rebbeim, and you ask for guidance in this matter:

It is well known that the primary path for a chossid is to engage in the study of Chassidus, both in terms of understanding the concepts and, more importantly, in terms of applying them to one’s own avodah. This is the essence of the instruction, "To know the G-d of your father and serve Him." 

Regarding your question about hiskashrus: Hiskashrus is not merely an emotional state or a feeling of closeness. True hiskashrus is measured by the extent to which a chossid lives by the teachings of the Rebbe and implements his directives in daily life. When a chossid studies a sicha or a maamar, he must ask himself: "What is the practical takeaway for me here? How does this change the way I daven, the way I conduct my business, or the way I interact with others?"

The Rebbeim have provided us with the tools, but the avodah itself is the responsibility of the chossid. Do not be discouraged by the challenges you face; the struggle itself is part of the process. As the Alter Rebbe explains in Tanya, the very fact that you are experiencing this struggle is a sign that you are on the right path. 

May you be blessed with success in all your endeavors, and may you see much nachas from your family and from your efforts in spreading the wellsprings of Chassidus outward.

## 1867

1867

B"H, 7 Tishrei, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

Regarding why I did not write specific details in the content of the blessing: Aside from the fact that there is a concept that a person should use the language of his Rebbe, this is also understood according to the revealed dimension of Torah, and quite simply—based on the premise brought in the Taz and Magen Avraham, which is cited as a halachic ruling in the Shulchan Aruch of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, Siman 582, Seif 7, that during these days [the Aseres Yemei Teshuvah] one must be precise and careful with one’s speech.

Now, if I were to have specified in my letter, in addition to the general blessing, a particular matter—even if it were a single, unique one—it would have created a case of a "general and specific" within the same subject, as they are close to one another. In accordance with the teachings of our Sages regarding "general and specific," this would have resulted in either a "general and specific" where the general contains only what is in the specific, or a "specific and general" which some say should be interpreted as a limitation and an expansion that limits the matter, or a "general, specific, and general," or a "specific, general, and specific" where you can only judge based on the nature of the specific (see Nazir 35b). All of these categories would have served to limit the content of the blessing, as opposed to when it is stated in a general manner, without any particularization or limitation. As mentioned above, I am surprised that you suspected me of something for which, on the face of it, there should have been no room for you to innovate such a thought about me.

I conclude with a blessing for a *chasimah v’gmar chasimah tovah*, and may it be the will of Hashem that He pour out His influence upon your students and upon circles of our fellow Jews to instill within them the spirit of *yiras shamayim* as explained in the teachings of Chassidus, which is the teaching of *Toras HaChassidus*.

#### ***1867***

Most of the letters are from the secretariat's copies, and some are from a photocopy of the letter itself. They are not marked unless the source is different or they have already been printed.

**Regarding why I did not.. specific details:** In continuation of this, see below, letters 1868 and 1819.

## 1868

1868

B"H, 13 Tishrei, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, Torah-scholar, and Chassid,
Engaged in communal needs, etc., Rabbi Yitzchak, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the day after Yom Kippur 5713. Although time does not permit any lengthiness, I would like to offer a remark regarding your comment on the matter of *brachos*—that *brachos* which are more specific are more important. In my humble opinion, this does not apply to our current discussion. This is understood based on the distinction between *birchas hanehenin* (blessings of enjoyment) and *hoda'ah* (thanksgiving) on the one hand, and *birchas tefillah* (blessings of prayer) on the other.

If one only gives thanks for a general quality shared by many things, and not for the specific quality of this particular thing, he is not acknowledging the kindness of the Ribono shel Olam as he should. Therefore, a more specific *brachah* is more important, as it demonstrates that he recognizes the unique virtue of this specific item within the general category.

However, this is not the case regarding the *brachah* of *tefillah*—where *brachah* is derived from the term *himshechah* (drawing down), such as in *Birchas Hashanah* (the blessing for the year), etc. In that context, if one draws down the entire whole, which includes within it all the details, then "he who has two hundred has one hundred" [i.e., the greater includes the lesser].

The distinction between *birchas hanehenin* and the *brachos* of *tefillah*, etc., is explained according to Chassidus in *Biurei HaZohar*, Part 5, beginning of *Parshas Eikev*.

With blessings for a *chag sameach*.

## 1869

B"H, 1st day of Chol Hamoed Sukkos, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

The First National Convention of N'shei U’Bnos Chabad
in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established
Safria - Kfar Chabad

Blessings and peace!

In response to the invitation card for your convention, which will take place, G-d willing, tomorrow, Tuesday, the Rebbe sent a telegram of blessing, the content of which is as follows:

"At your convention during the days of Moed and Hakhel to fear Hashem, you will surely inspire [one another] to take practical action to draw down the *Tzila D’Mehemnusa* into the inner experience of all four types of Jews, as required by the teachings of Chassidus and the directives of our Nesi’im, may their merit protect us. With blessings for success and a happy holiday."

It was surely received in time and read with the appropriate explanation, and there is no doubt that you will report in detail on the results of the convention, the election of the leadership, etc., etc.

With holiday greetings,
**Secretary**

## 1870

B"H, 25 Tishrei, 5713
Brooklyn.

...And once again I come to urge you regarding the establishment of a fixed time for the study of the revealed Torah and the teachings of Chassidus, the recitation of Tehillim every day, and the giving of a few coins to tzedakah before davening. All of the above are tried and tested segulos to refine the soul, so that it may absorb — *as zol zich opgleign bay ihr* — a matter of Torah and mitzvos and a matter of Elokus, which, through this, brings true nachas ruach to the soul of a person.

With blessings, awaiting good tidings.

## 1871

B"H, 25 Tishrei, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter... it is surprising that you do not mention anything regarding your influence within your community, in strengthening Torah and spreading Yiddishkeit. Surely you do not forget that, after all, this is the primary purpose of the position of Rabbonus, and the matter of the livelihood derived from it is secondary in comparison to the aforementioned purpose. Elaborating on this is surely superfluous. It is also understood that the essence of the work is in matters of proper chinuch, both for the young and for the old. And the most essential point of all is to explain to them that the main thing is the act itself—meaning, the performance of mitzvos in actual, day-to-day life...

## 1872

1872

B”H, 25 Tishrei, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and refined,
Engaged in communal needs, R’ Yehoshua, may he live.

Greetings and Blessings,

I received your letter in due time, along with the *pidyon nefesh*, which was read at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, during a time of favor. Surely, he will awaken great compassion for all those mentioned in the *pidyon nefesh*, for each according to their needs.

Thank you, in particular, for the *kuntres maamarim* in honor of Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur. May it be the will of Hashem that you continue to add strength and vigor to the strengthening of Yiddishkeit and the dissemination of its ideas in general, and specifically the memories of days gone by regarding the atmosphere of Chassidus and the conduct of Chassidim. If this was of great necessity at any time, it is all the more so in these days, when the centers of Chassidus in Poland, Galicia, and so on, are no more, may Hashem avenge their blood.

Enclosed is the *kuntres maamarim* that was published in connection with the past Rosh Hashanah, etc., which I am sure will interest you.

With blessings,

Note: As I leafed through the *kuntres* in haste: 1) The acronym for *teshuvah* that the Alter Rebbe cited in the name of the holy Rabbi R’ Melech of Lizhensk is: *Shivisi Hashem l’negdi samid* (I have set Hashem before me always), and the *hei* stands for *hatznei leches im Elokecha* (walk humbly with your G-d). See the explanation of this in the *kuntres Toras HaChassidus* at the end. 2) The statement of our Sages, “The King will in the future...” refers to: *Malka Meshicha* (the King Moshiach) will in the future **bring back** the righteous in repentance (*l’asava tzadikaya b’tiyuvta*). See *Likutei Torah*, *Devarim* (92b); *Shir HaShirim* (50b). In another place, it is brought that this statement of our Sages is in the *Zohar*—but for the time being, I have not found its location. 3) Regarding the acronym for the word *Elul* in citing the source and the allusion in each—see the introduction to *Kuntres Tzad*, but it is known that one does not raise questions on a *drush*.

## 1873

1873

B"H, 28 Tishrei, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Regarding your Bar Mitzvah celebration this coming Shabbos Bereishis, I hereby extend my blessing that it should be in a good and auspicious hour, and that you should succeed in your studies and in the fulfillment of the mitzvos.

It is a well-known teaching of our Alter Rebbe—which is also found in the Shelah—that the Torah portion read at any given time is connected to that specific time. On this coming Shabbos, we read the parsha of Bereishis, which begins, "In the beginning, Elokim created the heavens and the earth," and continues, "and the earth was..." and "darkness..." and "And Elokim said, 'Let there be light.'"

This serves as a general instruction for all Bnei Yisrael in general, and specifically for a Bar Mitzvah who is beginning his life as one obligated in all the Torah and mitzvos. As he approaches the avodah of Torah and mitzvos in this world, he must always keep the following clear knowledge before his eyes:

1) That Elokim created the heavens and the earth, and from this it is understood that He, may He be blessed, is the sole Master of the entire world and everything within it.

2) That the portion of the world assigned to man is still "darkness," and it is his task to rectify it and illuminate it.

3) That the beginning of his avodah in this is to reveal "And Elokim said" in the world—namely, the study of Torah, which is the word of Hashem, and the fulfillment of the mitzvos, which are the commandments of Hashem, may He be blessed, regarding which it is said, "For a mitzvah is a candle and Torah is light." Through this, he transforms the darkness of the world into light, or in the language of the holy Zohar, "to turn darkness into light and bitterness into sweetness."

By keeping this knowledge before his eyes at all times, he will walk his path securely—the path of Hashem—to perform charity and justice.

With blessings.

## 1874

1874

B”H, 28 Tishrei, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the G-d-fearing, esteemed, and distinguished, who occupies himself with communal needs, a man of noble character, a scion of an illustrious lineage, etc., R’ Sh.Z. [Shazar] – may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I acknowledge with thanks the receipt of your telegram conveying New Year greetings, etc. I was also pleased to receive regards from you through my representative, the director of the Refugee Bureau, the esteemed and distinguished Rabbi, who occupies himself with communal needs, etc., R’ Binyamin Eliyahu Gorodetzky – may he live.

Although I must speak the truth: after our conversation regarding this matter, it was my hope that the appropriate institutions would take upon themselves the entire cost of the building for the Youth Aliyah in Kfar Chabad. This is because it is known to us all that the situation of the villagers is such that they are unable to bear this burden, and our own treasury here is also burdened with debts. Furthermore, considering the unique nature of the Chabad people—and given that this is the first attempt to establish a settlement in their spirit and style—they were worthy of being gifted the building.

However, since it appears that it was not within your power to bring this about, I must agree to the second option I proposed: that the institutions provide the full expenditure for the time being, on the condition that I repay half of it over time. I have authorized my aforementioned representative, Rabbi Gorodetzky, in his capacity as director of the Refugee Bureau, to sign a formal contract for these terms if such a contract is required, and to discuss the specific details of the conditions, namely the methods and timing of the payments. I hope that in this matter, too, you will provide your full assistance.

With respect and blessing for true health, awaiting good news,

My letter with New Year greetings was surely received in due time.

***

1874

R’ Sh.Z. Shazar. Further letters to him: above, Vol. 5, 1809, and the references in the notes there. Below, 1886.

That I repay half of it: See above, ibid. Below, letters 1878, 1885, 2242.

## 1875

[28 Tishrei 5713]

...And the act of naming is a matter of revealing an *hemshech* from the root, the source, and the state of concealment, into actual, practical matters. As is explained in *Chassidus* in many places, the concept of naming is to connect the *neshamah* with the body, and so on. Based on this, one can also explain the dispute regarding whether Adam gave names to the fish; for they are similar to the creations of *alma d’itkasiya* (the world of concealment), which is the opposite of the concept of revelation. However, this *alma d’itkasiya*—relative to the world above it—is also called revelation. This is the basis for the opinion that the fish were also given names. See *Tosafos* to *Chullin* 66b, *Chizkuni* and *Radak* to *Bereishis* 2:19, *Midrash Chaser V’Yaseir*, and elsewhere...

#### ***1875***

Printed in *Likutei Sichos*, Vol. 4, p. 1247.

## 1876

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Mar-Cheshvan, 5713
Brooklyn.

Mrs. Rachel, may she live,

Blessings and peace!

...I hope that while you were in the Sukkah, you heard what was discussed regarding the organization of N'shei U'Bnos Chabad—that is, all women who have some connection and bond with Chabad. The idea is that from time to time, they should gather together to study the halachos relevant to running a Jewish home, topics that can help improve the chinuch of the children, as well as study the parsha of the week, the sichos of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and similar matters. If there is a Jewish section where you live, it would be appropriate for you to look into the possibility of organizing such a group. I hope that with a suitable approach to the matter, you will find the ways to accomplish this. It is well known what my father-in-law, the Rebbe, said in the name of his father, the Rebbe: that it is a chazakah that efforts in outreach (ta'amulah) do not return empty.

With blessings for what is needed, for you and your husband, may they live.

## 1877

1877

B"H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Agudas N'shei U'Bnos Chabad
May they live, Hashem bless them

Blessings and peace!

It was with pleasure that I received the news that the foundation has been laid for the work of N'shei U'Bnos Chabad in your city. May the Ribono shel Olam help that this should be a good beginning for the entire year ahead.

Surely you have made good resolutions on how to strengthen this for the future, as well as a program for subsequent meetings. It goes without saying that this program should not be rigid in all its details; it should be possible to change and adapt it to the needs of the members of your branch, as not all places are the same in this regard.

General guidelines for this work were provided in my letter to the N'shei U'Bnos Chabad in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt, and a copy is enclosed herewith.

I would just like to add a few words:

Our holy Torah is eternal; from it, one can learn and derive instructions and guidance in all matters, for all kinds of times and in all the lands where one finds oneself.

The Torah begins with the parsha of Bereishis, where the order of the creation of the world is recounted. Naturally, the Torah is not merely a book of stories, but rather, as the interpretation of the word Torah implies—**horah** (instruction)—it is a guide for daily life, showing how to conduct oneself correctly in both *gashmius* and *ruchnius*.

In the Torah’s narrative of how the world was created, among all the deep allusions, there is also the indication of how various matters come into being in this particular world.

Every endeavor and every movement that is created, whether *ruchniusdik* or *gashmiusdik*, is: **"Bereishis"**—the beginning and the essence of it is to know and remember that **"Elokim created"** the heavens (*ruchnius*) and the earth (*gashmius*). Hashem Yisbarach creates it, but He desires that it pass through specific people, who must consider themselves His *shluchim* to carry out His will.

At the beginning of creation, **"the earth was *tohu u'vohu* and darkness..."**—at the start of any good, *kedusha*-filled endeavor or movement, it may seem as though it is empty, desolate, and dark all around, and that it will be difficult to build it correctly so that it aligns with the goal. The holy Torah tells us that right at the beginning of creation: **"And Elokim said, 'Let there be light,' and there was light"**—Hashem causes light to suddenly appear where there was darkness. Afterwards, order was created; *tzomei'ach* (vegetation) was created, then *chai* (living creatures), which are higher than *tzomei'ach*, and then Adam HaRishon, who is the *mivchar habriah*, the highest of creation.

So too, in every endeavor and movement of *kedusha* (see Vayikra Rabbah, ch. 25:3), one must be strong in the resolve that it must be created. Then, even in a place where it was previously truly dark, it becomes light in an instant. This is the beginning of the creation, growing ever better and higher, as the Sages say, "We elevate in matters of *kedusha*," meaning that in every matter connected with Torah and *mitzvos*, one goes and ascends from strength to strength.

With blessings for good, both *gashmiusdik* and *ruchniusdik*, for all the members of your branch, for them and their families, may they live.

## 1878

1878

B"H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Yosef, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 27th of Tishrei, surely the confirmation of receipt has already arrived, as well as the letter from the Vaad HaMaamad. As our Sages of blessed memory have said, "The wine belongs to the master, but the thanks go to the one who serves it."

You conclude your letter by mentioning that you are endeavoring to arrange one hour of religious education for young children each week. Surely you will write with further details regarding this. It seems this is similar to the hour of religious studies—*SHL*—that is conducted here in accordance with the law of the state. Perhaps it would be worthwhile for you to be in contact with Rabbi Yaakov Yehuda Hecht, may he live, who has been deeply involved in this matter for many years. Furthermore, you have surely seen the publications of the *ML*H specifically for this hour of study. I am enclosing one booklet (a total of 24 booklets have been published). May Hashem grant you success in this work of Heaven, to bring the hearts of the sons and daughters of Yisrael closer to our Father in Heaven.

With blessings for proper health.

#### ***1878***

**Rabbi Yosef:** Player. Additional letters to him appear above in Vol. 5, 1570, and in the references noted there.

## 1879

B"H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...And let this be known: it appears that several of anash are mistaken and interpret my position against relocating from France as being motivated by the benefit of maintaining the mosdos and preserving them, while being willing to forgo the individual benefit of the people involved. This is not the case at all. My view—and to my regret, I have seen this tangibly until now—is that in the relocation, almost all of them have lost out in ruchniyus, and at the same time, they have not gained in gashmiyus. I do not yet see any reason why this would change in the near future. Consequently, I am puzzled by those who insist on relocating. In connection with all of the above, the point that each person emphasizes in their letter—that their relocation will not cause damage to our mosdos—is irrelevant to the matter, since the concern is preventing the damage that the relocation causes to the traveler and the person relocating themselves.

#### ***1879***

**Against relocating from France:** See above, Vol. 6, letters 1564, 1769. Below, 2071, 2120.

## 1880

1880

By the Grace of G-d, 1st of Mar-Cheshvan, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the Directorate of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad
in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily,
May they live.

Peace and Blessing!

I received with pleasure your letter from Erev Sukkos, along with the newspaper clippings attached to it. I thank you for the report on the past, and I reiterate my request for the future: to inform me in detail of your good works in raising the banner of Judaism in general, and in disseminating the wellsprings of Chassidus in particular.

2) I am especially interested in the details regarding the implementation and the good resolutions concerning activities during the month of Tishrei. Surely, in addition to the actual activities, you publicized these matters in the newspapers and the like, so that the information would reach even those places where you were not present. May Hashem grant you success in all of the above.

3) I enjoyed the transcript of the radio broadcast. Surely, for the future as well, you will arrange such things well in advance so that they can be broadcast at the appropriate time. Seemingly, this is relevant now regarding the upcoming Chag HaGeulah, 19 Kislev.

4) I was pleased to hear about the establishment of study sessions with a number of students from other yeshivos. Surely, the study with them now should be adapted to their habits—that is, focusing on matters of explanation, logic, and intellectual grasp, rather than pursuing *iskafya* beyond what is appropriate. In the beginning of drawing someone close, one must adapt to the habits of the recipient, and slowly, little by little, it will change to match the content of the study being taught, as is understood.

5) I enjoyed the *Bitachon Chabad* booklet, of which two copies were received here. May the strength of those who participated in this be fortified, and through this, may the wellsprings be disseminated both within and without. Enclosed is a check (in the name of the editorial board members) for my participation in the printing and distribution costs.

6) It is understood that, consistent with what I have written previously, it is necessary to arrange the aforementioned in such a way that it does not preclude the publication of news and *sichos* in other newspapers as well, as has been the custom until now, since those newspapers reach circles to whom the aforementioned booklet is not relevant or does not reach.

7) Regarding what you write—that you did not arrange a program for 18 Elul because of the celebration in the village—in my opinion, this is no excuse at all. Besides the fact that there are two evenings—the night of 18 Elul and the conclusion of 18 Elul—and the celebration was only on one of them, surely there were many of *anash* Chabad who were not at the celebration in the village, and consequently, they could have visited other places.

8) I look forward to detailed news regarding the gathering **in memory of** the *ha-kahal*. (I emphasize the word **in memory of** to dispel any misconceptions, etc., and surely you were also careful about this, so as not to give an opening or opportunity to those who wish to mislead in this matter, and *d'l*).

9) I have read the detailed report of your gathering from the 7th of Tishrei. Time does not permit me now to go into the details regarding its content, but what is most concerning is that in the list of participants, there are very, very few names of new members. Aside from the fact that the sign of a living thing is that it grows and expands, it is known that the ruling of our Sages (some say it is from the Torah) is that we elevate in matters of holiness. It is also known what my father-in-law, the Rebbe, said regarding this: it is like a person climbing a high, steep mountain, where standing still is impossible, and constant ascent is mandatory. If there is no ascent, there will be a descent, Heaven forbid. This is also true regarding the *avodah* of each and every one of us, and also regarding the number of members in your movement—growth is mandatory. If not, it is an indication of the opposite, Heaven forbid, even if the number of members on the list has not decreased.

10) ...Although it is known from our Sages that a person should always study Torah and perform *mitzvos* even *shelo lishmah* (not for their own sake), the reasoning of our Sages is that "from *shelo lishmah* one comes to *lishmah*." Especially according to what our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe wrote in *Hilchos Talmud Torah*, Chapter 4, *Kuntres Acharon*, subsection 1, the reason is that the *mitzvah* and the study are performed as they should be. But without that, etc.—and even if you were to say that they are performed as they should be, at the very least, even *misnagdim* are not worthy of being particular about matters of *shelo lishmah*, and certainly not those into whom our *Nesi'im*, and especially my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulalleh*, *navgam*, *ziya*, poured *Elokus* in abundance. It is understood how completely rejected this matter must be. As mentioned, I do not wish to elaborate on this, and my hope is that these few lines will suffice to uproot this approach from its source. The main thing is that it should be uprooted not only from the world of abstract thought, but in actual practice—for "action is the essential thing." This uprooting should be expressed not only in matters of "turn from evil," but primarily in "do good." I will await detailed good news regarding this.

With blessings for success in your holy work.

## 1881

1881

B"H, 1st of Mar-Cheshvan, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding your daughters, may they live, in my opinion, you should speak with a shadchan agency—without your daughters, may they live, knowing about this—to inform the shadchan of the details regarding your daughters and to request that he work energetically to find suitable shidduchim for them. Even though arranging matches is the domain of the Ribono shel Olam, nevertheless, every single thing must have a foothold in nature as well. It is proper that you give 18 cents to tzedakah each day—on weekdays—before davening Shacharis, on behalf of your daughters, may they live, and your entire household, may they live. This will serve as a vessel for the drawing down and receiving of the blessings of Hashem in all of the above.

You do not write in your letter what your occupation is now, whether it is in the craft of shechitah or in another matter. It is known from our Sages, of blessed memory (Chullin 30b), "The term 'v'shachat' (and he shall slaughter) implies only 'v'mashach' (and he shall draw)," which means that just as there is the matter of shechitah in the physical sense, there is also the matter of shechitah in the spiritual sense. The matter of shechitah in the spiritual sense is "drawing" in its literal meaning: to draw the "animal" within a person away from the "public domain"—that is, from the many and varied desires and cravings—into the "private domain," the Unique One of the world. This depends on the manner of one's vitality—the intensity of one's immersion in desires and cravings. If one's vitality is small, then the shechitah—that is, the drawing—does not need to be so great; but if one's vitality is great, then a great shechitah is required, and so on. May Hashem grant you the merit to influence your surroundings to draw them toward Torah and mitzvos, toward the one Torah given to us all by the Unique King, the Life of the worlds.

With blessings, and awaiting good news.

***

**"The term 'v'shachat' implies only 'v'mashach'":** See also above, Vol. 6, letters 1782, 1813, 1833; below, 2169.

## 1882

1882

B”H, 1st of Mar-Cheshvan, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to see you at the Simchas Beis Hashoeivah, but I am accustomed to seeing you also on Motzaei Simchas Torah, and this time I did not see you, even though the farbrengen continued for a few hours after Havdalah—for others. It is well known that spiritual matters are not bound by place, and even when at times it seems that one does not feel it openly, one nevertheless receives the effect. I hope that the good thoughts regarding you have reached you, and even if you did not feel this openly, it was received in the pnimiyus, and in time it will emerge publicly.

My father-in-law, the Rebbe, used to say that Chassidim are wise; consequently, they do not put off until later that which can be done sooner. May Hashem help you, that for you this should be as soon as possible in good and happy matters...

With blessings, awaiting good tidings.

#### ***1882***

## 1883

1883

B"H, 1st of Mar-Cheshvan, 5713

Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I have just received with pleasure your telegram regarding the birth of your daughter, may it be for good fortune. I am happy to see your reward, and the reward of your wife—may they live—for your involvement in the field of proper chinuch, bringing the hearts of the sons and daughters of Yisrael closer to our Father in Heaven. For whoever teaches the child of his fellow Torah, Scripture considers it as if he had given birth to him; from which it is understood that this is a segulah for the birth of sons and daughters. ## 1884

1884

By the Grace of G-d
3rd of Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

It was with pleasure that I learned that a son has been born to your son, Mr. [Name]—may he live and be well—mazal tov. I wish to express to you and your wife—may she live and be well—my heartfelt mazal tov, and I ask that you also convey my mazal tov to your son and his wife—may she live and be well. May the Ribono shel Olam grant them the merit to bring him into the covenant of Avraham Avinu at an auspicious and successful time, and to raise him to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds, in comfort and abundance. May the grandparents on both sides derive from them true Yiddishe nachas and Chassidishe nachas.

The Midrash relates that the Chazal asked: If Hashem desires that the Jewish people observe the mitzvah of milah, why did He not create man already circumcised? The Chazal answered that many things in this world were created in such a way that they require human refinement; this is the goal of man—to bring about this refinement in creation. It goes without saying that Hashem does not, chas v’shalom, depend on man, for from Above there is the possibility for a perfected thing to come into existence immediately. Rather, Hashem wished to grant merit to Yisrael, so that every blessing of children, life, and sustenance that He, blessed be He, gives to Jews should not be merely a gift, but also something earned. Therefore, He, blessed be He, left a place and a possibility for a Jew to perform the shlichus of the Hakadosh Baruch Hu. Consequently, all the good things that he subsequently receives will not be "bread of shame," but rather things earned through the avodah of man to Hashem. Moreover, the more good that Hashem gives a Jew, the more this itself is proof and evidence that the Jew must increase the avodah that is required of him.

This is also one of the reasons why "the Rebbe honors the wealthy." When a wealthy person gives from his money to tzedakah for individuals or institutions, in truth, Hashem—who sustains the entire world with His goodness—could have provided the influence directly to those individuals or institutions. It is simply that He makes the wealthy person a shaliach, so that he should give them the portion that resides with him. This is only out of the kindness of Hashem, who gives a Jew yet another opportunity to demonstrate his avodah by performing tzedakah with the money that is in his possession—money that, in truth, belongs to others. At the same time, this also shows that the Hakadosh Baruch Hu trusts this wealthy person, knowing that he will give away another’s portion, even though the yetzer hara may try to convince him that it is actually his own. Nevertheless, he gives it to the poor person or the institution, which is at times a difficult nisayon. Therefore, "the Rebbe honors the wealthy," because from Above, the wealthy person is tested with the difficult nisayon of wealth. Furthermore, because "according to the camel is the burden"—meaning he has the capacity to withstand the nisayon—when he stands firm in this nisayon, in addition to the reward for the mitzvah of tzedakah, the wealthy person receives an additional reward: "Tithe so that you may become wealthy." Through giving tzedakah, not only is he not lacking what he gave away, but it draws down an additional increase in wealth beyond what he had until now.

***

**The Chazal asked:** See Midrash Rabbah, Bereishis, Chapter 11, and the commentaries there.

## 1885

B"H, 3 Cheshvan, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Great peace to the great man, the brilliant Gaon, the G-d-fearing, noble, and distinguished, who sits in judgment, leads his community with integrity, a man of valor and many accomplishments, who illuminates and shines, whose actions and fruits are beautiful, of the seed of holy ones, etc., etc., the honorable, his Excellency, the Gaon, Moreinu HaRav Meir Abuchatzeira, Shlita, Chief Rabbi of the holy community of Erfoud and its environs, may it be built and established.

Peace and blessing!

With pleasure I received your letter dated the 6th of the month of the Eitanim, the year 5713. I have received a blessing and I return a blessing to you, and I reiterate the blessings I wrote to your Excellency for Rosh Hashanah, which encompass all matters: for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual terms, with goodness that is visible and revealed.

Regarding what your Excellency writes, that you sent me a letter with the good news that you have been appointed as Av Beis Din in the city of Erfoud and its environs—it seems that the aforementioned letter did not reach me. However, a blessing is appropriate at any time, and I wish your Excellency, Shlita, my blessing for extraordinary success in your new position, to serve with splendor as the Mara D'Asra. As is known, the interpretation of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and the Shulchan Aruch, is that the matter is to be understood literally: *Mara* comes from the language of mastery and ownership, meaning that the Mara D'Asra is the master and owner of the city, not only in spiritual matters but also in material ones.

Many thanks for your precious gift, the portrait of your grandfather, the Gaon, the Chassid, the Mekubal, leader and guide of communities in Israel, who stood at the springs of fear of Heaven and the inner dimensions of Torah, Moreinu HaRav Yaakov, zt"l, Abuchatzeira.

And last but certainly not least, is the good news that surpasses all others: that on the 24th of the month of Elul, a son was born to you, and his name in Israel is called David Chai, for long and good days and years. I hereby express my blessings that you and your wife, the Rabbanit, tichyeh, may raise him, along with his brothers, shlita, to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds, with true peace of mind. And in his days, may we merit the complete Redemption through David, our righteous Moshiach, David, King of Israel, who lives and endures, Amen.

With blessing,

As per your request, I have sent you in a separate package the holy books of the Alter Rebbe, zya, from those available to me: Torah Or, Likutei Torah, and Shulchan Aruch. I trust you will confirm their receipt.

## 1887

1887

B"H, 4th of Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Surely you will not withhold the good from me, and you will inform me of good news regarding the aforementioned health, and likewise regarding the spiritual health of everyone. As is known from our Sages, of blessed memory, the 248 positive mitzvos correspond to the 248 limbs of a person, and the 365 negative mitzvos correspond to the 365 sinews of a person. It is simple that this is not merely a coincidence of numbers, but rather that the limbs of a person receive vitality through the performance of positive mitzvos, and the sinews of a person become pure channels—not damaged, Heaven forbid, in the flow of blood—through the observance of the 365 negative mitzvos. It is understood that the spirituality and the physicality of a Jewish person are not two separate things, but one thing entirely, and the one is dependent upon the other. All of this is hinted at briefly in Likutei Torah by our Rebbe, the author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, Parshas Nitzavim, page 45c.

With blessings, awaiting good news.

## 1888

1888

B"H, 4th of Mar-Cheshvan, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, refined, and diligent in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Avraham, may he live, Shochet and Bodek

Greetings and blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter from the 3rd of Cheshvan, along with the enclosure. Following up on what was said during the farbrengen in the Sukkah, I hereby repeat my blessing of Mazal Tov upon the bris milah of your grandson, may he live.

It is well known what is brought in the Acharonim—and the Rogatchover Gaon elaborates on this—that in the mitzvah of milah there are three aspects: 1) that one must perform the circumcision, 2) that one must not remain an arel (uncircumcised), and 3) that one must be a nimol (circumcised). Several practical differences and distinctions are brought regarding this.

One may explain this matter in terms of avodah, briefly, according to what is explained in the teachings of Chassidus: It is obvious that there must be the aspect of "turn away from evil," which is the requirement not to be an arel. There must also be the aspect of "do good," which is the requirement to be a nimol. And above all, according to what my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, related in the name of our holy Rebbes, of blessed memory: "A Chossid does not hold of 'automatically' (b'derech mimila); every matter must be through toil and through avodah." This is why there must also be the active effort of the milah itself.

May the Ribono shel Olam grant each one of us the merit, in all our affairs and actions, to fulfill these three things—turning from evil, doing good, and being an "eved Hashem" (servant of Hashem) in the present tense.

With blessings for proper health and long, good years—with all the interpretations—for him and his wife, may they live.

***

**Rabbi Avraham:** Gordon. Another letter to him—see above, Vol. 4, 1159.

**Three aspects:** See Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 3, p. 759 and onward.

## 1890

1890

By the Grace of Hashem, 4th of Mar-Cheshvan, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the distinguished, G-d-fearing, learned, and esteemed R' Chaim Shaul Zev, may he live:

Shalom u’Bracha!

I received your letter of 19 Elul in due time. Due to the pressures of the past month of Tishrei, my response to this letter was delayed (you surely received my letter of blessing for the New Year in time).

You need not apologize for writing in detail, nor for writing in Yiddish. The essence of a letter is its content, not the language in which it is written. The simpler the writing, the more heartfelt it is; it removes the barriers that separate one person from another and strengthens that which unites them.

I was pleased to read in your letter that you remember the warm connection you had with my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. As our Sages teach us, a Tzaddik remains in this world even after his passing, and he continues to bestow influence here—even more so than when he was present in a physical body. The reason for this is that the body, even at its highest level, is limited by its surroundings. However, for a Tzaddik, once the limitations of the body are removed and his soul alone is the master, and especially in the case of a Nasi HaDor, the soul possesses the power and ability to accomplish in this world even more than before.

Consequently, all the blessings you received from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for yourself and your family, may they live, in both material and spiritual matters, remain in their full force and strength even now. Even if you have not yet seen the fulfillment of some of these blessings, it is certain that you will see it soon, even with your physical eyes.

You should not be distressed or take to heart—as you write in your letter—the fact that you are in your business for only a short time each day, rather than from morning until late at night as you were previously. For that which Hashem Yisbarach wishes to grant in terms of parnassah and wealth, He can provide even while you are in the business for only a short time; your wife and children can fill the remaining time. Furthermore, as for anything beyond what Hashem wishes to grant: 1) one should not desire it, and 2) being in the business more than your health permits will not help.

The main thing is that you should not, G-d forbid, diminish your conduct regarding davening, reciting Tehillim, giving tzedakah, and similar matters. These are all areas that Hashem has placed within the realm of human choice—bechirah—and it depends on a person’s own will to increase and expand these good practices. By increasing these activities, which serve as vessels and channels for the blessings of Hashem, the influence, blessing, and success that the Holy One, Blessed be He, grants to those who are connected with Him, may He be blessed, are likewise increased.

With blessings for proper health and Yiddishe nachas from your wife and children, may they live.

**M. Schneerson**

## 1891

B"H, 8 Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write that you have stood for a driver’s license examination several times and have not yet received it: "To everything there is a season," and surely in the future you will succeed in this examination, naturally after the appropriate preparation. And since it is known that the physical and the spiritual are interconnected, especially in the case of a Jewish person, you should take courage in the conduct of your "chariot"—that is, the 248 limbs and 365 sinews of the physical body, which are a chariot for the *nefesh*, and the *nefesh* is a chariot for the *neshamah elokis* (it is understood that the term "chariot" here is not precise, as explained in the teachings of Chassidus regarding the advantages and disadvantages of a chariot; the intent is that which is secondary, which must be directed by the primary, which is the *nefesh*).

Surely you are strengthening yourself in the observance of the three daily study portions established for every person by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nevgam, zya*—namely, *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*—and you are also participating in the *shiurim* that are studied in public. May Hashem grant you success.

With blessings.

## 1892

1892

B"H, 8 MarCheshvan, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

For some time now, I have been deliberating whether to write to you regarding the following matter, but I have finally reached a decision, as I have no other choice and I am compelled on my part to write... It is necessary that your daughter, *tichyeh*, wear a *sheitel*. I understand that there are several difficulties here, *v'd"l* (and a word to the wise is sufficient), but I do not see any other possibility. It has already become customary in the United States and in many other places for the younger generation to adopt customs and *hidurim* (stringencies) that their parents did not yet hold by. Especially since, in the present case, this is not merely a matter of a *hidur* or custom, but much more than that. For understandable reasons, I do not wish to elaborate on this, and even though I am writing in *Lashon HaKodesh*, I am certain you will be able to explain this both to yourself and to your daughter and wife, *tichyena*. I await good news that the matter has been accepted by you in a positive spirit, for then it is certain that the matter will be carried out *un glatterheit* (smoothly), and the *Kiddush Hashem* involved in this (especially in an environment where they are being watched with seven eyes and where there is opposition, etc.) is very great. And from the implication of the positive, etc.

With a request for forgiveness—if it is necessary to ask for forgiveness for this—I am hopeful to receive word from you as soon as possible that the matter has been arranged in the best possible way, *guterheit un glatterheit*. It will certainly be an additional channel and vessel for the drawing down and receiving of the blessings of the *Ribono shel Olam* for the young couple, in everything they need, both materially and spiritually.

Enclosed is a copy of my letter to the Agudas N'shei U'Bnos Chabad (and surely they, too, will begin this work in their camp), which also relates to the above. Even if it sometimes seems that the required matter *halt men noch weit derfun* (is still far off), we learn this as well from the creation of the world in general: that the beginning was in a state of *tohu vavohu* and darkness, and it was precisely through that that light was created—a light so great that even after the rectification of the world, it is not fitting to use it (which is why it was hidden away for the future, for the *tzaddikim*, and in the Torah). It was precisely through such a beginning that there was an order in creation, gradually from below to above: *tzomei'ach* (vegetative), *chai* (animate), *medaber* (speaking).

I will repeat once again that I am not writing this for the sake of debate, but only so that the matter will be carried out, *az ayer tachter tichyeh zol onton a sheitel* (that your daughter should wear a *sheitel*), and that the wedding should take place at a good and auspicious time.

Awaiting good news, with blessings.

## 1893

B"H, 8 Marcheshvan, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, involved in communal needs,
Rabbi Ephraim Eliezer, may he live, HaKohen

Shalom u’Bracha!

Following our conversation when you were here, it is somewhat surprising that I have not heard from you since. Surely, every delay is for the good.

Enclosed is a copy of my letter which, although written to the Agudas N'shei U’Bnos Chabad, is in truth relevant to the avodah of each and every person. As everyone can see for themselves, at the beginning of many matters, one sees—or imagines one sees—that the situation is in a state of *tohu v’vohu* and darkness. However, with a firm resolution that it must be brought into actuality, the beginning is not gradual, but rather through the command "Let there be light." It is a light so intense that a *tikkun* (rectified) world is not even fit to utilize it, let alone a state of *tohu v’vohu* and darkness. And precisely through this beginning—which is entirely beyond proportion—and the fact that it must subsequently be "hidden away" for the future, for the *tzaddikim*, and for Torah, it becomes possible to begin an orderly avodah from below to above: *tzomei'ach* (vegetative), then *chai* (animate), and then *adam* (human), the pinnacle of creation. *V’d”l* (and to the wise, a hint is sufficient).

With blessings.

## 1895

Brooklyn.

In response to your letter of the 5th of Cheshvan, in which you inform me that the opinion of two additional expert physicians is to remove the eye, and that there are two ways to proceed: either to replace the entire eye with a glass one, or to replace only the pupil,

## 1826

B.H., 8 Mar-Cheshvan, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive your regards through the esteemed Chossid, the G-d-fearing man, involved in communal affairs, etc., Rabbi Yosef Weinberg, may he live. He also conveyed your request for a blessing regarding the difficulties you are currently experiencing, etc. When I visit the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention you for a blessing in this matter.

It is surely unnecessary to remind you—especially at length—that when one does business with another, much depends on the goodwill and disposition of the merchant with whom one is dealing.

Everything that is done here below is a reflection of what exists above. This is also true regarding people, and especially regarding Yidden.

Each of us needs and desires blessings from Hashem Yisbarach. To receive them, one must have the necessary preparation—that is, to create within oneself a disposition to want to connect with the Hakadosh Baruch Hu. (In this, it is not like things here below, where one must create a disposition in the merchant, because the Hakadosh Baruch Hu is always ready and desires to give blessing and success; it depends only on the *mekabel*—the recipient—for sometimes one wants to connect with Hashem Yisbarach, and sometimes, due to certain reasons, one is not in that state.)

How can one connect with Hashem Yisbarach, who is the Creator of the entire world, when the one asking for the blessing is nothing more than a human being of flesh and blood? And through what does one connect with Him?

The truth is that, of one’s own accord, one would not have the strength for this. Rather, because the Hakadosh Baruch Hu desires that we connect with Him, He has given us the possibility to do so, so that we can attain it.

Since we understand through our intellect that there can be no connection or parity between the Creator and the created, and it is only because such is the will of the Creator, it follows that the things which connect the created with the Creator are not subject to the understanding of the intellect or the approval of the intellect.

With this, it is resolved and understandable that Torah and mitzvos—which are the things that connect a person, a Yid, with Hashem Yisbarach—do not require, nor is it possible for, the human intellect to provide its approval for them. For Torah and mitzvos come from Hashem Yisbarach Himself. When one is *zocheh*, one’s own intellect also becomes brighter and clearer, such that one also understands Torah and mitzvos as they should be understood. But even when one has not yet reached that understanding, it should not hold one back from fulfilling Torah and mitzvos, because, as stated above, one does not need the approval of the intellect for this.

This is also the idea recounted in the Chumash and explained in the Gemara and Midrashim: that through what did Yidden merit to receive the Torah? Only through the fact that they preceded *naaseh* (we will do) to *nishma* (we will understand). That is to say, they promised to do even without knowing what they would be told to do, and consequently without knowing if it would align with their own intellect. It is specifically through this path that one can accept Torah and mitzvos, which are the wisdom and will of the Hakadosh Baruch Hu.

I hope that for you personally, such an explanation is not necessary, and that you are observing Torah and mitzvos—especially Shabbos, tefillah, kashrus, and giving tzedakah as required. However, there are surely those in your environment whom you can influence to conduct themselves in the path of Torah and mitzvos. We are assured by Hashem Yisbarach that when one acts and desires to accomplish, one succeeds.

With blessings, awaiting good news.

## 1897

1897

B"H, 11 MarCheshvan, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...In your letter, you write regarding your daily schedule, your Torah study, and your davening. I was alarmed to read about your conduct regarding fasting. It is surprising that, although according to your letter you meet from time to time with anash, it seems you still do not know that this is not the path of the Baal Shem Tov, his disciples, the disciples of his disciples, and all who follow in their footsteps.

It is true that one can ascend to the House of Hashem through this path as well, but aside from the fact that it is a longer route, not everything is clarified, and the avodah is not performed as completely as it is when one works and acts through joy. As the verse states, "Serve Hashem with joy," and as is known from the Baal Shem Tov’s interpretation of the verse, "If you see the donkey of one who hates you" (cited in *Hayom Yom*, 28 Shevat): "If you see the donkey" — when you look with careful scrutiny at your *chomer* (materiality), which is the body; "you will see" — "the one who hates you" — that it hates the neshamah, which yearns for Elokus and spirituality. Furthermore, you will see that it is "crouching under its burden" — the burden that the Ribono shel Olam gave the body so that it would be refined through Torah and mitzvos, yet the body is lazy in fulfilling them. And perhaps it will occur to you: "You shall surely forsake [your desire] to abandon it" — that you will be able to fulfill its mission. For if you begin with *sigufim* (ascetic practices) to break the materiality, the light of Torah will not dwell in that way. Rather, "you shall surely forsake [your desire] with it" — to clarify the body and refine it, not to break it through *sigufim*.

Especially in these generations, when physical health is fragile, it is explained in several books—including the Rambam—that when the body is weak, it also results in a weakening of the power of understanding, which consequently disrupts Torah study and the kavanah of tefillah.

Therefore, my suggestion is that you consult with the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing man, who engages in communal needs, Rabbi Nissan Nemanov, may he live, the director of the Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim in Brunoy, as it is possible that you require *hataras nedarim* (annulment of vows) for this, etc. Instead of the fast—which diminishes one’s fat and blood due to the lack of food—you should eat at the proper time, in a manner suitable for physical health. As the Rambam rules, maintaining a healthy body is one of the ways of Hashem. You should exert your body to increase in Torah and mitzvos. It is also essential that you have some business or trade through which you can earn a livelihood, as written in the Rambam, *Hilchos Talmud Torah*, Chapter 3, Halachos 10 and 11: "Love work," and "Any Torah that is not accompanied by work will eventually be nullified." It is a great virtue for one to support himself through the work of his hands; it is the practice of the early Chassidim, and through this, one merits all the honor and goodness of this world and the World to Come.

I conclude my letter with a blessing for a successful arrangement of the above, and I will await good news from you.

With blessings.

#### ***1897***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 16, p. 584, and completed according to the secretariat's copy.

## 1898

1898

B"H, 11 MarCheshvan, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Enclosed is a copy of my letter to the Agudas N'shei U'Bnos Chabad here and also in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. In accordance with the principle that "a shaliach surely fulfills his mission," I am certain that you have also shared with your wife, may she live, what we discussed regarding this during the festival of Sukkos. It would be appropriate for you to encourage her regarding this, and together you can consult on the methods of how to bring this from potential into action within your camp. I have already stated that one should not be particular that the members must specifically be women and girls from families that have a "certificate" of being from Chabad. On the contrary, to be lenient in accepting members as much as possible is praiseworthy, provided that the new additions do not express opinions on spiritual matters; then it is good for them and for those who stand at the head...

#### ***1898***

## 1899

B"H, 11 MarCheshvan, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 3 Gimmel Cheshvan, I was pleased to read of your study schedule in both Nigleh and Chassidus. Surely, in accordance with the ruling of our Sages that we increase in matters of holiness, you will add to this in quantity, and most importantly, in quality—namely, in consistency, diligence, and depth of study. As is known from our Sages: "You have labored and you have found."

Regarding your notification of your upcoming birthday: On the day of the Torah reading closest to it, you should receive an aliyah to the Torah and also recite the Book of Tehillim. As brought down in *Hayom Yom* for 11 Nissan, "On one’s birthday, a person should seclude himself, recall his memories, and contemplate them; those that require rectification and teshuvah, he should repent and rectify." You should set aside a few moments for this seclusion, during which you should study a *maamar* of Chassidus and make a *hachlatah tova* (good resolution) for the coming year. This should be something appropriate for your level—that is, something within your capacity that fits the *yeshiva* schedule and relates to Torah and *yiras shamayim*. You may consult with your *mashpia* regarding this.

Regarding your question as to whether you should put on *tefillin d'Rabeinu Tam*: For the time being, it is sufficient to be careful to avoid *hesech hada'as* (distraction) while wearing *tefillin d'Rashi*.

With blessings for success in Torah study, with *yiras shamayim*, and with success.

***

**1899**

**Tefillin d'Rabeinu Tam:** See also below, letter 2084.

At the very least, he should do so now by writing to the *Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch* regarding which books from our publications interest him and which he does not yet possess. 1901

Brooklyn.

...We have heard several times from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of saintly memory, based on the words of our Sages, that the attribute of Hashem is "measure for measure." Therefore, whoever engages in proper chinuch, drawing the hearts of the sons and daughters of Yisrael closer to our Father in Heaven, their reward in particular is true nachas from their own offspring. It is my firm hope that for you and your husband, the Rabbi, may you live and be well, this will be fulfilled through the attribute of Hashem, from His full, open, holy, and expansive hand.

## 1812

1812

B”H, 11 MarCheshvan, 5713

Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I am interested to know if you have a set time for the study of Chassidus, as this study leads to the love of Hashem and the fear of Hashem (and I would point to the beginning of Chapter 2 of Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah). These are among the mitzvos whose obligation is constant and never ceases from a person, not even for a moment throughout his entire life, as is written in the author’s introduction to Sefer HaChinuch.

With blessings.

## 1903

1903

B"H, 16 MarCheshvan, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

It was a pleasure to receive your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh, in which you write about your involvement in the field of kosher chinuch, bringing the hearts of the sons and daughters of Yisrael closer to our Father in Heaven. Regarding your statement that you are not satisfied because you have not succeeded much in matters of discipline: I have already told you before to dismiss your melancholic thoughts, which have no basis. As for your lack of success, it is surely in accordance with the words of our Sages (Megillah 6b): "If a person tells you, 'I have not labored and I have found,' do not believe him." However, before that it is stated: "If a person tells you, 'I have labored and I have not found,' do not believe him." Consequently, this matter is in your own hands.

2) Regarding what you wrote that you are not satisfied: this is actually a good sign. Dissatisfaction can lead to the revelation of hidden powers when one's revealed powers are insufficient. Satisfaction, by contrast, usually leads to yeshus, etc., and a lack of avodah—or at the very least, a lack of avodah with the appropriate vigor—which is the opposite of the desired goal. The intention is that a person’s avodah must be specifically through yegiah. Further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

With blessings for success in both general and personal matters.

Awaiting good tidings.

## 1804

1804

B"H, 16 MarCheshvan, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 8 Cheshvan after the long interval, and thank G-d that your health has improved. You are surely aware of the doctors’ opinion—and you can see this tangibly as well—that regarding high blood pressure, the absence of agitation is a tried and tested remedy. In order to attain this state of being free from agitation, it would be appropriate for you to study with the necessary focus *Iggeres HaKodesh* by our Alter Rebbe (which is the fourth part of Tanya and is printed and bound with it), Letter 25. This is also understandable through human intellect, and one may add a bit of emphasis: it is tangibly evident that becoming agitated over worldly matters not only brings no benefit, but actually causes damage.

2) Regarding what you wrote about publishing news concerning Torah and mitzvos in the *Morgen Journal* newspaper: since the state of *am ha'aratzus* (ignorance of Torah) is prevalent in this country, you are surely aware that such people are not readers of the Yiddish newspaper, but only of the language of the country. As for those who have some knowledge, Torah-related matters are printed in the press from time to time (though I am not entirely comfortable with this either, as they are often not suited to the goal. Above all, it is difficult to calculate the balance of damage versus benefit, since contradictory matters regarding Torah and mitzvos are printed in the same newspaper, and it is difficult to estimate in advance which items the reader will study more closely, and what will be more deeply engraved in his memory). You are surely aware of the policy of the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch, which publishes matters of Torah and mitzvos in the language of the country in the form of stories or simple articles and the like. The reason more is not published is only due to a lack of resources; when Hashem grants that the situation improves, this publishing effort will also grow.

3) Regarding your question as to whether there are restrictions concerning the *bracha* of *Asher Yatzar* for someone who requires it several times a day: there is no distinction to be made in this matter. If it is due to a laxative, see the *Acharonim* in *Orach Chaim* 67.

4) Regarding your second question, concerning someone who maintains both practices—praying in the synagogue on Shabbos while also going to his shop on that day—and the question of whether he will receive reward for being in the synagogue: you do not specify in your letter what the practical implication is. Seemingly, this is a matter for the Angel Michael, who records the merits of the Jewish people. A mitzvah that one performs is indeed a mitzvah, and he will certainly receive reward for it. However, it goes without saying that this does not help to diminish the gravity of the transgression of *chilul Shabbos*, especially sitting in a shop, which is a matter of *b'farhesia* (public desecration). It is the duty of those who know such a person to explain to him that there is no such concept as "buying oneself off"—that because he prays in the synagogue, the gravity of the *chilul Shabbos* that follows is diminished. Further elaboration on this is superfluous.

5) Regarding what you wrote in your letter that you spoke with Rabbi... *sh'yichyeh* about what will be after a long life and years, etc.—I am very surprised at you, for you still have many good years ahead in which to rectify and accomplish in this world. You should divert your mind from such thoughts and delve with appropriate depth into how to rectify your portion in the world, while in good health and with peace of mind. May Hashem grant you success in this for many years to come.

With blessings,

P.S. Enclosed is a copy of an excerpt from what was discussed during the past Sukkos holiday. Its content is that in our activities, the beginning must be through an **abundance** of light, and only afterward do we proceed from level to level. This will surely be of benefit to you in your outreach in your surroundings.

#### ***1804***

**From what was discussed during the holiday of Sukkos:** See also above, Letter 1876, and the references in the notes there.

## 1895

B"H, 16 MarCheshvan, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding your son, may he live, concerning the matter of a suitable shidduch, may it be in a good and auspicious hour: He himself must also be awakened to the fact that all matters below are drawn down from above, and consequently, they follow the pattern of matters above. Therefore, *is'arusa d'le'eila* (arousal from above) comes about through *is'arusa d'letata* (arousal from below). This is also the inner content of the Sages' teaching that the attributes of the Ribono shel Olam are "measure for measure." 

Consequently, he himself—as well as all those for whom the matter of your son’s, may he live, marriage is relevant—must strengthen themselves in those matters that lead to the *yichud* (unification) of *Kudsha Brich Hu* and *Shechintei* (the Holy One, blessed be He, and His Shechinah), as it were, in accordance with what is explained in Tanya, Chapter 41, and in many places in *Chassidus*, to be understood.

I trust you participated in the *farbrengens* that were held during the month of Tishrei among *anash*, and I am interested to hear the details regarding this.

With blessings.

## 1806

B"H, 16th of Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter from Thursday, in which you write regarding the situation in the business and the friction between you and... in the business...

Regarding this detail, I must add that we see tangibly that becoming agitated over worldly matters not only fails to help, but actually causes damage. This is especially true regarding the relationship between one person and another; when one becomes agitated, the other becomes agitated as well. At the time when emotions are revealed, they obscure the intellect and the mind, and afterwards, one realizes that one shouldn't have said that word. Furthermore, the lack of peace is unhealthy for the business as well, sometimes both materially and spiritually. When you work on yourself to be more in the realm of intellect and less in the realm of emotions, then, as a matter of course, ways will reveal themselves to stabilize the business, and the work in the business will also be as it should be.

One of the mistakes seen among *avreichim* is that they separate the material world from the spiritual (which, in the final analysis, is a matter contrary to faith, for the faith in Hashem as One and His Name as One applies both to the material and the spiritual). Consequently, it seems to them that if the business is not as it should be, one only needs to seek to fix things regarding the business itself. They do not consider that perhaps this is because they need to fulfill something in matters of Torah and *mitzvos*, **which are** the channel for *parnassah*. When you are strong in keeping the three *shiurim* that are equal for every soul—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—which are well-known, and also in setting fixed times for Torah study in addition to the above, in both *nigleh* and Chassidus, then the material aspect of the business will also go from strength to strength and with joy.

With blessings for success, both spiritually and materially, for you and your wife, *shichyu*.

## 1907

1907

B"H, 16 MarCheshvan, 5713

Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...It is surprising that even in this letter of yours, you write nothing regarding your daughter, *tichyeh*. Furthermore, I am somewhat puzzled that in these lists of those participating in the activities of Chabad in our camp in various fields, I did not see your name. It is surely unnecessary to arouse you regarding the "rock from which you were hewn," etc., for as is explained in many holy books—and as we see tangibly—fathers bequeath their strengths and characteristics to their children. Consequently, there is much good stored within you, yet you are not utilizing it. This is a pity, both for the environment that is not receiving this influence, and consequently for you as well, for as the well-known parable goes, in truth and in essence, the poor man does more for the householder than the householder does for the poor man.

Surely there are several reasons for all of the above, but it seems to me that the primary and fundamental reason is the interruption in time—in the German language, "the disconnection"—that has existed until now. However, the only advice for this is **returning** to one's matter and place (a place in spirituality, which is a matter of level and standing). *Un dos iz dokh keynmol nit tzu shpet* (And this is, after all, never too late), especially at the beginning of the year.

With blessings for success and for proper health.

Awaiting good news.

## 1808

B"H, 23 Mar-Cheshvan, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your letter of the 17th of Cheshvan, in which you describe your situation in the army and that you are being sent to an officer training course that begins in the month of Kislev and ends at the end of the month of Shevat. You are in a dilemma, as the original plan was for your wedding to take place in Kislev, but doing so would require you to miss the opportunity to attend this course.

If the bride and the parents on both sides agree to this, it is my opinion that on the day originally set for the wedding, you should write the *tenaim*. If you have already written the *tenaim* beyond the initial *vort*, then the parents from both sides should gather to discuss the details pertaining to the wedding. This gathering should be held with joy—that is, accompanied by a *seudas mitzvah*, such as a *siyum masechta*, *melaveh malkah*, or the like. The wedding itself should take place, at a propitious and successful time, in the month of Adar, may it come upon us and all of Israel for good. I am certain you will inform me of your decision regarding this as soon as possible.

With blessings that whatever you decide, it should be with success in both material and spiritual matters.

## 1809

B"H, 23 Mar-Cheshvan, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., R' Nissan, may he live.

Shalom u'Bracha!

In response to your letter of the 17th of Mar-Cheshvan, in which you write regarding what you have been through and that, thank G-d, everything has passed peacefully: It is well known from our Sages of blessed memory that the Jewish people are compared to the stars, and when they begin to rise, etc. See also Bava Basra (12b), "and all who benefit him, etc." May it be Hashem's will that this be in a manner of good that is visible, revealed, and tangible.

Regarding your question concerning your future endeavors, especially since you were informed from London that for the time being there is no demand for shochtim: In my opinion, you should exert the greatest possible energy to obtain an entry visa to Morocco, specifically to Casablanca, and take part there in the educational work in the vineyard of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. Regarding the methods for obtaining the papers—since you must provide the names of people on-site who are requesting you—you should immediately contact the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, who is involved in communal needs, R' Shmuel, may he live, of Toussaf, and he will provide you with the details regarding this. At the start of the matter, it is appropriate that you travel yourself, and afterwards your family, may they live, will join you there. It is to be hoped that this will be a place of livelihood for you—both materially and spiritually.

I await good news and bless you with success.

#### ***1809***

**R' Nissan, may he live:** Pinson, Paris. Another letter to him—below, 2018.

## 1810

B”H, 23 Mar-Cheshvan, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the honorable Rabbi, the Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned man, who occupies himself with communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Shneur Zalman, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from the eve of Shabbos Noach, the second day of the week, the eve of Shabbos Lech Lecha, and the eve of Shabbos Vayeira, along with their enclosures.

2) It causes me distress that the matter of collecting the various pledges remaining from the campaign is still being delayed. Although the honorable Rabbi, the Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned man, who occupies himself with communal needs, etc., Rabbi Chaim Mordechai A. Hodakov, conveyed to me the reasons for this that he heard from you, it is a known saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: In matters such as these, which in truth concern the Angel Michael, the Prince of Israel—who brings the merits of Israel into account—since the reason given is a true one, there is not only no room for the opposite of reward, but it even enters into the account of "he intended to perform a mitzvah and was prevented by circumstances, and Scripture credits him as if he had performed it." However, regarding the action and the labor itself—which is the task of man upon this earth in this physical and material world—when the action and labor are missing, it simply does not exist, and it is self-evident that the results of it do not exist either.

Regarding what you write to me on this matter: even though, on the face of it, the reasons you explained are appropriate—for surely for every matter in the world one can find a way to rectify it, except that sometimes revealed powers are sufficient, while at other times one must also engage hidden powers, and even among those, higher and higher levels, until it is possible to reach even essential, primal powers—in order for such powers to be revealed, there must usually be two things: a) the hope that if they are revealed, one will succeed, and b) that one recognizes the necessity of the matter, which makes the effort and toil worthwhile. I hope to hear good news from you that you have begun to seek ways to remove the aforementioned reasons, and my confidence is strong that **at the beginning** of your search, you will see how the reasons are nullified and the matters come to fruition.

3) I was very pleased with what you wrote regarding your visit to Canton, Ohio, on your way from here, although it is a pity that you did not delay, at least for a short while, in the two towns you mention in your letter, Nareestan and Carlisle. Even though you write the reasons for this, it is the same concept explained in the previous section. And even if it would not have been effective, the saying of the Baal Shem Tov is well-known regarding a Jew who wanders on the road and through towns (copied in the notes at the end of *Likutei Torah*, Kehot edition)...

I am interested to know if there was any practical outcome regarding what I spoke about with your wife, may she live, in your presence, concerning the *Agudas N'shei U'bnos Chabad* in your camp. Enclosed is a copy of my letter to some of the branches of such organizations that have already begun their good work. This is truly relevant to all branches, including those that will open in the future, and therefore, yours in the camp is included as well. It is also understood that what was discussed regarding the order of the creation of the world in general, and the "small world" (man) in particular, should be utilized in other propaganda efforts as well.

With blessings for success in your communal work, which will surely serve as a channel and vessel for additional blessing and success in your personal affairs.

Awaiting good news.

## 1811

1811

B.H., 24 MarCheshvan, 5713
Brooklyn.

Agudas N'shei U’Bnos Chabad of Montreal
May Hashem keep them alive

Blessings and peace!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter from Parshas Vayeira, in which you write about your first meeting on Tuesday, 2 Cheshvan, regarding the resolutions you adopted, and also the names of the women who participated in the meeting.

I hope that, just as every living thing grows, so too will this grow—both in quantity, in the number of women who will participate in Agudas N'shei U’Bnos Chabad, and in quality, by expanding the work in various areas: both in the spiritual realm, by studying the appropriate subjects, and in the physical realm of spiritual work, regarding assistance to the holy institutions. As our Sages, of blessed memory, have said: "A person sanctifies himself a little below"—meaning, a person sanctifies himself even just a little in this physical world—"and they sanctify him much from above"—they give him help and sanctify him with a much greater measure and with strengths from Above.

Enclosed is a copy of a letter of mine to the Agudas N'shei U’Bnos Chabad in various places, which in truth is relevant to the Agudas N'shei U’Bnos Chabad in all places where they already exist and which, with the help of Hashem, will yet be established.

With a wish for blessing and success in the aforementioned work, and may this also serve as a channel and vessel for blessing and success in your personal matters, and I look forward to hearing good news.
