## 1812

B”H, 24 Marcheshvan, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...It is self-understood that the aforementioned matter does not involve any concession whatsoever regarding the Lubavitcher shul in the Ninth Camp. From time to time, Chassidic farbrengens should be held there, along with all other activities appropriate for a shul that has merited to be called by the name "Lubavitcher Shul." I am confident that through appropriate and calm explanation, the leaders of the Lubavitcher shul will also strive toward all of the above—namely, that their shul should be suitable and worthy of its name.

Regarding what was said to them—that this is merely a matter of inheritance—this is indeed true, and it is the entire merit of the Jewish people wherever they may be: the merit of the forefathers, Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov. As we **preface** every single prayer with "G-d of Avraham, G-d of Yitzchak, and G-d of Yaakov," and only afterward do we present our various requests as appropriate for the time—whether on weekdays, Shabbos, or Yom Tov. One should not be ashamed in the slightest of matters of inheritance, as the prayer states: "Happy are we, how good is our portion, how pleasant our lot, and how beautiful our inheritance." Without a doubt, the congregants of the Lubavitcher shul also recite "G-d of Avraham, G-d of Yitzchak, and G-d of Yaakov" in the Shemoneh Esrei, and they also say "how beautiful is our inheritance." If Hashem has granted them the merit that, within the Jewish people themselves, they have also merited to be connected to Lubavitch and to all the influences and blessings that come and are poured forth through our Nesi’im of Lubavitch, from our Rabbeinu HaZaken until my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—then they must create suitable vessels to receive this additional merit. They have no choice in the matter of whether to do so or not, for this is the merit of their fathers and forefathers who are in the World of Truth, watching from there with an open eye—and not only at the times when Yizkor is recited, but throughout the entire year. To elaborate further on this is unnecessary, for surely this will suffice.

May Hashem spread and expand their borders to illuminate the light of the inner dimension of Torah—which is the Torah of Chassidus, its ways, and its customs—throughout the entire city, in accordance with the desire of Rabbeinu HaZaken, who said that Chassidus is the inheritance of the entire Jewish people and belongs to everyone. The words of the Tzaddikim are alive and endure forever for those who draw near to them. Ultimately, holiness will spread throughout the entire world, in accordance with our Sages’ statement that Eretz Yisrael is destined to expand into all lands. And as for Eretz Yisrael, the interpretation is well-known: that it desired to do the will of its Creator, in the manner of the avodah that is called by its name, the name Yisrael, for "you have struggled with G-d and with men, and you have prevailed."

With blessings for success in your holy work to spread the light of our holy Nesi’im in every place and at every time.

## 1813

1813

B"H, 25 MarCheshvan, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the distinguished Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, involved in communal needs, etc.,
R' Shalom, may he live.

Shalom u'Bracha!

In response to your notification requesting a blessing for Mr. ...

It is surprising, as I have several times urged Anash, may they live, that when requesting something on behalf of another person, one should also provide details regarding his age, his family status, and—most importantly—his standing and situation regarding the matters of Torah and mitzvos. This is also understood logically, for every form of *hashpaah* requires appropriate *keilim*. Since, through *Hashgacha*, the requester has come into connection with me—even though it is certain that help can come in other ways as well, since Hashem is the One who bestows all matters, and especially to the sons and daughters of Yisrael, regarding children, life, and sustenance, which do not depend on merit—as it is in the *Beis Din*—but rather on *mazal*—which is Hashem—it depends (see the final note to the *sicha* of *Shabbos Mevarchim* the month of Elul, printed in *HaPardes* for the month of Tishrei of this year)—it is reasonable to say that the intention is that I must arouse him regarding some matter of Torah and mitzvos. Consequently, I must know where to begin, for which the aforementioned information is necessary. I am certain you will provide this in your next letter.

Enclosed is a copy of my letter to the branches of Agudas N'shei U'Bnos Chabad in various locations. It would be appropriate for you to seek strategies and advice on how to organize this matter in your camp as well. It is understood that officially this must be done by women, but you and your household, may they live, should be the life-force behind the work. I will await good news regarding all of the above.

#### ***1813***

**R' Shalom, may he live:** Rivkin, St. Louis.

**The Sicha:** In *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 2, p. 632, note 42.

**My letter to the branches of Agudas N'shei U'Bnos Chabad:** Above, 1777.

## 1814

B.H., 25 MarCheshvan, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Sh. Z. [Hecht], may he live.

Peace and Blessing!

...Regarding what you wrote in your letter concerning the organization of N'shei U’Bnos Chabad in your camp, it is certain that you should include all those women who have contacted me over the past months with various requests. Naturally, each one should be involved according to her capacity, whether as a general member or by taking part in some form of activity or outreach. I believe that Mrs. Levitansky spoke about matters of this nature when she was here some time ago. It must be emphasized to each one that for the N'shei U’Bnos Chabad organization, one does not need a "complete certificate" of someone who davens specifically according to the Nusach of the Alter Rebbe and also puts on Rabbeinu Tam tefillin, etc. Rather, all those who acknowledge that one must serve Hashem not only with the feeling of the heart, but that the vessels of the intellect must also be filled with the knowledge of Hashem—they are, by definition, included in Chabad. As for what they may lack in other areas, there is no solution to be found in excluding them from the organization; on the contrary, by joining the organization, they will also fill in the deficiencies in the various areas where they are lacking.

I heard from someone who came to interview me that he could not restrain himself and informed me immediately upon the conclusion of our conversation that the custom is, "from a word one makes a quart" (i.e., to exaggerate). The aforementioned did this, of course, without asking permission. However, regarding what I wrote in my proposal to the N'shei U’Bnos Chabad, he has my permission to make "from a word a quart."

## 1815

B"H, 25 MarCheshvan, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

It was with pleasure that I learned about you from the Rav, the Chassid, the G-d-fearing man, who is involved in communal needs, etc., Moreinu HaRav Shneur Zalman Hecht, may he live, and regarding his efforts to raise the banner of Yiddishkeit through appropriate advocacy concerning the necessity of kosher education in particular, and the observance of Torah and mitzvos in general. The immense value of this matter is beyond measure. And even though it sometimes seems that one is speaking and yet no effect is visible, we have no way of knowing the details of Hashgacha Pratis. Furthermore, regarding words that come from the heart, the holy Torah has already ruled that they enter the hearts of the listeners; consequently, it is **certain** that, ultimately, they will have their effect. Even if the person who is doing the seeing does not always see this effect, the reason for this could be: a) that the effect will come after some time, or b) that man sees with his eyes, but Hashem sees into the heart. It is possible that the soul of the listener has already been shaken, and the darkness has been turned into light, and the bitterness into sweetness. Although, in truth, one detail does not depend on the other—for the one who rebukes and inspires must rebuke, and by doing so he has already fulfilled his own mitzvah—nevertheless, for the pleasantness of the avodah, our Sages have informed us that in addition to this, the reward for performing a mitzvah is, as our Sages said, "the reward of a mitzvah is the mitzvah itself"—meaning the fulfillment of the mitzvah itself—there is an additional reward: that he has succeeded in bringing a son or daughter of Yisrael closer to our Father in Heaven. The magnitude of the joy on both sides is understood: both on the part of the Father, the Holy One, blessed be He, and on the part of His only child, the son or daughter of Yisrael—who have been brought closer to one another through the speech or action of the one who rebukes and inspires. And great is this joy, which breaks through barriers to bestow upon the one who rebukes and inspires blessing and success in all that he needs, both materially and spiritually...

## 1816

1816

B.H., 25 MarCheshvan, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to hear from the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing, etc., Moreinu HaRav Shneur Zalman Hecht, may he live, regarding the rescue of your daughter, may she live. I hope that this will be a good beginning, so that from now on you will have *nachas* from her in a peaceful and tranquil manner—*Yiddishe nachas*, which is the true *nachas* that a Jew can have from children. This has always been the case, and especially in these times when there are many upheavals and changes, the security one can provide for children is by connecting them to the Borei Olam, who, blessed be He, is the Master of the entire world and directs all its details. This connection with Hashem Yisbarach is achieved by living a life of Torah and mitzvos. May Hashem Yisbarach help you to carry this out with joy and expansiveness.

2) I was also pleased that you recognize, in the incident with your daughter, that this is a matter of Hashgacha Pratis. This should strengthen within you the proof that Hashem Yisbarach watches over you and your household. Once one understands the hint—*remez*—that is given from above, one is thereby discharged for a long time, and for all time, so that one should not, Heaven forbid, need to be reminded in such a way again, because one remembers on one's own.

3) From everything a Jew sees, one can derive a lesson for one's personal life, as we have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the name of the holy Baal Shem Tov. From your business, too, one can derive a *remez* regarding this:

4) According to what Rabbi Hecht, may he live, writes to me, your business involves automobiles. The nature of an automobile is that it possesses the materials and the power through which it moves and travels from one place to another, but the initial push—*dchifah*—comes through a spark. This starting is the beginning of all the subsequent movement of the automobile. However, it is not good that this starter spark should need to be given often, or for every part of the automobile's movement. So it is also with a person, and especially with a Jew: the purpose of a Jew is to be an *oved Hashem*—to serve the Almighty, blessed be He—and to serve with the powers that Hashem Yisbarach has placed **within his** *nefesh elokis*, and also with his *nefesh habahamis*. At the beginning, or from time to time, the person takes on a spark that starts the entire procedure. However, it is not good that one should need to rely on the spark too often, and certainly one should not allow this to happen, by listening to the first spark—*remez*—and serving Hashem with the very powers that Hashem has placed **within** the person.

5) Surely you recite Tehillim after davening every morning, and it would be appropriate for you to give a few cents to *tzedakah* every Monday and Thursday. May Hashem Yisbarach grant you success.

With blessings.

## 1817

B"H, 26 Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...It is known that a remedy corrects from this point forward (Kesuvos 74b), but it is also possible to uproot the entire [matter] from its source (see Chullin 48a; Responsa Tzafnas Paneach, Vol. 1, Sec. 14). Now, the vitality and health of the body are dependent upon the soul, and the vitality and health of the soul of a Jewish person are dependent upon Torah and mitzvos. As our Sages of blessed memory stated, the 248 positive mitzvos correspond to the 248 limbs, and the 365 negative mitzvos correspond to the 365 sinews (Zohar, Vol. 1, 170b). This is not merely a coincidence of numbers; on the contrary, it is because the matters are related to one another that they are equal in number (see Tanya, Chapter 51).

In the spiritual healing of a person—the healing of the soul, from which the healing of the body evolves—there are likewise two methods: either one merely corrects the situation from this point forward, or one uproots the matter from its source. This occurs through avodah from yirah or from ahavah (Yoma 86a). Through avodah from ahavah, not even a trace of the previous inappropriate state remains in the spiritual realm, and one returns to one’s strength in both the physical and spiritual sense—to the strength in the body through the revelation of the strength in the soul (see Kuntres Acharon in Tanya, s.v. *V'Tzedakah K'Nachal*; Likutei Torah, beginning of Parshas Re'eh, s.v. *Anochi Nosein Lifneichem Hayom Berachah*).

## 1818

B"H, Sunday, 28 Mar-Cheshvan, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the special assembly of the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch,
May Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

As you gather today to hear a report on the good works and activities of the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch and to discuss its material standing, I express my blessing that you will succeed in finding the counsel and methods to strengthen this holy institution, to place it on a firm foundation, and to provide it with the means to expand the scope of its influence.

The institution of Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch was founded by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and was precious to him with exceptional love and affection. Every single member of Anash, according to their capacity and situation, is obligated to participate in this work, both in overt efforts and in private efforts—in the field of disseminating proper education and maintaining it, and in the preservation of Yiddishkeit in its traditional purity throughout all corners of the world.

The expansion and broadening of this work and outreach in general, and specifically the founding and maintenance of proper educational institutions in the most necessary places, depend to a great extent on providing the means required by the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch.

The responsibility that rests upon the shoulders of us all is great, and the fulfillment of the financial deficit is considered as nothing in comparison to it.

It is my hope that each and every one of those gathered today—and through them, this call of mine will surely be conveyed to the rest of our friends, Anash, to whom it is obviously also directed—will appreciate the words stated here, take to heart the magnitude of the responsibility placed upon them, and strive with all their ability to assist the work of the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch in all its branches. In doing so, you will provide it with the possibility to fulfill its mission and the role assigned to it by its founder, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, to fulfill them in accordance with his will.

May Hashem grant each of us the merit to realize all our good resolutions in their entirety, with abundance and in good health.

With a blessing for great success.

## 1819

B”H, 28 Marcheshvan, 5713
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chassid, who is involved in communal affairs, etc.,
Rabbi Yitzchak, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 18 Marcheshvan and the one preceding it, I ask for your forgiveness for the delay in my response due to the many pressures and the volume of letters that accumulated over the past month of Tishrei. Regarding the letters that require practical action, I have seen that the custom is to prioritize them over those that discuss matters of Midrash (see *Pischei Teshuvah* to *Yoreh Deah* 242, subsection 9). I am certain that you will forgive me for the delay, knowing the reason for it.

Regarding your comments:

1) As for my reference to *Biurei HaZohar* on Parshas Eikev, it was never my intention from the outset to suggest that the exact matter we are discussing in our correspondence is explained there. Rather, I followed my usual practice: when I find a concept in the *nigleh* (the revealed Torah), I take the opportunity to search for an explanation of that concept in the teachings of Chassidus. Conversely, when studying an explanation in Chassidus, I look for a parallel in the *nigleh*, even if the explanation there is of a different nature. However, upon further reflection, there is more to add: since the aforementioned *Biurei HaZohar* discusses the concept of *berachos* of enjoyment (*berachos ha-nehenin*), one can certainly find additional illumination there regarding the content of our letters. See there in various places, and especially at the end of the *maamar* beginning with the words *Hashem d’a raza d’emtza’ita*, which states: "And this is the explanation of 'Blessed are You, Hashem...'—in order that there be an *ha'ala* (elevation), meaning that the fruit of the physical tree can be included in the utterance 'a tree yielding fruit,' etc. And this is the explanation of 'Creator of the fruit of the tree,' and similarly in all *berachos ha-nehenin*—and a word to the wise is sufficient." From this, it is understood that if one recites a general *beracha*, it is included in the general utterance that precedes the specific utterance for that species. This is not the case when one recites a specific *beracha*; it is then included in the utterance specific to that species, whether it is stated explicitly—as in the *beracha* for the fruit of the tree mentioned in *Biurei HaZohar*—or in an utterance that comes through exchanges and substitutions, as explained in *Shaar HaYichud* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, Chapter 1 and the end of Chapter 12.

2) In short, the matter can also be explained in another way: just as the superiority of a general *beracha* over a specific one lies in the fact that, in addition to the specific detail, it **includes** within it other details, this very same logic applies to why, in *berachos ha-nehenin*, one must recite a specific *beracha* for that particular species. For then, in addition to the gratitude for the qualities of the category—such as the category of vegetation—there is **added** gratitude for the qualities of that specific species within that category, such as the fruit of the tree. This is analogous to the concept of "the general and the additional" found in the *Shas*, and this is well understood.

3) If I were not hesitant, I would add another reason why the custom is to recite a general *beracha* formula on Rosh Hashanah—because the essence of Rosh Hashanah is the **general** aspect of the entire year.

4) You point out in your letter to Rashi on *Devarim* 33:29, arguing that his commentary implies that even in a general *beracha* there is a specific element that is not in the general. I did not understand your intent, for Rashi’s language is: "After he detailed the blessings for them, he said to them: 'Why should I detail them for you? The general rule is that everything is yours.'" If so, on the face of it, it would seem to imply the opposite.

Relying on your previous statement that I may send you anything that is published, I am enclosing a segment from what was discussed at the *farbrengen* of Simchas Torah. Its relevance to the above matters is that in the dissemination of Torah and *yiras shamayim*, there are those who hesitate or advise against studying the "light of the Torah"—which is the inner dimension of the Torah—because they wish to proceed from the easy to the difficult, to "fill their bellies" with *Shas* and *poskim* first, and so on.

However, it is known in many places in Chassidic teachings that the "depth of the heights" and the "depth of the depths" are one and the same. Just as the descent into the "deep pit" is possible only for one who has been on the "high mountain," so too, the subsequent ascent to a level even higher than the "high mountain" is achieved specifically through the descent into the "deep pit." As is known, there is a difference between the descent of the angels below, which leads to their fall, and the descent of the souls below, which is precisely what enables them to "attach themselves to the body of the King." It is the same regarding the study of Torah itself: to arrive at studying with affection (*Nedarim* 81a) and to fulfill the *mitzvos* precisely, even in the details and the details of details—this comes (especially in our days) specifically through a connection to the inner dimension of the Torah (see *Tanya*, Chapter 4: "And without it, they have no true existence"). This is also the concept of the light created on the first day, which Hashem **hid** in the Torah (cited in the name of the Baal Shem Tov; see also *Zohar Chadash* I, 264a; *Zohar Chadash* II, 179a; *Tikkunei Zohar* 6; *Zohar Chadash* Ruth 85a). Further elaboration for someone like you is surely superfluous.

With respect and blessing.

## 1920

1920

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you convey a request... to be blessed with sons who are healthy and G-d-fearing:

It is appropriate that the aforementioned person increase his strength in *ahavas Yisrael*, love of Torah, and love of Hashem Yisbarach. As is well known in the books of Kabbalah and Chassidus, the birth of love in the spiritual realm is a *segulah* for the birth of a son in the physical realm. Consequently, it is understood that the maintenance and strengthening of this love in the spiritual realm—which is achieved through *hisbonenus* in His greatness, as per the language of the Rambam (*Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah*, beginning of Chapter 2)—draws down long life, for length of days and good years, for sons in the physical realm.

Therefore, without a vow, until his wife—may she live—gives birth to a son, he should give a franc or two to *tzedakah* every weekday before *davening* Shacharis. It is appropriate that this *tzedakah* be connected to the food and drink of poor students. When a son is born to him, he should name him after *kavod kedushas* our master and teacher, the Rebbe, *ztzukulalleh nbg"m zya"u ysu"o*, which is Yosef Yitzchak. May Hashem Yisbarach grant you the merit to bring good news regarding all of the above.

With blessings for success in general matters and in your personal affairs.

#### ***1920***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 12, p. 179, and completed according to the secretariat's copy.

**Segulah for the birth of a son:** See above, Vol. 6, Letter 1776, and the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 1921

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter from the 26th of Tishrei, and due to various reasons, my response has been delayed.

In your letter, you ask regarding your studies in the yeshiva and also regarding the matter of accounting, with the intention that this should later serve as a vessel for parnassah, and you ask for my opinion on this: whether you should continue your studies in accounting.

You do not write in your letter the main point: how much time you have already spent studying accounting and how much time you still need to finish it.

In general, it is self-evident that in one’s younger years, time is much more precious than in later years, because what is gathered in youth is like a sowing for the later years, from which a single grain can grow into many plants or an entire tree.

If the time required to finish is not too long, and is also not connected with subjects that are a contradiction to yiras shamayim, then since you have already spent time studying this and it is also the wish of [your] mother, tichyeh, it is worthwhile to finish it. However, if you still need to dedicate a long time and many hours a day to this, you should think it over well and calculate the gain and the loss in this. May Hashem help you to be successful in your affairs, both in gashmius and in ruchnius.

With blessings for yiras shamayim.

## 1922

B"H, 1st of Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all those who cherish Torah and Yiddishkeit, may Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

In many places in the Gemara and Midrash, Chazal extol the great merit and privilege of the Jewish woman—the *akeres habayis* who helps establish and maintain the Jewish home upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, and in whose hands lies, to a very great extent, the upbringing of children in a truly Jewish, Torah-true way.

The **"Beis Rivkah"** schools, which operate under the supervision of the "Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch," perform a most important and necessary task by educating Jewish daughters with *chinuch hakasher* and preparing them so that they may, in the future, be responsible Jewish women and mothers.

Thanks to their tireless and dedicated work, the **Beis Rivkah institutions**, over the course of their eleven-year existence, have educated hundreds upon hundreds of students in the spirit of Torah, *yiras shamayim*, and *midos tovos*, who are a source of *nachas* to their parents and a pride to the Jewish people.

At this moment, the institutions find themselves in a difficult economic situation, and the activists of the institutions—led by the esteemed Chossid, a man of energy and many accomplishments, etc., Rabbi Y. Jacobs—are making the greatest efforts to enable their continued existence.

On Sunday, the 13th of Kislev, may it come upon us for good, the **annual celebration** of the **Beis Rivkah** institutions will take place, *im yirtzeh Hashem*. I turn with a call of affection and inspiration to all those who hold Torah and Yiddishkeit dear and who correctly appreciate the importance of *chinuch hakasher* for the daughters of Israel:

**It is a holy obligation upon everyone, man and woman, to support the "Beis Rivkah" institutions with all their capabilities.**

**Participate in the annual celebration and help provide the financial means, which are highly necessary to maintain the Beis Rivkah institutions.**

**It is not merely help, but a rescue for a fortress of *chinuch habanos* on the purity of holiness.**

And in this merit, may the Ribono shel Olam help all the participants, supporters, and helpers in whatever they are in need of—with children, life, and abundant sustenance, both materially and spiritually.

With a blessing for success and much goodness, materially and spiritually,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1823

B"H, 1 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 13 Cheshvan, in which you write regarding the state of the Yeshiva: I am very pained that its borders are not expanding with more students. It is surely impossible that with appropriate effort and energetic searching, one cannot find attentive students in [the city] and its surroundings to enter your Yeshiva. It is well known in many places in our Sages' teachings that even for the sake of one child, one must exert many efforts, and certainly for the sake of several children. We do not know the extent of the impact, as related in the Gemara (Yevamos 62b): "For you do not know which will succeed." And in Maseches Bava Basra (91a): "One out of sixty is diligent." Surely you will all consult together on how to approach the work of outreach in this regard, and Hashem will grant you success.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the demolition of an oven, that you heard there is a letter from my father-in-law, the Rebbe (Rashab) n'e, regarding this: enclosed is a copy of this letter, which is found in the collection of letters of the aforementioned Rebbe. As is apparent from its content, although it is also printed in the name of the Tzemach Tzedek (in the book Tzeror HaChaim, p. 30 – Bilgoraj, 5673).

Regarding the will of the Rih [Rabbi Yehuda HeChasid] concerning whether one should be careful about a place where a mitzvah was performed: see Sefer Eretz Tzemachim, Ayin 5, and the sources cited there.

With blessings for success and regards to all Anash, may they live.

## 1,924

B"H, 1 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of the Talmud Torah of Kfar Chabad, may they live:

Peace and blessing!

I have been approached with a request regarding the child... who wishes to be accepted into the Talmud Torah. As I have been informed, he is eager for this, even though it appears he is not yet five years old. However, since he is only short a few months, if the doctor agrees to this from the perspective of the aforementioned child’s health, these few months are not an impediment (see also the Laws of Talmud Torah by our Alter Rebbe, Chapter 1, the entry beginning "In the fifth year, etc." Although he concludes there **"in his home,"** it is a well-known principle that the custom from then until now has changed in this regard. For at that time, the custom was to take a child to a *melamed* when he was six or seven full years old, which is not the case in recent generations. See also the book *Sichas Kayitz 5700*, page 60 and onwards; although it is obvious that this is not a general instruction, as the Tzemach Tzedek was about three years old). Perhaps you have specific reasons [for your hesitation], and it would be kind of you to inform me.

With blessings for success in your holy work.

## 1925

B"H, 8 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn.

To my mechutan, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, etc., R' Ze'ev Dov, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I trust that you have already returned home in peace and found your family, may they live, in good health. As I requested, you have also conveyed my warm Chassidic regards to Anash, may they live, and as is the custom of Chassidim, you did so in the spirit of a heartfelt farbrengen. Thank you.

Enclosed is a kuntres containing the maamar for Parshas Vayeira, as I promised. It is my hope that it reaches you even before the Chag HaGeulah, the upcoming 19th of Kislev. Consequently, you will be among those who merit the many, by enabling them to benefit from the light that is hidden within the "light" of this kuntres. This is one of the functions of Toras HaChassidus: to reveal even that light which was created on the first day—which is brought in the name of the Baal Shem Tov as having been hidden within the Torah (see also Zohar Vol. I, 264a; Zohar Vol. III, 179a; Tikkunei Zohar, Tikkun 6; Zohar Chadash, Rus 85a). [The goal is] to reveal this light in a manner that will also affect the body and the nefesh habahamish, so as to serve Him, may He be blessed, with all your heart—with both your inclinations.

With regards to all of Anash, may they live, and with blessings for success,

Your mechutan.

Just now received your letter from Rosh Chodesh.

## 1827

8 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned man, involved in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Peretz, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter of 27 Cheshvan and the previous one with pleasure. I was happy to read about the various study programs that have been established and the farbrengens held at appropriate times. It is surely unnecessary to point out that it is self-understood that there is no issue here of encroaching on others' territory or causing a decline in their spirit; there is enough avodah for each of us to do without touching our fellow’s livelihood in spirituality, etc.

Regarding what you wrote in parentheses concerning the matter of mashke: as it seems this is a continuation of what I discussed with the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned man, involved in communal needs, etc., Rabbi B.Z. Shemtov, shaliach, it appears that he did not convey the reasoning as well. In my opinion, the situation has changed since the time when the custom of drinking mashke in abundance was prevalent, due to two factors:

a) The kochos have already been granted to anash, through the many maamarim that are accessible and the sichos on matters of explanation and understanding, to influence the listeners without them needing mashke in abundance; even a small amount is sufficient.

b) Since in recent times, and especially now, we are required with extra emphasis to engage in the dissemination of the wellsprings **outward**, the matter of abundance in mashke is liable to interfere with this significantly—something that was not as relevant when the dissemination was contained within the four cubits of the Chassidim and anash alone.

I found support for point (a) in something I once heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in Riga. He said, "I am now" (and the intent of the word **now** was not only for that specific hour, but for those years since he began to reduce his intake of mashke) "as if after a little bit of mashke." Although the external reason at that time was that the doctors had ordered him to reduce his intake of mashke, this is, of course, a reason on the external plane. Consequently, it is accepted only by those on the outside, not within the inner circle of anash who know Chassidus from an internal perspective. Surely, this is also an instruction regarding the matter in general. According to the known principle that the body follows the head, the Chassidim are drawn after our Nasi, my father-in-law, the Rebbe. The fact that he said he is now "as if after a little bit of mashke" is an instruction for all Chassidim and a granting of the ability to also be in such a state.

During my conversation with the aforementioned Rabbi B.Z., I told him explicitly that this is not, G-d forbid, a matter of prohibition or a command, etc. (regarding the consumption of mashke), nor is it a total prevention. Rather, it is simply what I perceive to be the difference between the effect of a farbrengen with a small amount of mashke and the effect if one increases it to the point of going beyond one's vessels.

With blessings for success in communal matters, which will also serve as a channel and vessel for the drawing down and receiving of blessing and success in your personal affairs.

P.S. Regarding your request to send a document that would serve as a basis for a travel permit to come here, I have passed this on to the administration of Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch, and they will surely send it in the coming days.

Enclosed is the Kuntres that was published; may you surely merit to share it with the many.

***

**Rabbi Peretz:** Motzkin, Montreal. Additional letters to him: above, Vol. 3, 1757. Below, 2:22.

## 1828

B"H, 9 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the avreich, Yisrael Aryeh, may he live.

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter from the beginning of the month of Kislev, in which you write regarding your efforts together with the avreich Meir Tzvi, may he live, concerning the rescue of boys and girls from those who incite and lead them astray, G-d forbid, and you are in doubt as to whether to continue in this, since until now you have achieved almost nothing, and furthermore, it interferes with your seder halimudim.

It is not clear from your letter whether the commencement of this work was with the agreement of the administration or whether you did this on your own initiative, as you write only that the administration now agrees that you should go during the day and on Erev Shabbos, and that they will agree to more time only upon a letter from me.

On one hand, the magnitude of the matter of saving even one Jewish soul is beyond measure. Furthermore, regarding what you write—that until now you have achieved nothing—aside from the fact that it is impossible to know if you have not achieved anything (for "there is none among us who knows how long," and "man looks at the eyes" and does not know what is happening in the heart of his fellow), it is also possible that the efforts made until now are the plowing and sowing or planting (as is explained in Chassidus in many places regarding the difference between sowing and planting) for the fruits that will be seen in the future, which cannot exist without prior plowing, sowing, and planting.

But on the other hand, the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe (the Rebbe Rashab), of blessed memory, is well known: that sometimes the yetzer hara comes disguised in a silk kapote, especially among students who are engaged in the study of the inner dimensions of the Torah, whom it tries to deceive by dressing in various guises. This is similar, in a small way, to what is explained regarding the matter of 19 Kislev, which had to be brought about specifically by those who possessed a "reflection of a reflection."

Consequently, in your case, you must consult with the administration of the yeshiva, which knows the local conditions and is also familiar with your talents. They will surely decide according to the truth. Inform me of their decision in this matter, and may Hashem grant that it be successful.

With blessings to you and to your friend, Meir Tzvi, may they live.

P.S. The pidyon nefesh enclosed in your letter has been received.

***

1828

Yisrael Aryeh: Drovskin, Lod.
Meir Tzvi: Gruzman.

## 1829

1829

B"H, 9 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter of 27 Cheshvan, in which you inform me and lament that, for the time being, you have not been granted an exit permit to travel here. You should look at the beginning of *Hemshech Mayim Rabim 5636*. My perspective on this is surely known to you, and I believe I have even written to you about this specifically: the students of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod have a vast field in which to be active in Eretz Yisrael—may it be rebuilt and established—and thereby illuminate their portion of the world, which in turn will draw down success in their personal affairs as well—namely, in the study of *Toras HaNigleh* and *Toras HaChassidus*, and likewise in success in the *avodah* of Hashem. Despite this, you asked and asked again, and you also asked indirectly, in a manner not according to the usual way. I answered you regarding this: "Why not?" If you wish, try, and I agree to it. But if, after that, you were shown once again that there is *avodah* for you (in the sense of "tanned hides," as explained in many places in *Chassidus*, such as *Torah Or*, beginning of *Parshas Mishpatim*, etc.)—meaning that this is your task, where you are needed, and where you must toil, rather than your intellect demanding it because there is a *geshmak* for the body and the *nefesh habahamit*—then, even after this instruction, you are complaining again and seeking advice and schemes to travel specifically now, at a time **when he wants to**.

...Regarding your birthday that you mention... You are certainly aware of the order of a birthday: in general, an *aliyah* to the Torah, and specifically since your birthday falls on Shabbos, repeating a *maamar* of *Chassidus* in public, reciting the book of *Tehillim*, and giving *tzedakah* before *davening*—if it falls on a weekday, or on the day before if it falls on Shabbos or *Yom Tov*. You have surely also seen what is brought in *Hayom Yom*—11 Nissan—regarding *hisbodedus*, which is copied from the letters of my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

May Hashem grant you the merit to fulfill your *shlichus* in this world for long, good years, and may you be a *Chassid*, a *yirei shamayim*, and a *lamdan*. The intention of the word *lamdan* is not only in *Toras HaChassidus*, but also in *Toras HaNigleh*, and with the addition of the long *nun*, it is in the manner of our Sages' teaching regarding *ravtzan*—one who is accustomed to it, and not merely by chance (*Bava Metzia* 33a). This is in the manner of what is brought in *Chassidus* regarding *Gershon* and *tidbakun* with the addition of the long *nun* (*Likutei Torah, Naso* 21a; see 20b)—to draw these matters down into actual practice below.

With blessings.

#### ***1829***

## 1,930

1,930

B"H, 9 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote concerning your personal situation and your thoughts about settling in one of the countries abroad: surely you are aware of my perspective on this, based on what I have seen among Anash—people of stature and professional standing—who relocated to the United States, Canada, or South America. The relocation led to a blurring of their character, Heaven forbid. Given the prospects you describe in other places, I am very concerned that there is no guarantee that this relocation will yield better results. It is understood that this is not a matter of a final decision, but merely a perspective based on experience, etc.

It is a great pity that since your thoughts (and apparently your desire as well) are wandering to all countries other than your current location, then, according to the saying of the Baal Shem Tov that "where a person's desire is, there he is," this at the very least causes a detachment of the appropriate focus from the matters of your current place. Consequently, this leads to a lack of benefit for those matters and for your health. I fear this applies to your wife, *tichyeh*, as well, for it is impossible that such a scattering of the soul (*pizur hanefesh*) would not affect your health and the health of those close to you. I do not wish to elaborate on this, so that you do not interpret my words as a matter of rebuke, Heaven forbid; I am merely attempting to rectify the matter if it is possible.

With blessings for success and proper health for you and your wife, *shichyu*, and that you may share good news soon.

P.S. Enclosed is the *kuntres* that was just published, and surely you will merit the public with it.

## 1831

B"H, 9 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote about your own spiritual state, etc., and consequently your claim as to how you are capable of influencing others: the blunt answer is what my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, answered [to a similar claim]: "Why do you demand of me? Demand of yourself." However, I hope that in this case, this is an unnecessary harshness. When you divert your attention from your own desires and personal matters and occupy yourself more with how to influence those you are responsible for—with pleasantness, closeness, and love—to instill in them the spirit of Chassidus and its flavor, then, as the saying goes, you will have no one to make a claim against. For on one hand, your own state will improve, and on the other hand, it will not concern you as much, because you will be preoccupied with the state of others. The two are interdependent.

With blessings for success in communal matters and in your personal affairs.

## 1832

1832

B"H, 9 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you inform me that you are beginning to build a home for yourself, may it be the will of Hashem that it be with success in both the physical and spiritual realms, for you and for your family—may they live—in every detail.

As is explained in the teachings of Chassidus in several places regarding the three matters of food, clothing, and a home—that these correspond to the concept of Torah and mitzvos, which come by way of a *makif d'makif* (an encompassing light that transcends the encompassing) — see *Torah Or* at the beginning of the discourse on the concept of "What is the house that you will build for Me," and similarly in *Likutei Torah* for *Gimmel Parshiyos* there, in *Likutei Torah* at the end of *Parshas Bracha*, in the *Hemshech* of *Mayim Rabim-5636* at its conclusion, and in many other places—it is therefore understood that for the construction of a physical home, it is highly necessary to increase one's strength in the matter of a spiritual home. This means through the study of *pnimiyus haTorah* and in matters pertaining to the *avodah* of *tefillah*. These two are interdependent, or more accurately, one should unite the physical and the spiritual—truly as one—as is known regarding the interpretation of why Yisrael is called **"one nation on earth"** (see *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Epistle 9).

Regarding your question concerning your son... *shichyeh*, his thought to wait with external studies until he has a full grasp of *Gemara, Poskim, and Tosafos* is correct.

With blessings.

## 1833

1833

B”H, 9 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 27 Cheshvan, in which you inform me of your study schedule at Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim and ask for my opinion regarding your difficulty in studying two tractates simultaneously—specifically, which one you should continue with:

Since you have merited to be in the Yeshiva, and the virtue of studying Torah in public is well-known in many places in the Midrashic teachings of our Sages—and this is also one of the forty-eight ways through which Torah is acquired (see also Iggeres HaKodesh by the Alter Rebbe, Epistle 23)—you should study the tractate that is part of the Yeshiva’s curriculum.

Regarding whether to study a large amount for the sake of fluency (*girsa*) and to be proficient in them, or to study a small amount with deep analysis (*iyun*):

Generally, this depends on the proficiency and knowledge you have acquired until now, as well as your personal talents (see Gemara at the end of Berachos, end of Horayos, and the Yerushalmi there; and in the Chassidic discourse *Amar Rava Chayav Inish* of 5708, beginning of Chapter 12, and the footnote there—printed in Kuntres 54). Therefore, you should consult with the Yeshiva administration on-site, and they will instruct you in detail. In a general sense, it is already well-known that everyone must have a study session for *girsa* and a study session for *iyun*, both in the revealed aspects of Torah and in the teachings of Chassidus.

I trust you are keeping the three daily study portions that are incumbent upon every soul, as established by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe—namely, the well-known portions of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya. It is appropriate that you give a few coins to tzedakah each weekday before davening—without a vow—until the tenth of Shevat, upcoming.

With blessings for success in Torah study with yiras shamayim.

## 1834

B"H, 9 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the entire congregation of Yeshurun, lovers and supporters of Torah and mitzvos, may Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

This year marks the thirteenth year of the existence in the United States of America of the "Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim-Lubavitch," whose work and development here began through the hands and by the command of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, immediately upon his settling in America in the year 5700.

Thank G-d, and through the merit of our holy Rebbes, of blessed memory, the sowing and planting of this field and vineyard have borne fruit with extraordinary Divine success. Today, many hundreds of students—may they multiply—from these yeshivos serve with distinction as Rabbis, heads of yeshivos, shochtim, and in other holy positions in important communities in Israel. Furthermore, even those students and alumni of Tomchei Temimim who earn their livelihood in other ways remain at their post in the holy service, working—each according to his standing and situation—in the field of disseminating Torah and yiras shamayim, and taking a leading role in the efforts to strengthen Yiddishkeit in all the places where they reside.

Along with the flourishing and expansion of the institution, the expenses involved in its maintenance in all its branches have also grown. Recently, the debts have increased and reached a critical point, to the extent that they threaten the existence of the institution and greatly burden its administration and development.

Substantial help is needed as soon as possible.

On Sunday, Parshas Bo, 2 Shevat, the upcoming annual celebration of the "Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim-Lubavitch" will take place, G-d willing. The administration looks toward this event to provide a significant and defined income in order to lighten, at least to a certain degree, the burden of the debts and to provide the possibility to continue the work of the institution in the future, with the help of Hashem.

I hereby turn to all lovers and cherishers of Torah and mitzvos with a request and a call to assist and help in every possible way with the preparations for the annual celebration, to come and participate in this celebration, to contribute a holy donation with a generous heart and an open hand, and to influence their friends and acquaintances in this direction as well.

We are already assured by our Sages that the merit of supporting those who study the Torah of life—the words of the living G-d, the source of life—is great, protecting all who act and do, and that they will be blessed with all the best, with children, life, and abundant sustenance.

With a blessing that your heart's desires be fulfilled for the good, and that we may all merit to see the raising of the horn of Torah and the horn of Israel, and a near, true, and complete redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

## 1835

B"H, 10 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the distinguished Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned R' Dovid Meir, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter from Erev Rosh Chodesh Kislev in due time. Regarding your question concerning the *Hemshech* of Rosh Hashanah 5703, which is currently being printed, where several levels of *ratzon* (will) are distinguished on high—you found it difficult to reconcile this with the established principle found in many places that He is simple with the ultimate simplicity, etc.

The matter is explained in many places. The crux of the question is how, after acknowledging that He is simple with the ultimate simplicity, the emergence of multiplicity in the world is possible. The various approaches and resolutions to this are brought in the *maamar* of the Tzemach Tzedek known as *Shalosh Shitos* (printed at the end of *Sefer Derech Mitzvotecha*, Part II). Since I do not know if you have access to it, I am transcribing here the names of some of the books cited there: *Sefer HaChayis*, Chapter 3; *Pardes*, Gate 4, Chapter 4; *Avodas HaKodesh*, Part I, Chapter 2. See also *Likutei Torah* for the three *parshiyos*, 35, end of side a, and in many places throughout *Chassidus*. In each case, the levels explained regarding the aspect of *ratzon* in the aforementioned *Hemshech* are based on what is explained in *Shaar HaYichud* by the Mitteler Rebbe and in many other of his *maamarim*.

Enclosed is the *kuntres* that has just been published, in which you will surely find much content, for it is from the "light of the Torah."

With blessing and regards to his children, may they live.

## 1851

1851

B"H, 10 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter—which was received with some delay—in which you write regarding the state of your daughter’s health... may she live.

You must be strong in your trust in Hashem, for without any doubt, Hashem will help and everything will be as it should. Since we are now in the month of Kislev—*der chassidisher chodosh* (the Chassidic month)—during the days of Chanukah, when the flask of oil that was sealed with the seal of the Kohen Gadol—*der Rebbe fun yenem dor* (the Rebbe of that generation)—prevailed, and years later, the Alter Rebbe and with him all the Chassidim and their descendants until the coming of Moshiach and even thereafter prevailed, it follows that this is a redemption in the physical sense as well, literally, to draw down health for each person in the manner that they require. It is understood that you must listen to the doctor’s instructions and act according to his guidance, but you must completely reject any sense of melancholy. Then you will see with physical eyes that there is reason to be satisfied and joyful.

Enclosed is the *kuntres* that was just published, and surely you will share its merit with the many.

With blessings for the *Chag HaGeulah* of the Mitteler Rebbe, and with blessings for the *Geulah* of the Alter Rebbe which is approaching in the coming days, and with regards to all *anash*—may they live.

Awaiting good news, and [for you] to begin serving Hashem with joy.

## 1838

1838

B"H, 15 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Anash and all who love and cherish Torah and the light within Torah,
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

In anticipation of the Chag HaGeulah, the redemption of our souls and our liberation, I hereby propose that farbrengens be held on Shabbos Chai Kislev, the days of 19-20 Kislev, and the days of Chanukah—whether on all of these days, or on some of them, and at the very least on two of them. These farbrengens should include: farbrengens in many locations within the camp, and a farbrengen with a large crowd—a majority in both quantity and quality—in one central location.

The program should include: studying the maamar (from Shabbos Parshas Chayei Sarah 5703) titled "Ko Amar Hashem... Karov Yeshuati Lavoh" (in its entirety, or at least a portion of it), and a segment from the sicha of Simchas Torah 5730 regarding the concept that "spreading your wellsprings outward" is a vessel for the light of the revelation of Moshiach, speedily in our days, amen.

Explain to those gathered the ruling of our Sages in the Mishnah, that it is not the study that is primary, but the deed that is primary; for "Thus says Hashem: Observe justice and do righteousness," and as explained in the aforementioned maamar regarding the nature of this "observing" and "doing."

And at this time of favor, let us adopt resolutions concerning actual, practical action, both immediately and for the days ahead, for ourselves and for all of Israel, for good.

With the blessing of the Chag HaGeulah, and in the language of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory: A gut yom tov. May you be inscribed and sealed for a good year in the study of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidim.

## 1829

By the Grace of Hashem, 16 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Anash in Kfar Chabad,
And at their head, the signatories, the G-d-fearing men who are involved in communal affairs:
R. Chaim Meir Gerlik,
R. Yosef Nachman Furman,
And R. Moshe Zalman Kamenetsky.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 22 Mar-Cheshvan, in which you inform me once again of the situation in the Kfar, and specifically regarding agricultural matters in connection with the question of relocating to a new village—a matter in which there is an opinion that a portion of the villagers should remain in their current place for now, while those who desire agriculture, who according to your letter number about thirty families, should relocate to the new village...

1) Surely it is superfluous to offer apologies for what you inform me of and write regarding the above. It is understood that it is my desire and wish to know, in as much detail as possible, about all matters concerning Anash, may they live, and especially regarding the question of relocation, which in my opinion is a fundamental issue both materially and spiritually.

3) Regarding the substance of the question, which is the main point: in my opinion, whenever one transitions from one state to another that is entirely different, one must adopt greater safeguards and extra caution.

As I have observed through many signs, the transfer of Anash from the living conditions in our former country to the living conditions in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established, to the United States, and the like, has caused a crisis. It is my strong hope that the signs of this crisis will continue to diminish, and not, G-d forbid, the opposite. When I say "crisis," I mean it both materially and spiritually. This is not surprising, for it is understood that a change of routine and a change of order from one extreme to the other is a very strong shock, which urgently requires the adoption of strengthening measures, or at the very least, not to weaken one's standing.

4) In some respects, the conditions for those Anash who moved to Eretz Yisrael are more favorable regarding this crisis, because they are all together in one place. Consequently, they have the ability—if only unity prevails in their environment—to gradually accustom themselves to the changes, and there is no necessity for an immediate, total reversal from one extreme to the other.

5) Although in our former country, Anash were forced to be together because of external necessity—namely, the persecutions and pressure on those who fear Hashem in general, and on Chassidim and Anash in particular—once beyond the borders of our former country, and especially in Eretz Yisrael, there is no such external pressure. On the contrary, there is a "pulling force" that draws everyone in different directions, and often to different places and for different goals. Consequently, it is easy to foresee that after a short time, the contradictions between one "pulling force" and another will begin to manifest.

6) It is almost certain in my eyes that the moment Anash begin to divide into camps—even if the beginning is only two camps—it will be the start of many more divisions. Ultimately, G-d forbid, their minority in quantity will lead to their being nullified, and consequently, there is a fear of their nullification in quality as well. This is especially true in Eretz Yisrael, where the nullification in quantity and quality in spiritual matters, and the nullification in quantity and quality in material matters, are dependent upon and linked to one another—especially regarding the youth, the sons and daughters, may they live.

7) The conclusion from all the above, in my opinion: if a portion of Anash moves to the new village, even if there were a temporary material gain, it would immediately bring about a spiritual loss. Over time, the material gain would continue to diminish, while the spiritual loss, on the contrary, would grow.

8) There is room to say that the material gain in relocating to the new village is merely imagined at present, due to the deficiencies in their current location which create a desire to relocate. This desire biases the intellect. When they arrive on site and begin the whole process anew, and they sober up, they will see that they miscalculated entirely, and that it was not worthwhile even materially—perhaps even from the start. If they were to invest the effort and energy required for the relocation and reorganization in the new place into improving the situation in their current place, they would certainly gain much more than they would in the new place.

9) Even if the material and spiritual gain of those relocating to the new place were certain, one must also consider the weakening that the relocation would cause to those remaining in the Kfar (even though there are those who suggest that it is actually good for them, as there will be more space), and also to the affairs of Chabad in Eretz Yisrael in general.

10) The conclusion from the above, regarding practical action: in my opinion, for their benefit materially—and certainly spiritually—they should throw themselves with full warmth and Chassidishe vitality into improving the situation in their current place. They should throw themselves into this with complete detachment from the idea that this is only a matter of a few weeks or months, and that then they will lobby the Agency, myself, and everyone else to relocate to another place—which apparently confuses their minds regarding their current place entirely. When they approach this direction with the aforementioned premise, they will surely demand with appropriate force at the relevant offices that they be granted the land plots in the Chevrath HaMehadrin area as soon as possible.

It is most surprising that according to your letter, the discussion is about 500 dunams, when at the very least you should have demanded 1,000 dunams.

11) It seems to me that if it were clear to the Agency that there are no differences of opinion among Anash on this, and that there are none who would agree under any circumstances to remain in their current place, they would have given them the aforementioned land long ago.

12) It is superfluous to note that it is my hope and confidence—and in my opinion, it cannot be otherwise—that the primary occupation of the Kfar will also be agriculture. And not as a secondary matter, but as a primary one. If there are families who, for various reasons, are not suited for agriculture, there are surely enough families—and according to your letter, at least half the village wants and is suited for agriculture—and they must grasp every means to settle specifically in agriculture, and other matters should only be as a branch.

13) It is superfluous to explain that I do not at all reject the idea and aspiration to establish more Chabad settlement points in Eretz Yisrael. With the appropriate energy, in my opinion, this may not be in the distant future. However, one must build in a new place without destroying the current one, for then, G-d forbid, neither will survive.

... May the Almighty grant each of us to bring each other tidings of only good, materially and spiritually.

With the blessing of the Festival of Redemption, and that the promise of the Rebbe HaZaken—in the verdict of the Heavenly Court that in every matter of Torah, fear of Heaven, and good character traits, the hand of those who are bound to him and follow in his footsteps will be on top—be fulfilled speedily in our days.

With the blessing of the Festival of Redemption.

P.S. Enclosed is the *Kuntres* of the *Hemshech* of *Maamarim* 5703, which contains the *Maamar* titled *Kerovah Yeshuati Lavoh*, which I suggested that Anash study during the days of the 19th and 20th of Kislev and the fifth candle of Chanukah, may it come upon us for good.

It is superfluous to note that this letter of mine, and my letters in general, are not a matter of command at all, as that is not my concern. Rather, I am writing the situation as it appears clear in my eyes.

## 1840

1840

By the grace of Hashem, 16 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, engaged in communal affairs,
Rabbi Efraim Eliezer, may he live, HaKohen

Shalom u’vracha!

I received with pleasure your letter containing the story regarding the Maggid, Rabbi Yisrael of Kozhnitz, of blessed memory, and the importance of such precious matters. Especially the stories of the Tzaddikim, the leaders of Chassidus. Just as they emphasized the virtue of stories about Tzaddikim—that one finds within them the *neshamah* and the *neshamah d’neshamah* of the Torah—so too, the attribute of the Ribono shel Olam is *midah k’neged midah*. Those who occupy themselves with these stories merit that it is fulfilled in them as well: that their own stories, even if on the face of it they are but a garment for the body, are able to illuminate [within them] the *neshamah d’neshamah*. As is known, according to the Zohar, this includes both *chayah* and *yechidah* (see Zohar Vol. III, 152a).

Regarding your question: Since on Rosh Hashanah there is an ascent of the *pnimiyus* (inner) vitality (the ascent of the *oros*, *Sefer HaMaamarim 5703*, p. 38—see *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Epistle 14), and on Shabbos there is an ascent of the *chitzoniyus* (external) vitality—the ascent of the *keilim* (see *Kuntrus Acharon* to *Tanya*, 157b)—how is this vitality drawn down when Rosh Hashanah falls on Shabbos?

Seemingly, a similar difficulty exists regarding every Shabbos: since the *chitzoniyus* of the vitality ascends, why is no change noticeable in the world? The answer to this is understood from the discussion between the Tzemach Tzedek and his grandfather, the Alter Rebbe. The Tzemach Tzedek writes that the ascent on Shabbos occurs within the *pnimiyus* of the power within the food, and therefore it is not noticeable from the outside to the eye of the observer (*Sefer HaMitzvos* of the Tzemach Tzedek, *Mitzvas Lo Teva’aru Esh*, at the end). From this, it is understood that the ascent of the *chitzoniyus* on Shabbos is actually the *pnimiyus* that is within the *chitzoniyus*, which is not perceptible to the human eye as any change. That is to say, the physical receives vitality from a place where there is no change at all. Consequently, the same applies when Rosh Hashanah falls on Shabbos.

Furthermore, it is known that there are many levels within *pnimiyus* and many levels within *chitzoniyus* (*Etz Chaim*, Shaar 1, Branch 2; *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Epistle 29), and "this corresponds to that, and this *klipah* corresponds to that." There are general matters and specific matters. Through this, one can also understand that on Yomim Tovim which fall on a specific day of the week, there is the order of the day connected to the days of the week—as we say, "Today is the first day, the second day of the week," where every single day performs its specific function. Together with this, there are also the matters connected to the days of the Yom Tov, which are general matters pertaining to the entire year. In addition to this, there are also matters dependent on the days of the month, as is known from the meaning of the name **Rosh Chodesh**: that on this day, a general vitality is drawn down for the entire month, which is subsequently drawn down to each and every day according to its nature. See *Sefer Nahar Shalom*, printed at the end of *Etz Chaim* (Warsaw, 5651 edition), page 39c, *d.h. Yadua Mah Shekatav HaRav* and *d.h. Hinei B’chol Yom*. See also the sources marked there in the *Hagahos U’Biurim*; what is stated there is also a foundation for the above.

Enclosed is the *Kuntrus* that was published not long ago by the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory, through which you will surely bring merit to the many. Especially since what is stated therein is based on the virtue of the eating of the Kohanim, which is higher than the eating of the Altar, for it draws down a new light that is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus*.

With the blessing of *Chag HaGeulah*.

## 1851

1851

B"H, 16 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter and your *pan* (which I will read at an auspicious time at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory),

It is surprising that you are causing such a stir over matters that are not particularly relevant, and in any case, are not your concern at all. When I wrote to you and informed you of my opinion regarding your conduct, it seems that because you did not see a complete, radical change the very next day, you are already writing again, clamoring insistently about why things have not changed immediately, and that it is a pity on you, etc.

The path of holiness is well known, as it is written in the Torah: "Little by little I will drive them out from before you." How does this apply to a *yeshiva bochur* who, after sending a letter, demands to see miracles in practice and wants to be able to go to sleep already, because it has been two or three days that he has been practicing *mesiras nefesh* and studying the *shiurim*, etc.? The *Shechinah* has been in *galus* for more than 1,800 years, waiting for the *birur hanitzotzos* to be accomplished through him, and She has patience—yet you do not want to wait, you are pushy and impatient, and you want to be shown immediately on a silver platter that you have already done your part! I do not know how many pages of *Gemara* you have studied during this time, or how many *maamarim* of *Chassidus* you have studied since you wrote to me, but you know the tally yourself. When you contemplate that tally, you will surely not be surprised that you have not yet seen *Elokus* tangibly with your own physical eyes, and you will not make such a scene in your letters. As a *yeshiva* student, you should study *nigleh* and *Chassidus* and keep the *yeshiva* schedule, and not storm about how it is a pity on you, that one must answer you, and that it is a matter of life and death for you. Then you will see that you are on the right path—only it happens slowly, not with the haste that the *Yetzer Hara* demands, showing you that you are already worthy of it.

May *Hashem* help you to engage in Torah and *yiras shamayim*, while diverting your attention from matters that should not be of concern to a young man who is occupied and sitting in the "tent of Torah." May you gain strength in keeping your *shiurim* and in maintaining your physical health, in accordance with the doctor's instructions. For this—the body—is one of the possessions of the *Ribono shel Olam* (as noted in the beginning of the *Rambam’s* laws of *Rotzeach*), which is given as a deposit to a Jewish person. Consequently, it is incumbent upon the one who holds the deposit to guard it so that it remains whole and healthy, even in a simple, physical sense.

With blessings for success in Torah and *yiras shamayim*.

#### ***1851***

For the content, see also letter 1856 below.

## 1942

1942

B"H, 16 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, occupied with communal needs, etc.,
R' Dovid Nosson, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive the candles in connection with the upcoming days of Chanukah. May it be the will of Hashem that, in accordance with what is explained in Chassidus (see Zohar Vol. III, 166b; Likutei Torah, Maamar beginning "Vehayah Lachem Letzitzis" [the second one]), that the word *ner* (candle) has the numerical value of the 248 positive mitzvos and the *yirah* (fear/awe) within a person, may Hashem grant that he be able to influence his own 248 [limbs/mitzvos] as well. That is to say, that the performance of the mitzvos should be founded upon *yirah*, for then it is a true performance, as written in Tanya, Chapter 4.

In anticipation of the upcoming Chag HaGeulah, I have enclosed the continuation of the *maamarim* of 5703, specifically the *maamar* beginning "Ko Amar Hashem... Karovah Yeshuati Lavoh" (My salvation is near to come). I have suggested to Anash, may they live, that they study it during the days of Yud-Tes and Chof Kislev and the fifth candle of the upcoming Chanukah, each in their own environment. The main thing is to bring it into actual practice, in accordance with the ruling of our Sages that it is not the study that is the main thing, but the deed. That is, to influence them to fulfill what is stated in the aforementioned *maamar*, and then we are promised by Hashem that "My salvation is near to come and My righteousness to be revealed."

With blessings for the Chag HaGeulah.

## 1843

1843

## 1844

1844

B"H, 16 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and refined, involved in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Nissan שיחי'

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letters in due time, as well as the *pidyon nefesh* delivered by the esteemed Torah scholar and Chossid, the *avreich* Rabbi Shalom שיחי' Haskind. I was distressed to read that you suspect my lack of response was due to some extraneous reasons; that is not my intention at all. The reason is solely the abundance of preoccupations, and that during these days I have been occupied—in addition to the usual burdens—with the publication of the enclosed *kuntres*, as well as the *maamarim* of the year 5703. Regarding the *maamar* from *Parshas Chayei Sarah*, "Thus says Hashem... My salvation is near to come," I have suggested to *anash* שיחיו that they study it during the days of 19-20 Kislev, as well as on the fifth night of the upcoming Chanukah. And according to the ruling of our Sages, "The study is not the main thing, but the deed"—to bring the matters discussed therein into actual practice, especially since our subject matter is the teachings of Chassidus, which demands a "therefore" [i.e., a practical application].

You will surely make an effort to organize *farbrengens* on Shabbos and the following Sunday, 19 Kislev, and especially on the fifth night of Chanukah, and to some extent on the days in between. As I have suggested in the past, at times it should be in terms of "quantity"—meaning in several locations—and at times in terms of "quality"—meaning that all *anash* belonging to those areas should gather in one place, and also include those who fall into the category of "those outside." These days are auspicious for spreading the wellsprings there, in accordance with the desire and will of our *Nesi'im* that "your wellsprings be spread outward."

With blessings for the *Chag HaGeulah*—for him, for all the students, and for all *anash* שיחיו, their households, their sons, and their daughters, to each one individually.

With blessings.

## 1945

B"H, 16 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter from the end of Cheshvan, in which you write about the Tefillin club; the greatness of this matter cannot be measured. The fact that it seems to you like a small thing is a tactic of the *yetzer*, and as is well known, the statement of our Sages, "Whoever sustains one soul of Israel, it is as if he sustained an entire world." It seems to me that I have already written to you before to contemplate what is written in *Tanya*, Chapter 25: "And this unification is above [time], or eternal forever and ever, for He, may He be blessed, and His will, are above time; and likewise, the revelation of His will in His speech, which is the Torah, is eternal, as it is written, 'And one word of His stands forever,' and 'His words are living and enduring,' etc." — and I hope that this will give you the strength and vitality to see to it that you accomplish everything you can...

With blessings for *Chag HaGeulah*.

## 1846

1846

B"H, 20 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 17 Kislev with the enclosed *pidyon nefesh*, when I am at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will read it there.

Regarding what you write in your letter, expressing distress over the matter of receiving an answer to several of your concerns: I have already written at length regarding such matters to a friend of yours. It would be appropriate for him to convey to you at least the essence of my letter. The point is that *avodah* in holiness is achieved slowly, gradually, and through *yegiah* (exertion). Consequently, one should not demand of the *Ribono shel Olam* that a miracle occur for them, such that suddenly and unexpectedly, without the appropriate *yegiah*, they will be transformed from one extreme to the other. On the other hand, they are guaranteed by the ruling of our holy Torah: "You have labored and found." This is especially true since the *Ribono shel Olam* has privileged them to study the teachings of *Da"ch*—the teachings of Chassidus. Even if it is not with the appropriate diligence and dedication, still, even a little light pushes away much darkness. There is no need to make a commotion; one must maintain physical health, for as the Rambam rules, keeping the body healthy is one of the ways of Hashem. One should draw closer to His *avodah* slowly and gradually, and not be discouraged by the fact that the *hisorerus* (inspiration) is only momentary and then passes. For this, there is a simple remedy: diligence in the study of Torah in general, and diligence in the study of the teachings of Chassidus in particular, which is what leads to the love and fear of Him. It is self-understood that all of this must be done without disrupting the order of the *yeshiva* in which they are located; rather, they should arrange this after consultation with their *mashpia*.

With blessings for the study of Torah with *yiras shamayim*.

**I have already written:** See letter 1841.
