## 1848

21 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Agudas N'shei U’Bnos Chabad, may Hashem grant them life.

Greetings and blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received in due time the good news that the foundation for the organized work of N’shei U’Bnos Chabad in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) was laid at the gathering held on the third day of Chol HaMoed Sukkos. Surely, you have already begun to move toward practical action in the field of work, according to the outlines and the plan I noted in my previous letter.

May Hashem grant that this be a good beginning for productive and practical work. I look forward to hearing good news regarding this.

Since the laying of the foundation for your practical work took place at the **beginning** of the year, the year 5713, and everything is by Divine Providence, one should draw a lesson from the beginning of your work and the beginning of our holy Torah.

For our holy Torah is eternal, and from it a Jew should draw guidance and lessons for action in his conduct in all matters, at all times, and in all places where he may be.

The Torah begins with Parshas Bereishis, in which the order of the creation of the world is recounted. It is self-understood that the Torah does not come merely to tell stories; rather, its purpose—as the meaning of the word "Torah" implies—is **instruction (hora'ah)**, that is, to serve as a guide in daily life, to show the path that is good for us in both material and spiritual matters.

In the order of the work of creation, as recounted in the Torah, among all the hints and secrets of Torah, there is also a practical lesson for the implementation of various matters in the private world of each and every person, and especially in general matters:

In every endeavor or movement that is about to be put into action, whether in spiritual or material matters, the **beginning**—the starting point and the essential element—is to know that **"Elokim created"** the heavens (spirituality) and the earth (materiality). This means that Hashem is the Creator, Maker, and Fashioner of all spiritual and material things. However, Hashem desires that these matters be brought into reality through a specific person, and the one who has merited this must view himself as an emissary of the Almighty to bring His will from potential into action.

At the beginning of creation—**"and the earth was tohu and bohu and darkness..."**—at the beginning of every work and effort in a matter of holiness, it seems as though *tohu*, *bohu*, and darkness prevail all around, with many obstacles and hindrances to carrying out the matter in a way that fits the goal. Therefore, the Torah immediately hints that the beginning of creation is: **"And Elokim said, 'Let there be light'"**—Hashem transforms the place of darkness into light, and the light pushes away the darkness. And then the order of creation proceeds: **vegetation**, and above it **living creatures**, and afterward man, the choicest of creations and the purpose of creation.

And so it is in every endeavor and movement in holiness (see Vayikra Rabbah 25:3): there must be an absolute will to act, and then, even in a place where darkness truly prevails, in one moment it becomes light. This is the beginning of an action that will grow and ascend higher and higher, as our Sages of blessed memory said, "We ascend in matters of holiness," meaning that in every matter of Torah and mitzvos, one goes from strength to strength.

With blessings for material and spiritual good for all the participants and their families.

Enclosed is a check for seventy [currency units] for the expenses of Agudas N'shei U’Bnos Chabad; please acknowledge receipt. Also [...] Agudas N'shei U’Bnos Chabad.

**Establishing** schools at this time is premature.

## 1849

1849

B"H, 22 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal needs,
Rabbi Ephraim Eliezer HaKohen, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

Following up on my previous letter and what I said to you personally regarding the story of the Maggid, Rabbi Yisrael of Kozhnitz, of blessed memory—where it is recounted that he asked for the name of the angel appointed over pregnancy, and it was found in an old book of Kabbalah—

The version of the story as cited requires further study (*tzarich iyun gadol*). It is explicitly stated in the Gemara (Niddah 16b) and in the Zohar (Vol. I, 91b) that his name is Lailah, based on the verse also cited in the story: "And Lailah said, 'A man-child is conceived'" (*Iyov 3:3*). It now appears to me that the aforementioned version [in the story] came about as a slip of the tongue, and it should instead refer to the name that is *segulah* for, or associated with, pregnancy. This is the name *Tachah* (תכ"ה), which is the eighth of the well-known names derived from the three verses of *Vayisa, Vayavo, Vayet* (*Beshalach 14:19-21*). It is also alluded to in several verses, as brought in the books of Kabbalah and collected in *Kehillat Yaakov* (under the entries for *Keter* and *Tachah*). According to this version, even if the response of the son of the author of *Ketzot HaChoshen*—who said it relates to the verse "And Lailah said, 'A man-child is conceived'"—still requires study, it is at least understandable what the Maggid of Kozhnitz, of blessed memory, meant: that it is a *notrikon* (acronym) of the verse "Behold, you are with child and shall bear a son" (*Bereishis 16:11*). As is brought in the book *Regel Yesharah*, the name *Tachah* is a *segulah* for the visitation of the barren and for pregnancy, and it is alluded to in the verse "Behold, you are with child and shall bear a son."

With blessing.

#### ***1849***

**Rabbi Ephraim Eliezer:** Yalles. Further letters to him—see above 1893, and the references in the notes there.

**His name is Lailah:** See below, letters 240, 218.

## 1951

B"H, 22 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, etc., Moreinu HaRav Moshe HaKohen, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive regards from the shluchim, the distinguished Rabbi and Chassid, G-d-fearing and occupied with communal needs in faith, etc., Moreinu HaRav Shmuel Levitin, may he live, and Moreinu HaRav Eliyahu Simpson, may he live. Especially [noteworthy is] that they parted from one another following a farbrengen of brotherly love, in which case the separation is only in location and, consequently, is not real. This is as explained in several letters of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the power of thought—that location, and even time, do not create a separation. Furthermore, it is within the power of thought to transport, elevate, and raise a person to a place and time where he has never been physically. This is based on the Baal Shem Tov’s resolution to the difficulty regarding the verse, "Seraphim stood above Him" (*Yeshayahu 6:2*): How is it possible for the angels to stand above the Master, who sits upon a high and exalted throne, given that the world of angels is below the world of the Throne, as explained in many places—in books of Kabbalah and Chassidus, as well as in works of philosophy? The Baal Shem Tov explained that wherever one’s desire is, there one truly is (and the Seraphim, their very name is derived from the fact that they are "burned" [serufim] by their love and yearning to be included and to ascend even higher than the world of the Throne).

It is my hope that they will also hold a farbrengen on one (and perhaps even more than one) of the days of the upcoming Chanukah, and may it be His will that it be successful...

## 1852

*[Month of Redemption]*

...Regarding your precise observation in your last letter—based on the Rambam, Hilchos Avodah Zarah 6:8, that "because this was the way of the idolaters to plant trees, etc.," implying that regarding an *asherah* there is no issue of actual *avodah zarah*—this does not seem correct to me. In this *halachah*, the discussion is not about an *asherah*, but about a tree in general (it is just that he did not want to skip or shorten the text for the sake of a single word, and therefore he also copied the word *asherah*. Furthermore, planting it is prohibited **in any case**). However, see the Mishnah (*Avodah Zarah* 48a) regarding the dispute between Rabbi Shimon and the *Tanna Kamma*. See also *Moreh Nevuchim*, Part 3, Chapters 29 and 32.

2) Regarding your suggestion that an *asherah* is like a *matzevah* (monument), which only **afterwards** became hated by Hashem, whereas in the days of the Patriarchs it was not—it is difficult to understand where you derive this from. It is a major *chiddush* even regarding a *matzevah*, that a defender should turn into a prosecutor because of fools (see *Avodah Zarah* 54b). And one does not derive a rule from a *chiddush*. Especially since we do not find anywhere that the Patriarchs planted trees for the sake of Hashem. Based on this—that an *asherah* was always hated—it is understood and clarified why our Sages (*Sotah* 10a) struggled to interpret the verse "And he planted an *eshel*... and he called there..." in a way other than its literal meaning.

And this requires study in *Zohar Chadash* 49a.

3) What should be noted in the Rambam there is what he writes: "Even though he made it for beauty, etc." (a) From where does this distinction arise? (*Or Sameach* points to the *Mechilta*: "I will make a beautiful sanctuary before Him." Perhaps that is his intention to resolve this difficulty. But it is forced.) (b) If there is a logical basis for a distinction, from where do we know that there is no practical difference, and that even if he made it for beauty, he is liable?

It may be said that the distinction is that if he made it for beauty, it is secondary to the purpose of being adorned by it, similar to the beauty of a *sukkah* (*Sukkah* 10a). Nevertheless, the ruling is that he is liable, because the entire way of the idolaters in this matter was such that the tree was secondary and subordinate to their altar, so that the people would gather there.

Based on the above, another detail in the Rambam there is understood:

4) The words "so that... the people" are seemingly superfluous. For what practical difference does it make? And based on the above, it is understood that from this we learn that even for beauty and aesthetics it is forbidden. And I will not elaborate further.

5) The concept that a *matzevah* was beloved and after the Giving of the Torah became hated, according to *Chassidus*, is explained in *Or HaTorah* by the Tzemach Tzedek, beginning of *Parshas Vayeitzei* (198a).

#### ***1852***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 14, p. 292. In the secretariat copy—23 Kislev.

The letter is to Rabbi Alter Hilvitz, may he live. Additional letters to him—above, Vol. 3, 453, and where noted in the footnotes there.

**Rabbi Yosef:** Blumenfeld.

**Regarding what was discussed at the farbrengen:** 19 Kislev (*Sichos Kodesh*, p. 104), whether the time is a single point or a collection, etc., and regarding a *nazir*, the periods are separate from one another. If so, it is from the month of Kislev (see below in the footnote to letter 2092) and if so, what is "a kosher and happy holiday"? This requires further study.

**Regarding the time:** See also above, Vol. 4, letter 773.

**His proof from *Kerisus*:** That the days in between constitute knowledge to divide [the periods].

## 1953

B"H, Month of Redemption, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, learned, and pious, etc., etc., our teacher Rabbi Yosef, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

Your letter—following up on what was discussed at the farbrengen—was received. As I wrote, my intention regarding the matter of "days that interrupt" mentioned by our Sages in Nazir (7a), and in anticipation of the days of the festival approaching us and all of Israel for good, I hereby express my blessing for a kosher and joyous festival.

And for the fulfillment of the hoped-for promise: "As in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt, I will show you wonders," with our true and complete redemption, in his days and in our days, through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With respect and festival blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

Regarding the nature of time—whether it is a single point, a collection of points, a completion of the initial point, etc.—see Tzafnas Paneach by the Rogatchover, second edition (26a, 9a) for brilliant insights and remarkable comparisons.

Regarding your desire to divide the time of Shabbos, your proof from Kerisos (16a) requires further study, as there the time of exemption that occurs in the middle creates a division. However, one should note the Tosefos Yom Tov in Yoma (81a, bottom) and the Responsa Tzafnas Paneach by the aforementioned author, Vol. 2, 332.

I will not elaborate further here. See also Torah Or, Toldos (18d), that a day is long even at its **beginning**.

## 1,950

B"H, 23 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 14 Kislev, in which you write that there is a rationale to schedule the wedding of your daughter, may she live, in the second half of the month of Teves:

In my opinion, one should endeavor to schedule the wedding in the month of Adar or Nissan, and if in the month of Shevat, then in its first half. In the month of Adar, the entire month is a month of joy, as explained in the verse.

You do not write in your letter the reason for specifically the second half of the month of Teves; perhaps it is due to the matter of *chupas niddah*, etc. However, the ruling of our Nesi'im, our holy Rebbes, is well known, and I also heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the name of the Tzemach Tzedek, that they were not particular regarding *chupas niddah*. Regardless of how you decide, may it be the will of Hashem that it be in a good and auspicious hour.

With blessings, and awaiting good tidings.

## 1,957

B”H, 23 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...In connection with the upcoming days of Chanukah, may they be for a blessing for us and for all of Yisrael, I wish to emphasize just one of the allusions contained in the Chanukah candles, which is as follows:

The mitzvah of candles for Yisrael consists of the candles of the Beis Hamikdash, the candles of Shabbos, and the candles of Chanukah. The difference between the candles of Chanukah and the other candles is that the candles of the Beis Hamikdash and the candles of Shabbos must be lit while the sun is still shining, and they remain the same in number each time. This is not the case with the candles of Chanukah, which must be lit specifically after the sun has set, and from day to day one must add more light—another candle. And one is dependent upon the other: when there is light outside as well, one can be satisfied with continuing in the light of Torah and mitzvos in the usual manner, and in most cases, this suffices—and the Torah speaks of the majority. However, when the sun—for "Hashem Elokim is a sun and a shield" (Tehillim 84:12)—is not shining openly in the environment, then one cannot be satisfied with serving Hashem today just as one did yesterday, or tomorrow just as one did today. For in such a case, not only will the darkness not be broken, but there is also a danger that the darkness will penetrate even into a place that until now had been illuminated. Therefore, it is necessary to add more light each day, in accordance with the dictum of our Sages, "We increase in matters of holiness." The analogy is quite clear and requires no further explanation.

May Hashem grant each of us success in illuminating our portion—within our soul, our body, and the world—with abundance.

With blessings and regards to all the chaverim, may they live, and to their households and their offspring, may they live.

#### ***1,957***

Sent to several recipients. Regarding its content, see also below, letters 1,961 and 1,968-9.

## 1858

26 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn

To Anash in the city of Dublin, may Hashem protect them,

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 20 Kislev, in which you write about the celebration of the day of the announcement, the Chag HaGeulah of 19 Kislev, with the participation of several people, the completion of Maseches Sotah, a seudah, etc. I am certain that you also made positive resolutions regarding the *hafatzas hamaayanos* (spreading the wellsprings of Chassidus outward), both among Anash and in reaching out to those outside. It is a known ruling of the Heavenly Beis Din, which my father-in-law, the Rebbe, conveyed in one of his letters (printed in *Kitzurim VeHe'aros LeTanya*, p. 122), that in every matter of Torah, yiras shamayim, and good character traits, the hand of those who are connected to [our Rebbeim] and follow in their footsteps will be uppermost.

2) I was very pleased with what you wrote regarding the Nshei U’Bnos Chabad organization, which has already begun holding farbrengens, study sessions, etc. Enclosed is a copy of what I wrote to some of the other branches, which also contains points regarding the study and farbrengen activities. It is understood that there is no need to be overly particular about the membership of the organization, provided they are from the circles of Anash and are willing to participate and draw closer to Chabad; this is sufficient, etc., and the wise will understand.

It is understood that for the benefit of the matter, it is worthwhile that the members themselves participate by being the ones who study and present the material, as this will draw them deeper into the heart of the matter. It goes without saying that this does not preclude having one of the men teach them if they find it appropriate, etc.

3) In accordance with the aforementioned classes and the beauty of this avodah, it has already been discussed at farbrengens that, based on what is explained in Chassidic discourse—and specifically in *Likutei Torah*—the "unpleasant" matters written in Parshas Bechukosai and Parshas Savo are, in truth, blessings. The same applies to the *Baraisa* at the end of Maseches Sotah. Regarding the matters mentioned there—that in the footsteps of Moshiach "impudence will increase," "the young will shame the old," "a daughter will rise against her mother," etc.—in the context of avodas Hashem, this means that a person, without regard for his own standing or status, and even regarding simple matters of *midos* and *avodah*, possesses the breadth (*di breitkeit*) to become a *mashpia*, an awakener, and a guide in his surroundings. This applies not only to *dinim* (halachic rulings), but also to the paths of Chassidus and their conduct; and not only regarding the study of the *nigleh* (revealed) Torah, but also regarding the study of the *nistar* (hidden) Torah and the secrets of secrets—which are also included and explained in the teachings of Chassidus. Furthermore, even those who have acquired this wisdom—the Torah—but have not yet merited the "light" within this Torah (which is the teachings of Chassidus), and he himself is still "young," etc.—[in this sense] "the young will shame the old." Moreover, even within his own home, if for some reason there was leniency in certain matters due to the conditions of life in the past, "a daughter will rise against her mother and a daughter-in-law against her mother-in-law," and they conduct themselves as is proper even in these matters, without considering the conduct of their mothers and mothers-in-law until now. Ultimately, the mothers and mothers-in-law will also conduct themselves like them, and the wise will understand. May the Ribono shel Olam merit us, in the near future, to see with our physical eyes how He will turn the curse into a blessing, for Hashem your G-d loves you.

With blessings for a happy Chanukah,

P.S. Enclosed is an excerpt from my letter in English, which I am sure you will use in an appropriate manner.

## 1859

B"H, 26 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, involved in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Shneur Zalman, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

...I was pleased by what you wrote in your letter, that in this journey of the Shluchim, the spirituality of the matter was palpable. And although the physicality involved in this is not the physicality of "the way of the world," nevertheless, it does not compare to the spirituality and the **feelings** of the *baalei batim* who participate in a *farbrengen*. I emphasize "feelings," because if one were to contemplate it, there is room to argue the opposite: for when a participant in a *farbrengen* also participates in the physical aspect of the matter—as explained in *Tanya*, Chapter 32—he can thereby acquire the life of his soul. And over time, having surely invested all his strengths in it, he is participating with his entire being. This is in contrast to the spirituality, which he receives either through his intellect or through the emotion of the heart, which is only a part, and not the essence of the soul. But it is understood that all this is from the perspective of the truth of the matter, and it is not so for those who are *farbrenging*...

A copy of the message for the days of Chanukah has been sent via the secretariat, which I am sure you will use in the appropriate manner.

With blessing.

***1859***

## 1860

B”H, 26 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., R’ Daniel, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter in due time, in which you request some guidance regarding your conduct in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, in your camp, where everyone is simple folk, refugees from various places.

I have already stated for some time that since we are in the *ikvesa d’meshicha* (the footsteps of Moshiach), it is incumbent upon everyone to strive in the *avodah* of preparation for the coming of Moshiach, in accordance with the Baal Shem Tov’s teaching that this will be when "your wellsprings spread outward." This *avodah* is now incumbent upon each and every one of those who have merited the light of the teachings of Chassidus. Since, according to your letter, everyone in your camp is simple folk, you have a vast field for this *avodah*.

It is well known—and has also been explained in the *sichos* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe—that in earlier times, and within the revealed Torah, the order was that the *mashpi’im* would wait for the recipient to come and receive. The Baal Shem Tov, however, instituted—as did many of his students and their students after him—that the *mashpia* should go to the recipient. This is also the case regarding Chassidim: they must roam the streets and draw the souls and hearts of the sons and daughters of Yisrael closer to their Father in Heaven through the conduct of Chassidim, the ways of Chassidus, and the teachings of Chassidus.

Since this is required of us, we have certainly been given the *kochos* (strength) for it, for the Holy One, blessed be He, does not deal tyrannically with His creatures, and "according to the camel is the burden." We must thank Hashem for our good portion, that we have merited to be in such generations where the teachings of Chassidus have been revealed in letters and concepts understandable to all, so that each and every one of us has been made a *mashpia* who will merit to draw the hearts of Yisrael closer to our Father in Heaven. The magnitude of this matter is beyond measure and estimation, and to elaborate on it is superfluous.

I am certain that you participated in the *farbrengens* of the month of Kislev, and I am interested to know the details regarding this.

With blessings for long life and good years, and as per the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe: "good" with all the interpretations.

## 1861

B.H., 27 Kislev, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the Anash gathered at the farbrengen of the day of redemption, the redemption and salvation of our soul, 19 Kislev, at the Nusach Ari Beis Medrash on Pine Ave. in Montreal, may they live:

Peace and blessing!

It was with pleasure that I received the news regarding your farbrengen on the luminous day of 19 Kislev.

According to the statement of our Sages, "When ten sit together [to study Torah], the Shechinah rests among them." Rabbeinu HaZaken explains this matter (in his Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 23) that when ten Jewish people gather, this in itself brings about the resting of the Shechinah. And especially when this gathering is for the purpose of celebrating the liberation of the Nasi of Israel, Rabbeinu HaZaken, the Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch, who sacrificed himself for Ahavas Yisrael, Ahavas HaTorah, and Ahavas Hashem, and one undertakes good resolutions regarding these aforementioned matters—at that time, the resting of the Shechinah is with even greater intensity and strength.

Consequently, there is also a special success in the good resolutions that one undertakes, such that one will certainly continue throughout the entire year according to the resolutions accepted at that time, and even with an addition to them.

This is also the hint in the manner of the mitzvah of the Chanukah candles: that one must "ascend in holiness" from day to day, especially in the darkness of the time of Galus.

This is, after all, one of the differences between the Chanukah candles and the candles of the Beis HaMikdash. In the Beis HaMikdash, the number of lights was always the same, whereas with the Chanukah candles, it is "increasing and growing." This can be explained by the fact that the Chanukah lights are kindled *mishetishka hachamah*—after sunset—while the candles in the Beis HaMikdash were kindled a long time before sunset.

And this is a lesson for us: when the environment is not bright, one cannot be satisfied with the same measure of good deeds today as yesterday, or tomorrow as today. Rather, one must strive every day to add to the previous day, *ma'alin bakodesh*—ascending in holiness. With the proper energy and effort, one realizes this, and it proceeds with success.

With blessings for material and spiritual good for each and every one of those gathered—them, their households, and their offspring, may they live.

With blessings that you should share good news very soon.

With blessings for all that is good.

#### ***1867***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 14, p. 575, and completed according to the secretariat’s copy.

*) This is how it appears in all editions of the Rambam that I have seen, and the *halacha* requires further study. Seemingly, it is clear that there is an omission here by the early printers (and subsequent publishers followed them without paying attention to this, especially since few study the *Hilchos De'os*). It should read: "It is one of the ways of the **avodah** of Hashem." This follows what is written there at the end of the previous chapter: "He should set his heart to keep his body whole and strong so that..." and "He finds himself walking in this path all his days, **serving** Hashem constantly..." and "that his body be whole **to serve** Hashem..." Regarding this, he writes at the beginning of chapter 4: "Since (as explained above) the body being healthy and whole is one of the ways of the *avodah* of Hashem..." Alternatively, it should read: "It is one of the ways of the **knowledge** of Hashem"—based on how he concludes and brings proof: "For... that he may understand or know something of the knowledge of the Creator." I have not found any of the commentators on the *Yad* who address this.

## 1868

1868

B"H, the fifth night of Chanukah, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, renowned for his name, praise, and glory,
Of the lineage of *tarshishim*,
The scion of holy ancestors, our teacher and master, Rabbi Menachem Binyamin Ben Zion, shlita.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to hear from the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing and pious man, who engages in communal needs, etc., Rabbi Shmuel Zalmanov, that the health of the Rebbe, shlita, has improved. May Hashem grant that his state of health continue to go from strength to strength.

As is well known, the ruling of our Sages is that "we increase in matters of holiness" (*ma'alin bakodesh*). (According to many authorities, this is a Torah-level obligation. See the sources cited in *Sdei Chemed*, *Kelalim*, letter *Mem*, *Klal* 194; *Me'asef Lechol Hamachanos*, *Orach Chaim*, section 26, subsection 12; and in *Shulchan Aruch* of our Rebbe, *Orach Chaim*, end of section 34, he writes that it is a Rabbinic enactment. However, the text for that entire paragraph is enclosed in parentheses. It is known that in several places this is because there was still some doubt regarding this, and this is not the place to elaborate.) Since a healthy and complete body is "among the ways of Hashem" (*Rambam, Hilchos De'os*, 4:4), and furthermore, the body is the property of the *Ribono shel Olam* (see *Rambam, Hilchos Rotzeach*, beginning; *Radbaz* to *Rambam, Hilchos Sanhedrin*, end of chapter 18; *Shulchan Aruch* of our Rebbe, *Hilchos Nizkei Guf*, section 4; and one should examine the language of our Rebbe in his *Shulchan Aruch*, *Orach Chaim*, second edition, end of section 4).

We have already spoken at a *farbrengen* regarding the concept of *ma'alin bakodesh* in the context of the Chanukah lights. Although they were instituted and came about as a result of the miracle that occurred with the lights in the *Beis Hamikdash*, they differ from one another in several details. One of these is that the lights of the *Beis Hamikdash* were always a fixed number, whereas the Chanukah lights increase and grow.

One may suggest a reason for this, *derech efshar*: The mitzvah of the lights in the *Beis Hamikdash* came from above to below, and not through a battle against the darkness and the impurity of the oils **within the *Heichal*.** On the contrary, it was a testimony **to all who enter the world, etc.**, and that Israel is beloved (*Rashi, Shabbos* 22b). However, the Chanukah lights came about because they were preceded by the darkness of the wicked Kingdom of Greece, as well as by the lawless ones among the Jewish people (*Daniel* 11; see there in *Rashi*, *Metzudos*, and others, as written at length in *Yosippon*, cited in *Rashi* there). Therefore, there is an advantage in the Chanukah lights over the lights of the *Beis Hamikdash*, in that one adds to them and they increase (they are also eight lights and not seven, similar to the distinction between the *kinor* of the future and that of the *Beis Hamikdash*—*Arachin* 13b; explained in *Likutei Torah, Tazria* 21d; see also *Shu"t HaRashba*, Vol. 1, 69—and they endure forever—*Ramban*, beginning of *Parshas Beha'aloscha*). This is like the advantage of light that comes from darkness over light that comes without it (*Tanya*, chapters 26, 27, 36; and see *Zohar*, Vol. III, 47b).

It may be suggested that, similarly, there is an advantage in the aforementioned *avodah* of Hashem through the body and within the body—when it is healthy and complete—over the *avodah* of Hashem through the *neshamah* alone (see *Tanya*, ibid., and *Iggeres HaKodesh*, end of section 8).

With respect and blessings.

## 1869

By the Grace of Hashem
Fifth Night of Chanukah, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the women and girls of Chabad, may Hashem grant them life,

Peace and Blessing!

In connection with Chanukah, the sefer *Beis Rebbe* (in Yiddish)—which has just been released from print—is being sent to you as a Chanukah memento.

I hope that you will make much use of this sefer at your gatherings, in order to become more closely acquainted with the life and work of our Rebbes, the "Founding Fathers of Chabad," may the merit of their holy souls protect us. By drawing from their living fountains, you will be better able to fulfill your duties as women and daughters of Chabad: to spread the light of Torah and mitzvos in the spirit of the teachings of Chabad, not only within your own homes, but in your entire surroundings.

Just as everything occurs through *Hashgacha Pratis*, the fact that *Beis Rebbe* was released from print during the month of the redemption of Chabad, and specifically during the days of Chanukah, contains a lesson for us.

The difference between the Chanukah lights and the Shabbos lights—both of which women are obligated to light—is, among other things, that the Chanukah lights are kindled **after** sunset, when it is already night, whereas the Shabbos lights are kindled **before** sunset, while it is still day. Furthermore, on Erev Shabbos, one kindles the same number of lights as always, whereas the Chanukah lights increase in number each night.

This is an indication that one cannot be satisfied with illuminating one’s own home with the light of Torah and mitzvos and the *Maor ShebaTorah*—the inner light of Torah, which is the teachings of Chassidus. One must also illuminate the "street," which is alluded to by the Chanukah lights (whose place is "at the entrance of his house, from the outside"). Moreover, at a time when it is dark on the street, it is not enough to simply kindle a light; one must be *mosif v'holech*—constantly adding new light, increasing one's efforts, and expanding the work more and more, in accordance with the path of Chabad Chassidus, which is based on the foundations of *ahavas Hashem*, *ahavas haTorah*, and *ahavas Yisrael*.

I hope that your work will also be like the Chanukah lights—*mosif v'holech*—and through this, you will draw down Divine light upon yourselves and your households, may they be blessed with children, life, and sustenance.

With blessing.

## 1870

B.H., Erev Rosh Chodesh Teves, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, the G-d-fearing, who is involved in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Nissan [Nemnov] may he live.

Peace and blessing!

Although I have already acknowledged the receipt of your letters in general, I wish to specify once again that the letters you inquired about were indeed received in due time. They are: 22 Elul, along with the lists; 30 Tishrei; 9 Mar-Cheshvan; Rosh Chodesh Kislev; and 3 and 13 Kislev, along with the items enclosed with them. The lists and the *pidyon nefesh* were read at the appropriate time at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zya*. Surely the telegram regarding the distribution of *Chanukah gelt* as in previous years has arrived.

2) I derived pleasure from your detailed letter regarding the students, their standing in their studies and in *yiras shamayim*, as well as the matter of memorizing *Tanya* and reviewing *maamarim* of *Chassidus*. It is unnecessary to elaborate on the necessity for the students to review *Chassidus* in public, and specifically in such *maamarim* that the listeners can grasp with their own intellect. Beyond all other considerations, this is also a way to increase the number of listeners, for "a friend has a friend." Perhaps it would be worthwhile for the older students among them to also relate some episode from the lives of our *Nesi'im*, etc., so that the listener can later recount it at home to his sons and daughters. This is along the lines of what my father-in-law, the Rebbe, wrote regarding the benefit of *sichos*, etc.

3) Regarding what you write about the study of *Yoreh Deah* in the Yeshiva: as it seems from your letter, this is included as a mandatory course for all those entering the advanced class, and they study—in the words of your letter—primarily *Yoreh Deah*, with only two hours for *Gemara, Poskim, and Tosfos*.

Now, if all of them are being prepared to become Rabbis and already possess a foundational knowledge of *Gemara, Poskim, and Tosfos*, perhaps this order is correct. However, if one of these two conditions is lacking, it might be worthwhile to increase the number of hours for *Gemara, Poskim, and Tosfos*. Even within *Shas* itself, they can choose those tractates that have a greater connection to *halacha l'maaseh*, although it is understood that knowledge of the tractates studied in other yeshivos is also necessary.

8) Regarding the list of those who know *Tanya* by heart: you write about some who knew it and have forgotten. Surely you can find the appropriate words to stir them to seek ways to restore their learning. Although "the old is harder than the new," this matter is explained in many places regarding the gravity of the matter—that one who forgets even one thing, etc.—even if the *Mishnah* in that specific context is not speaking about them. For them, it is certainly along the lines of what is explained in *Hilchos Talmud Torah* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, Chapter 2, Section 7 and onwards.

9) Regarding the list of those who review *Chassidus*: it would be worthwhile, at least from now on, to also note the *maamar* or the part of the *maamar* that they reviewed. As mentioned above, in my opinion, these should be *maamarim* that are understandable to the listeners.

11) Regarding the order of examinations that you write about in your letter: it might be worthwhile that at least once or twice a year, you arrange examinations with the participation of those from the outside—that is, not from the *Roshei Yeshiva*—whether from the city’s Rabbis or from the refugee Rabbis, etc. (And, of course, this must be *durchgehalten politisch* [politically handled with care], and therefore you should consult on this with the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, the G-d-fearing, involved in communal needs, etc., Rabbi B.A. Gradetzky, may he live). The benefit in this is for the publicity of the Yeshiva, and surely also for the collection of funds, publicity in other countries, etc.

13) Regarding your question about the study of *Chassidus* for the class *far zich* [on their own]: it is difficult to say anything definitive from a distance. It is up to the local administration to decide, in accordance with the capabilities of the majority of the students in the class, after assessing how the division of subjects between *Nigleh* and *Chassidus* will affect them in this way or that. May it be the will of Hashem that they decide for success.

14) Regarding your question about the review of *Tanya* by heart: you do not write the reason for the decline in this area. If it is due to laziness—because that is easier—then it is obvious that one must fight against it, as is known regarding the detriment of laziness in general, and specifically laziness in the study of *Chassidus*. If the reason is that they are taking time away from review for their regular studies, whether in *Chassidus* or in *Nigleh*, then surely not everyone is the same in this regard; there are those for whom this is the only reason, and perhaps there are those for whom a weakening in *yiras shamayim* is also a factor. Depending on the cause, one should speak to each individual according to his nature.

15) Regarding your question about the study of *Shulchan Aruch Yoreh Deah*: I have already written in general above. I would add that to receive *semicha*, there must also be knowledge of at least some *sugyos* in *Shas*, in addition to the ability to read through various topics in *Shas*. Regarding the study of *Shulchan Aruch Yoreh Deah* itself, surely you are aware that due to the shortness of the students' study time compared to the time they used to study in the past, they do not dedicate as much time to the nuances of the *Pri Megadim* and the like.

19) Regarding... and also the students who came from Morocco: it is known from our Sages that a child, etc. (and consequently, also a "child" in the knowledge of Torah in general and the Torah of *Chassidus* in particular), should be "pushed away with the left hand and drawn close with the right." Especially in the aforementioned case, one should increase the "drawing close with the right" and minimize the "pushing away with the left." For their presence in the Yeshiva will pave the way for others to be added, whether in the Yeshiva itself or in other places where they will be added. In these places and times, this is also a literal rescue from the darkness that is in the world, for they bring there the light that is in the Torah—this is the *pnimiyus haTorah* [inner dimension of Torah]. As it is unified with the human intellect, the *Chabad* in the head will be filled with them, and the body follows the head. Consequently, at least for the first while, one should *nachgeben zei* [give in to them] regarding the time for studying *Nigleh* and *Chassidus*. One should stir them during a *farbrengen*—naturally in a general way and not by speaking to individuals—about the great necessity of studying *Chassidus*, the inner dimension of the Torah, which is called the "soul of the Torah," and that this also draws down vitality into the study of the *Nigleh* of the Torah, which is called the "body of the Torah." It is highly probable that the students from Morocco are in correspondence with their friends in other places, and their satisfaction will also influence their friends who are far away.

20) Regarding the students from Morocco: it is known how much they are influenced and moved by stories of *Tzaddikim*, and this is the way to influence them in other matters as well.

21) I have already written, and I will write again, that if there is a delay in my response to letters, the reason is usually just the abundance of preoccupations. *Min haTorah* [by Torah law], we follow the majority, and therefore one should not read any other meanings into it until the matter is explicitly stated by me.

1871

B.H., Erev Rosh Chodesh Teves, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter from the 20th of Kislev, Erev Rosh Chodesh Teves, before my departure to the Ohel of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and I mentioned you and your family, may they live, there for what you are in need of.

2) Regarding your question—perhaps you should settle in another place where there is a rationale for a good residence in a good environment, good work, and good parnassah, etc.—and you ask for my opinion on this:

My opinion on this—and I ask you to convey this to Anash, may they live, of Kfar Chabad, as this should serve as an answer to some of them who have approached me with such a question—is the following:

According to your letter—and everyone knows this as well—all of your journeys to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, took place during the lifetime of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in this world. You had letters from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the manner of your settlement, and as he wrote to you many times, that you should hold together and build up Kfar Chabad, etc., etc.

It is known what is stated in Chassidus in many places, that in general, the matter of parnassah now is similar to the way the manna was in the desert; that is to say, it is in a miraculous manner. For according to logic, "a person's sustenance is as difficult [to provide] as the splitting of the Red Sea," etc., and in these times in particular, it is only in a miraculous manner. It is only because of the *helem* (concealment) of the *galus* that this—parnassah—is given in such a way that there is room for error, etc. This is the case even in *chutz la'aretz*, and especially in Eretz Yisrael, which is still, for the time being, in its state of destruction, may it be rebuilt and established; it is understandable that there, the matter of physical parnassah is even more difficult. Therefore, one must hold on to all those things that make it easier, and not do, G-d forbid, any things that would make the matter even more difficult.

One of the primary ways to receive blessings is the matter of *achdus* (unity), as stated in Tanya, Chapter 32, and explained in many places in *Divrei Elokus Chassidim*, and also in *sefarim* of *mussar*, and it is understandable to human reason. Another aspect of this is that one must hold on to the *tzinor* (conduit) that the *Nasi* of the generation, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, has pointed out; for when one tries with one's own conduits, sometimes one hits the mark, and sometimes, G-d forbid, not. A third aspect of this is that in order for the *hashpa'ah* (divine influence) to flow through these conduits in its fullness, one must adhere to the instructions and ways of the one who pointed out these conduits, and who is the *memutza hamchaber* (the intermediary who connects) the source of all *hashpa'os* to the recipients.

The conclusion from all of the above is that the matter of the opposite of *achdus* and the separation of hearts... is not only the opposite of the will of our *Nasi*, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, through whom all *hashpa'os* are drawn down, but anyone who has a part in this, G-d forbid, is in the category of one who harms himself and harms others. And the saying of my father-in-law, the Tzemach Tzedek, is known: *Aleph, Beis, Gimmel, Dalet*. *Aleph*—*Achdus* (or *Ahavah*); *Beis*—*Bracha*; *Gimmel*—*Ga'avah* (pride); *Dalet*—*Dalus* (poverty).

3) It is self-understood that the *bracha* that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, bestows is first and foremost for **the** *olim* from our Anash of our country, from Kfar Chabad, and afterwards to those who have settled in other places. Therefore, one must strive with all possibilities, if possible, to receive the *bracha* in that place, and not settle further away, which would make the path longer until it arrives and reaches there.

It is close to say that there are some of Anash, may they live, whose place of parnassah is not in Kfar Chabad, but according to the conduct of Torah, first of all, one must follow the path that appears to be the majority; only if one has already tried everything and sees that it is impossible, only then should one try other ways.

4) If in all places one must hold on to the various *takanos* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, then all the more so—those who have not yet settled completely, and especially in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, where "the eyes of Hashem your G-d are upon it from the beginning of the year to the end of the year," and one needs an even greater *zechus* there for every matter—it is certain that one must hold on to the *takanos* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and through this, merit the *brachos* and *hashpa'os* in a way of *derech hateva* (the natural way) that is *lemala min hateva* (above nature), which everyone needs for themselves and all their family members.

5) As stated earlier, you will certainly convey this to the Anash, may they live, of Kfar Chabad, and primarily emphasize the first point, the greater necessity for the *kiruv halevavos* (drawing of hearts together), as it is explained in the *maamar* "Hechaletzu" with the addition of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. This matter is even more important in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, and especially for *Chassidim* and those connected to the *Nesi'im* of Chabad.

With a blessing that the Holy One, blessed be He, will give them the correct idea of where to settle, and it should be a success both physically and spiritually.

## 1972

B"H, 1 Teves, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the G-d-fearing, esteemed individual, engaged in communal needs, R' Yosef, may he live, son of Maimon.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter dated the 5th of Kislev in due time. Since my secretary is unable to write in Spanish, I am compelled to write to you in Lashon HaKodesh, the content of which I am certain you will understand. It is as follows:

When my representative, the esteemed Rabbi, the Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and engaged in communal needs, etc., R' Binyamin Eliyahu Gorodetzky, may he live, was here not long ago, I spoke with him once again regarding the situation of the student dining hall in Madrid. It has been about ten days since Rabbi Gorodetzky returned to Paris, and he will surely do whatever is within his power there to rectify the situation. If any new details have arisen in the interim, please be so kind as to inform Rabbi Gorodetzky directly, in order to expedite the matter, and send a copy here.

I hope that during the days of Chanukah, you and your friends gathered together and spoke about the miracle of Chanukah—"in those days"—and that even now, it is **imperative** that the sons and daughters of Yisrael stand firm against all those who wish to make them forget the Torah of Hashem Yisbarach and cause them to stray from the laws of His will. Ultimately, Hashem Yisbarach succeeds and brings salvation and great deliverance to all those who walk in His ways.

With blessings for success and regards to all your friends, may they live.

## 1873

[1st of Teves, 5713]

...May Hashem fulfill the days of your wife’s pregnancy, may she live and be well, in the proper manner and with ease, and may she give birth to a healthy child in its proper time and season, in the proper manner and with ease.

## 1974

B”H, 5 Teves, 5713
Brooklyn.

To our masters and teachers, the Rabbis and Geonim who sit in judgment, each in his camp and community; to the communal activists engaged in raising the banner of Torah and Yiddishkeit in the spirit of our ancestors; and to all our brethren, the Children of Israel, lovers of Torah and mitzvos, wherever they may be, may Hashem grant them life—

Peace and abundant blessing!

With this letter, I authorize the esteemed Rabbi, the Chossid, the G-d-fearing man, who engages in communal needs with faithfulness and is a trusted member of the household, Rabbi Eliyahu Simpson, may he live, to visit the settlements of our brethren, may they live. He will convey my greetings to them and bring back their regards, inform me of the state of Yiddishkeit and the standing of the Torah and educational institutions in their respective camps, and stir them to address matters requiring improvement and strengthening in accordance with the spirit of our ancestors. He will also explain the status of our institutions in this country, in our Holy Land—may it be rebuilt and established—in Europe, and in Africa.

Relying on the verse, "I sleep, but my heart is awake," and on the words of our Sages of blessed memory that even in exile the heart of Israel is awake to every good thing—and "good" refers only to Torah, mitzvos, and good deeds—I am certain that they will assist him in fulfilling this mission in practice, as well as in matters concerning the strengthening of our institutions in the aforementioned locations.

May the Holy One, blessed be He, grant each and every one of us the merit to fulfill our role in this world by illuminating our surroundings and our portion of the world with the light and radiance of love of Hashem, love of Torah, and love of Israel.

With respect and with blessings for goodness, both material and spiritual.

## 1875

1875

B"H, 5 Teves, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of the Reshet in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt,
May they live,

Peace and Blessing!

...2) I have already written in the past that, in my opinion, you should concentrate on the work, even if it will not be as expansive, provided that what is done can serve as a model of excellence and distinction. This is especially true since you are limited in both financial resources and in teachers, both male and female, etc. It is therefore understood that one must avoid a dissipation of energy across various fields, and even avoid superficial expansion within this field itself. In accordance with the above, regarding the matter of establishing kindergartens and also establishing a dormitory, which you mention in your letters—your involvement should be limited only to investigation and inquiry into the matter, and perhaps also preparation, to a certain extent, for the activities themselves. If they are suitable for Chabad, they should be handed over to another institution that is appropriate for this. It is understood that you can also be involved in this institution, and perhaps even be members of the administration, but in any case, this does not fall under the program and activities of the Reshet...

9) If the kindergartens can be a continuation of and in complete unity with their respective Chadorim, and they have the appropriate personnel ready for their administration, as well as the necessary expenses for this, then in a place where it is necessary, one should take an interest and act upon it. However, this is only an instruction for a time of duress.

10) I was very, very pleased with what you organized—what you call in your letter **"Study Days"**—and it would be appropriate to find a suitable time and organize them again. It is understood that for the sake of the excellence of the matter, it would be worthwhile for more of anash and friends to participate, and not only as listeners, but also as lecturers and leaders...

13) Surely you utilized the days of Chanukah, and you will make appropriate preparations for the upcoming 10th of Shevat, and simply also for the upcoming Purim—to explain to the students the significance of these days, and primarily, the moral lesson regarding practical application.

14) It is surely good to introduce the study of our seforim, provided that this does not cause too much of a change or divergence in the knowledge of the Reshet students compared to the knowledge of other institutions. Regarding what you write that our seforim cannot be obtained in Eretz Yisrael, it would be worthwhile to inquire about the costs of printing them there, and also to find out if a special license is required if we wish to send them from here, and to what address and in what quantity it is permitted to send...

With blessings for success in your holy work.

Awaiting good news soon.

## 1996

...Regarding the extracurricular involvement of the students: I have already expressed my opinion several times, that **all** matters concerning the yeshiva students must be conducted by the yeshiva administration and with their consent. This is as we have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and therefore this is the case here as well. However, the administration must be considerate of the individual student’s sensibilities—not to overstretch the string—and also consider matters that, due to the situation, sometimes fall into the category of a mitzvah that cannot be performed by others, in which case one interrupts Torah study. In such instances, one must be careful and take precautions so that this does not cause a weakening in the other students to whom this ruling does not apply...

## 1977

B"H, 15 Teves, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your three letters, and most importantly, your second letter from Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Mikeitz, in which you write that you have remained at your post—the holy post in the vineyard of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—which is, without any doubt, for your benefit, both materially and spiritually, as well as for the benefit of your family, may they live. May your heart be confident in Hashem, for you will surely see this with physical eyes as well, and may Hashem grant that this happen soon. It is a well-known story of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, that a Chossid as he should be must be permeated with the idea that he is the "beast of burden" of the Holy One, blessed be He (see Tanya, end of Chapter 46 and Chapter 18 there), and consequently, he must fulfill His affairs—which is the "giving of milk" and the like—while his sustenance and all his needs are the responsibility of his Master, the Holy One, blessed be He.

With blessings for success in all your affairs, and especially in your holy work of bringing the hearts of Yidden closer to their Father in Heaven. I await good news.

## 1878

17 Teves, 5713
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Agudas Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may they live,

Greetings and blessings!

I received your telegram regarding Mr. Kol’s visit here. He visited me this past Thursday, and during our conversation, he stated simply that he would fulfill his promise regarding the construction of the agricultural school in the Kfar. For my part, I confirmed once again that I take responsibility for the fact that within five years, they will repay the Jewish Agency for half of the construction costs. In response to my question, he told me that in his opinion, it is better to consider prefabricated wooden houses imported from abroad. However, I later had the opportunity to speak with a person involved in construction in Eretz Yisrael, who told me that although it involves additional expenses, one must make every effort to ensure the building is a permanent structure made of concrete and bricks, etc., due to the intense heat and dry air, which affect the longevity of the aforementioned wooden houses. Surely you will clarify this on-site as well. Mr. Kol also told me that the construction will take about half a year, even if it is the aforementioned wooden building, and even longer if one considers a brick building, etc. I await your clarification on this.

I was approached by the Center for Taharas HaMishpacha in Jerusalem (under the administration of Rabbi Halperin), through their representative and shaliach here, Rabbi Barzel, and later also by a direct letter from Jerusalem, to assist in the construction and completion of mikvaos in Eretz Yisrael. I promised them my help, but through our representative in Eretz Yisrael—namely, Agudas Chabad. According to their letter, the most urgent matters are those noted in the margins of the letter, along with the sums required for each location. I suspect that the amount is certainly higher than what is actually needed, and this was one of the reasons I said that it is impossible to proceed unless my assistance is channeled through Agudas Chabad, and their representative visits the site to assess the situation. Of course, this is without them establishing an independent center for building mikvaos; rather, in the same place where they provide assistance, they will examine the situation and ensure that the funds provided go only toward this purpose. Although he was not happy about it, Rabbi Barzel had to agree to this, though he requested that they know it was through his efforts, and naturally, I agreed to this. It would be good for you to consider and assist in one of these locations, specifically in a place where there are, at the very least, Chabad activities in the vicinity. Furthermore, the mikvah must be constructed in accordance with the instructions of the Rebbe (Rashab), as he is our posek. As is also known in halacha, in the place of a Rav, one must conduct oneself specifically according to that Rav, even if in the place of Shmuel, etc. There is no issue of "do not create factions" here for several reasons. I am writing this so that you may look into it, as they will surely try to persuade you to do it according to other instructions. It is understood that you should not enter into a conflict, but rather explain that it is against the halacha to force someone not to act according to the words and ruling of his own Rav—especially in such matters, where both types of mikvaos are kosher according to halacha for all opinions, but some are stringent to fulfill the opinion of these poskim while waiving the opinion of others, and some do the opposite.

Regarding what you wrote, that they have already approved the five hundred dunams for the Kfar, and in the meantime, my letter was received stating that it would be worthwhile to strive for one thousand dunams—consequently, there are those who say and interpret my words as meaning that one should not accept the five hundred dunams, but rather begin efforts for one thousand and wait until then. I was alarmed that everyone wants to attribute their own twisted logic to me, as if that were my opinion. It is obvious that one must take and immediately utilize the land provided, and also begin efforts for an additional five hundred.

Since I only received the information regarding this specific line of reasoning from you, I am not writing to others about its rejection.

With blessings for success in your holy work—awaiting detailed good news at the earliest opportunity regarding all of the above,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1,979

B"H, 18 Teves, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding what you conclude in your letter, that "much is expected of him," and you entreat the Ribono shel Olam to assist you in this, as you feel you are not measuring up to what is expected of you, etc.: It is well known that our Sages ruled that one who sanctifies himself a little below is sanctified much from above. However, at the very least, there must be that "little" sanctification—to open up an opening at least the size of the eye of a needle. These powers have been given to us in abundance by our holy Nasi, may the merit of the righteous protect us, but one must keep the channel of hiskashrus with him open and widen it as much as possible. This is achieved by walking in the path he taught us: observing his takanos, studying his Torah, etc. And above all else is the matter of ahavas Yisrael; for through unity with another Yid in general, and with anash in particular, one creates a vessel that holds blessing—the blessing of the Ribono shel Olam, which is a blessing without end—and consequently, this applies to both material matters and spiritual matters.

## 1880

1880

B”H, 18 Teves, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 13 Teves, in which you inform me that your son... *sheyichyeh* will turn three years old on the upcoming 24 Shevat, and you ask whether to move the *upsherinish* to the *yom hilula* of 10 Shevat:

It is a well-known *minhag Yisrael*—which is Torah—that the *upsherinish* is not performed before the day the boy completes three years of age. Consequently, he should follow this custom, and may it be in a good and auspicious hour. A passage from a letter of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the *upsherinish* is transcribed in the margin.

Regarding what you write about your current concern for your *parnassah*: it would be appropriate to give a few coins to *tzedakah* every weekday before *davening*. The ruling of our Sages is well known: "Give a tithe so that you may become wealthy," regarding which Hashem says, "Test Me now with this." It is brought in the *Acharonim* that according to many *poskim*, the verse "Test Me now..." applies even to general *tzedakah*. See *Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah* 247 and the commentaries there; the various opinions on this are cited in *Sdei Chemed*, *Klallim*, *Ma’areches Nun*, 16.

It is surely unnecessary to remind you to strengthen your commitment to the three daily *shiurim*—the *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*—established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, which are incumbent upon every soul.

With blessings for success in *parnassah*.

#### ***1880***

**Excerpt from a letter:** See above, Vol. 5, Letter 1233, and elsewhere. Below, 2098.

## 1881

1881

By the Grace of Hashem, 18 Teves, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your prompt letter of the 1st of the month, in which you write and complain about the situation of the Yeshiva under your management and ask for my advice:

Although I have already told you several times my clear perspective regarding the Yeshiva under your administration in general, and your role within it in particular, I am writing this once more, at least in brief, so that my perspective may be clear. I will write in Yiddish, perhaps you may wish to read this letter to someone else. As a general introduction to all the points that follow, it is a known **ruling** of the Baal Shem Tov that the avodah of Hashem must be done specifically with joy. It is also a known ruling of the Rambam in *Hilchos Deios*, in the *Tur Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim* (siman 231), and in many places in *Chassidus*, that the avodah of Hashem must be "in all your ways know Him"—meaning in **all** the matters of daily life. My points of perspective are:

1) It is time to understand—and I am certain that you also understand this, and one can see it even with physical eyes—that the fact that you were given the task of the Yeshiva is not because one wants to burden you, nor because one wanted to send you to a small town, but rather that this is your fulfillment of your *shlichus* in this world. Consequently, this is the channel through which the Ribono shel Olam has given, gives, and will give blessing and success in everything you need for yourself and for your family, *shichyu*, both materially and spiritually. It is certainly unnecessary to elaborate on this, for even with a slight *hisbonenus* into the revealed miracles over the course of the last two years, both in your personal matters and in the general matters, one understands and sees this.

2) Since this is your fulfillment of *shlichus*, and you belong to the community of *Anash* and Chassidei Chabad, whose *derech avodah* is with joy, it is a certainty that if you simply do not choose to bring *marah shechorah* (melancholy) upon yourself and complicate the situation, you will certainly be able to carry out all matters with joy. This is not a contradiction to the fact that sometimes matters are achieved through *yegiah* (toil), as is known from the *maamar* of our Sages: "If you have not toiled and found, do not believe." However, *yegiah* and joy are not only not contradictory; rather, in most cases—and this is how it should be—when one achieves something through *yegiah*, there is more *taanug* and joy in it than when one receives it as a gift, which is *nehama d'kisufa* (the bread of shame).

3) It is self-evident that since the institution is growing—and like every living thing, it wants to grow even more—if in the beginning, with momentum, one person could drag and carry the entire matter, and it did not harm the institution or the person, that was **perhaps** all well and good at the start of the matter. Even regarding that, I am not certain. But especially now that the institution continues to grow, this is certainly not as it should be—neither for the development of the institution, nor, consequently, for the person who drags all the matters upon himself at once...

5) It is self-evident that **anyone** who manages a job cannot help but feel that if he were to hand it over to someone else, it would not be managed any worse than he would have done it. This is what the sin of the *Eitz HaDaas* brought about: that **every** creature feels **himself**, and it often happens that way in truth, in the beginning, until the new person accustoms himself to the work, that there are flaws, and sometimes it takes a longer time. Yet, one must not forget that it is worth losing a penny in order not to lose a dollar—even though the difference between a penny and a dollar is only in quantity—and *kal v'chomer* that it is worth losing a small thing, small both in quantity and in quality, in order not to lose a thing that is great both in quantity and in quality.

6) The conclusion from all the above: It is a must—a necessity—that you devote your entire time to public relations and maintain the general leadership, including the internal matters of the Yeshiva. But in actual practice, that which concerns the *seder halimudim*, checking capable *melamdim* and *moros*, testing the students, etc.—all of this must be handed over to someone else. From among the staff of the Yeshiva, one can find someone who will be qualified for this, at least over time. And if it is not possible to hand it all over to one person, then divide the functions: some functions to one, and some functions to another. But in any case, you should not occupy yourself with this, and it is self-evident, not to teach a class yourself.

7) I hope that my suggestion will not upset you. And in any case, even if it does, as the Rebbe, my father-in-law, told in the name of his uncle, the Rebbe Rashab, *n.e.*, that he used to say: when one gets upset, one should wait at least 61 minutes, and then one can think about the matter as it is in its truth. And do not let it seem to you—even though to a certain extent you are perhaps also right—that so-and-so will not succeed, or that so-and-so cannot manage his class, etc. For as I said above, one must yield on smaller things, relatively speaking, in order to maintain more important details to a greater degree...

With blessings for true peace of mind and for the expansion of the mind, which will consequently bring success in general and personal matters. I await good news.

## 1882

B”H, 18 Teves, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., R’ Peretz, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter in which you inform me that in the coming days, with the help of Hashem, you will complete the six orders of Mishnah (and surely you also have several chapters of Mishnah memorized by heart), I say: *Yasher koach, yasher koach* for this good and joyous news. It is well known how highly my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, praised the importance of studying Mishnah. You may also refer to the second *Kovetz Michtavim*, where the great virtue of reviewing Mishnah by heart while walking in the street, "when you walk by the way," etc., is explained. Furthermore, according to what is explained in the writings of the Arizal that the letters of *Mishnah* are the same as the letters of *neshamah*, this study will surely illuminate your mind and heart with the "candle of Hashem, the soul of man," to the point that this added light will be felt even in physical matters, and likewise regarding your son and family, may they live.

With blessings for success in the study of our holy Torah, both in *nigleh* and in *Chassidus*, and for proper health.

## 1883

1883

B"H, 21 Teves, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the G-d-fearing, esteemed, and distinguished, who engages in communal needs with faith,
Moreinu Harav Moshe, may he live, Hakohen

Greetings and blessings!

...I hope it is unnecessary to remind you that this coming Sunday, 24 Teves, is the yahrtzeit of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and the Shulchan Aruch. Consequently, this is a day auspicious for success, both in matters pertaining to the teachings of Chassidus and in matters pertaining to the revealed Torah. It is appropriate to utilize such an auspicious day to hold a farbrengen—a warm farbrengen—and to strengthen one’s resolve with good decisions regarding Ahavas Yisrael, Ahavas HaTorah, and Ahavas Hashem. This is a particular merit for Kohanim, to whom the mitzvah of blessing Yisrael was entrusted, a blessing that must be given out of Ahavas Yisrael, as per the text of the blessing: "to bless His people Yisrael with love" (Shulchan Aruch of the author of the yahrtzeit, Orach Chaim 128:19), and to draw down Ahavas Hashem upon those being blessed (Zichronos, p. 343).

With blessings for proper health for you and your wife, may they live, and for success in your general and personal affairs.
