## 1884

B”H, 21 Teves, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the illustrious Rabbi, the G-d-fearing Chossid, a scion of holy ancestors, etc.,
Rabbi Chaim Shlomo, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your inquiry regarding the passage in Likutei Torah, end of Parshas Naso, which discusses giving gifts to a chassan—seemingly, what is the connection between a chassan (which implies *nachus darga*, a descent in level) and the giving of gifts?

The matter is explained there itself (29b): In order to draw down something **new**, one requires the bestowal of power from Above. This is the concept of a gift—it is not a matter of wages or a purchase acquired through toil and effort, but rather something given to him beyond what he has earned. The toil and effort involved serve only to provide *nachas* to the soul, which in turn causes the gift to be bestowed. This is explained further in many places in Chassidus; see also Likutei Torah, Shir HaShirim, in the maamar beginning *Ki Al Kol Kavod Chuppah*, and in the maamar beginning *Tanu Rabbanan Keitzad Merakdin*.

With respect and blessing,

***

**1884**
**Rabbi... Chaim Shlomo:** Horowitz, the Rebbe of Strizov. Another letter to him appears above, 1837.

## 1885

21 Teves, 5713
Brooklyn

Mr. Moshe Kol

Greetings and blessings,

I was very pleased to have the opportunity to meet you in person and to discuss with you matters concerning an important segment of our people. I was particularly gratified to hear that you see the various branches of the Chabad movement in Eretz Yisrael as a venue for joint work and for significant assistance on your part.

The matters are as follows:

(a) The matter of the educational institution and its branches for children rescued from the missionary influence. Based on the letters I have just received, it is within our power to organize this. According to your words, if the building and the staff are suitable, the offices under your administration will undertake half of the financial expenses involved in supporting such an institution, and the other half will surely be provided by the government offices with whom you are entering into discussions regarding this.

In accordance with your suggestion, I am writing to my representatives in Eretz Yisrael to contact your deputy, Mr. Yaari. By the time they contact him, he will already have instructions from you regarding this.

(b) Regarding the students of our educational institutions in Morocco who wish to immigrate to Eretz Yisrael with our consent: if we guarantee them that they will be able to continue their education according to their wishes and the wishes of their parents, you told me that it goes without saying that there will be no coercion. They will be able to continue their education in the institutions of the stream they declare at the Aliyah office in Morocco. Furthermore, the students who immigrate will receive, in addition to the costs of Aliyah, all their needs in Eretz Yisrael until they reach the age of 17, from the funds of Youth Aliyah.

(c) Regarding the establishment of an agricultural school in Kfar Chabad: in accordance with the negotiations that have taken place, this matter will be realized with the help of your office, the Youth Aliyah office. You expressed your estimation that the time required for the construction of the building is approximately half a year if it is a prefabricated building, or a slightly longer time if it is a standard building. As mentioned, the Youth Aliyah office will provide the money required for the construction of this institution, on the condition that half of the money will be considered a loan for which I am responsible for repayment over five years.

The payment schedules and the methods and details of this will be finalized in the continuation of the negotiations that my representative, Rabbi Gorodetzky, will conduct with you or with your representative.

I will mention one more detail, which is what I said: that for my part, I am prepared to discuss additional institutions similar to the aforementioned agricultural institution, since I believe there will be a significant demand for agricultural training among us. To this, you replied that you wish to wait and see how the first building is organized, and then you will be interested in more institutions of this kind.

I will emphasize once again that I derived satisfaction not only from what was discussed regarding our own affairs, but primarily from the general attitude reflected in your words regarding what you termed "joint work" that lies before us. This inspires in me a firm hope for good results in actual practice, to your satisfaction and ours alike.

Before I conclude my letter, allow me to emphasize a general point, in continuation of what you told me regarding the city of your birth and your heritage:

Everything is by Divine Providence, and this goes without saying regarding matters that concern a wide circle of people or the community as a whole. Regarding the aforementioned—your role in the administration of Youth Aliyah—it is understood that the fact that you have been granted such ability and influence imposes upon you an extra responsibility. For the attitude of our Torah in general, and the teachings of Chassidus in particular, toward the special importance of youth is well known. Every matter, even the smallest and most minute, that occurs in the lives of boys and girls is liable to influence the course of their spirit, their character, and their temperament for all the days of their lives. As is known, the parable of the seed: even a slight scratch in the seed is revealed later as great damage to the tree, whereas that same scratch on the tree itself would leave only a small mark in its place.

However, together with the great responsibility placed upon a person who has the ability to shape, to a significant degree, the course of the lives of the youth, there is also a special merit in this: that from Above, the ability has been entrusted to him to influence hundreds and even thousands of the sons and daughters of Yisrael. According to the saying of the Baal Shem Tov that we have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, each one of them is in the category of the importance of an "only child," and their preciousness to our Father in Heaven. Together with the responsibility and the merit, a person is also given from Above the talents and strengths required to fulfill this role in our world in its entirety. Only so that it should not be "bread of shame," free choice was given as to whether to use the powers given to him in their fullness and with the upright intent, or, G-d forbid, the opposite.

I will conclude my letter with my wishes that you merit to carry out, in the best possible way, the role and the merit that have been given to you in relation to those whom it is in your power to benefit, both materially and spiritually.

We are assured in our Torah that fulfilling one's duty regarding the community brings blessing and success also in the private matters that concern oneself and all that one has.

With respect and blessing.

## 1886

1886

B”H, 22 Teves, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who occupies himself with communal needs and possesses noble character traits, a scion of noble ancestors, etc., R’ Sh. Z. [may he live and be well],

Greetings and blessings!

In addition to the telegram I sent you, I would like to thank you once again for the telegram you sent me regarding the meetings with Mr. Kol [may he live and be well].

Mr. Kol visited me, and I am enclosing a copy of my letter to him.

I would like to note that during Mr. Kol’s visit, I recognized that even before he came to me, he had already been prepared and primed with a positive attitude regarding the matters we discussed. Now, I have confirmed from the telegram you sent me that your influence upon him was for the good. I hope that the positive results that will materialize will bring you satisfaction and contentment.

Relying on the ruling of our Torah that “one mitzvah leads to another,” I am confident that in the future as well, you will extend your assistance to us in an ever-increasing measure in all areas of our movement—by speaking on our behalf. As the Sages say, “Throw a stick into the air, and it will land on its base [ikarei].” The word *ikarei* can be understood in two ways: the root, and the essence and inwardness of the stick; the two are interdependent.

It goes without saying that what I wrote at the end of my letter to Mr. Kol regarding responsibility, as well as regarding the merit and the strengths granted from Above—since they are applicable to Mr. Kol, they are all the more applicable to you, as it is within your power to influence Mr. Kol and his colleagues to utilize their strengths in the desired direction and to the fullest extent.

With regards and blessings.

## 1887

B"H, 22 Teves, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...In continuation of our conversation when you were here, and regarding what we spoke about then... the mistakes made at the time by the Mensheviks in our country back in the year 5677—mistakes which ultimately led to the seizure of power by the Bolsheviks. When the Bolshevik party did something that was considered an error in the eyes of the people (namely, their attitude toward the German government of that time), it would have seemingly been the duty of the Menshevik party, which held the reins of government, to exploit that error and capture the hearts of a significant portion of the people and of the Bolshevik party itself. Instead, they also committed an "error" which, from the perspective of the majority of the people, was no less significant than the aforementioned error: they aligned themselves with the representatives of the wealthy class (the bourgeoisie). Naturally, the Bolsheviks immediately raised a hue and cry over this "betrayal," claiming that the Mensheviks had crossed over entirely to the camp of the opposing class. Consequently, they argued, an alliance with Germany was preferable to an alliance with the class of the *baalei batim*—the hostile class—and therefore the government should be handed over to those who held to this [Bolshevik] ideology, and so on...

## 1888

B.H., 22 Teves, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the brilliant Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing, and involved in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Nissan, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter in which you write that you were told there is a tendency in Lubavitch not to use a rubber stopper (plug) — this is indeed the instruction of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe (Maharashab), of blessed memory. It is also printed at the end of his book (subsection 11). I have not explicitly heard the reason for this, other than what is written in the aforementioned instructions: because it is an object that is susceptible to tumah. This has already been cited in your own book, referencing the opinion of the Maharsham in his Responsa, Part 1, Siman 2.

Regarding what you wrote — that it was not designated for treading (midras) — it can be explained simply: Since it plugs a hole in the floor, and furthermore, it often happens that only a small part of it protrudes above the floor, the person immersing or the one plugging the hole steps on it, either accidentally or intentionally to properly seal the opening. Even if it protrudes significantly, sometimes people use it to stand on in order to reach something on the walls of the mikveh or the like. It is obvious that if one steps on it, even accidentally, it becomes part of the floor and has been designated for that purpose. Furthermore, if one steps on it to properly seal the hole, then through this sealing, it becomes part of the floor that is intended for treading, and this too is considered a designation for treading. Perhaps there is more to add here, as there are many stoppers made in the style of the stoppers made of zinc, meaning they are hung on a chain attached to a metal plate on top of the stopper, and in the plate there is a small receptacle, which is an additional reason for the aforementioned practice.

Incidentally, the aforementioned Responsa of the Maharsham is not at hand, and I have relied on what you cite in your book, *Taharas HaMayim*, page 182, which is also cited briefly in *Darchei Teshuvah*, Siman 201, subsection 273. He also discusses at length there the opinion of those who are stringent regarding valves (ventilen), contrary to those who permit them on the grounds that they were made to serve the ground of the building.

With respect and blessing.

Enclosed is a Kuntres that was just published.

## 1889

1889

By the grace of Hashem, 26 Teves, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, engaged in communal affairs, R' Menachem Man, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter, in which you write the heartening news that Anash gathered on Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Vayishlach and celebrated the Chag HaGeulah of 19 Kislev. You sang the nigun of the Alter Rebbe and also read the account of his imprisonment and liberation, etc. May the Ribono shel Olam help, in accordance with the teaching of our Sages that "joy breaks through barriers," that this joy should remove the barriers and concealments in the place where you are now. May even those people who **think** they are opponents come to the true truth—that every Yid is a Chassid. As my father-in-law, the Rebbe, used to say, Yidden are called "a spring of gardens, a well of living waters," and also "a land of desire." This can be seen tangibly: in every place one digs, one eventually reaches the spring and well of living waters. The only difference is that in one place, it is enough to remove a thin layer of sand, mud, or stones, while in another place, the layer is thicker and heavier. But the common denominator is that every place possesses it. The same is true regarding the point of Yiddishkeit—which is Ahavas Yisrael, Ahavas HaTorah, and Ahavas Hashem, all of which are one—that every Yid possesses this. The difference is only, as mentioned above, that for one person it is on the surface, while for another, more effort is required to uncover it within him.

You write in your letter that the Rav of the shul asked you why Tachanun was not recited on 19 Kislev, given that: a) in the Shulchan Aruch of our Rebbe, it does not state that one should not recite Tachanun then; and b) why should those who wish to recite Tachanun not be allowed to do so?

Regarding the first question, you yourself write the answer in your letter: the Shulchan Aruch was written by our Rebbe before the events of 19 Kislev, while he was still in Mezeritch (see the introduction of his son to the Shulchan Aruch). As for the second question—why not allow those Yidden who wish to recite Tachanun to do so—there are two reasons for this. 

a) Those who do not recite Tachanun on 19 Kislev demonstrate thereby that they agree that our Rebbe was entirely innocent, and that the Torah of Chassidus—whether one studies Chassidus himself or not—is the Torah of Hashem. Consequently, since a Yid was arrested for disseminating this Torah, his liberation is a "Torah celebration." However, for those who are opponents and insist on reciting Tachanun on 19 Kislev—whatever reason **they** may have in mind—what will people say? It implies that they do not support the Rebbe’s liberation or the Torah of Chassidus, which is a part of the Torah of Hashem that he revealed, and that they agree with the various accusations against him. The proof is that they pay no heed to his liberation and do not consider it a Yom Tov at all.

b) At a time when hundreds of thousands of G-d-fearing Yidden have, over the course of seven generations, accepted and maintained the day of 19 Kislev as a Yom Tov, and since every matter is surely by Divine Providence, it is certain that this came about with consent from Above. This means that Above, on this day, there is an additional "shining of the countenance," for in the "light of the King’s countenance is life." At such a time, the *dinim* (judgments) and *kitrugim* (prosecutions) are weaker. It is not even like Shabbos, of which it is said that "all *dinim* are removed from it," yet the day of 19 Kislev also effects a great weakening of the *middas hadin* (the attribute of judgment). (And therefore, 19 Kislev is a day of *segulah* for accepting good resolutions regarding Torah, mitzvos, and refined character traits.) However, reciting Tachanun is a matter of **arousing *dinim***, as stated in the Levush, Orach Chaim, section 131, and also in the Ateres Zekeinim there, subsection 3, and this is also brought down in the Mishnah Berurah there, subsection 20. Consequently, if someone wants to arouse *dinim* on a day when hundreds of thousands of Yidden do not do so, he causes harm not only to himself but also to the entire minyan of Yidden where he is davening. Further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

In a separate package, two copies of the book "Beis Rebbe" have been sent to you, which was recently printed in Yiddish. I ask that you give the second copy to Mr. Aaron Hakohen (Harry Katz), along with the enclosed receipt for what he sent through you.

I also ask you to convey to Mr. Aaron Hakohen Katz my greetings and wishes for all good things and for sustenance in abundance.

With blessings.

## 1990

B"H, 26 Teves, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...It is well known what Chazal have told us: that Hashem desires that a person should act on their own, at least to the extent of their ability, and then Hashem gives them much more in accordance with His power; but one must do that little bit on their own.

The expression of Chazal regarding this is that Hakadosh Baruch Hu says to the Yidden, "Open for Me an opening like the eye of a needle, and I will open for you an opening like the entrance of the Ulam"—meaning, one need only open an opening like the one made by the sharp point of a needle, and I—Hakadosh Baruch Hu—will make for you an opening like the entrance to the Ulam that was in the Beis Hamikdash.

The expressions of Chazal are very precise and measured. The purpose of the *chuda shel machat*—the sharp point of a needle—is not merely to make a small hole through which a thread can pass; rather, the intent is that the thread should join two things together to become one. So too is it with the *teudas ha'adam*—a person’s mission: to make a small opening—meaning, to set aside their own desires and cravings—so that through this opening, they can draw through the thread of Torah and Mitzvos. Through this, a Yid joins gashmius with ruchnius, and through this, Hashem grants the Yid blessing and success in their gashmius matters as well.

May Hashem help you to take upon yourself to fulfill this statement as mentioned above, and may the expression of Rabbeinu HaZaken, Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch, be fulfilled in you: that Hashem gives Yidden gashmius, and they make ruchnius out of that gashmius—and may it be with abundance.

With blessings.

With blessings for success in your holy work.

## 1892

B"H, 26 Teves, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and meticulous in his avodah, etc.,
Rabbi Nissan, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

...Regarding what you wrote about your distress concerning the practice you instituted of memorizing Tanya: The virtue of knowing Tanya by heart is well known, as mentioned in the sicha of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, from 5691 in Riga. See also the letter printed at the end of *He'aros V'Kitzurim L'Tanya*.

What was said in my name regarding this matter is only this: Since the students are limited in their study time and, consequently, lack even a superficial knowledge of many, many subjects, it is self-evident that they should dedicate the time within the yeshiva's schedule to acquiring these subjects, and thus there is not much time left for memorization. However, it is understood that there is nothing in this to cause you distress or the like, especially since you informed my father-in-law, the Rebbe, about this at the time.

It would be appropriate to speak with the students, since they are within the walls of the yeshiva all day in Paris, that they should take time for the memorization **also** from their own time—outside of the yeshiva study hours—in addition to the time they will set aside for it **within** the yeshiva schedule.

Regarding your daughter and her husband, the Rabbi, and their children—may they live—all is well. The bris took place in its proper time. May you raise your children to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds, and may you and your wife—may you live—see and derive much Chassidishe nachas from them and from all your descendants.

With blessings for success in your holy work and for proper health, for a healthy body is one of the ways of Hashem.

P.S. I spoke with the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and meticulous in his avodah, Rabbi Binyomin Eliyahu Gorodetzky, may he live, before he traveled from here, regarding his efforts to travel here, and if possible—that it should be a few days before Yud Shevat. It is surprising that he does not mention anything about this in his letter.

Enclosed is a kuntres that was published recently.

## 1993

B"H, 26 Teves, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters, from 7 Kislev, Parshas Vayigash, and Parshas Vayechi, along with their enclosures. Once again, I reiterate what I told you before your departure: that your journey should be a success in both material and spiritual matters alike. Naturally, the precision of the phrase **"alike"** is significant, for the one is dependent upon the other. For "Yisrael are one nation on earth" (see Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 29, in both versions), which means that even on earth and in worldly matters, the unity that is "He is King over all" is evident to them. There is no duality in the world at all, for everything stems from the Simple Unity, and consequently, this is found throughout all of creation, down to the most minute details. It is only that, in order for there to be the matter of free choice, there are places where the possibility is given for one who wishes to err to do so.

And according to the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, "Chassidim are clever, and do not put off until tomorrow (the future—to receive their reward) that which can be done today (the present—to perform them)." Thus, they are in agreement even at the beginning of their journey, in the midst of their journey, and even before they reach their destination—the "desire of Hashem" (cheftzei Hashem), where everything is one.

All of this length is encapsulated in the brief saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, to the shluchim and those sent from the yeshivos: that their task is to harvest—to gather—materiality, and to sow spirituality. However, as explained in the Zohar (Vol. II, 184b), every avodah must be performed with joy and gladness, for then one draws down a "higher joy" (chadva achra ila'ah); that is, success is granted from Above through a joy that breaks through all barriers...

#### ***1993***

**And according to the saying:** See also above, Letter 1882, and the references in the notes there.

**In the brief saying:** See also above, Vol. IV, Letters 935, 1134, 1140, 1196.

## 1994

26 Teves, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive regards from you via the telephone conversation with the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and accomplished, Rabbi Chaim Mordechai Aizik Hodakov, regarding the meeting you had with the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and faithful, Rabbi Eliyahu Simpson. I was also pleased to hear of the good and well-received decision, made in a good and auspicious hour, that a certain portion of the income which will be generated, with the help of Hashem, from the sources of the "Beersheba Company," should be given to the various charities that were founded and are directed by me in the spirit of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisroel.

It is a well-known teaching that we heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that when a Jew down here makes a firm decision to give a large sum to tzedakah, even if at that very moment he does not see the practical possibility of how he will be able to fulfill it, nevertheless, Above, a decree is immediately issued for him for *parnassah* with abundance—in such a measure that he will indeed be able to practically fulfill his good decision. I am certain that this applies to your situation as well; although it has not been so until now, since you and your partner have accepted this good resolution with your whole heart, it has surely already been decreed Above to grant you *parnassah* with abundance and success, so that you may fulfill your good will with a joyful heart and an open hand.

It is a known theory explaining the formation of oil that it is created from the remains of living creatures that lay under great pressure, and over time, this became oil, which is used for heating and illumination.

It is also a well-known expression of the Baal Shem Tov that from everything a Jew hears and sees, it is being shown to him from Above so that he may learn a lesson for his *avodah* and *shlichus* in this world—especially regarding something one encounters day in and day out, which should serve as a lesson for each of us in our *shlichus* in this *olam hazeh*.

One must contemplate the fact that physical (corporeal) things have no inherent vitality, as a person can see for himself that his own vitality comes from the *neshamah*, and Hashem has bound the *neshamah* to the body. The intent in this is that one should apply pressure upon physical desires and inclinations. When there is the proper pressure from the *neshamah* upon the body, the body itself—which of its own accord has no vitality—becomes something that warms its surroundings and illuminates its entire environment. The *nimshal* (the lesson derived) is clear and requires no elaboration.

I wish to reiterate my blessing that Hashem Yisbarach grant you success in *parnassah* in the aforementioned matter, and that you may be able to fulfill your good decision in practice, and to an even greater extent than you currently anticipate.

With blessings,

## 1895

B"H, 26 Teves, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding your question on the interpretation of the word *hanolad* (the "born" or "future"), whether it refers to the future or the past, and your reference to Maseches Yevamos 11a, where the Alter Rebbe explains "Who is wise? He who sees *hanolad*" as referring to the past: In Chassidic discourse, both interpretations of this statement of our Sages are cited (Tanya, Chapter 42; Likutei Torah, Shemini Atzeres 91b)...

With blessings.

## 1996

By the Grace of Hashem, 27 Teves, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Yishai Halevi Meir
Shalom u’Bracha,

I have received your letter of 13 Teves. Since my secretariat does not correspond in French, I am replying in Hebrew, which, as is evident from the few words in your letter, you read and understand.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the perspective of the Torah and traditional Judaism on the theory of evolution—evidently referring to the theory founded by Darwin (or perhaps the theory of Lamarck, which is a theory of evolution by leaps, unlike the former)—the perspective of the Torah is clear. One of the reasons for the mitzvah of resting on the seventh **day** of every week is, "For in six days Hashem made the heavens and the earth, and on the seventh day He ceased from work and rested." From this, it is understood that the six days of creation are days in the literal sense, not as those who wish to interpret them as six eras. This is also proven in many places in the words of our Sages, that the six days of Bereishis were days of twenty-four hours each (see Pirkei D’Rabbi Eliezer, ch. 3 and following; Midrash Rabbah, Bereishis; Sanhedrin 38b, and many other places).

2) The narrative of creation also details the **order** of creation—those creatures created on the third, fourth, fifth, and sixth days—meaning that the species were each created **individually**. As the literal text of the Torah states, the earth brought forth plants, fish, sea monsters, birds, beasts, and cattle, and only afterward was man created; they did not evolve from one another.

**Note:** It is well known that there are interpretations found in certain books—specifically the essay by the Ohr HaChaim that you mention in your letter—that attempt to connect them with the theory of evolution. However, anyone who examines these books and essays will see that they were written not out of an internal conviction in the necessity of the theory, but for a specific purpose that we find in apologetic literature: the desire to show the nations of the world that their opinions and theories can be found even in the Holy Scriptures and the words of our Sages. The authors themselves recognized that this was nothing more than a highly strained interpretation, a justification born of duress and necessity, yet they felt compelled to write this way in order to improve the perspective and attitude of "the world" toward our holy Torah—even though they themselves knew it was not the true interpretation. And who is greater than the Rambam, of whom the greatest of Israel said, "From Moshe [our teacher] to Moshe [ben Maimon], there arose none like Moshe"? Yet, one who examines his book, *Yad HaChazakah*, will see to what extent the interpretations in *Moreh Nevuchim*, and particularly the reasons for the mitzvos, were not his own personal view within the Torah. This is the case with many of the G-d-fearing Jewish scholars of the Middle Ages and our own time, who think that one must sanctify the Name by twisting the interpretation of the words of our Sages to align them with "scientific" theories, because by doing so, their prestige is elevated in the eyes of certain circles among the Jewish people and the nations of the world.

Another example of this: It is known how some of the greatest of Israel struggled to reconcile the literal interpretation of the verses that indicate the movement of the sun and moon, and that "the earth stands forever," with the theory of Copernicus, which for a long time was said to be the absolute truth—until Einstein’s theory of relativity came along and proved (and it is understood that this is a proof according to the state of knowledge **now**) that from a scientific point of view, it is impossible to prove in any way, regarding the relationship between the stars and the earth, which is standing and which is revolving. Consequently, it is entirely possible that the earth is stationary and the stars revolve around it, and there is no need to remove the verses from their literal meaning and twist them through complications and strained interpretations. The same applies to the words of our Sages; they should be understood according to their literal meaning.

3) Regarding the theory of evolution itself—the scientific approach to creating any theory is known: the necessity of the theory must stem from the need to explain phenomena and difficult matters observed in reality, and the theory must be based on foundations taken from nature and the senses. In other words, the purpose of a scientific theory is to explain a difficult-to-understand phenomenon through explanations and proofs from nature itself—to make this phenomenon **simpler**. One of the first requirements of a scientific theory is that it must be possible to test its conclusions in nature to see if they are accurate or not.

The same applies in our case: there were those who asked how the many types and species that exist in nature were created and where they came from—in the inanimate, the plant, the animal, and the human kingdoms—and they thought to resolve the magnitude of the difficulty through a theory that, according to it, there were initially only the simplest organisms, from which more complex and complicated creatures evolved over time, until from the first beginning of a single-celled creature, the higher animals, including the human species, evolved. Now, for this theory to be called "scientific," it must fit and fulfill several conditions, among them, as mentioned:

(1) The evolution from a simple creature to a complex and complicated one must be a phenomenon observed in nature, or at the very least, there must be a reliable person who can testify that they have seen this phenomenon occur even once.

However, it is a fact known to all that there is not **one** piece of reliable testimony from anyone who has seen the evolution of one species of creature from another. What they have seen, and even what Darwin himself recounts in his famous book, are only minor changes in certain organs, and the fact that they found skeletons of dead creatures similar to a species existing today, and they concluded in their minds that it is a correct **hypothesis** to say that one species evolved from another. This is the case regarding the species of pigeons and the species of the horse, upon which the theory of evolution relies most heavily.

(2) The situation and description according to the theory of evolution must be more understandable and simpler than the belief that everything was created—*yesh me'ayin* (something from nothing).

But there is no proof **in nature** to say that it is easier for a simple creature to eventually turn into a human than for a human to be created *yesh me'ayin*. Or, in other words: the explanation that a group of atoms and molecules united all at once in such a way that they formed the existence of a human is no more difficult than saying that a group of simple cells, having undergone a change in their "living" conditions, changed over time into organs that are entirely different from one another, such as the brain in the head, the eyeball, and the heel of the foot.

4) There are many creatures, both in the plant kingdom and among the lower animals, whose lifespans are extremely short, and consequently, a person can examine the course of change in their bodies over many, many generations.

Furthermore, it is in the power of the researcher to change their living conditions to a very great degree. Despite all this, scientists have not yet succeeded in evolving one **species** from another. Their achievement is only in having changed a characteristic of a plant or animal to a certain degree, or in having crossbred two species to produce a hybrid, but not in the evolution from a species of a lower level to a species of a higher level.

5) The law accepted by all scientists is known, which is the "eternity" of matter, so to speak, or, according to the most recent conclusions of science, the "eternity" of the total sum of matter and energy. If so, according to this law, all the atoms and their components already existed at the beginning of creation (or have existed eternally, according to the view of the heretics). According to the theory of evolution, one must say that from the beginning, **all** the atoms already existed, but they were scattered, and afterward, they gathered one by one in various strange ways and under special conditions, which, according to the calculation of statistics and probability, the possibility that such suitable conditions would be found, and all **at once**, is **extremely** remote. Furthermore, according to this theory, one must say that these conditions (which from a scientific point of view are almost impossible) existed for millions and billions of years, and everything was moving in **one** direction—namely, evolution from the lower to the higher and more developed.

On the other hand, from the perspective of the believer, that the Holy One, Blessed be He, created the entire number of atoms that exist in the world *yesh me'ayin*, it is not difficult for him to say that it is within the power of the Creator to create not only a single-celled creature, but also a creature with millions of different cells all at once.

**Note:** There are **believers** who hold to the theory of evolution because, without it, they find it difficult: Why would the Holy One, Blessed be He, need to create so many different species in which **they** do not see any utility, etc.?

But this difficulty is not resolved by the theory of evolution, because according to the Torah, even the laws of nature are by the will of the Holy One, Blessed be He. If so, the question remains: what is the utility of such laws of nature that, as a result, created many species which, according to the understanding of the questioners, have no utility, etc.?

6) There are several other difficulties and complete misunderstandings within the theory of evolution itself, and many scientists also disagree with it. See, for example, the books of Fleischmann and Schindewolf (listed at the bottom of the letter), in which you will find sharp criticism of this theory. It is surely also known to you that within the theory of evolution itself, there are several contradictions. For example, regarding the calculation of the age of the earth: the calculation based on the amount of salt in the ocean, the calculation based on the amount of radium, lead, and uranium in a certain place, the calculation based on the current state of the sun, the calculation based on the remains and layers of the earth in different places, one on top of the other—the results of these calculations are in **complete** contradiction to one another.

7) It should be noted that even if someone were to come and say that it is possible that one species could evolve from another **now**, and he saw this with his own eyes, there is no contradiction to our **religion and faith** (although, as mentioned, this is a strange and wondrous phenomenon that no scientist should accept until they bring conclusive evidence that this is the truth). What I said above is only that the order of creation in actuality was as it is recounted in our holy Torah—namely, that on the third day it was: "Let the earth sprout vegetation... fruit trees bearing fruit **after its kind**," meaning each and every species individually, as the words of our Sages state (Chullin 60b). All of this was created during the twelve hours of the third day. Similarly, the creation (or suspension) of the luminaries of the heavens and the stars occurred on the fourth day, the creation of the fish and birds on the fifth day, and the cattle, beasts, and the human species on the sixth day.

With blessings to you and your colleagues—that you may succeed on the path that leads to the House of G-d—this is the path of Torah and the fulfillment of mitzvos—in actual practice.

***

By the Grace of Hashem, 28 Adar, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Yishai Halevi Meir
Shalom u’Bracha,

You have surely received the letter from the Rebbe Shlita dated 27 Teves, and it is surprising that its receipt was not confirmed. However, what primarily interests the Rebbe Shlita is how the conference went and the discussion regarding the question of evolution—the subject of the correspondence—and what the results were.

On this occasion, I have been instructed by the Rebbe Shlita to inform you that he has received the article by Dr. S.B. Ullman, which was published in the journal *Sinai*, Jerusalem, 1943, Vol. 12, and has now been reprinted in English in the book *Encyclopedia of Biblical Interpretation*, New York, 1953, by Rabbi Menachem M. Kasher.

In the aforementioned article, a whole series of scientists who have spoken out against the theory of evolution is brought.

Since you may not have the book at hand, I have noted some of them at the bottom of the page. It should be noted that I have listed below (according to the instruction of the Rebbe Shlita) only authors from recent times, without mentioning others from the 19th century who were also brought in the aforementioned article.

With respect and blessing.

## 1997

1997

B"H, 6 Shevat, 5713

Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...And the most essential point of all is that it is not worthwhile to spend time complaining about others, since there are two doubts involved: a) Whether one is justified in his complaints. b) Even if he is justified, whether he will succeed in this, for the choice remains with the other person whether or not to listen to him. This is not the case if one were to devote this time to complaints against himself to improve his own situation; then, the aforementioned doubts are nullified because: a) The permission and the ability are given to each and every person to make an honest accounting of his own soul, and consequently, the complaints will be justified. b) According to what is explained in Tanya and also ruled in Rambam, the permission and the ability are in the hands of each and every person to rule over himself and to follow his own will...

## 1998

B"H, 6 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, involved in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Yitzchak, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

Your letter from Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Va'era has just been received, along with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed within it. I will, G-d willing, read it at the *tziyun* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, at a time of favor, and may Hashem grant that you be able to share good news regarding all the matters mentioned in the *pidyon nefesh*.

2) Regarding your question: since you recite *Kaddish D'Rabbanan* before *Hodu*, is it permitted to interrupt the *Pesukei D'Zimra* for this? In my opinion (as time does not permit me to research this, and it also seems straightforward), since this is not a personal obligation of yours, but rather one incumbent upon the *minyan*, there is no justification for you to interrupt in a place where one is not permitted to interrupt.

3) Regarding your question about youths who arrive late: if they are not told to skip the order preceding *Hodu*, they will be unable to *daven* with a *minyan*. How should one conduct oneself in this matter?

It is known from our Sages, "Who is wise? He who foresees the consequences." This applies to every matter, and naturally to this case as well. Although the law is clear that one may skip (in the sefer *Shaarei Tefillah* by R. Yaakov Rakach, he brings 91 opinions that hold this way), one must "foresee the consequences." Over a short period of time, we have seen tangibly that the permission to skip leads immediately to a lack of appreciation for the importance of *tefillah*. First, they skip the order preceding *Hodu*, then *Pesukei D'Zimra*, and then, etc. This is especially true in your question, which concerns youths, etc. Therefore, in practice, although it is impossible to rule publicly against the law, one should maneuver in every possible way so that they do not even know of the permission to skip. This is similar to the statement of our Sages, "The Torah said: Violate one Shabbos so that he may observe many Shabbosos" (*Shabbos 151b*). This is all the more so in our case, where both matters concern the same person.

Regarding the *hasagos* (objections/attainments) of Moshe Rabbeinu, which you asked about some time ago—this is explained in the *maamarim* of *Ra'aya Mehemna* in the *Zohar*. See *Zohar Chadash, Vol. 3, 116b* and there. Also in the *maamar* entitled *Vayetzei 5666*.

With blessings for success in your holy work, and regards to all your colleagues in this work and those you influence in general, and in accordance with the statement of our Sages, "And from my students, more than all of them."

P.S. My suggestion regarding the customs for the day of the *hillula* is the same as last year.

Enclosed is the *kuntres* that was published recently.

## 1999

B”H, 6 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and refined, engaged in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Tzvi, may he live,
And his wife, the Rabbanit, may she live,

Peace and Blessing!

...4) Enclosed is my suggestion (from last year) regarding customs for the day of the Hilula of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, as well as the Kuntres that was published not long ago. In a separate envelope, I have also sent you the *Beis Rebbe* which we recently printed here in Yiddish, which I am sure you will utilize for the benefit of your avodah, in addition to the benefit for yourselves.

5) It would be appropriate to investigate whether it is possible for one of you to publish short maamarim, stories, or similar content at regular intervals in the newspapers currently appearing in your country, or even in your city. It is understood that this can be in the local language, and someone else can translate what you write, provided that it is certain that the translation remains faithful to the inner point. The intention here is twofold: a) Publicizing your names, which in turn strengthens your standing in all matters. b) Publicizing ideas that are appropriate, whether regarding yiras shamayim in general or Chassidus in particular.

6) It would be appropriate to investigate and find a suitable translator who can translate the sichos and talks, or other Kehot publications, into the local language. You should consult among yourselves as to which booklets and stories should take priority in this, and inform me of the expenses involved and the expected benefit, and then it will be possible to make a final decision on this...

Certainly, when you publish in the press as mentioned above, or when there are any printed materials in general related to this, you should send a copy here.

Furthermore, please be so kind as to inquire whether there might be rare books in the shul or even among individuals, or perhaps manuscripts—especially from the Sefardic books that are not being used. If so, it would be worthwhile to send them here, and if requested, they can be exchanged for any of the Kehot publications known to you.

**Rabbi Tzvi, may he live:** Chitrik, Brazil.

## 1,500

B"H, 6 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter from Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Va'era, along with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed within it, which—*bli neder*—I will read at a time of favor at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zy"a*.

Regarding what you wrote, that you find studying *Chovos HaLevavos* difficult: surely you recall that I told you my intention was not [for you to study] *Shaar HaYichud*, but rather the chapters that follow it. If even that is difficult for you, then [you should] study *Pochei'ach Ivrim*, or the *maamarim* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, from Yud-Beis Tammuz and Yud-Tes Kislev from various years, in whichever place your heart desires. May Hashem help you and save you from the "judges of your soul," so that you may ascend higher and higher, until it is evident in you that you are a "shoot of the planting" of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the *yeshiva* of *Tomchei Temimim*, where you were privileged to be a student for several years.

With blessings for success in all your affairs and for the health of your entire household, may they live and be well.

## 201

B"H, 6 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...It is surely unnecessary to awaken you regarding the profound concept that "Israel is one nation on earth." This is not merely in the simple sense that they believe in one Hashem and one Torah, but rather that they draw down this unity into all matters. That is to say, there is no duality in the world at all; for just as the Ribono shel Olam is called "One"—an absolute, simple unity—so too, within the world, there exists a unity between all its components. In particular, physicality and spirituality are not two separate matters; it is only that space is provided, as our Sages of blessed memory said, for **whoever wishes** to err to come and err. But in truth, they are one.

It is the task of the Jewish person to understand and feel within himself the unity of Havayah, and to convey this understanding to his surroundings, to all those he influences, and to every place his hand can reach. This applies as well to the matter of health: when an increase in the health of the body is needed, it must correspond to an increase in the health of the neshamah, in accordance with the expression of our Sages, "Whoever adds, they add to him."

Therefore, I will take the liberty of suggesting that it would be appropriate for your father, shlita, to increase his study of the shiurim of our Torah—the *Toras Chayim* (Torah of Life)—through which "He planted eternal life within us." One of the interpretations of this is that while being in this world, one should live with *chayim amitiyim* (true life), which must be felt and seen also in the physical body, as per the ruling of the Rambam: "For one who is healthy and whole is following the ways of Hashem" (*Hilchos De'os* 4:1).

Awaiting good tidings.

With blessings for success in your holy work.

**M. Schneerson**

## 203

B"H, 6 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I have received your two letters (the first without a date of writing, and the second from 2 Shevat), and in response to your questions:

a) As you yourself write in your letter, the instruction heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, at the time, is that the Bris Milah should be performed when the health of your sons—may they live—is in perfect condition. If there is any doubt, or a double doubt, it is possible to perform it the next day or the day after. The language of the Rambam in the end of Chapter 3 of Hilchos Milah is well known, and the Tzafnas Paneach explains that he holds that a delayed Milah is rectified retroactively.

b) Regarding your question whether to delay the Bris Milah so that it may be performed for both of them together: I do not understand this reasoning. You should perform it for one when he is healthy and whole, and for the other when he is healthy and whole, even if it is not at the same time.

c) Regarding specific days to perform a Bris Milah when it is not on its proper time, I have not heard of such a thing. It is evident from several places that there are no special days for this. One should not delay it without a valid reason.

d) Regarding the names you intend to give your sons—may they live—we know the approach of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, on this: "He does not say." The matter is understood based on what is brought in the writings of the Arizal, that Above, the thought is placed into the heart of the father and mother as to which name to give their children, a name that is appropriate for their soul. Consequently, you should call them names that you and your wife—may she live—agree upon, and may it be for long life and good years, in both material and spiritual matters.

f) Please convey my Mazal Tov wishes to your wife, the Rabbanit—may she live—and I extend my blessing to both of you together, that you should bring your newborn sons into the covenant of Avraham Avinu at a good and auspicious time. Just as you bring them into the covenant, so too may you bring them to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds, together with your son... may they live, and may you raise them in perfect health and with abundance.

With blessings of Mazal Tov.

## 2.4

B”H, 9 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter of 12 Kislev, and I was also pleased to receive regards from you through your son-in-law, *sheyichyeh*. I derived particular pleasure from your writing about memories from the days of old regarding *mechutan* Admur Moharash *n.e.*, which you heard from your father. Surely you are utilizing his influence in your surroundings to introduce them to Chassidus in general, and Chassidus Chabad in particular.

Regarding what you write in your letter that there is no one to speak a *lebediken vort* (a lively word) to: we have heard many times from *mechutan* Admur Moharash *zatzuklaleh-h nebga-m ziya* in the name of our Rebbes, the *Nesi’im*, that when one speaks with a Yid, the *neshamah* hears it immediately. Furthermore, when the speaker does not cease and does not become weary of speaking, it eventually penetrates (*nemt em durch*) within the other person. There is a *chazakah* (presumption) that *ta'amulah* (outreach) does not return empty-handed. A person must do what depends on him, and Hashem will grant success in the way that only He, *yisbarach*, can. This will serve as a channel and vessel for drawing down blessing and success in the matters that you yourself are in need of.

May Hashem grant you proper health, so that for long, good days and years, you may be the channel through which the light of Chassidus is increased in the place where you are located.

Enclosed is a *kuntres* that was recently published, which will surely be of benefit to you in the aforementioned.

With blessings.

## B’H

B’H, 13 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the great Gaon, the great Chossid, G-d-fearing and renowned, who sits in judgment and directs his congregation with integrity, etc., Moreinu HaRav Dovid, shlita,
Ovadia
Spokesman of the holy community of Sefrou

...I hereby express my warm thanks for your precious gift, the book "Yismach Levav," containing rulings and legal principles by your father, the great Gaon, the great Chossid, etc., of blessed memory. Although time has not yet permitted me to study the book as it deserves, out of appreciation for it, I have leafed through its pages.

It is surprising that, although in a few places I found mention of the books of the Alter Rebbe, the author of the Tanya, it appears this is only from secondary sources—even though his books have spread throughout the entire world and he has been accepted as a posek among all of Klal Yisrael, without distinction between Chassidim and non-Chassidim. It goes without saying that, for the time being, I did not find any mention of the books of the Tzemach Tzedek, even though they are cited several times in the "Sdei Chemed" by the Sephardic sage, who is himself mentioned a few times in the book "Yismach Levav."

I am taking this opportunity to point out a few references for Part One, which is the section on Orach Chaim of the aforementioned book, from the works of our Rebbe, the Nasi, the Alter Rebbe and the Tzemach Tzedek:

Orach Chaim, Siman 1 – See Responsa Tzemach Tzedek, Orach Chaim section, Siman 17.

Simanim 4, 5, 6 – See "Seder Birchas HaNehenin" printed in the Siddur of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe.

End of Siman 8, regarding the measurement of *k'dei achilas pras* – See Responsa Tzemach Tzedek, Shaar HaMiluim, Siman 9 (see also my notes in the *Reshimot* to the *Megillas Eichah* of the Tzemach Tzedek, page 61).

Simanim 10-12 – See the letter of the Alter Rebbe printed in his Siddur before the entry of Shabbos, which is mentioned in this Siman in the book "Yismach Levav," page 10, column 3, in passing (and see also the book "Bein HaShemashos" by Rabbi Tukachinsky of Jerusalem, where a **multitude** of opinions from Rishonim and Acharonim are cited, whose view aligns with that of our Rebbe, the author of the Tanya).

It should also be noted regarding the author's introduction, in note 3, to the Laws of Talmud Torah of the Alter Rebbe, Chapter 2, note 1.

In passing, regarding Siman 8 on the laws of measurements: Some years ago, the book "Shiurei Torah" by Rabbi Avraham Chaim Naeh was printed in Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established, and a new edition was also released there in the year 5707. It contains all the opinions on the measurements of Torah from Rishonim and Acharonim, as well as in the second part of the aforementioned book, titled "Shiur Mikveh," Jerusalem 5711.

**Postscript:** See also the references in the *Talmudic Encyclopedia*, entry **Bein HaShemashos.**

## 206

B"H, 13 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding the content of your aforementioned letter: I already told you during our conversation here that it is **not at all** correct for a yeshiva student—in any yeshiva whatsoever—not to recognize the authority of the yeshiva administration. It is an **absolute** necessity that he conduct himself in accordance with the yeshiva’s regulations, as failure to do so causes great confusion, both for the student himself and for his peers in the class.

It is well known that when my father-in-law, the Rebbe, served as the active administrator of the Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch yeshiva, his father, the Rebbe [Rashab]—may his merit protect us—would not interfere in the yeshiva’s management, but rather would act only through him, as he was the active administrator. On the one occasion when a matter was handled differently, he immediately corrected it and arranged for the instruction to be issued through my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

It goes without saying, and is simple to understand, that I am not comparing the yeshiva administration to my father-in-law, the Rebbe, just as I would not compare him to the Rebbe [Rashab]—may his merit protect us—(to distinguish between the living and the Source of Life—though this is along the lines of Yevamos 105b). If so, the moral lesson for each and every one of us is that when a son or relative enters a yeshiva, it is necessary—there is no other way—to set aside one’s own will. Rather, one must use all the influence one has to ensure that the son fulfills the administration’s instructions one hundred percent. Even if there are matters that do not seem right to the father or relative, consider:

a) There is doubt as to who is correct—the yeshiva administration or the father.

b) Even if the father is correct, the administration has the assistance of the yeshiva’s founder and of the one who appointed them to their post. Consequently, they have been granted the strength to succeed, even in their mistakes—along the lines of "this too is for the good" (which is an even higher level than "everything the Merciful One does, He does for the good").

...Furthermore, the proper path is to present one’s claims to the yeshiva administration and ask them to review them. If, even after their review, they maintain their position, one can rely on Hashem that in a Tomchei Temimim yeshiva, ultimately, it will turn out for the good. Then, one can be strong in the confidence that one’s son will succeed in his studies, both in Nigleh and in Chassidus.

I hope that you will take it upon yourself to try this for at least a few months—conducting yourself with absolutely no interference, and on the contrary, making it easier for your son—may he live—to maintain discipline and conduct himself according to the yeshiva’s order.

With blessings for true health and all the best in body and soul, awaiting good news.

## 27

B"H, 13 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter (without the date of writing), in which you write that in connection with the merger... you are in need of a blessing for the fortification and expansion of your position there, in light of the changes that may occur as a result of this merger.

It is surely unnecessary to remind you of the statement of our Sages that the Ribono shel Olam did not create a single thing in His world in vain. Consequently, each and every one of us is given the strengths and possibilities through which we can execute and fulfill our shlichus and role in this world. The magnitude of these strengths and possibilities is commensurate with the role. However, since the role incumbent upon each of us is a matter of holiness, the authority and ability are granted to expand it. According to the teaching of our Sages, "Whoever adds, they add to him"—when a person takes upon himself an additional shlichus, he thereby expands the channels and vessels through which strengths and possibilities are drawn to him from above.

May it be the will of Hashem that you, too, resolve to increase your avodah and efforts in strengthening Yiddishkeit and spreading the love of Torah and mitzvos in general, and the teachings of Chassidus, its customs, guidance, and foundations in particular—for this is, after all, the root of your origin, and therefore your primary personal role. And in this way, your work and status in... and your communal activities in general will naturally grow and strengthen as well.

With blessings.

## 208

B"H, 13 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

This week provided a fitting time for you to come to my mind, as it included 10 Shevat, the yahrtzeit of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, the *tzaddik yesod olam*—may his merit protect us—who dedicated his entire life to guiding the sons and daughters of Yisrael, wherever they may be, on the path that ascends to the House of Hashem, through *ahavas Hashem*, *ahavas haTorah*, and *ahavas Yisrael*—the pillars of the teachings of Chassidus.

We have a tradition from the Mitteler Rebbe, son of the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch and founder of Chabad Chassidus (see *Kitzurim VeHe'aros* to *Likutei Amarim*, published by us, page 122), that "because of this *mesiras nefesh* for the teachings of Chassidus, it was decreed in the Heavenly Court that in every matter of Torah, *yiras shamayim*, and refined character traits, the hand of those who are connected to him and follow in his footsteps shall be uppermost."

Since I receive good news from time to time regarding your assistance and participation in our holy work of proper education in your country, in the institutions founded in the name of the *baal hahilula*, you are remembered for good—especially during this *eis ratzon*—to draw down upon you blessing and success in actual practice, both in your work for the benefit of the community and in your personal affairs, for you and your household, may they live in goodness.

Enclosed is the *maamar* "The Holy One, Blessed be He, does not deal tyrannically with His creatures" by the *baal hahilula*, which we published recently, and you will surely find it of great interest.

With blessings.

## 29

B.H., 13 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 5 Teves, in which you describe your situation—how the various trades and businesses you have undertaken have, for the time being, not met with success—you seem to be puzzled by this. Yet, at the beginning of your own letter, you have already written the answer, though it seems you have not reflected upon it. You begin your letter by stating that without any prompting on your part, you received a letter from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in which he wrote: "Arrange a good shidduch and occupy yourself with a suitable business." Immediately after this, you explain how you began engaging in business, etc. All the while, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, clearly instructed you to arrange a good shidduch *and* occupy yourself with a business, yet you began with the latter without making the preparation for it as instructed by the Tzaddik of the world, the Nasi of Yisroel.

In general, there is no need to search for proofs as to why my father-in-law, the Rebbe, wrote and linked these two matters together—and furthermore, why he began with the matter of the shidduch and only afterwards the business. However, it can be explained according to the statement of our Sages, also cited in *Likutei Torah* (end of Parshas Berachah), that a man’s blessing comes through his wife (see there for the reason). Even though many people are granted their livelihood regardless, or on account of the future, a "blessing" is specifically through one’s wife. Consequently, it is clear that you should have fulfilled the instruction of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, to arrange a good shidduch. As our Sages say, it is the way of a man to seek [what he has lost], and a *chassan* is called so because he descends in rank [to find his match]. The words of the Tzaddikim endure forever; since he instructed you to arrange a good shidduch, if you do not interfere with your own free choice, Hashem will provide it for you. Certainly, afterwards, the verse "to leave a blessing upon your house" will be fulfilled in you. It is surely superfluous to point out that you must immediately increase your study of both the *nigleh* of Torah and the study of Chassidus. This will serve as an additional channel and vessel for the drawing down and reception of Hashem’s blessing in the aforementioned matters.

Regarding your observation concerning the free choice of the celestial ministers above in relation to Yisroel and the nations—you did not clarify your question, what exactly is bothering you. In brief:

a) The ministers and angels have no free choice at all; they are merely like an axe in the hand of the one who hews with it (*Derech Mitzvosecha*, Mitzvas Milah, Ch. 3; see also *Likutei Torah*, Behar 38b).

b) Yisroel receives all their affairs, even the physical ones, only from the side of holiness—that is, from that which is *batul* to Him, blessed be He, in actuality—for "Hashem’s portion is His people" (*Iggeres HaTeshuvah*, Ch. 6; *Derech Mitzvosecha*, ibid.).

c) When it happens that some among Yisroel receive from the *heichalos* of the *sitra achra*, it is only through their having done what is evil in the eyes of Hashem, and even this is only for a temporary time (*Kuntres U’Maayon*, p. 47).

d) The nations receive all their affairs (from the externality of the Supreme Will, which is the source of the vitality of the *sitra d’le’o’vaz*, i.e.,) from the *heichalos* of the *sitra achra*, where Elokus does not shine in a revealed manner except through a concealment of the countenance, and they feel their own *yeshus*—the two are interdependent (*Kuntres U’Maayon*, Maamar 2-3). By way of course, and *a fortiori*, this is the case for the nations to whom He apportioned them. Therefore, they were not commanded regarding *shituf* (partnership/association with Hashem), unlike Yisroel, "the people near to Him."

With blessings, awaiting good news.

## 210

B"H, 13 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, who occupies himself with communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi A. Chanoch, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

After the longest of intervals, your letter of 4 Shevat was received, in which you inform me that you will soon send a photocopy of three letters from the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory, and that you have already sent a photocopy of another letter. Many thanks for your efforts in this regard. It is presumably a continuation of the letter I sent through you to the son of Rabbi Cohen, and I trust you will continue to exert yourself in such matters in the future.

It is surprising that throughout this entire time, not a single clipping has been received regarding Chabad in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, especially since, in accordance with my last letter, you were tasked with receiving these clippings and sending them here. Is it really the case that for several months, not a single item has been printed regarding the teachings of Chabad Chassidus and its affairs? Furthermore, you do not write regarding the progress in editing *Beis Rebbe* in the Holy Tongue in a corrected and expanded edition (meaning, to include what is found in the *sichos* of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, regarding the Alter Rebbe)? And similarly, regarding the Mitteler Rebbe, etc., over the course of time. For, G-d willing, if the attempt to edit *Beis Rebbe* regarding the Alter Rebbe is successful, I intend to also consider *Beis Rebbe* regarding the Nasi'im who followed the Alter Rebbe.

These days, *Beis Rebbe* was printed here in Yiddish, and you are surely aware that it contains stories that were not included in the *Beis Rebbe* in the Holy Tongue. It is certain that the Yiddish *Beis Rebbe* can also be found in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, and you will be able to see it and incorporate those stories into the corrected *Beis Rebbe* that you are preparing.

This letter was delayed, and a letter from 11 Shevat was received with the enclosed. Many thanks for the photocopies, and especially for the good news regarding your activities in the new housing development in the vicinity of Lod. I trust you will now exert yourselves to continue this matter, so that after the "plowing and sowing," you will also reap and gather the grain and the fruits. May Hashem bless you with success in all of this.

Awaiting good news, with a blessing for success in the above.

## 211

B"H, 13 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 2 Shevat, in which you share the good news regarding the health of your daughter... *tichyeh*. May Hashem enable you and your wife *shichyu* to raise her to Torah, *chuppah*, and good deeds, in good health.

Regarding what you wrote, that you do not have a set time for studying Chassidus: it is understood that this is not correct at all. It is obvious from everywhere in the words of our Sages that Torah study must be done with consistency, as the expression goes, "Set times for Torah." It is also well known in this regard the saying of the Alter Rebbe, that the matter of "consistency" (*keviyus*) must be not only in time, but also in the soul, and one depends on the other, as is evident in a tangible way. Furthermore, we are required by the words of our Sages (Taanis 7a) that a person learns more from his students than from his peers or even his teacher; therefore, it is necessary that you also have a recipient, meaning that you should spread the light of the teachings of Chassidus in your surroundings.

Regarding your notification about your wife *tichyeh*: It would be appropriate to have the *mezuzos* in your home checked. Also, your wife *tichyeh* should give a few coins to the *tzedakah* of Rabbi Meir Baal HaNes every *Erev Shabbos*. You should strengthen yourself, at least until after the birth, *b'sha'ah tovah u'mutzlachas*, by keeping the three daily study portions established by the Rebbe, which are accessible to everyone: the *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya* as is well known. May Hashem fulfill the days of your wife's pregnancy properly and with ease, and may she give birth *b'sha'ah tovah u'mutzlachas* at the proper time, properly and with ease.

With blessings,

P.S. Surely you took part in the arrangements connected to the *Yom HaHillula* that took place the day before yesterday.

## 215

B"H, 16 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, who engages in communal needs, R' Ze'ev Dov, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter from the month of Geulah in due time, and I thank you for the good news regarding the farbrengen that was held. It is known from our Sages that "where ten are gathered, the Shechinah rests," and as our Alter Rebbe explains, this applies even if they are not speaking words of Torah (Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 23; see also Kuntres Acharon to Yerushalmi, Eruvin, Chapter 1, Halacha 10). How much more so, and how much more certainly, is this the case when those gathered there hear words of Torah. Surely, good resolutions were also made regarding practical application, and may it be the will of Hashem that these good thoughts and resolutions be drawn down into actual deed.

Enclosed is a brief overview of the life story of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, may his merit protect us, the Nasi of Yisrael, which I am certain will be of benefit to you in strengthening the light of Chassidus in your surroundings.

With blessings for Chassidishe nachas from all your offspring, and may you yourself be included among them.

## 217

B"H, 21 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and refined, involved in communal needs,
R' Moshe Yehuda, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

Your *pidyon nefesh* for yourself and your entire family, may they live, for the day of the *hilula*, has just been received. G-d willing, I will read it at a time of favor at the gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

It is well known what is explained in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Epistle 7, regarding our Sages' statement, "In what [mitzvah] was your father most careful?" Even though every Jewish soul must fulfill all 613 *mitzvos*, nonetheless, in a specific sense, each person has a particular *mitzvah* through which their *Torah* and *mitzvos* ascend and are drawn down (see *Sefer HaSichos* Summer 5700, page 22).

Now, for many people, the *mitzvah* that serves as this gateway is clear, in accordance with our Sages' statement, "Even the head of a small irrigation ditch is appointed from Heaven." Especially for one who has merited to be a *mashpia* to the Jewish people, to bring their hearts closer to our Father in Heaven through the light of Torah—which is the *Torah* of Chassidus—it is understood that the *hemshech* (drawing down of Divine influence) regarding him and his entire family, even in material matters, depends on a preference, care, and extra alacrity—with greater intensity and double-fold strength—in that specific *mitzvah* of his, "far above the other *mitzvos*" (the language of the aforementioned *Iggeres HaKodesh*). May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant him success so that his contemplation of all this will immediately be translated into action in all his spheres of influence, so that their education will be in accordance with the will of our holy *Nasi*, of blessed memory.

With blessings, and awaiting good news and peace.

## 20

20

B"H, 26 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter informing me of the establishment of a Tanya shiur in your shul, and that you are teaching them—as you write in your letter—according to their level of understanding. The magnitude of the merit in this, in bringing Bnei Yisrael closer to the study of Chassidus, the *pnimiyus* of Torah, is beyond measure or estimation. We are assured that this will draw down an additional blessing upon all the affairs of the one who studies and inspires others to study the aforementioned.

Regarding what you wrote—that you teach according to their level of understanding—it is well known what is written, and what we have heard orally many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that the Sefer Tanya, which is called the *Torah Shebiksav* of Chabad Chassidus, is like the study of the *Torah Shebiksav* itself. Even the greatest of the great cannot reach its ultimate depth, yet even the smallest of the small can begin to study it. As our Sages of blessed memory said, "Once a child begins to speak, his father teaches him Torah," and so it is with the study of Tanya: everyone learns according to their own understanding, for everyone has a grasp and a place within it. There is no room here for discouragement, regardless of the level one finds oneself on, for even the greatest of the great has not yet reached its ultimate end. May Hashem grant you the merit to continue in this study for yourself and for your listeners, and may the study be for the purpose of observing, performing, and fulfilling.

When I am at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, I will mention you and your wife, may they live, for whatever you may need, as you wrote in your letter.

With blessings, and regards to all the participants in your shiur.

P.S. Enclosed is a *kuntres* that was published in connection with the third *yom hilula* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, which I am sure will also be of benefit to your audience. May Hashem grant you success in all things.

## 21

B"H, 26 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter—with some delay—in which you write regarding your situation and ask for my opinion as to whether you should travel now to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt speedily by Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

In my opinion, since you are in a country where, recently, several G-d-fearing people have arrived in addition to those who were already living there, and since no one among us knows with certainty the Divine intent behind why one is located in a particular place—for "the steps of man are established by Hashem"—you should fulfill within yourself the instruction, "Do not leave your place." You should influence your surroundings in an appropriate manner to strengthen them in Torah and mitzvos, and warm them with Yiddishe warmth. May Hashem grant you long life and good years to illuminate your surroundings, and even more so with the "candle of a mitzvah and the light of Torah," and the "light of Torah"—which is the Torah of Chassidus, its ways, and its customs. Even for the sake of a single good deed, it is known from the Tanya, Chapter 26, that when performing any mitzvah whatsoever, it becomes an eternal matter Above, forever and ever. It is also known from the saying of the Baal Shem Tov, which we heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that a neshamah descends below and is clothed for several decades in a Jewish body in order to do a favor for a fellow Jew, whether in material or spiritual matters.

With blessings for long life and good years, with all the interpretations.
