## 223

B"H, 27 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal needs,
Rabbi Mordechai, may he live, Hakohen.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 14 Shevat, as well as the one preceding it, the response to which was delayed until now due to several reasons. Regarding your request for my opinion:

a) Concerning the investigation into the Calabria esrogim: In truth, I am not pleased that doubts were raised for you regarding this. However, since the matter has already been set in motion, your proposal to travel there to clarify the situation on the spot is correct. (The story is known, which we heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe: Once, on the night of Nittel, someone entered the study of the Tzemach Tzedek and found him studying. He asked him, "Rebbe, is it not Nittel today?" The Tzemach Tzedek replied, "Open! Who told you to speak?" Yet, despite this, the Tzemach Tzedek closed the book and ceased his study.)

b) Regarding your question about relocating from Italy: This does not seem right to me at all. Since Hashem has granted you the merit to be in a place where you can truly accomplish things in matters of Yiddishkeit in general, and in matters connected to Chassidus in particular, it is completely incomprehensible why you should think about relocating and searching in other countries. Especially since, according to the information available, the situation is not as it should be in the countries you mention. As for the apprehension you write about in your letter regarding the general state of the world: aside from the fact that it is unknown which place is safer, seemingly, in the near future, one will be left only with fears. And since such fear is a matter that depends on one’s will, there is the option not to be afraid and to be confident in the kindness of Hashem—a free gift of kindness—that there will be no cause for distress, G-d forbid.

c) Regarding what you wrote—that in a place where one wishes to draw rainwater, it must be into ground capable of absorbing it, and whether it is permissible to do this using cement: This has already been brought in *Darchei Teshuvah* to *Mikvaos*, section 201, subsection 206, in the name of the *Responsa Imrei Yosher*, that "it is obvious that through cement, the drawing of water is kosher." (It is still worth investigating and clarifying whether the composition of cement has changed since then.)

d) I was pleased by what you wrote, that the *avreich*... participated and assisted you with the mikveh project. Aside from the matter itself, one must seek every opportunity for *kiruv* to strengthen him in his standing in Yiddishkeit and in his participation in Chabad affairs. I am writing to the aforementioned person now regarding the necessity of printing Chassidic content at regular intervals, and regarding the "atmosphere" of Chassidus, specifically in the local language. Surely you, too, will encourage this from your side.

e) It is my hope that by the time you receive my letter, rain will have already fallen and you will be able to use the mikveh. In connection with this, it would be worthwhile to conduct a campaign once again regarding the laws of *taharas hamishpachah*, for it is impossible otherwise; the health of the children who are born, and even that of the husband and wife, etc., depends on this. May Hashem grant you the merit to bring good tidings regarding all of the above, as well as regarding the health of your wife and yourself—may you live long. Your efforts to bring the hearts of the Jewish people closer to their Father in Heaven will surely draw for you additional success in your personal matters, both materially and spiritually, as explained in the beginning of *Torah Or*, that through *tzedakah*, one’s mind and heart become refined a thousand times over.

f) Surely you have received the *pidyon nefesh* from Mr. Tzifel, may he live, and I have also passed on some funds through him. It would be appropriate to hold a *farbrengen* at a suitable time and to arouse the participants regarding matters of Yiddishkeit in general and matters of Chassidus in particular. May Hashem grant you success.

With blessings.

## 24

B"H, 27 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received with pleasure your letter from Motzaei Shabbos Beshalach, along with the newspaper clipping regarding 19 Kislev enclosed therein; thank you for sending it to me. I also received in due time your letter accompanied by the Sicha of Shabbos Mevarchim Elul of this past year, which was printed in Italian. It is well known that regarding a mitzvah, one does not say "thank you," for the reward of a mitzvah is the mitzvah itself. It would be appropriate—as I believe I have written to you previously—that at frequent intervals, not too far apart from one another, matters from the Torah of Chassidus, its stories, and its guidance should be printed in Italian. This applies to the near future regarding 2 Nissan, the festival of Pesach, Lag B'Omer, etc. You will surely find material for this in the printed volumes of Sichos and Likutei Dibburim, and for the rest, you can consult with the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, R' M. Perlow, who surely possesses several of the aforementioned publications.

2) In accordance with the above, it is a correct initiative that you wish to print a booklet in Italian regarding Chabad activities. It would be best if it were modeled after what is printed here in Lashon HaKodesh and now also in English—the latter of which also contains additional information regarding our work in Morocco, which I enclose herewith. You will surely find someone there who understands English. Naturally, if time permits, it would be worthwhile to send a copy of the draft here before it is printed.

3) Regarding your writing that the booklet will be published by the Milan newspaper: since I do not know the nature of the newspaper clearly, it is difficult for me to decide on this. It would be best for you to consult with the esteemed Rabbis Perlow and Gansburg, who are on the scene, as to whether it is better for the booklet to be published by the Chabad organization or by the newspaper, as there are advantages to both. In any case, it is worthwhile that Chabad matters be printed in the newspaper at frequent intervals, from time to time, as mentioned above. It is understood how great the merit is for one who endeavors to disseminate information regarding the Torah of Chassidus, its customs, and its guidance in their local language as well.

4) I was very pleased to read that the construction of the mikveh is already complete and that you also made the channel out of weak cement. Surely, by the time you receive this letter, rain will have already fallen, and consequently, it will be possible to use it. I await good news regarding this.

5) Regarding what you wrote in your first letter concerning the "mili d'shtusa" (words of foolishness) mentioned in the Zohar, that you wish to interpret it as referring to secular wisdoms, which are called "folly" in relation to the wisdom of holiness: you have hit upon the truth, as is explained at length in the Maamar titled *Vayomer Moshe... Bachar Lanu Anashim* (1949), printed in Kuntres 63; see there, Chapter 2 and onwards.

6) I trust you received the regards I sent you through Mr. Zipel.

With blessings.

## 25

B"H, 27 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter of 23 Shevat, in which you briefly describe the sequence of events regarding how you entered the Tomchei Temimim yeshiva in Lod, and conclude by noting that you are now fifteen and a half years old, asking whether you should leave the yeshiva to learn a trade or not.

It is a simple matter that since you have miraculously—as you write in your letter—merited to enter the yeshiva, and specifically a yeshiva where both Nigleh and Chassidus are studied, you must understand that you are being assisted from Above to be placed in the best possible position, both materially and spiritually. It is also understood that, in order to test you, thoughts sometimes occur to you to stop your studies; therefore, you must dismiss them and dedicate yourself to the shiurim in Nigleh and Chassidus with great persistence and diligence. **It is obvious** that He who sustains and provides for all will, when the time comes that you need to support yourself, also provide your livelihood. You should not confuse yourself at your age by occupying yourself now with preparing for a livelihood, which depends solely on the Ribono shel Olam. Consequently, connection to His Torah and His mitzvos is a wonderful counsel to facilitate one's livelihood later on, whereas leaving the "tent of Torah" before the proper time hinders this. May the Ribono shel Olam grant you the merit and success to study Torah with yiras shamayim.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

**The Secretary**

## 226

226

By the Grace of Hashem, 27 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Shomrei Shabbos Gemilas Chasadim Society, and at its head, the esteemed and distinguished individuals who engage in communal needs with faith, etc., Rabbi Avraham Sharfstein and Rabbi Yochanan Gordon.

Peace and Blessing!

I was pleased to hear of your good works, as well as to receive the brief report regarding your turnover during the past year. I hope that, just as every matter of holiness is one that "increases and continues," the scope of your work will also expand in the days to come—though may it be that Yidden should not need to borrow out of distress, but rather because their businesses will grow and improve.

My sainted father-in-law, the Rebbe, once spoke (in a sicha from 5701) about the greatness of the mitzvah of gemilas chasadim, as understood by a Polotsk shopkeeper, R' Yisrael, a Chassid of the Tzemach Tzedek. While in Lubavitch by the Tzemach Tzedek for Parshas Vayeira, R' Yisrael heard a maamar chassidus from the Rebbe, explaining that Avraham Avinu was generous with his body, his wealth, and his soul. The Tzemach Tzedek explained how Avraham Avinu, while here below, exchanged his physical gemilas chasadim with the Sefirah of Chesed of Atzilus, from which it is understood that Avraham was higher than the middah of Chesed of Atzilus, etc. R' Yisrael did not grasp the entire maamar, but those few words moved him deeply. Upon returning home, he recounted them at a Chassidishe farbrengen and then went to his business. Although he did not need money, he went to Nachman the shopkeeper to borrow a gemilas chasadim, because he wanted to grant him the merit of the mitzvah of gemilas chasadim. Other shopkeepers, too, having heard of the virtue of gemilas chasadim, would borrow from one another every day. When R' Yisrael came to Lubavitch again, the Tzemach Tzedek called him in and asked about his conduct. Later, the Rebbe Maharash asked the Tzemach Tzedek what he had seen in R' Yisrael, and the Tzemach Tzedek replied that he had seen a pillar of light of Chesed of Atzilus upon Yisrael the shopkeeper.

If the mitzvah of gemilas chasadim is so great even when one is not in need of the money, then all the more so when someone truly requires it. The magnitude of the reward for gemilas chasadim is beyond measure, and is explained in many places in the words of Chazal.

I would like to emphasize one aspect of this reward. As is known, the primary Giver of kindness in the world is the Ribono shel Olam Himself, who gives each of us the powers of the nefesh elokis by way of a loan, so that we may carry out our shlichus in this physical world, and even in this material world. The profit from this Divine gemilas chasadim is, as explained in Chassidus, the concept of the descent of the neshamah and its ascent—a descent for the sake of an ascent, and an ascent beyond comparison. At the same time, the Ribono shel Olam—who is the Lender, giving us all our matters by way of a loan—is also, kavyachol, "profiting," as it says in the Midrash: "When Yisrael does the will of the Makom, they add strength and power Above" (as explained at length in the maamar of my sainted father-in-law, the Rebbe, titled *Ta'ameh Ki Tov Sachrah*, 10 Shevat, 5709).

I wish to conclude this letter with the wish and blessing that it be fulfilled in you, in all of us, and within all of Klal Yisrael, that each person should carry out his shlichus in this world with joy.

With blessings for success.

Enclosed is my contribution to the gemilas chasadim fund: a check for $100 as a donation, and another check for $100 as a loan.

## 27

B"H, 28 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs,
Rabbi Yitzchak Zalman, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your *pidyon nefesh* for the 10th of Shevat, which I will, G-d willing, read at an auspicious time at the *tziyun* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

On this occasion, I would like to note a few details regarding the bulletin that I have just received. Since I am hopeful that you will be able to correct these, they are as follows:

a) There is no mention at all regarding *Machatzis Hashekel*, neither on the first page nor the second, which is particularly relevant this year, as it falls out on *Motzaei Shabbos*.

b) Regarding *Mishloach Manos*, it should be added that it must specifically consist of food items.

c) At the end of the second page, after the word "nachas," it would be good to add and emphasize "Jewish nachas."

d) On the third page, regarding those in mourning, it is appropriate to add the customary phrasing practiced among the Jewish people: "May the *Makom* comfort them among the mourners of Tzion and Yerushalayim." Aside from the necessity of this in its own right, since you are addressing mourners, one should utilize every opportunity to publicize the laws and customs of the Jewish people.

e) On the fourth page, as well as at the end of the third page, and generally wherever the names of several people are listed, one of the ways to avoid complaints and grievances regarding who is listed before whom is to arrange the names in alphabetical order. 

By the way, I noticed on the third page that you list the events that occurred in the life of the Jewish people during the days of the month. You may find the book *Dvar Yom B'Yomo*, which has been reprinted in recent years, useful for this.

I look forward to hearing good news regarding all of the above.

## 230

B"H, 1 Adar, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the Honorable Rabbi, the Honorable Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc.,
Rabbi Dovberish, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I have received the galleys of your notes on the Meiri (presumably for Maseches Mikvaos). Although time does not permit me to study them as thoroughly as they deserve—especially since I do not have the Meiri on Mikvaos and Niddah at hand—out of affection for the subject and out of respect for you, I have looked through them to the extent that time allowed. I will content myself with two observations:

1) Regarding the beginning, where you commented on the Meiri, Perek 2, Mishnah 1: On the face of it, I have a difficulty with your note. For there are generally two distinct matters regarding a mikveh: 
a) The requirement that the **tevilah** (immersion) must be such that one immerses his entire body at once. On this, everyone agrees that it is a requirement from the Torah. 
b) The matter of the **mikveh’s** measurement—whether it is fixed at 40 seah, or whether there is a distinction between a small person, a large person, and an average person. On this, there is a back-and-forth among the Rishonim and Acharonim as to whether less than 40 seah suffices for a small person, and whether more than 40 seah is required for a large person. It is obvious that for those who permit a large person to use 40 seah, this is only if he immerses his entire body at once. The measurement is a matter concerning the *mikveh*, while the requirement that his entire body be covered at once is a matter concerning the *tevilah*. Consequently, when the Meiri writes in Niddah, "If he is so large that his entire body does not 'ascend' in them, or if the water is too shallow, it is nothing," he is surely coming to inform us that even if his entire body is covered at once, it is "nothing"—and not as you, may you live, wrote.

In truth, one could say that this is the precise meaning of the Sages’ language: that his entire body **"ascends"** (*oleh*) in them, rather than "is covered" by them. For the fact that the tevilah must be at once is learned from a different verse (Toras Kohanim, Vayikra 22:10), and here the precision is on the word "ascends." Whether this is as the Chasam Sofer says—that it is nullified by the water—or whether we interpret it in another way, in any case, the intent here is not "covered." Furthermore, it is obvious that for the body to be able to be covered at once, no specific measurement is required; for if the configuration of the mikveh were designed to match the configuration of the body of the person immersing, and it were only slightly wider and longer than the body of the person immersing, it would be possible to cover the entire body in a single drop of water. It is worth noting what the Acharonim point out regarding the variation in language in this matter in Toras Kohanim, the Gemara, and the Poskim. In Toras Kohanim, the language is: "that his entire flesh 'ascends' in them, and how much are they? A cubit by a cubit by a height of three cubits" (Toras Kohanim, Vayikra 15:16). Thus you say the measurement of the mikveh is 40 seah—meaning the measurement is a cubit by a cubit by a height of three cubits. And in the Gemara (Eruvin 4b): "A cubit by a cubit by a height of three cubits, and the **Sages** measured the water of a mikveh as 40 seah." And in the Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah, beginning of Siman 201, the order is reversed: "Forty seah, and its measurement is a cubit by a cubit by a height of three cubits."

This has already been addressed in *Gulos Aliyos* on Mikvaos, Perek 1, Mishnah 7, Piska 1. See all the opinions on the aforementioned subject collected in the book *Shiur Mikveh* by Rabbi Naeh of Jerusalem, page 3 and onwards.

Furthermore, it should be noted that according to those who say that 40 seah is sufficient for a large person, the teaching that "his entire body ascends in them" is seemingly a sign, not a legal requirement. This is a subject to be elaborated upon, but this is not the place.

2) Regarding your comment [on another matter]: On the face of it, according to the Meiri, it remains difficult why he did not include a mikveh among those things listed in Perek 17 of Keilim.

Seemingly, one can answer that in the Mishnah in Keilim, those matters were brought which, even according to Rabbinic law, have no measurement—neither a maximum nor a minimum. This is not the case with a mikveh, where, in order to avoid making distinctions, they required 40 seah even for the smallest of the small.

A note at the end:
Regarding what you wanted to answer to the question of the *Shu"t Yehuda Yaaleh*—that in Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah, Siman 120, Se'if 12, it is written that one must immerse the handles of vessels generally, and at the end of Hilchos Tevilah he distinguishes the law of long handles, and you wish to say that the opinion of the Shulchan Aruch is that one must immerse the entire handle, but that *chatzitzah* (interposition) only invalidates up to the point of the measurement—in my opinion, it is impossible to say so regarding the language of the Shulchan Aruch, for he explicitly wrote: "he immerses up to the point where he intends to cut them, **and that is sufficient.**"

As you requested, the proofs are returned herewith, and again, many thanks for sending them for me to read, to the extent that time allowed.

Enclosed is a *kuntres* that was published recently, which I am sure will interest you.

With blessing for Chassidic *nachas* from your daughter, may she live.

## 231

B"H, 1 Adar, 5713
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, who engages in communal needs, R' Meir, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter from this past Monday... May Hashem grant you success in your teaching in public, and through this—that you bring the hearts of the children of Yisrael closer to their Father in Heaven—there will certainly be drawn down for you an added measure of blessing and success in your personal affairs, both in material and spiritual matters.

My opinion is already known, based on what is brought in many places in Chassidus, regarding the immense importance of *asiyah b'po'al* (actual practice). One must strive with all possible means to know the *dinim hametzuyim* (commonly applicable laws). Therefore, one who teaches in public should dedicate at least a few moments to the study of these laws, most of which are found in *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim*. By way of a clever interpretation, one might also apply to this the teaching of our Sages on the verse, "**Orach Chaim** (a path of life) lest you weigh [the paths of life]..."—do not sit and weigh the mitzvos of the Torah [deciding which are more important to study], etc. This is contrary to the common misconception that studying *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim* is only for those of a lower level, etc.

With blessings for true health, and regards to *anash*, may they live.

## B'Lamed-Gimel

B"H, 4 Adar, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Although it is not my custom to involve myself in such matters, it appears that the "leaven in the dough" has spread too far. Consequently, I am stepping out of my usual bounds in the following lines, and I am writing in Yiddish so that there will be no need to translate them from one language to another:

1) As is explained in the *sefarim*, and as is the simple faith of every Jew, Hashem—and Hashem alone—is the "One who feeds and sustains everything," whether individual people or institutions and organizations. As we say in *Birkas Hamazon*, in the first blessing that Moshe Rabbeinu instituted: "Our G-d, King of the world, who feeds the **entire** world... for He is the G-d who feeds and sustains everyone."

Just as Hashem wishes to grant Jews the merit of *mitzvos*, it often happens that Hashem tests someone and gives him money that is actually the *parnassah* of another person or an institution. Then, they look from Above to see if the person to whom the money was entrusted is trustworthy and understands that the money belongs to Hashem, and that he has merely been granted the merit of a *shlichus* to pass the money on to someone else. If it turns out that the person can be believed and trusted, then beyond the reward for the *mitzvah* of *tzedakah*—where "a person eats its fruits in this world, and the principal remains for the World to Come"—he will also maintain his position with Hashem, so that Hashem will continue to give him a *shlichus*. That is to say, he will have success in his business and the *parnassah* to support specific other people or institutions; he will be the *tzinor* (channel) through which *parnassah* flows to others.

It is self-understood that the *yetzer hara* cannot stand by and watch such a thing, and it seeks all sorts of ways to convince the person that the money he earns is not because Hashem wills it so, but because he, the person himself, is a great genius and a great merchant, and therefore, with his own power and intellect, he earns the money. And since that is the case, he is the "owner" of the money, and another person who is a "fool" and cannot earn as much money is, by definition, inferior to him—though he will do him a favor and toss him a few cents.

Therefore, the one who is the recipient must understand that he has done him a tremendous favor, and he must, *lehavdil*, "bless" him—not as in *Birkas Hamazon*, where Hashem is the Provider, but rather that his *zan u'mifarnes* is flesh and blood. And if the other person does not want to act that way, he does not want to have anything to do with him, because he is the full "owner" of the money.

To guard against such a false thought, every Jew is told to say, right at the beginning of the day, *Shehechezarta bi nishmasi b'chemlah*. It is nothing more than Hashem having mercy, and that is why He returns the *neshamah*. Also, the first request in *Shemoneh Esrei* is *Atah chonen l'adam da'as, chaneinu mei'itcha*—through which the Jew acknowledges that he himself is no genius, not a *bar seichel* and not a *bar da'as*, but that everything depends on Hashem, and one must depend on Hashem’s kindness at every time and every moment.

So, when a person is *zoche* and does not let himself be misled by the *yetzer hara*, he remains, as explained above, for long days and years, Hashem’s *shaliach* through whom money is given to private individuals as well as, in general, for matters of *Torah* and *mitzvos*.

If, *chalilah*, one is not *zoche*, it is superfluous to elaborate on the consequences, for every Jew wants to speak and write only about the good. One must, however, know the *cheshbon* well.

2) There is a further case: when someone not only does not want to become Hashem’s *shaliach* to pass on entrusted money that belongs to private individuals or matters of *Torah* and *mitzvos*, but, even more, he becomes a *shaliach* of—*lehavdil*—the *yetzer hara* to cause damage to the money.

However, since Hashem is *rachum v'chanun*, specifically in such a case there exists the concept of *teshuvah*. *Al pi pashut*, this means that if one intended to make a mistake, one should be able to correct it. And if it involves a matter connected to another person or a matter of *Torah* and *mitzvos*, the *teshuvah* must be done in time, before the damage becomes such that it can no longer be corrected.

After this introduction, I want to briefly describe what occurred here regarding the printing matter.

Information was received from a Jew that he wanted to take upon himself the expenses so that a *sefer mussar* could be printed—a *sefer* that had placed him personally on the proper path of *Torah* and *mitzvos*. Therefore, he had the *ratzon hatov* that this *sefer* should reach hundreds and perhaps thousands of other Jews, and also draw them closer to Hashem and to *Yiddishkeit*. It is a clear thing that this *ratzon hatov* comes from the *yetzer tov*, from Hashem. And when one expresses this desire in words—and certainly when one informs others—it is like **a neder** that one makes to **Hashem**. In other words, it means that one is saying to Hashem: "I acknowledge and believe that You have granted me success and given me the money, and I understand that for this and this amount of it, I am nothing more than a *shaliach* to carry out Your will and *shlichus* to make it easier for many Jews to draw closer to *Yiddishkeit*." There can be no mistake that this desire came from the *yetzer hara*.

In order for the *ratzon hatov* of the person in question to be brought into reality, the information about this desire reached people who are involved in printing such *sefarim*—that is, those who have been *zoche* to be *shluchim* to print *sefarim* that draw Jews closer to Hashem and *Yiddishkeit*, and also not with their own powers, but as written above, with Hashem’s power.

Knowing that they were dealing with *frum* Jews, and wanting to hasten the matter as much as possible, they did not wait until the money arrived. They took money that other Jews had given for other matters of *Torah* and *mitzvos*—which had been set aside—and borrowed that *tzedakah* money in order to immediately bring the *ratzon hatov* of the Jew who wanted to print the *sefer* into actual reality, so that the influence of the *sefer* could also begin as soon as possible.

Then, extraneous matters interfered, and conflicts began between the one who had ordered the printing of the *sefer* and those who had printed it, until the end result was that he regretted his *ratzon hatov*. This means two things: To Hashem, he is saying that what he had previously promised to print a *sefer mussar*, acknowledging that the money belonged to Hashem—he is now retracting it and saying, "I told You so before, and now I regret it and say the opposite; do something to me." And to the people who printed the *sefer*, he says: "I know that you had the order from me, and you borrowed *tzedakah* money for it, which you actually did on my *shlichus*, but nevertheless, I am not moved by that and will **not give over** the money, because I have a grievance against you that you 'annoyed' me."

To explain in even greater detail how both of these things are referred to in the *Torah*, I believe is unnecessary. May Hashem only help **all** who are involved in this to correct it before the damage becomes such that, *chalilah*, it can no longer be corrected.

And now, all of the above is regarding... *shlita*, and even more than what is written here is understood according to what is explained in *Chassidus*, the words of the living G-d, regarding matters such as these. And regarding *k'vod toraso shlita* himself, it is known from the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov that everything is by *hashgacha pratis*, even the details of the details, and that in this entire matter, *k'vod toraso* was one of the intermediaries, and apparently the primary intermediary. And it is explained in the teachings of *Chassidus* that there are two types of intermediaries: an "intermediary that connects," meaning he is not an entity unto himself and understands his role is to connect two things so that they become one; and an "intermediary that separates," meaning he is an entity unto himself, and consequently, when the matter of the *shlichus* comes to him, he translates the matter into his own "letters," and consequently, he mixes his own existence into it. And since *tzaddikim* are few, and the majority of the world are in the category of *beinonim*—whom both [the *yetzer tov* and *yetzer hara*] judge—the *yetzer hara* also states its opinion. The task of a person is to nullify the opinion of the *yetzer hara* immediately, as explained in *Tanya*. And the same applies to him, that he was *zoche* that the *Kadosh Baruch Hu* chose him to be an intermediary through whom he would give from his money for the printing of a *sefer mussar*...

With blessings for proper health in physicality and proper health in spirituality, that Hashem should give him the desire to carry out Hashem’s will, through which all of the above will be resolved for the good as soon as possible.

## 234

234

By the Grace of G-d
5 Adar, 5713
Brooklyn

To the G-d-fearing, distinguished, and esteemed individual, involved in communal affairs, R. Boruch, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I have received your letter from the 3rd of Yisro, a response to my letter to you. I am interested to know whether you have received a response to your telegraphic and written inquiry to the Jewish Appeal, and what the content of their response is.

One must know, however, that when one wishes to help our Holy Land, one must do so by strengthening the matters of Torah and mitzvos there. For one cannot outsmart the Ribono shel Olam, and if He—blessed be He—has exiled us from our land, it is not because that is what the Romans and Vespasian wanted, but rather because "due to our sins we were exiled from our land." Eretz Yisrael is a land, as it is written in our holy Torah (end of Parshas Acharei), that cannot tolerate sins. Therefore, anyone who truly wishes to help and desires the true good of our Holy Land, and the good of the Yidden who are there, must first and foremost safeguard this detail. One must not be persuaded that there are more important things, or at the very least, things of equal importance. In the maintenance of a house and its existence, the first thing is a healthy foundation; if, Heaven forbid, the foundation is not good or properly suited, then the larger the building, not only does it bring no benefit, but it is the exact opposite, Heaven forbid. Since regarding Eretz Yisrael one should not speak empty words, unless it pertains to the practical implementation of a matter, it is difficult for me to elaborate on this. Especially since I am certain that for you, this brief summary will suffice.

You write in your letter regarding the electric saw for Kfar Chabad that you are to send, but that the freight must be paid. I would like to know approximately what the sum is that the freight will cost, and also whether a permit (license) is required to import the saw into Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established.

I wish you a happy Purim, and until Purim you should also utilize the time to strengthen the matters of Torah and mitzvos, for which there is never too much. And when one desires it in truth, Hashem Yisbarach grants success so that one performs mitzvos joyfully and in a joyful manner.

With Purim blessings.

## 235

B"H, 7 Adar, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your *pidyon nefesh* from Erev Shabbos, 28 Shevat. When I am at the *tziyun* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will read it, as well as the *pidyon nefesh* you wrote on behalf of your father-in-law and mother-in-law, may they live and be well.

It is surprising that you do not mention anything regarding your good works at Yeshivas Oholei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch. This is especially relevant in light of what is brought in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Epistle 7, and in *Sefer HaSichos* Summer 5700, page 22, that every soul has a specific *mitzvah* that serves as a gateway through which all of one’s *mitzvos* and good deeds ascend, and through which influences are drawn down from above to below. Since you have merited that your *mitzvah* is in the "tent of Torah"—in an institution founded and conducted in the name and spirit of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe—then every request and *pidyon nefesh* is connected to your activities in this institution. May Hashem grant you the merit to succeed and to share good news regarding all of the above.

With blessings for a *Purim Sameach*.

## 236

B"H, 7 Adar, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, engaged in communal needs, R' Yosef, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 3 Mishpatim, in which you inform me that, thank G-d, you are seeing success in your work with your students, may they live—may it be the will of Hashem that you be granted additional strength and fortitude in this. As the Sages have ruled, one must always ascend in matters of holiness; you should not be satisfied in the slightest with the current situation. Aside from the fact that every matter of Torah and mitzvos is "longer than the earth and broader than the sea," it is also understood through human logic: since this is the Torah and the mitzvos of the Ribono shel Olam, the true Ein Sof.

Regarding your observation that in many places it is explained that the body is too small to contain the essence of the neshamah, while in another place it is explained that there is no change in the light of the neshamah from childhood to adulthood, and that the nefesh of an infant could animate the body of Og, King of Bashan:

This is not a contradiction. As is explained in the maamar "Ki Imcha Mekor Chaim" (5700), the light itself does not undergo change; however, when we speak of the **enclothement of the essence**, the body is indeed unable to contain it.

## 237

B"H, 8 Adar, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 3 Adar, which put my mind at ease after I had heard that you were not in the best of health upon your return from here to your city... and as is apparent from your letter, thank G-d, you have already returned to your strength (*le'eitno*).

In a playful vein, one could interpret *le'eitno* based on the Sages' teaching as *letna'o*—referring to the condition (*tenai*) that Hashem stipulated: that the Jewish people would observe the Torah and mitzvos, and in turn, the heavens and the earth would be sustained. It is well known, as explained in works of *mussar* and Chassidus, that "the heavens" encompass all spiritual matters, while "the earth" encompasses all physical matters. For a Jewish man and woman, the endurance of these matters depends upon the fulfillment of Torah and mitzvos, which are the channels and vessels for all their affairs, as it is written: "If you walk in My statutes... then I will give..."

I was pleased to read at the conclusion of your letter that this past Sunday there was to be a meeting of the *Nshei U'Bnos Chabad*. I am certain it was successful and in a manner that further increased their desire to strengthen their *avodah* for the days to come, especially in the month of Adar, where from the very beginning of the month we "increase in joy" due to the festival of Purim. And although our Sages said regarding Chanukah and Pesach that "they too were part of the miracle," the participation of women is most highlighted during the days of Purim.

To conclude with words of Torah regarding what you began in your letter—the matter of greeting one's teacher, where you also noted *Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah*, section 242, paragraph 16—please examine the commentaries on the *Shulchan Aruch*. It is known that this is also one of the differences between the inhabitants of Eretz Yisrael and the inhabitants of Bavel, as brought in the book *Chilufei Minhagim*. Since the book may not be readily available, I am transcribing the references: *Berachos* 27b; *Nazir* 20b (see there the difference in the versions of the *Rif* and the *Rosh*); and *Maadanei Yom Tov* there; *Bava Kamma* 73b and *Tosafos* and *Yefeh Einayim* there; *Shevuos* 32a (see there); and the *Yerushalmi* to *Berachos* and *Nazir* in those places.

#### ***237***

A portion was printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 23, p. 358, and it was completed according to the secretariat's copy.

**Nshei U'Bnos Chabad:** See above, letter 1869, and the references in the notes there.

## 238

238

B"H, 8 Adar, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote about your son... *sheyichyeh*, concerning his trip here: Surely you are aware of my perspective on this. In these times, there is an extremely vast field for activity in Eretz Yisrael *tiv*, including among the youth; they can utilize their strengths in this direction. Specifically regarding your son, the Yeshiva in Lod must be transformed into a Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch Yeshiva. For the time being... those who have come from there and have been here for some time, a lack of discipline and responsibility is felt. I do not know the clear reason for this. This applies especially to the students coming from Eretz Yisrael *tiv*, as I have told them: leaving Eretz Yisrael *tiv* was permitted only under certain conditions, and for them, it is for the purpose of studying Torah. Consequently, when they come here and conduct themselves according to their own desires, it requires study and clarification whether this is the permission that our Sages of blessed memory intended, etc. This is not the place to elaborate, as in truth this should be written to the administration of the Lod Yeshiva. However, I have shared this observation with you regarding your son, Mr.... *sheyichyeh*, and therefore my opinion is that, at the very least, he should spend this winter and the coming summer days in Lod. In the middle of the summer, I will surely receive an opinion about him from the Yeshiva administration, and we will consult on this once again.

With blessings for Chassidic *nachas* from all your descendants, and that he and his wife *shichyu* may receive *nachas* in good health, both physically and spiritually.

## 339

B"H, 8 Adar, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished and eminent Rabbi, a man of stature, a scion of noble lineage, a man of great deeds, G-d-fearing, one who contemplates good, etc.,
Rabbi Dovid Sasson, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

I received your esteemed letter of 13 Shevat with pleasure, containing three photographs of three ancient manuscripts. From these, the authenticity of the ruling of the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, to write the word **dacha** (in the verse "He whose stones are crushed [dacha] shall not enter") with an *alef*, is evident.

Surely, your honor is aware of the multitude of opinions expressed on this matter, all of which have been gathered in the book *Mishnas Avraham*.

It is worth noting what I heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: when he was in the city of Worms, he saw there the Sefer Torah that they had received, which was written by the Maharam of Rothenburg, of blessed memory, and the word *dacha* was written there with an *alef*. He also saw the same in a Sefer Torah in Prague, which, according to their tradition passed down from generation to generation, was corrected by Ezra the Scribe.

As a token of appreciation, I am sending your honor, in a separate package, the *Sdei Chemed* for the Sephardic *Chachamim*.

With respect and blessings.

## B.M.

B.H., 8 Adar, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, occupied with communal needs,
Rabbi Ephraim Eliezer, may he live, HaKohen

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter from the beginning of the month of Adar with pleasure. Regarding what you noted concerning the angel appointed over pregnancy—that the Gemara states his name is Lailah, and that in the name of the Maggid of Kozhnitz it is suggested this is a name of Hashem—you explain that this is according to the opinion of Tosafos HaRosh in Niddah 16b, that Hashem grants the woman pregnancy, and subsequently the angel attends to it.

Seemingly, if one wishes to distinguish and explain that the name of Hashem is not an angel but refers to Hashem Himself, without being enclothed in an angel, then even according to Tosafos one could say so. For it is obvious that every single thing comes from Hashem, and consequently, it has a connection to a certain name, even if it is subsequently handed over to an angel.

Regarding what you wrote in your letter concerning the farbrengen on the upcoming festival of Purim: as is customary, the farbrengen will begin in the shul after the eighth hour of the evening. It is understood that according to the ruling of our Sages and their exposition on the verse "the Mishkan according to its law," that which is in the south shall be placed in the south (Yerushalmi Shabbos, Chapter 12, Halacha 3).

With respect and with wishes for a happy Purim.

***

**It is understood... in the south:** Meaning that they should seat him at the main table in the south of the shul, near the Rebbe, may he live.

The great necessity for this requires no explanation; after all, this is the whole of man: "Fear G-d and keep His mitzvos."

With blessings for success and for positive influence in your community and your surroundings.

B”H, 19th of Adar, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, engaged in communal needs,

7) I was pleased to hear what you wrote regarding the improvement in your state of health. This should be understood as follows: Since you see an improvement in your health, this is a clear indication that there was no [underlying] issue there, but rather that it was intended to remind you not to rely on your own intellect and calculations, but to surrender yourself to holiness. This is in accordance with the instruction of the Baal Shem Tov, as explained by the Nesi’ei Chabad: The path is not to detach oneself from physicality, but rather to serve Hashem *within* physicality. This is like the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov on the verse, “If you see the donkey of one who hates you crouching under its burden...” [Shemos 23:5], which was also brought in the *maamar* *Basi LeGani* of this year. You will surely find the appropriate terminology there to explain this.

With blessings for success in your holy work, which will also bring about an increase in blessing and success in your personal matters.

## 246

B"H, 12 Adar, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who conducts his business with integrity,
Rabbi Yaakov HaKohen, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

... I conclude with a wish for a *Purim sameach*, and [that we reach the level of] "until one does not know the difference between 'cursed be Haman' and 'blessed be Mordechai.'" This means that the primary focus should be on what is essential, not on the matter of "cursed" and "blessed," but rather to be bound with the *Ilana D'Chayei* (Tree of Life), which connects one to the *Atzmus* of *Ein Sof* B"H, which is higher than "cursed" and "blessed." For this is *Etzem HaTov* (the Essence of Good), as is known from the statement in the *Zohar*: "There is no left side in this *Atik*; all is right." The strength for this has been given to every Jew, so that he may be able to say, "This, too, is for the good," and when one says this with truth, it truly becomes so.

With blessings for proper health for him and for all his household, may they live.

## 249

B"H, 12 Adar, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your notification regarding the engagement of your daughter, may she live and be well: May Hashem grant that it be in a good and auspicious hour, and may it be an everlasting edifice built upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, as they are illuminated by the "light of Torah"—which is the teachings of Chassidus.

It is well known that the path of holiness is one of "slowly, slowly." Consequently, one must find appropriate ways to draw the groom—may he live and be well—closer to the teachings of Chassidus, its ways, and its conduct. This is especially true in light of the Sages' teaching that a son-in-law is like a son. It is well known that the mitzvah of the education of a son is incumbent upon the father, particularly the mitzvah of Torah education, which is a Torah-mandated obligation upon the father, as ruled by our Rebbe in the beginning of the Laws of Torah Study and in several other places. It is simple that the study of the teachings of Chassidus is included in this.

With blessings for a mazal tov.

## B'N

B'N
B"H, 12 Adar, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and refined, etc.,
R' Schneur Zalman, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

I was very pleased to receive your letter of 9 Adar, written in your own hand. According to the words of our Sages (Megillah 16a), "when they ascend, they ascend to the stars," so surely your own state of health will also go from strength to strength. Thank you for the good news regarding this. It is known that the custom of our Rebbes is that this serves as a directive for daily life—that their blessings are expressed in both physical and spiritual terms. That is, they connect and prioritize the physical to the spiritual. If so, the improvement of health in the physical sense is a necessity, as it immediately causes an improvement in health in the spiritual sense. This is especially true since, in and of itself, it is a matter of **avodah**, as per the ruling of the Rambam in Hilchos Deios, Chapter 4, that maintaining a healthy body is one of the ways of Hashem.

As you approach your birthday on 18 Adar, may it be the will of Hashem that you have long life and years, in accordance with the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the name of his father, the Rebbe (Rashab): "Good things," with all the interpretations that implies. Regarding the inquiry about your wife through her husband, please convey my regards to your wife, may she live. May you both have long lives and years together, in goodness and pleasantness, both physically and spiritually.

With blessings.

## B'na

B'na

B"H, 12 Adar, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I have just received your letter from the 8th of Adar, in which you write regarding a shidduch that you see as being impossible according to the natural order. This is not news, for it has already been said that "it is as difficult to pair them as the splitting of the Yam Suf." It is well known how great the miracle of the splitting of the Yam Suf was, yet it is the way of the world that one finds a shidduch, gets married, and builds an everlasting edifice. The same will be true for you as well. You simply need to divert your mind from all the difficulties that exist in this matter, and you must reach a firm resolution that this is a mitzvah among the mitzvos of the Torah. Since Hakadosh Baruch Hu does not deal tyrannically with His creations, once Hakadosh Baruch Hu demands that one fulfill this mitzvah, He will, for His part, pair you up at the appropriate time.

However, just as all things must have a foothold in nature—as our Sages of blessed memory said, "it is the way of a man to pursue a woman"—in order to hasten this, you should take upon yourself—without a neder—to give a coin to tzedakah every day before davening in the morning. And, it goes without saying, you should keep the three daily shiurim instituted by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—in Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya, as is well known.

With blessings, awaiting good news regarding the above.

## 252

B"H, 12 Adar, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Your letter from Erev Shabbos Terumah has just been received. In it, you write regarding a misunderstanding of my intent concerning the examinations. It is obvious that I have no intention whatsoever to diminish the stature of anyone. However, since it is the desire of us all to maintain a connection with one another—and the connection of a Yid, like all matters, is dependent upon Torah and mitzvos, and for those within the walls of a yeshiva, this is primarily along the line of Torah—therefore, I wish to know as clearly as possible the standing of each individual, both in Nigleh and in Chassidus. As I have stated from the outset, this information is for my own knowledge only.

It is obvious that for those who turn to me from time to time in their letters, there is no place to describe their situation—about which they are inquiring—in a way that does not correspond to reality. Furthermore, if that were the case, my response would not always be appropriate to what I intend to answer, as is well known from the adage common among Chassidim: "As one asks, so one is answered." As a preface to all matters that you bring before me, both in the present and in the future: for those whom Hashem has merited to place in this "corner of light," which is Torah, it is appropriate, based on the above, that I know the status of the inquirer regarding their knowledge in Nigleh and in Chassidus. It is understood that this information, too, must correspond to the truth.

With blessings for a happy Purim, and may it be that "the Jews fulfilled and accepted," etc., as our Sages of blessed memory explain regarding this verse.

## 554

554

By the grace of Hashem, 15 Adar, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the learned Rabbi, the distinguished scholar, who occupies himself with the study of Torah and the service of Hashem, etc., Moreinu Harav Yitzchak, may he live.

Shalom u’vrachah!

In response to your letter of 9 Adar regarding your observation on the *Biurei HaZohar*, *Parshas Vayechi*, page 30a, where you ask how it is possible for an influence to come from *Sefiras HaYesod* without passing through *Sefiras HaMalchus*:

While you are correct that it is a necessity that all influences in the worlds must come through *Sefiras HaMalchus*, there is a distinction to be made as to whether this occurs through "enclothement" (*hitlabshut*) or merely by way of passage. If it occurs through enclothement, it is named after the garment (the *Malchus*). This matter is explained in *Tanya*, *Kunteres Acharon*, page 158a, and in the *Hemshech* of 566 (which I believe you have), in the *maamar* beginning "Koh... my covenant day and night," as well as in many other places in *Chassidus*.

Thank you for your note regarding the explanation in *Biurei HaZohar* concerning the distinction between *hirhur* (thought/reflection) and *machshavah* (thought/contemplation), in light of what is written in the *Chiddushei HaRashba* on *Berachos* 15a, that "with *hirhur*, the concept of 'language' does not apply." If we interpret the words of the *Rashba* according to their simple meaning—that "language" does not apply because one is contemplating the concepts but not the letters—then a difficulty arises: How does the *Gemara* conclude that even in such a case, *hirhur* is considered as speech? For one must necessarily know from the text *Shema* that there are two requirements: that one must make it audible to one’s own ears, and that it may be said in any language. Perhaps one might force an interpretation of the *Rashba* to mean that the *sanctity* of language and its superior status do not apply—in which case it would align with the words of the *Biurei HaZohar*. I have now seen in the *Tzlach* (15a, 4) the following: "See the *Chiddushei HaRashba* who writes that if one fulfills the obligation with the intention of the heart, it is self-evident that one fulfills it in any language, **for the intention is the essence.**" This was gratifying to me.

With respect and blessing.

**Note:**
a) The words of the *Biurei HaZohar* are based on what is written in the *Likkutei Torah* of the Arizal, *Bereishis*, in the *maamar* beginning "Lama Hitchilah," that *machshavah*, *hirhur*, *dibbur*, and *maaseh* correspond to *Atzilus*, *Beriah*, *Yetzirah*, and *Asiyah*. It is known that the reason for the name *Beriah* is "something from nothing" (*me'ayin l'yesh*), as per the commentary of the Ramban on the Torah at the beginning, and the beginning of the existence of the *keilim* (vessels) is in *Beriah*.

It is explained in many places that "letters" and "vessels" are one and the same. Seemingly, this warrants study, given what is written in the *Zohar Chadash* (Vol. 3, 229, bottom of page) that *hirhur* and *machshavah* are *Chochmah* and *Binah*—which is the opposite of all the above—(this is also cited in *Pardes*, *Shaar Archei HaKinuyim*, entry *Machshavah*), and I have not yet found anyone who notes this. Seemingly, one could say that there is a *hirhur* that is above *machshavah* and a *hirhur* that is below *machshavah*. For *hirhur* in its general sense is a light thing that lacks substance, and *hirhur* below *machshavah* is light relative to speech, while *hirhur* above *machshavah* is light relative to *machshavah*. This can be connected with what follows:

b) It is understood and simple that although in many places *hirhur* excludes *machshavah*, in many other places it includes *machshavah*, even the most subtle *machshavah*. This is found in many synonymous terms; even though there is a distinction between them in many places—especially when both appear together—it is common that where only one term is used, it includes the second, third, etc. For example, one can cite the words of our Sages, "The *hirhurim*... are more difficult than the sin itself." This also refers to a case where it is still a very subtle *machshavah* that has not been drawn down into letters, and perhaps even higher than that—as is understood from what is written in *Rabbeinu Bachya* on the Torah, *Parshas Nitzavim* 29:18, in the *maamar* beginning "And if a questioner asks." See also *Sefer Moreh Nevuchim*, Chapter 2 (this is in the *Bachya* print; it appears it should be: Part 3, Chapter 8). Similarly, this is also in *Tanya*, Chapter 12: "Rather, **immediately** upon its ascent, etc."

c) Seemingly, based on the distinction between *hirhur* and *machshavah*, one can explain the *Gemara* in *Kerisus* 19b regarding the distinction between *kavanah* (intention) and *machshavah*, for seemingly, since he forgot, what difference does it make that his intention was from before the time of the action, etc.?

Therefore, it must be that even at the time of the action, the *kavanah* exists, even if he is thinking in a different manner. Based on the above, one could say that one is *hirhur* and the other is *machshavah* (and the term *machshavah* is used in the sense of *garev* in *Bechoros* 41a). I will not elaborate further here.

Enclosed is the *Kunteres* that I suggested be studied during the past Purim days.

## 255

B"H, 22 Adar, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Your *pidyon nefesh* was received in due time and was read at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

I am writing regarding the current situation. Based on reports received from... and from those traveling here, it appears that your physical health is not being attended to at all. Naturally, this cannot help but affect your spiritual health as well. As is well known from the statement of the Maggid to his son, R' Avraham HaMalach: "A small hole in the body causes a large hole in the soul." This is also a ruling in *nigleh*, as the Rambam writes in *Hilchos Deios*, beginning of Chapter 4, that maintaining a healthy and sound body is one of the ways of Hashem. It is a pity to spend time debating such a simple matter. Therefore, if you will listen to my voice, you will simply and literally look after your health regarding eating, drinking, sleeping, etc., through which it will be better for you in spiritual matters as well. The statement of the Baal Shem Tov on the verse, "If you see the donkey of your enemy... you shall surely help **with him**," is already well known.

I am certain you will confirm receipt of this letter and inform me of your intentions regarding all of the above. Please also inform me of your positive activities in the yeshiva specifically, and in Chabad matters in general.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach for you and your entire household, may they be well.

## 256

B"H, 24 Adar, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Your letter from the conclusion of Shabbos, Parshas Tisa, has just been received; your previous letter was also received in due time.

I was alarmed by what you wrote regarding yourself. I have already recounted several times what I heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, who told me that someone once entered his room for yechidus and asked for a tikkun for certain matters. While doing so, he described his spiritual state in alarming terms. My father-in-law, the Rebbe, replied that the severity of the matter of lashon hara is well known—that it is forbidden to speak it about one's fellow, and likewise about oneself; and to the wise, a word is sufficient.

In my humble opinion, one can add an explanation to this based on what is known in several places regarding the distinction between lashon hara and motzi shem ra.

Motzi shem ra involves lying, whereas lashon hara applies even when one is speaking the truth. See the commentary of the Rambam on the Mishnah, end of Chapter 1 of Avos; Hilchos Deos 7:2. Nevertheless, the prohibition is severe, based on what is explained in Chassidus: when one describes a deficiency of one's fellow—or even of oneself—one often draws and reveals that deficiency from the world of thought into the world of speech. It is understood that as long as it remains in thought, it does not produce an effect, whereas when it comes into speech, it causes damage. This is as our Sages, of blessed memory, describe the "three-fold tongue" (lashon hara), and all the more so in your case, as you have also committed this to writing, which is an act.

May Hashem grant you success in resolving to hold fast to the path of "do good"—that is, by drawing light into your soul and into your portion of the world through increased courage in Torah and mitzvos, and in the light of Torah, which is the Torah of Chassidus. If a little light pushes away much darkness, then how much more so does a great deal of light.

It is known that, by nature, one whose profession is a butcher is from the line of Gevuros, as our Sages, of blessed memory, state (Shabbos 156a). It is possible that this is also the reason for what you write about yourself in your letter. Yet, the ultimate purpose of avodah is to transform one's natural character traits, and as you occupy yourself with this, you will surely succeed.

The Purim money you sent for yourself and for your family, may they live, has been delivered for its intended purpose. Although one may perform a merit for another in his absence, nevertheless, because of the aspect of chinuch involved (see Kiddushin 30a, that chinuch applies until the age of twenty-four), it is appropriate that your son... may he live, should personally give a few coins to the aforementioned collection, in addition to what you gave on his behalf...

Enclosed is the Kuntres that was recently published, and surely you will merit to bring merit to the many through its contents.

With blessings for a kosher and joyous Festival of Matzos.

## 257

B"H, 24 Adar, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you inform me that you are studying *sofrus* (scribal arts) and are in Yeshivas Toras Emes, and you ask for my opinion on what to do to succeed in your endeavors:

It is well known what is written in our holy Torah: "If you walk in My statutes and keep My commandments..." and "the land will yield its produce..." Rashi explains "If you walk in My statutes" to mean that you should be *ameil* (toil) in Torah. If so, the path is clear: since Hashem has merited to place you in this "corner of light"—which is Torah—you must be *ameil* in Torah. This means toiling beyond your usual habit and nature, which is why it is called *amal* (toil). Even if you are studying *sofrus*—as you write in your letter—there is certainly enough free time remaining to be *ameil* in Torah, and surely the Ribono shel Olam will fulfill His promise, "I will give your rains in their time..."

It is understood that this is an essential matter, especially for those who have merited to study in a yeshiva founded and directed by our Nesi'im, the *tzaddikei yesodei olam*, the Rebbe (Rashab) and my father-in-law, the Rebbe—*ztzukulleh"h nebag"m zya*. It is imperative that you study their Torah—this is the Torah of Chassidus, the words of the living Elokus. Through this, one connects with an added connection to the *ilana d'chayei* (tree of life), and consequently, an added measure of blessing and success is drawn down for him in *chayei olam*, which also refers to life in this physical world.

With blessings for Torah study with *yiras shamayim* and for success in your affairs, and to celebrate the festival of Pesach with *kashrus* and joy.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

**The Secretary**

## 257*

B"H, 24 Adar, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter from Shushan Purim, in which you write that you caught a cold in both senses of the word, and consequently did not participate in the farbrengen (a Chassidic gathering which radiates Chassidic light and warmth to those who attend). Surely you understand on your own that despite what you wrote, the more the cold increases on the outside—that is, in the *nefesh habehamis*—the more one must increase the warmth from within—that is, in the *nefesh elokis*. Fleeing from a farbrengen is not a piece of advice, not even as a joke.

I was sorry to hear that your children, *shichye*, are not in the best of health as they should be. It is my hope that by the time you receive this letter, their health will have already improved, and you will share good news in this regard. May the *Ribono shel Olam* fulfill the days of your wife’s, *tichye*, pregnancy properly and with ease, and may she give birth to a healthy child properly and with ease. May you all celebrate the upcoming *Chag HaPesach* together in holiness and joy. It is unnecessary to elaborate that even regarding joy there are two modes. As is known, the custom of the *olam* is to be stringent in accordance with the opinion that increases the concern regarding dancing and clapping on *Shabbos* and *Yom Tov*. Consequently, this is done with a change—that is, with the backs of the hands against one another rather than the palms—and they drink cups of milk, which induces sleep (*Shoftim 5:25*). It is understood that all of this causes a cooling effect, *v'd'l*. May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant you the merit to reveal fully that which was sown and planted in you during your time as a student in the *Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim*, and of which fruits have already been seen—except that a love for witticisms sometimes conceals it. When you experience a falling of spirit because of this, instead of being stirred to additional courage in the battle against the body and the *nefesh habehamis*, you wave your hand and explain to yourself that you lack *chayus*, and so on and so forth. Since, ultimately, you will surely emerge from the straits to freedom—that it should be a matter of true freedom—remember the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe: "Chassidim are clever and do not put off until tomorrow that which can be done today."

With blessings for success in your holy work and for Chassidic *nachas* from yourself and your family, *shichyu*.

P.S. Enclosed is the *Kuntres* for the upcoming 2 Bais Nissan, with which I am sure you will merit to benefit the many.

#### ***257\****

**Note:** See also above, Letter 1882, and the references in the footnotes there.

## B'nach

B'H, 24 Adar, 5713
Brooklyn.

...It is surprising that you do not mention anything regarding the farbrengen which you surely held on the yahrtzeit of Yud Shevat that just passed, and on the recent holiday of Purim, and which you will likewise hold on the upcoming Beis Nissan. It is already well-known that in a letter from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, he writes regarding a response from the Rebbe (Maharash), of blessed memory, to one of his Chassidim who lived outside the Pale of Settlement and, consequently, lacked a Chassidic environment. The Rebbe told him that he must know he was not exiled to a distant place for the sake of his material livelihood, but rather that Hashem sent him there to bring life—to illuminate the surroundings with the light of holiness. How much more so is this true for you, may you live, who are in a city where there are several G-d-fearing and observant people who have not yet merited to benefit from the "light of Torah"—this being the Torah of Chassidus, its ways, and its customs. You must strive in this with added courage and strength. It is possible that when you fulfill this role, Hashem will provide you with a good opportunity to move to New York, in accordance with your long-standing desire.

With blessings for proper health and to celebrate the upcoming holiday of Pesach with kashrus and joy.

Enclosed is the Kuntres that was recently published, and surely you will merit to use its contents to benefit the many.

## 2072

B"H, 25 Adar, 5713
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, and diligent worker in communal affairs, etc.,
Rabbi Shmuel, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter of 21 Adar, in which you write that you and your wife, the Rabbanit, may they live, have already set the date for your journey to ascend to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, for Thursday, 24 Nissan, the coming year, by ship to Paris and from there by plane to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established.

In accordance with what we discussed when you were here, may it be the will of Hashem that the journey proceed properly, that your arrival there be successful, and that your return to your place at the appointed time be in a good and auspicious hour. It is surely unnecessary to repeat once more what we discussed: since Eretz Yisrael is a land upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year until the end of the year, just as one who prepares to enter the palace of a mortal king changes and beautifies his garments as much as possible, how much more so must this be the case regarding one's spiritual garments before ascending to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. A person’s garments are explained at length in Tanya as being his thoughts, speech, and actions, which are the garments of the neshamah. Consequently, one must add improvement and beauty to them every day. At the very least, and naturally without a vow, one should give a few coins to tzedakah each weekday before morning davening and set an additional shiur in Pnimiyus HaTorah—which is the Torah of Chassidus, referred to in the Zohar as the "Tree of **Life**" (Zohar Vol. III, p. 124b; explained in Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 26; and it is understood that this is especially appropriate for Eretz Yisrael, which is called the "Land of the **Living**"). Consequently, it is proper to contemplate for a few moments each day before davening on matters that lead to the love and awe of Hashem, which are found in abundance in the sefarim of Chassidus and maamarim...

Enclosed is the Kuntres published for 2 Nissan, the coming year; surely you will merit to share its contents with the many.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach, and regards to your son—who visited me together with you—may he live.

## 261

B"H, 28 Adar, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned man, who conducts his business with integrity and is involved in communal needs, etc., R' Yaakov, may he live, HaKohen.

Peace and blessing!

Enclosed is the kuntres that was printed for 2 Nissan, which has just been brought from the binder. I wish you a happy Shabbos Mevarchim, especially this Shabbos, which is also Parshas HaChodesh, where we begin to speak of the Geulah; may the Ribono shel Olam grant that we merit the complete and true Geulah. Surely, in accordance with the takanah of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, you will hold a farbrengen this Shabbos, and may Hashem grant that it be successful, both materially and spiritually.

Regarding your inquiry concerning the concept of the 85 nitzotzos (sparks), this is explained, albeit briefly, in Torah Or, Parshas Vayeishev, the maamar beginning "And behold, we were binding sheaves," Chapter 2. In general, the world was created from Divine forces, which are collectively divided into 288 nitzotzos, where each nitzotz is a general category that is further subdivided into many parts. From these, all things in the world were made—that is, the inanimate, the vegetative, the animate, the speaking, as well as matters of eating, drinking, clothing, etc. These must be "clarified" (mevarer)—meaning, the sparks must be extracted from the matters that conceal and hide them, which is accomplished by Yidden. During the exile in Mitzrayim, Yidden clarified 202 nitzotzos, as in the verse "And also a mixed multitude (**rav**) went up with them," and there remained to be clarified in the subsequent exiles the remaining 85 nitzotzos, which is the gematria of Elokim.

With blessing.

## 252

252

B"H, 3 Nissan, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, and distinguished,
Rabbi Moshe Yehuda, may he live, HaKohen

Greetings and blessings!

In anticipation of the festival of Pesach, which approaches us and all of Israel for good, I hereby wish you and your entire household, may they live, that you celebrate it in purity and joy, with true freedom—as our Sages of blessed memory taught, "freedom from the yetzer hara." Consequently, this will also be freedom from worries, both in spiritual and material matters. This is as explained in the Rambam, that this is the essence of the days of Moshiach; see there, Hilchos Teshuvah, end of chapter 9, and the end of Hilchos Melachim. It is well known that the Exodus from Egypt [the essence of which is awakened once again, specifically during the days of the festival of Pesach each and every year, as brought in the name of the Arizal in the sefer Lev Dovid by the Chida, that this is the interpretation of "and these days are remembered" (and then they) "are performed"], and the Exodus from Egypt is a preparation for the time of the coming of Moshiach, as it is written, "As in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt, I will show him wonders" [and see also in the Mishnah, end of chapter 3 of Gittin, "they examine the wine," etc., and in the publication Smadar, etc.].

With holiday blessings.

263

B"H, 3 Nissan, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, G-d-fearing and upright, engaged in communal needs,
Rabbi Mordechai HaKohen, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 19 Adar—which was received with a slight delay—regarding your question about the mikveh and whether it may be rendered kosher using artificial ice. It is known that there is a debate among the Acharonim on this matter, and many permit it (Shach to Shulchan Aruch, section 31; Tiferes Yisrael; Divrei Malkiel; Achi Ezer, Vol. 2; Poras Yosef. Conversely, see Yad Dovid, R. M. Epstein, and Darchei Teshuvah, subsection 147). Nevertheless, it is difficult for me to definitively rule on a matter of halacha, especially regarding a mikveh, where the custom is to fulfill the requirements of as many opinions as possible. Furthermore, you mentioned in your inquiry that the Sephardic Rabbi stated simply that it is forbidden; if so, it would cause confusion if I were to permit it. Since the other mikveh in your camp surely still exists, it should be repaired as much as possible and utilized. Surely the Ribono shel Olam will have mercy, and rain will descend from the heavens to saturate the earth.

As we approach the festival of Pesach, which is coming upon us and all of Yisrael for good, I hereby wish you and your entire family, may they live, that you celebrate it with kashrus and joy, in a state of true freedom. Enclosed is what I wrote to someone regarding this, which is included in a general letter.

It occurred to me that perhaps there is still something lacking in your mikveh, and that is what is delaying the rains. It is worthwhile to check all of its matters once again.

With holiday blessings.

## B's"d

[3 Nissan 5713]

Greetings and blessings!

... Soon we will all celebrate the Chag HaMatzos, the season of our freedom. A true freedom, according to the statement of our Sages, is freedom from the yetzer hara, which consequently brings about freedom in gashmius as well. In other words, this is what we ask of Hashem and hope that Hashem will fulfill our request: that the yetzer hara be removed from everyone, and that He grant blessing and success in all matters, both in gashmius and in ruchnius. Consequently, one will be free from worries of parnassah and health, and will be able to serve Hashem Yisbarach with peace of mind for long days and years. May Hashem grant you the merit to be able to report good news regarding all of the above.

#### ***B's"d***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 17, p. 453.

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 19, p. 543, and completed based on the secretariat’s copy.

**More or less:** And appropriate to the strength and depth required in the feeling and state of mind that come through memory—is the manner in which the memory is required, whether only in the heart (in thought) or also through speech and action. Regarding several opinions on this, there is also a debate regarding the obligation to remember the Exodus from Egypt throughout the year, where thought alone is sufficient, as opposed to the night of Pesach (see *Shaagas Aryeh*, end of section 13; *Minchas Chinuch*, section 21; *Sdei Chemed*, *Klallim* 7, 13; and this is not the place to elaborate).

**And a spirit.. a spirit:** *Zohar*, Vol. II, 162b; *Torah Or*, 38d; *Ohr HaTorah* [Chanukah], 286a.

**And as our Sages, of blessed memory, said:** *Remaz* in *Sefer Tikkun Shovavim*, cited in *Sefer Lev Dovid*, ch. 20. And the time itself is inherently auspicious for this, as elaborated upon in *Lev Dovid* there. Also known is the proof from the *Mishnah*, end of ch. 3 of *Gittin*: "They examine the wine..." and "at the emergence of the *semadar*..."

**To see himself.. from the imprisonment of the body:** *Rambam*, *Hilchos Chametz U’Matzah*, ch. 7, law 6; *Tanya*, ch. 45.

**Freedom.. from suffering:** *Zohar*, Vol. II, 114a; *Eruvin* 54a; *Shemos Rabbah*, ch. 41, 7.

**With the help of the Holy One, blessed be He.. engagement in Torah:** *Sukkah* 52b; *Tanya*, ch. 46; *Kiddushin* 30b.

## 257

B"H, 11 Nissan, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessings!

The days of the Festival of Matzos, the remembrance of our exodus from the land of Egypt, the time of our freedom, are approaching.

It is well known that the faculty of memory, imagination, and visualization acts upon the soul of the person who remembers and imagines, evoking an emotion and a state of mind similar, more or less, to the state of mind in which he—or a person like him—found himself at the time of the event itself. And to the extent that the powers of his soul are strong and hold dominion over the body, which is bound and restricted by time and place, so too will his soul’s state at the time of remembrance draw closer and closer to the state at the time of the event.

And "spirit brings spirit and draws forth spirit," with an *is'harusa d'lesata* (an arousal from below) bringing about an *is'harusa d'le'eila* (an arousal from above). As our Sages of blessed memory said, "And these days are remembered and performed"—that by remembering them below, they are performed in actuality above, and consequently, they are also bestowed below, and all the matters connected to those days are awakened.

This is one of the reasons we were commanded to remember the exodus from Egypt in every generation and every single day—including the nights—to see oneself as if he himself had gone out of Egypt today, gone out to freedom and been redeemed.

For every single day there must be an "exodus from Egypt"—the departure of the *neshamah elokis* (the divine soul) from the imprisonment of the body, a departure to true freedom.

And what is true freedom?

It is freedom in every sense—freedom from servitude, freedom from suffering—both physical servitude and suffering, and spiritual servitude and suffering.

The *avodah* that a person must perform every single day is this spiritual exodus from Egypt: departing from the straits (*mitzrayim*) and the limitations of his body and his *nefesh habehamis* (animal soul), and from the servitude of his *yetzer hara*.

And when a person frees himself from his *yetzer hara*—

With the help of the *Ribono shel Olam*, who chooses His people Israel and brought them out of Egypt, the place of impurity, and through engagement with Torah—

He is thereby freed from spiritual servitude and suffering—the immense war of the inclinations within his soul—and from physical servitude and suffering.

As it is written: "If you walk in My statutes... I will give your rains in their time... and I will grant peace in the land... I am Hashem your G-d, who brought you out of the land of Egypt."

With blessings for a kosher and joyous Pesach, and for true freedom speedily in our days, through our true and complete redemption by *Moshiach Tzidkeinu*.

#### ***257***

Printed in the *Haggadah Shel Pesach* with *Likutei Ta'amim*, etc. (Kehot, 5747), p. 573.
