## 209

B"H, 19 Iyar, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, etc., R' Dovid Meir, Shochet u'Bodek, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 27 Omer, regarding what you raise from the text in Kuntres 84, that in the *chayus* (vitality) there is no difference [between one part of the body and another], as there is in the brain or the fingernail of the foot, because the *chayus* is essential, etc. Yet, in several places—among them *Likutei Torah*, Parshas Emor, in the *maamar* titled *V'Nikdashti*—it is written that the *chayus* clothed in the head is on a higher level than the *chayus* of the body, etc.

The distinction between these two aforementioned places is that within the *chayus* itself, there exists the essence of the *chayus* and the manifestations of the *chayus*. Regarding the essence of the *chayus*, it is not appropriate to divide it and say that the foot is less alive than the head. This is not the case, however, regarding the manifestations of the *chayus* in the *kochot hanefesh* (powers of the soul); there are many powers of the soul, 613 in number, and this itself is proof that this is not the essence of the *chayus*, and they are divided according to the limbs in which they are clothed. See *Tanya*, Chapter 51.

One can find an analogy for this in the *nigleh* (revealed Torah) and in *avodah*: from the perspective of the point of *Yiddishkeit*, there is no distinction between the greatest of the great and the smallest of the small. This is not the case, however, from the perspective of *yediah* and *hasagah* (knowledge and comprehension). The same applies to matters of *Torah u'Mitzvos*, which contain a parallel to this. Just as regarding the matter of *V'Nikdashti*, which must take place in the presence of ten Jews—in this, there is no distinction between Moshe Rabbeinu and the lowest of the low in our generation, since in this, the essential point of *Yiddishkeit* rooted in each and every one is given, as well as the **essence** of the *chayus* of each and every one. This is not the case, however, from the perspective of the 248 positive *mitzvos* and 365 negative *mitzvos*, where there are many, many distinctions within the complete stature of the Jewish people.

With blessings for proper health for you and your wife, may they live.

## 2119

B"H, 19 Iyar, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 11 Iyar, in which you write that you wish to study at a Chabad yeshiva in Eretz Yisrael (you do not specify whether you intend to study at Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod or Yeshivas Toras Emes in Jerusalem), but that you are being held back by what you were told: that one of the conditions of the yeshiva is not to shave one’s beard. Since you intend to return to [your home country]... and are not at all accustomed to growing a beard, you are asking for a leniency—that is, to waive this condition, as it is difficult for you and almost impossible.

I find this question of yours surprising. Surely you are aware of the severity of *Chillul Hashem* and of breaching a communal standard, even if the matter in itself were not so severe. Picture the situation for yourself: you would enter a yeshiva where everyone has a beard, and you would be the only one breaking the standard by being clean-shaven. Furthermore, we are speaking of a yeshiva whose purpose includes the study of *Pnimiyus HaTorah* and guidance in the love and fear of Hashem. These are dependent, first and foremost, on what is written at the beginning of *Tur Orach Chaim*—and cited also in the *Rema* there—that one should not be ashamed before those who mock.

Without transcribing here what is written in *Pnimiyus HaTorah*, in the holy *Zohar*, and in many other books regarding how the hairs of the beard relate to the *Yud-Gimmel Tikunei Dikna* and how they draw down success in the study of Torah and the fulfillment of *mitzvos*, **everyone** agrees that the beard is a part of the *Tzelem Elokim*. Shaving the beard—even according to those who permit it under certain circumstances—means that, at the very least, the *Tzelem Elokim* is no longer upon one's face.

Consider this: a young man who has merited that Divine Providence has brought him to the land upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year to the end of the year, and who desires to add to his study of the revealed Torah the study of *Pnimiyus HaTorah*—the Torah in its entirety being the wisdom and will of the *Ribono shel Olam*, and *Pnimiyus HaTorah* being the secrets of the Torah which in earlier days were revealed only to the select few, though for various reasons they have been revealed and publicized to many of the Children of Israel in these generations—must not forget the truth: that this is the inner will and wisdom of the Almighty. What, then, are those who mock the *avreichim* who walk with beards—because they wish to beautify the *mitzvos* and have the *Tzelem Elokim* upon their faces—compared to this?

Moreover, a large portion of them are considered students of the *Tzemach Tzedek*, the *Posek* who ruled that this is a prohibition from the Torah (as explained at length in his *Responsa*, *Yoreh Deah*, Siman 93). It is unnecessary to elaborate on the severity according to the **Gemara** of acting in the place of a *Rav* in opposition to the *Rav’s* ruling. May Hashem grant you success in walking the straight path and on the road that leads to the House of G-d, and may you attain this without unnecessary trials.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
The Secretary

## B'ki

B'ki

B"H, 19 Iyar, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 26 Nissan, in which you write regarding the situation in the yeshiva, and also that for several reasons it has been suggested that you leave the yeshiva of... and move to work elsewhere, and you ask for my opinion on this matter.

It is obvious, and there is no doubt about it, that on the contrary—if, as you write, the situation in the yeshiva is not as it should be, then the advice is to fix it, not to leave the yeshiva. Rather, one should add strength and courage to improve it, to grow it, and to make it glorious. First and foremost, the responsibility for this lies with those who work and participate in the affairs of the yeshiva, and who recognize the preciousness of Talmud Torah in general, and the study of the inner dimensions of Torah in particular. Elaboration on this is superfluous. It is well known that the saying of my sainted father-in-law, the Rebbe, was that Hashem pays for every good deed—in his holy words, "The Almighty does not remain a debtor"—and especially since "according to the effort is the reward." If they are pressuring you and tempting you to leave the yeshiva, and you do not do so, then your merit and reward are exceedingly great. And according to the ruling of the Mishnah that "the reward of a mitzvah is a mitzvah," you will see reward through your success in your activities in the yeshiva, which will naturally also draw down additional blessing and success in your personal affairs.

With blessings for success in all of the above.

#### ***B'ki***

**Note:** See also above, Vol. 5, Letter 1564, and in many other places.

## 2112

B"H, 21 Iyar, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter from Lag B'Omer with pleasure, and I was very happy to read therein that you and your wife, may they live, are witnessing Hashgacha Pratis with their own eyes. You should explain to your wife, may she live, the matter more clearly: since she has seen tangibly how the sheitel brought her blessing and success, she should now have a "good eye" regarding others as well—as our Sages of blessed memory said regarding the traits of those who give tzedakah—and influence her surroundings in this direction. When such things are heard from a woman who was raised in the atmosphere of the United States, it has a very great influence upon them.

Regarding what you wrote, that you are buying a house in a place where there is no Orthodox shul, and consequently you will daven at home on Shabbos: in general, this is not the proper order, even if you travel to another place for Shabbos a few times a month. You should have sought ways to establish at least one minyan there; then, it would also be permissible to take a Sefer Torah to the place where the minyan will be, etc. It is understood that this must be done in a way that does not stir up unnecessary machlokes, and it is best if it is done without any machlokes at all.

I was pleased to hear that you are maintaining the daily Chassidus shiur, and also that you have renewed the study with the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, etc., R' Shlomo, may he live, Greenberg. Please convey my warm regards to him.

Enclosed is what I said to the students, may they live, this past Lag B'Omer. I am certain you will utilize it in an appropriate manner in your own surroundings as well. May Hashem grant you and your entire household, may they live, success in all that you need, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings.

This gratitude is expressed through an increase in strength in Torah and mitzvos. When this knowledge and thought is firmly planted in their hearts and minds, they too will stand strong against all the trials that stand in their path, for this, and only this, is the path to success and happiness for every Jewish man and woman.

I will conclude this letter as I began, with wishes for peace and blessings, and for a speedy recovery from the Source of Goodness, and for much nachas from your family, may they live, and from your distinguished son, Mr. Yosef, may he live, in particular.

## 2114

B.H., 23 Iyar, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter of 2 Iyar, in which you write the good news... that you have invited the students to the sedarim to influence them with love for Torah and mitzvos, which they should carry with them for the entire year. It is certainly unnecessary for me to elaborate on the importance of these matters, or on the Purim farbrengen you mention. As the statement of our Sages is known, "Great is a drink, for it brings [people] close," and if this is true regarding the side that is not good, then how much more so when one is successful in the side of good, when one connects it with words of hisorerus regarding Torah, mitzvos, ahavas Yisrael, ahavas haTorah, and ahavas Hashem Yisbarach. I hope that you will also utilize the coming days of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah, in this spirit.

Regarding what you write—that the exertion did not, chas v'shalom, harm your wife, tichyeh—I am certain that not only did it not harm her, but on the contrary, it did her good. However, regarding the future, it is self-understood that one must organize the farbrengen, but the physical labor involved should be shared among the other women. There is a double benefit in this, as it draws in more friends, as one sees tangibly.

For the same reason, it is also my opinion that one person should not cover the entire expenses of the mikveh. Aside from the fact that one must provide other Yidden with the zechus to participate, it is also relevant for the future; because when it costs someone money, it is precious to them, and they feel that they have a greater connection to it. It is self-understood that when the opportunity arises, you can prompt them regarding this, since they know that you have contributed money toward it.

You do not write regarding the method of the construction of the mikveh and how the water was drawn, though you surely acted according to the instructions of the Rabbonim of anash... for one must ensure that one fulfills the requirements according to all opinions, especially regarding a mikveh.

You do not mention in your letter regarding the shiurim in Chassidus, but I hope that it is only that you did not write about it, but that the actual work is not lacking. According to the ruling of our Sages that "we elevate in matters of holiness," you will certainly increase in this from now on. This is especially true at this time in connection with the approaching Yom Tov, the time of the giving of our Torah, which is an eis ratzon for Toras HaNistar. For at the time of the giving of the Torah, the revealed Torah was in a state of "hidden," because they only heard the Aseres HaDibros, and within that, the entire revealed Torah was included in the aspect of **nistar**. In contrast, Toras HaNistar—which is Maaseh Merkavah, the hidden of the hidden—all the Yidden **saw**.

With blessings for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness, and for an increase in beauty in the performance of mitzvos and the study of Torah.

Your pidyon nefesh will be read at an eis ratzon at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, ztzk"l, nbg"m, zy"a.

## 215

B.H., 28 Iyar, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter from Lag B’Omer, which is the yoma d’hilula of Rashbi. It is well known what is brought in many places in Chassidus regarding the precise language used in the holy Zohar, "He opened, etc." The explanation is that they opened the channel through which the avodah is made easier for all those who come after them. Therefore, it is surprising that in all your letters you do not mention the dissemination of the wellsprings of the inner dimension of Torah and the wellsprings of the Baal Shem Tov, whose yoma d’hilula is on the festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah. My hope is that this is only lacking in writing, but that the matter is being carried out with the appropriate effort, as is fitting for its great value. Especially since, contrary to the common opinion, it is precisely on the festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah, that the revealed Torah was given in a hidden and alluded manner in the Ten Commandments, while the hidden Torah—Maaseh Merkavah—was seen by all of Yisrael in a revealed manner, as is stated in the Midrash.

With blessings for receiving the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

## 2117

B"H, 28 Iyar, 5713

## 2118

B"H, 29 Iyar, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the distinguished Rabbi, the G-d-fearing Chossid, who occupies himself with the needs of the community,
Rabbi Ephraim Eliezer, may he live, HaKohen

Greetings and blessings!

I happened upon the sefer *Zechusa D’Avraham* by Rabbi Aryeh Mordechai Rabinowitz – Jerusalem, 5711 – and I found there on page 29 the story regarding the Maggid of Kozhnitz concerning the angel appointed over pregnancy, which you, may you live, wrote to me about some time ago. Since there is no joy like the resolution of doubts, I am transcribing here his wording regarding what was difficult for me in the story, and according to this version, my difficulty is resolved.

I received your letter of the 26th before I traveled to the holy gravesite.

Regarding *b’omer-l’omer*, see *Iggeres HaKodesh*, section 13.

With respect and blessings for a peaceful Shabbos.

...And the holy Maggid said to him that the angel appointed over pregnancy has the gematria of 75. He said to him, "Your Honor, where is this hinted at?" The Rabbi of Podhajce replied to the holy Maggid that it is explained in *Gemara Niddah* 16b that the name of the angel appointed over pregnancy is Lailah (Night), as it is stated (Iyov 3:3), "And the night said, 'A man-child is conceived,'" and the gematria of *Lailah* is 75. The holy Maggid replied, "You have spoken well, Your Honor, but that is from a place of darkness. I will tell you from a place of light, not darkness: In *Parshas Lech Lecha* it is written that the angel said to Hagar, 'Hinnach' (Behold you) pregnant and will bear a son; 'Hinnach' has the gematria of 75. And since *Hinnach* has the gematria of 75, therefore the man shall be blessed with a male child."

**Rabbi Ephraim Eliezer, may he live:** Yalles. Additional letters to him – see above 1893, and the references in the notes there.

## 2119

B"H, 29 Iyar, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 20 Iyar, in which you express surprise at what I wrote to you—that the matter of compromise distances the *baal-habayis* rather than the opposite—and you write that if so, the most pious rabbis should have the most magnificent *batei-kaneisiyos*, etc.

My words are based on the following:

a) The statement of our Sages (Sotah 41b, according to the version of the *Ein Yaakov*): "Whoever flatters... will eventually fall into their hands." The matter of compromise is a form of flattery toward those *baalei-batim* who are free from Torah and *mitzvos*, and therefore the aforementioned statement of our Sages applies to this. For were it not for the matter of falling into their hands, then—

b) It is simple that a person’s livelihood depends on Hashem and on the conduct of the one who requires the livelihood. This is one of the foundations of the faith of a Jewish man and woman: that **Hashem** is the One who feeds and sustains. To say that it is in the hands of another person to ruin one’s livelihood, even though Hashem has decreed otherwise, is not only the opposite of Jewish faith, but the opposite of the belief in *hashgachah* in general, even among non-Jews. The exception to this is the one to whom the aforementioned statement of our Sages refers; in that case, there is no complaint against Hashem for the fact that he falls, to a certain extent, into the hands of the wicked person—meaning that the wicked person is free to influence his livelihood.

c) Your question based on the aforementioned premise—why the most pious rabbis do not have the most magnificent *batei-kaneisiyos*—is an old question. In the language of the *Kesuvim*: "Why does the way of the wicked prosper?" See also *Berachos* 7a, that even Moshe Rabbeinu struggled with this and requested, "Make known to me Your ways." When you examine the aforementioned *Shas* and many places in the *sefarim hakedoshim*, you will find an answer to this. And even if you do not find an answer, it does not affect the practical reality. As my father-in-law, the Rebbe, wrote in one of his letters, it is not worthwhile to spend time dealing with the question of "why the way of the wicked prospers," and it is better to focus on one’s own affairs. The same applies in our case. In any event, it is simple and understandable to every person that although one must hold to the ways of nature—and consequently speak and exert effort with those upon whom the receipt of a suitable position depends—it is not that one’s livelihood depends on these individuals. Rather, it is only because the holy Torah has decreed that one should not rely on miracles, and therefore one must perform actions within the ways of nature to receive livelihood through them. Consequently, it is understood that it is impossible for the fulfillment of a *mitzvah* or the *hiddur mitzvah* to, *chas v'shalom*, ruin the influence from Hashem, who is the very One who commands the *mitzvah*.

d) Regarding the practical matter: I did not write in my letter that it is a decree that you must remain in... but only that this offer should not be ruled out. You must weigh all the offers before you and choose the one that is best for you and your family, *shichyu*, in both material and spiritual matters. Based on the information you have written about them until now, it seems, at least on a superficial glance, that the offer to continue the position of... is better than the others. May Hashem guide you in what is good for you and for all your family, *shichyu*, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings.

## 2120

B"H, 29 Iyar, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you ask my opinion regarding moving from France. A wise question is half the answer, and as you mention in your letter, you are already aware of my opinion on the matter of moving. However, it should be added that this opinion—that it is not advisable to move (except in isolated cases)—applies not only to those engaged in holy work, whether in Tomchei Temimim or another profession, but also to the rest of anash. And this is not only for spiritual reasons, but also for material ones. As you are surely aware of the difficulties and tribulations that anash—may they live—have experienced here and in Canada regarding organization and finding a source of livelihood. I am certain they are writing to you about the situation as it truly is, even though it may become clear from this that it is doubtful whether they did the right thing by moving here, and a word to the wise is sufficient.

With blessings for success in your holy work, which will naturally bring continued blessing and success to the health of your wife—may she live—and all your family members—may they live—and in all your personal matters in general.

With blessings to receive the Torah with joy and inwardness.

P.S. Enclosed is the Kuntres for the upcoming festival of Matan Torah, which I am sure you will merit to share with the public in an appropriate manner.

## 2121

B"H, 12 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs, a man of character and many accomplishments, etc., R' Chaim Zalman, may he live, known as Chazak.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive the news that, B"H, the operation went well. May Hashem send you a speedy recovery and strengthen your health, so that you may be able to increase your efforts in your communal work in general, and for the benefit of the mosdos of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in particular, even more than before.

In this week’s parsha — Beha’aloscha es ha’neiros — Chazal explain the concept of "beha’aloscha" (when you kindle): it is necessary only to light the Menorah in the Beis HaMikdash, and then the flame rises on its own. The Mikdash that exists in the heart of every Yid is also intact now; one must only occasionally ignite the internal fire, and then it flares up on its own. We see quite often in life how a little hisorerus that one inspires in a Yid leads him onto the path, and from there on, he acts on his own.

For a Yid, ruchniyus and gashmiyus are intertwined. I hope and pray for you that this should be the case in gashmiyus as well: that the fact that the doctors, with the help of the Ribono shel Olam, successfully performed the operation, should be the beginning of an improvement in your health. May it go from better to better, so that you may be able to increase your communal involvement with proper health and with expansion in both gashmiyus and ruchniyus.

With blessings of chazak and all the best,
Waiting for good news.

## 2123

B"H, 14 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, R' Melech, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter regarding the question of cutting down a fruit-bearing tree that is mostly dry, etc., where there are differing opinions, especially since in Eretz Yisrael most are lenient—yet in your own experience, it happened three years ago and did not turn out well, etc.

Beyond all the above, it is also known what is written regarding this in the Will of R' Yehudah HaChossid, section 53. There is also a discussion in the sefer *Shivim Temarim*. Based on all the above, in my opinion, you should refrain from issuing a ruling of leniency in this matter, since you have had a personal experience with it, even though according to what the Alter Rebbe wrote in *Hilchos Shmiras Guf V'Nefesh* at the end, it is permissible.

With blessings.

Since the aforementioned sefer is not very common, the seforim it cites are transcribed here: *Kerem Shlomo*, Yoreh Deah, section 368; *Ikarei HaDat*, Yoreh Deah, section 14, subsection 8; *Shulchan Aruch HaMei'ir*, chapter 35, 2; *Chasam Sofer*, Yoreh Deah, section 2; *Shu"t Shem Aryeh*, Yoreh Deah, section 27; *Pri Megadim*, Orach Chaim, section 263, *Mishbetzos Zahav*, subsection 3 (and references there).

## 2124

B"H, 14 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...In response to your question as to whether you should make an effort to travel here to study in our yeshiva: this is the correct thing to do, as it is well known that our Sages ruled, "Go into **exile** to a place of Torah." If there are difficulties in traveling here, you should make an effort to travel to the Tomchei Temimim yeshiva in Lod, in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. May Hashem grant you success in your study of the revealed Torah and the teachings of Chassidus, and may you become a G-d-fearing Chassid and a scholar. As our Sages ruled—even regarding the revealed Torah—the way to ensure that "the faith of your times shall be the strength of your salvations, wisdom and knowledge" is specifically through the fact that "the fear of Hashem is His treasure." [This relates to the concept of] "a salty land," as explained by Rashi and as elucidated in Likutei Torah at the end of Parshas Vayikra regarding the concept of salt in our holy Torah—which refers to the study of the inner dimension of the Torah, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus.

Regarding the order of your studies, you should consult with your mashpia and your rosh yeshiva.

With blessings for success in Torah study with fear of Heaven.

P.S.
Regarding what you wrote in the name of the avreich... who is from... and wishes to bring bochurim closer to... and asks if this is the right thing to do:

This depends on from which "side" he is taking these bochurim. If they are currently to the left of..., then he should be strengthened and continue his efforts in this, provided that he does not confuse them with political matters. If they are to the right of..., meaning that they are already more religious, then it is understood that in Torah and mitzvos, and especially in fear of Heaven, one must ascend higher and higher without limit (since this is the wisdom and will of the Ribono shel Olam, who is Ein Sof). Consequently, one must also advance in this, "journeying on, toward the south," and as our Sages ruled—even in the revealed Torah—that Torah scholars have no rest, neither in this world nor in the World to Come.

Enclosed is an excerpt from the sicha of Shabbos Mevarchim Sivan, which is worth publicizing in wider circles, since every day there is the matter of the giving of the Torah, and consequently, also the receiving of the Torah.

## B'kch

B'kch

B"H, 14 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 11 Sivan, in which you write regarding the conditions of your brother, Mr. ... (may he live and be well), and that you are distressed, etc.

It is a well-known saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: "One action is better than a thousand sighs." Since he does not specify the nature of the sigh, it certainly implies that this holds true even if the sigh comes from the depths of the heart. You should have spoken with the bride, especially since you write that she is an innocent young woman. It is possible that among the bride's relatives there are observant families; if so, they should influence her to decide, without wavering, to conduct herself according to the customs of proper Jewish daughters. Even if you do not see how you will be able to influence her in this, why should you concern yourself with the hidden ways of Hashem?

Furthermore, you should have explained to your brother (may he live and be well) that their happiness, both materially and spiritually, depends on their conduct in this matter—and not only their own happiness, but also that of the children who will be born to them later. It is a great responsibility to jeopardize the lives of children who have no choice in the matter, both in their material and spiritual lives, simply because the parents do not yet grasp the necessity of this. Even though many experts in this field state that it is necessary and impossible otherwise, etc., etc., surely with the appropriate interest, there will be no lack of words to explain this to them.

May Hashem grant you success, and may your brother (may he live and be well) succeed in the aforementioned, and may your brother build a home in Israel upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos as is proper.

With blessings.

## 2126

B"H, 14 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

After the long silence, it was a pleasure to receive your letter from the 8th of Sivan. As you requested, when I am at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention all those you wrote about who are in need, and I will await good news regarding this.

Regarding what you write about your son, may he live and be well: I was alarmed to see in your letter that after he had been engaged in the study of Torah—both in *nigleh* and in *Chassidus*—he is now continuing in a *yeshiva* where there is no study of *Chassidus*. While there was a time, many generations ago, when the study of the inner dimension of Torah was not an absolute necessity for everyone, it is well known that in our generations, to use the language of the Arizal cited in *Iggeres HaKodesh* by our Alter Rebbe (Letter 26), it is permitted and a *mitzvah* to reveal this wisdom. This is especially true in our current generation of double and redoubled darkness, where the situation is worsened by those who call darkness light and light darkness (and if this is seen abroad, then how much more so is it seen in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established speedily by our righteous Moshiach). It is therefore an absolute obligation to do everything possible in matters of *yiras shamayim*, of which the study of the inner dimension of Torah is one of the pillars. And Torah is acquired through the bond of friends.

All of this is in a general sense, but specifically in the case at hand: since your son has already been within the four cubits of this study, withdrawing from it, Heaven forbid, falls into the category of showing contempt for a part of the Torah. Even if the reason given is that the study is not suitable for this particular individual, the severity of such a prohibition is well known, as our Sages state in *Eruvin* 64a. As I mentioned, I am not entering into the question of how close his relatives or previous generations in your family were to this study—for which there is surely some merit—but it is entirely different regarding your son, since he has already reached the level of "having repeated it." It is also understood and simple that we see many *avreichim* who have not merited the "light" in the Torah—which is the inner dimension of Torah—and yet they are *yirei shamayim* and complete, and why should we delve into the hidden ways of the Merciful One? However, since through *hashgacha pratis* a certain individual has come to the knowledge that the inner dimension of Torah exists, and furthermore, due to several reasons, he has already been in an educational institution in the spirit of the inner dimension of Torah, his status is entirely different. I do not wish to elaborate on this further, so as not to cause you pain or distress, but I felt compelled to write at least these lines, since all of Israel is responsible for one another, and whoever has the ability to protest, etc., and it is known from our Sages (*Shabbos* 55a) "if it is revealed before You, etc." The main thing is, without getting into calculations, since in my opinion this could affect the foundations of your son's life, I have written these lines. And as mentioned, where possible, the success of one's studies depends on being in the appropriate environment.

With respect and blessings that you should report good news regarding all of the above.

## B'Katz

B"H, 15 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

It was a pleasure to receive your letter (though it was undated), and I was happy to receive, a few days later, a letter written by your mother—may she live and be well—who, thank G-d, is in improved health. May it be the will of Hashem that her health continues to improve, and may you derive much nachas from her and from her husband—may they live—a Jewish, Chassidic nachas, and may you be blessed among a generation of the upright.

I believe I have written to you about this a few times, and the point is this: Our Sages have ruled that it is not the study that is the essential thing, but the deed. We see this in our Torah and mitzvos as well, where the center of gravity is focused on action, less so on speech, and even less on thought. Although, on the other hand, the foundation of the existence of all the above depends on faith and opinions—especially according to what is explained in the teachings of Chassidus regarding "Know the G-d of your father," and regarding the love and fear of Hashem, which are the root for all of a person’s Torah and mitzvos thereafter—nevertheless, the majority of the day, the majority of the night, and consequently the majority of our years, require us to be engaged in the performance of deeds. It is therefore understood that this impacts and influences the intellectual aspect, ensuring it is as it should be. 

It is a remarkable thing that even regarding the Torah itself, as related by our Sages, there was a premise that it should be given to the ministering angels, who are devoid of physicality and therefore devoid of action—to the point that they are called by the philosophers "separate intellects." Moshe Rabbeinu, the shepherd of **all** of Israel throughout **all** generations, provided a decisive rebuttal to their claim: that the Torah of **Hashem** must be given to a creature that possesses a yetzer hara, and therefore descended **to Mitzrayim**, etc. Furthermore, it was specifically because the Jewish people preceded "we will do" (*naaseh*) to "we will hear" (*nishma*)—which refers to comprehension and understanding, the world of thought—that this served as the preparation for the giving of the Torah and its reception by the Jewish people.

My intention in the lines above is also a practical matter, namely regarding you (I take the liberty of writing this, as you touched upon it in your letter): It is worthwhile that, at least for a period of time, you shift your interest and focus to practical matters in daily life (even though they are surely not as interesting as the matters of the world of thought and contemplation). Without a doubt, this itself will improve and strengthen the course of your world of thought and contemplation. And how good it would be if, at the very least in your thoughts, you were to always keep before your eyes the motto of the Baal Shem Tov: "Serve—in all your ways—Hashem, and with joy."

## B'128

B'128

## 129

B"H, 15 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write regarding the improvement of your health and that the kidney attacks have ceased: Surely you see in this a hint from Above, in accordance with the saying of the Baal Shem Tov that in everything a Jewish person sees and hears, one must learn a lesson in the avodah of Hashem. The lesson here is that since Hashem has granted success and the physical kidney attacks have ceased, you must strive with even greater intensity and strength that the "kidney attacks" in your spiritual life should also cease. This is achieved through contemplation, specifically of what is written in Tanya, Chapter 41: "And behold, Hashem stands over him, and the whole earth is full of His glory, and He looks upon him and examines his kidneys, etc."

With this, your question in your letter is also resolved regarding someone you see who is worthy of and in need of rebuke, but who does not accept it, and you are seeking advice on this matter. Based on the above, the answer is understood, and it is from the well-known words of our Sages (Berachos 6b): "Whoever possesses yiras shamayim, his words are heard," and "words that come from the heart enter the heart" (Rabbeinu Tam in Sefer HaYashar, Chapter 13; cited in Shelah, Shaar HaOsios, letter Lamed).

With blessings for a complete recovery in body and soul.

## 230

B.H., 15 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...2) Regarding what you wrote about the radio—that one of the avreichim of the Temimim should speak from time to time and the others should listen—it is well known how our holy Nesi’im exerted themselves, and how they demanded of us as well, that the wellsprings be spread outward to the greatest possible extent. Therefore, if one is to consider the aforementioned idea, one must seek a method that can reach broad circles, not merely a limited number of people. Since I am not familiar with the regulations regarding this in this country, I am not writing in greater detail, but certainly, through inquiry and investigation, this too can be ascertained.

3) Regarding the question of whether one may now cook without prior kashrus supervision in the new electric ovens, where one can set the degree of heat and pressure, etc., and where one might consequently argue that the rule that "we are not expert in *chalitah*" (the law of *chalitah*—see *Pischei Teshuvah*, subsection 13, in *Siman* 69) does not apply, etc.: Stay away from this path. For in such a manner, the choice is given to every individual, and to every woman who has the authority to decide such questions, as well as the heat and pressure settings. Ultimately, this will also be decided by non-Jewish servants, to whom the cooking is sometimes entrusted, etc. We have already seen how many breaches began with "permissions" such as these (even if the initial permission was sometimes *oysgehalten* according to the *Shulchan Aruch*). We do not need to show off tricks, for we are not acrobats in a circus, etc.; rather, we are shluchim of the Ribono shel Olam to illuminate the world with the light of Torah and mitzvos. Consequently, one must salt the meat and rinse it before and after salting. And do not forget that the intent and the hint in extracting the blood from the meat via salt—the moral lesson therein—is that one must extract the vitality and the force from the *nefesh habehamis*. Only then will it be fit to be "meat like the meat of man" (*basar ke-basar ha-adam*), from the expression "I will be like the Most High" (*adameh la-elyon*)—to the "Man" above, who sits upon the Throne. Further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

## 2131

15 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn

To the esteemed and distinguished scholar, G-d-fearing man, etc., Rabbi Mendel, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I was very pleased to receive your regards through the esteemed and distinguished scholar, the dedicated communal activist, Rabbi Shlomo Zalman Hecht, may he live. It was a truly Jewish, Chassidic greeting—meaning, it is not only connected to *ahavas Yisrael*, for all Jews are responsible for one another, but it is also connected to *ahavas haTorah* and *ahavas Hashem*. Furthermore, beyond what Rabbi Hecht writes to me about you in general, he also informs me that, of your own good will, you have made a fine resolution regarding a significant matter that encompasses all three of the aforementioned elements: *ahavas Yisrael*, *ahavas haTorah*, and *ahavas Hashem*. This refers to your commitment to contribute a specific sum toward the maintenance of one of the "Ohalei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch" educational institutions, which are named after my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

In general, when one helps a fellow Jew in any way, it is an act of *ahavas Yisrael*. When one assists in the study of Torah, it is an act of *ahavas haTorah*. And specifically, when it involves raising Jewish children with an education of *yiras shamayim*, it is also an act of *ahavas Hashem*. According to the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov—as we have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe—these three loves (*ahavas Yisrael*, *ahavas haTorah*, and *ahavas Hashem*) are one and the same.

Rabbi Hecht also writes to me regarding the sum you have committed to give for the time being, within your current limited circumstances. I hope that through this good deed of *tzedakah*, the promise of our Sages of blessed memory, "Give tithes so that you may become wealthy," will certainly be fulfilled. Consequently, in time, you will also have the ability to increase this amount as Hashem expands your means, according to the needs of the institution, and in such a way that it will not cause you any hardship—not only in spiritual matters, but in material matters as well.

May Hashem grant that for long, good years, you will continue to perform *tzedakah* with other Jews, and especially with Jewish children, by supporting an institution of education in *yiras shamayim*. May you also perform *tzedakah* with yourself—specifically with your body and *nefesh habehamis*, which are the truly needy—by increasing your *shiurim* in Torah in general, and in *Toras HaChassidus* in particular. May Hashem grant you success so that all of this may be in good health, and that we may hear good news from one another, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings,

## 2132

B”H, 17 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt,
May they live.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby confirm receipt of your letters from the 4th and 24th of Iyar. Furthermore, my secretariat has already confirmed receipt of the second issue of the publication.

2) You mention in your letter that you are enclosing clippings from the newspapers *Amash* and *Davar*, but they were not found in the envelope.

3) The time has come to seek out methods and strive to ensure that there is actual growth and yield from the plowing and sowing you are doing. For although it is a great matter, and the necessity for advertising, radio broadcasts, propaganda, etc., is great—especially since we are assured by our Nasi that "propaganda does not return empty"—it is understood that the sooner one advances to the next stage, the better. There is no need to elaborate on this. Advertising and broadcasting are merely plowing and sowing from the perspective of the listeners and recipients (unlike the speakers and those managing the propaganda, for whom it is an active process, of course). Ultimately, one must penetrate the listener with the words and the propaganda until it reaches the stage of action. It is understood that the required action is not the same in every place you visit, but surely in **every** single place there is a way to engage in tangible activity, including on the part of the listeners and recipients. Among these, at first glance, are: establishing set times for learning—among them and by them, on the spot—Chassidus; drawing bochurim and youth to our yeshivos; and drawing avreichim and baalei batim to activities in the spirit of Chabad on the spot. And how good it would be if, in every place you pass through, you would entrust a few of the local people with whom you will maintain contact. It is understood that all this must be done without causing alarm; consequently, one must speak about sending booklets and the like, but you should strive, in an unofficial manner, that the people you choose will be the channels through which you can influence the place on a regular basis. It is understood that I am speaking only in general terms, and in accordance with the conditions of the place and the individuals, you must certainly find a detailed plan.

4) You mention in your letter that the lead musicians were Shalom Dov and Binyamin, but you do not write their last names. You will surely provide them at the next opportunity.

5) It is surprising that on Lag B’Omer in Meron, you bring many children for the *tisporet mitzvah* (haircutting ceremony), yet you do not mention anything about utilizing this matter for educational influence—by distributing booklets or an *aleph-beis* chart, and by ensuring that your address and some slogans relevant to the parents are included on the other side.

6) It is understood that all the above are merely points of critique. In general, fortunate are you and how good is your portion, that you have merited to be among those who disseminate the teachings of general Chassidus and the teachings of Chabad Chassidus in Eretz Yisrael, upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year until the end of the year. Therefore, my confidence is strong that this merit itself will enable you to improve the work from time to time, and "they ascend in holiness," and "to him who adds, they add [more]."

With blessings for success in your holy work.

P.S.
Regarding what you wrote that I should write to [name], it is surely unnecessary; it will be sufficient if you mention to him that you wrote to me regarding your budget. He will certainly do for your benefit everything in his power. Especially now, after the Almighty has granted him success in the matter of "seeing" (*re'iyah*), his offering of thanksgiving should surely be of a similar nature: the dissemination of the inner dimension of Torah—which is the teachings of Chassidus. The general distinction between the revealed and hidden dimensions of Torah is along the lines of "hearing" and "seeing." This is also hinted at by the fact that in the revealed dimension of Torah, regarding matters of study, the common expression is *Ta shema* ("Come and hear"), while in the hidden dimension, the expression is *Ta chazi* ("Come and see"). This is analogous to the distinction at the Giving of the Torah, where the subsequent study was in the manner of hearing, understanding, and grasping, whereas the Torah of Moshiach, when the reasons for the Torah will be revealed, will be a study in the manner of seeing. As is explained in many places in Chassidus, this explains how one person will be able to teach Torah to all of Israel; see the *derushim* in *Likutei Torah*, end of *Parshas Tzav* regarding Moshiach, in *Shaar HaEmunah*, *Parshas Noach* and onwards, and in many other places.

I have since found this in the book *Kocho Shel Rashbi*, page 42—along these lines.

Surely, in accordance with my letter to the *Reshet*, you have approached them regarding the printing of the *sicha* from Lag B’Omer for the young students here, and have discussed the practical implementation.

## 2133

B”H, 17 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, involved in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Asher, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

After a long hiatus, your letter of 13 Iyar regarding the affairs of the yeshiva was finally received. Surely, in the meantime, my response to the yeshiva administration has also been received. It is surprising that until now, you have not written about the progress of matters since then. May it be the will of Hashem that this is a sign for the good—that since you are not writing, it means all is peaceful and successful. It is certainly unnecessary to urge and awaken you that whatever is in your power to do regarding this, you should do; this includes the fact that even if travel to Melbourne is required more frequently, there should be no hindrance to this.

It is surprising that you do not mention anything regarding your communal work in Sydney. May it be the will of Hashem that this, too, is a sign for the good.

I read with pleasure the list of participants in the Shas distribution. Although it is not evident from the list when—G-d willing—they will finish, or whether they are joining with the Shas distribution here, which in any case is on 19 Kislev, or if they have set a different date, in any event—may it be successful. As explained in my letter from some time ago regarding the Shas distribution, according to the Gemara (Shabbos 93b) regarding two people who performed a task, where one cannot [complete it alone] etc., it can be said that **each** of the participants has the merit as if he had studied the **entire** Shas. Please convey my wishes and blessing to each and every one of the participants.

Enclosed is an excerpt from the sicha of Shabbos Mevarchim Sivan, the content of which is truly relevant all year round, since the giving and receiving of the Torah occurs every day—"as if new," and in the language of the blessing on the Torah: "Giver of the Torah," in the present tense.

With respect and blessing for success in all matters, both general and personal,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. Surely my notes on the maamar of yours that you sent me some time ago arrived on time.

## 2135

B"H, 18 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, occupied with communal needs, R' Yechiel Michel, may he live and be well.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 23 Iyar, in which you inform me that you have fully moved into your new apartment. May it be the will of Hashem that this change of place brings a change of fortune for the good, both physically and spiritually.

Regarding what you wrote in your letter concerning the repair of the mikveh, and what the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, occupied with communal needs, R' Avraham Chaim Naeh, may he live and be well, wrote to you—suggesting that due to the difficulty of the repair, perhaps some details should be changed—in my opinion, this does not seem correct. Since in matters of mikveh we are careful to fulfill as many opinions as possible, it is possible that by changing even a single detail—even if on the spot one does not see the difference compared to the arrangement of the Rebbe Rashab—upon further study, a difference might be found there as well. It is well known that the halachos of mikvaos are extremely complex, with varying opinions on every single detail. This is in addition to the reason that if one person changes it in this way, another will change it in another way, and it is not advisable to be the one to initiate such things. I have strong hope that with appropriate effort, you will be able to perform the repair in accordance with the arrangement of the Rebbe Rashab...

#### ***2135***

**R' Yechiel Michel:** Dobruskin. Additional letters to him appear above in 2029, and in the notes referenced there.

 In the present case, even in haste and before deep study, it seems to me that the proposal of R' Avraham Chaim Naeh involves two drawbacks: 1) Giving a se'ah and a se'ah according to the second explanation in the Ra'avad; 2) Zeriah (seeding) in flowing water—which is not the case according to the arrangement of the Rebbe Rashab. And this is not the place to elaborate.

**Change some details:** And to construct a mikveh on top of a mikveh in the otzar geshamim (and not in the place of immersion), and there the zeriah of the rainwater will take place, which will then come to the mikveh through the otzar geshamim.

**Two drawbacks:** (Translation of the Hebrew abbreviation *tarler*).

**Which is not the case according to the arrangement of the Rebbe Rashab:** See Likutei Sichos, Vol. 7, p. 311.

## 236

B"H, 18 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the distinguished scholar, G-d-fearing, and learned, engaged in communal affairs, R’ Tzvi, may he live:

Shalom u’Bracha!

Your letter was received, as well as your book on the history of the Maskil l’Eitan family, etc. Thank you for the book.

Regarding what you write at the beginning of your letter—that you wish to be "connected" but not a Chassid, as you are of the *Perushim*—surely you are aware that the Gra himself was called a *Chassid*. It goes without saying that my intention is not, G-d forbid, to be a "Chassid" of any private individual, or even of a general figure. Rather, it is as the saying of the Alter Rebbe goes: Once, when he was asked what the essence of a *Chassid* is, he replied that it is a person who waives his own benefit; and not only that, but he does not refrain from incurring a loss to himself, provided that he brings benefit to another. Since this was during the height of the controversy at that time, the questioner asked again, stating that he did not want proof from the *Toras HaNistar* (the hidden Torah), but specifically from the *Toras HaNigleh* (the revealed Torah). Our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe answered him that this is an explicit Gemara (*Niddah* 17a): "A *Chassid* burns it," even though by doing so he causes himself a loss—see the *Tosafos* there.

The connection of this concept to the teachings of Chassidus and its guidance can be explained simply. According to the *Shulchan Aruch*, the principle is known: "What reason do you have to say that your blood is redder?" And consequently, the reverse is also true: "What reason do you have to say that your fellow’s blood is redder?" Chassidus, however, places the "emphasis" on the fact that the beginning of *avodah* must be above *taam v'daas* (intellect and reason) and calculation. Only this can serve as a strong foundation for the fulfillment of *Torah u'Mitzvos* as they should be. When one does not enter into calculations, one is primarily concerned with the welfare of one’s fellow. This is especially true when one recalls the reason for the necessity of *avodah* that is above *taam v'daas* and calculation: If one holds onto making calculations—even calculations of *kedushah*—it is known that the measure of the Holy One, Blessed be He, is "measure for measure." Consequently, He will also be exacting with him if he is a "man of calculation" in his conduct, in his deeds, and even in his speech and thought—for "thoughts of transgression are more difficult than the transgression itself." In that case, it is clear that it is not "worth it" for him.

The question is well-known: If the study of Chassidus is a necessity, then what did the earlier generations do? Even in our time, there are those who do not know the teachings of Chassidus, yet they are G-d-fearing and whole.

But the answer to this is also simple: The world is not conducted by chance, G-d forbid, but by *Hashgacha Pratis* (Divine Providence) in every single detail. Just as we see in the animal kingdom that there are various organs necessary for one animal, without which it cannot exist, even though they are not found in another animal because it is possible for it to exist without them—so too, "from the beasts of the earth He teaches us," we learn that this is also true in the human species. The fact that one has not known until now of the study of the teachings of Chassidus, or that in those generations the study of this *Pnimiyus HaTorah* (inner dimension of Torah) was reserved only for select individuals, is itself proof that he is in such conditions and will not come to such trials that require this knowledge. This is not the case for those to whom the existence of this part of Torah has become known. It is obvious that this also falls under the ruling of the Rambam that even a single letter—and who is to say an entire part of Torah—has a *kedushah* equal to the verse "Shema Yisrael," etc.

The difference between an animal and a Jewish person in the above is only this: Since the Holy One, Blessed be He, desires that man’s goodness be complete, He did not want to force man in this. Therefore, free choice was given to him. Furthermore, He created the *Yetzer Hara*, which explains to man many reasons and arguments to remove him from the path. And if the *Yetzer Hara* has dealings with a G-d-fearing person, he clothes his reasons and arguments in the letters of the *Shulchan Aruch*. Surely, for one such as you, further elaboration is superfluous.

Regarding your question as to whether there are any residents of Yekaterinoslav here, I have no information about them.

Concerning my mother, the Rabbanit, may she live long, it would be best if you write to her directly, and she will surely write to you what she knows. You may write to her in any language you wish.

As you requested, I am enclosing a clipping that was printed here at the time of the passing of my father, of blessed memory.

I have received a blessing, and I shall return one. Since you were a messenger to convey regards from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the Gaon and Chassid, R’ R. Katz, it would be good if you would convey regards respectfully from me. Thank you.

May the Almighty grant you success, and may you merit that you and your wife, may they live, raise your son, Yehuda Leib, may he live, to Torah, to the *chuppah*, and to good deeds, with an expanded mind, and may he increase his strength in spreading the light of Judaism in his surroundings. May it be the will of the Almighty that you do this with Chassidic warmth.

With respect and a blessing for success.

P.S. I saw in the list at the end of your book that you have published several booklets regarding the question of science in its relation to religion. If you could provide them to my library, I thank you in advance, as the approach to this question is painful to me. For even the *Chareidim* who discuss this, the sum total of their propaganda is that there were several of the great Torah scholars who had great knowledge of science, and how much science is necessary for the Torah of Israel, such as in the laws of *Kiddush HaChodesh*, *treifos*, etc. At the same time, the approach should be entirely the opposite: that science has no foundation whatsoever without *emunah* (faith), and how many scientists would have been lost on the paths of life had they not held onto this, etc., etc.

## 2137

B"H, 18 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive regards from you via the *avreich*, the G-d-fearing and esteemed *moreinu harav* [Name] *shichyeh*, who, thank G-d, has seen an improvement in his health and his eyesight. I am certain that he will continue to observe the matters I wrote to him about. It would be very good if he would add to his daily study—or have someone study with him—a few lines from the holy *Zohar* and a few lines from the holy *Tanya*, in which the phrase "Come and see" (*ta chazi*) is frequently used. This is a directive of our holy Torah: that one should perceive *Elokus* tangibly. This is also a *segulah* and a remedy for the physical eyes to function as they should, and to see how all things are brought into being and sustained by the word of Hashem—the power of the Creator within the created.

With blessings for a *refuah* and for long, good years, both materially and spiritually.

## 138

B"H, 19 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

...In continuation of our conversation when you visited me, and regarding the theme of the day from the weekly parsha: it is a remarkable thing. For it is a known principle that there is nothing that can stand before teshuvah. Yet, even though the Children of Israel performed teshuvah for the sin of the spies and said, "Here we are, and we will go up to the place that Hashem has spoken of," Moshe said to them, "It will not succeed."

However, the explanation of this matter is clarified in the following verse: "Do not go up, for Hashem is not **in your midst**," just as it is explained at the end, that the Ark of the Covenant of Hashem and Moshe did not depart from the midst of the camp.

This means that even though Eretz Yisrael is designated for the people of Israel—and furthermore, it is a command of Hashem, as Calev ben Yefuneh said, "We shall surely go up and inherit it"—nevertheless, there is a condition that must precede the action: one must go out with the Ark of the Covenant of Hashem before them, as is recounted at length regarding the conquest of the land by Yehoshua. If not, chas v'shalom, it is impossible to "go up by force." And even though teshuvah is effective in atoning for a sin, whether of an individual or of the collective, it is impossible to change the manner of the conquest of the land—its true conquest—which is specifically as the promise of the Holy One, Blessed be He: that there will be a man from the house of Dovid who studies Torah and occupies himself with mitzvos like his father Dovid, according to the Written Torah and the Oral Torah, and he will compel all of Israel to walk in it and strengthen its breaches, and he will fight the wars of Hashem, etc. (and he, only he) will build the Beis Hamikdash in its place, gather the dispersed of Israel, etc., and perfect the entire world to serve Hashem (Rambam, Hilchos Melachim, end of chapter 11).

## 239

B"H, 20 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, who engages in communal needs, R' Shlomo, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

Your letters of the 5th and 14th of Sivan, along with their enclosures, have been received.

2) Regarding the sicha of Lag B'Omer: seemingly, it is worthwhile to print it as soon as possible and distribute it among the bochurim to whom it is relevant. For although the subject matter there concerns the days of Sefirah and the Yom Tov, the moral lesson derived from it applies to the entire year, as is understood. Especially since the esteemed R' Moshe, may he live, Lipsker, is also requesting some words of inspiration for the students. It may be worthwhile to print a number of copies on special paper and with a special binding, to be given as a prize to those bochurim who excel, in addition to the copies printed in the regular manner for general distribution.

4) Regarding what you wrote concerning the inner aspects of these matters and the guidance of the students: do not, G-d forbid, lose heart. It is impossible to fathom what takes place in the inner heart of a son or daughter of Yisroel. Even if it sometimes seems that great effort and toil yield meager fruits, it is impossible to know what will be in the near future, and who can say what will be in the distant future. It is understood that one cannot know at all what has been prevented in matters of *sogim chamuros* [serious transgressions] through this education and guidance. To elaborate on this would be superfluous. Especially since in our generation, we have seen wonders in this regard even with physical eyes, tangibly: how from one small seed that was planted, great and wondrous things have grown. With the proper perspective, you will **certainly** see such things among those you influence...

Awaiting good news, and with blessings for success in communal matters and in your personal affairs.

## 2140

B"H, 21 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent in communal affairs,
Rabbi Yehoshua, may he live and be well,

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter of 17 Sivan: I was alarmed to read at the beginning that you are finding things very difficult, etc., and that you are delving into the "hidden matters of the Merciful One." Regarding your citation of the Rambam that Hashem does not perform miracles that deviate from the laws of nature for an individual—we have seen with our own eyes miracles that deviate from the laws of nature for individuals, especially in recent years. This is particularly true in matters concerning the physical body, where, time and again, mistakes have been made even after all the tests. This is in addition to the fact that new medicines are being discovered from day to day. Rather, it is necessary—and there is no other way—to strengthen one’s hiskashrus with Hashem, the Healer of all flesh who performs wonders. The "Scriptural verse" cannot be stripped of its simple meaning, which is that He performs wonders in a tangible way for an individual; the proof of this is that every single person recites this blessing [in the morning prayers]. To elaborate further on this is unnecessary.

I wish that people would not engage in the practice of "increasing knowledge," etc., in such matters; it is better to fulfill the teaching of our Sages that "a person who experiences a miracle does not recognize his own miracle." It is understood that all of the above does not in any way negate the logic that one should obtain the opinion of at least two doctors in the field and their opinion regarding procedures, as is known from the Tzemach Tzedek’s statement that the Torah grants the physician permission to heal, but not, G-d forbid, to cause depression, etc.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the festival of Shavuos and the customs you found in Chassidic texts: We spoke about this during the farbrengen this past Shavuos. Contrary to common opinion, at the time of the Giving of the Torah, the revelation of the Torah was only in a state of concealment and hiddenness. On the day of the Giving of the Torah, the Jewish people heard only the Ten Commandments, and even then, with each utterance, their souls departed, which means that there was no room at that time for understanding and comprehension; the rest of the Torah was given only in a hidden manner. As is known in many places, and in the Azharos of Rav Saadia Gaon, all 613 mitzvos and the seven Rabbinic mitzvos are included and hinted at (in the 620 letters) of the Ten Commandments. However, the hidden aspects of the Torah—the secrets of secrets, which is Maaseh Merkavah—were seen by all of Israel, and even those who were secondary to Israel (and even those among whom there was a concern of "cutting down the saplings," G-d forbid, because they were of the Erev Rav; but as for the Bnei Yisrael, their impurity ceased at the Giving of the Torah, and even after the sin of the Golden Calf, although it returned to some extent, they were nevertheless changed from one extreme to the other, even physically, as is proven in Shabbos 146a).

With the blessing that Hashem should merit you to always share good news regarding your personal matters and communal matters.

## B'Kama

B'Kama

B"H, 21 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rav and Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, engaged in the needs of the community, whose work is the work of Heaven, etc., Moreinu Harav Yehuda Zev, may he live, Segal.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh: When I am at the holy Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention you and all your family members, may they live. Especially regarding your efforts in the Yeshiva, may they be successful beyond the natural order—namely, in the study of Torah and in the "light of Torah," which is the inner dimension of Torah. For then, "the fear of Hashem is His treasure," and consequently, the verse "And He shall be the stability of your times, a wealth of salvation, wisdom and knowledge" is fulfilled, as our Sages of blessed memory explained regarding this verse. May you see good fruit in your labor—both in the children, meaning the students, and in your own children in the literal sense, and in all your descendants, especially since they are also your students.

I was pleased to see in your letter that you recognize that those who approach you with complaints regarding the study of the inner dimension of Torah are merely presenting a test. This is explained in several sefarim; seemingly, since everything is revealed before Heaven, what is the purpose of the test? Rather, the benefit is for the person being tested: that which was previously only in potential comes into actuality. Furthermore, powers that were entirely hidden are revealed within him—from concealment to revelation—and through this, an additional vitality and light is added to all his affairs in Torah and mitzvos, beyond the specific matter in which he was tested. For someone like you, further elaboration on this is unnecessary. Without a doubt, you will stand strong at your post, the holy watch, to maintain a "good eye" toward all your students and to bestow upon them from the light of Torah, which leads to the love and fear of Him, may He be blessed, and to "know Him in all your ways," in accordance with the instruction of the Baal Shem Tov—in a manner of "serve Hashem with joy."

With blessings for success in all your general and personal matters... Awaiting good tidings, signing with regards to your family,

[Signature]

#### ***B'Kama***

**Moreinu Harav Yehuda Zev:** Segal. Additional letters to him appear above, [letter] 232, and in the notes referenced there.

## 2142

B"H, 24 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn.

Furthermore, one must constantly seek out advice and methods to deceive the Yetzer Hara, so that he does not sense that one is making an effort to ensure that a particular man or woman studies Torah or increases their hiddur mitzvah.

It would be very beneficial if you were also to add to your book a subject index of the Torah discourses you cite, so that one might easily find specific topics in Chassidus and what the great luminaries, the Nasi’im of Chassidus, have said regarding them.

## 2143

B"H, 24 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, occupied with communal needs,

Since, according to your letter, this was on the festival of Shavuos, and although it seems from your letter that you do not recall the Torah you heard clearly, it is well known—as brought in several places and cited by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, author of the Shulchan Aruch and Tanya, as a halachic ruling in his Hilchos Talmud Torah (Chapter 2, Paragraph 10)—that: "In the future, one will be reminded of every study that one forgot due to circumstances beyond one's control... and even now, this Torah ascends on high... forgetfulness comes from the side of the kelipah and cannot reach higher than the Kisei..." From this, it is understood that on high, forgetfulness did not hold sway over his Torah at all.

As you requested, when I am at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, may his merit protect us, I will read your Pidyon Nefesh. May it be the will of Hashem that you be able to share good news regarding all the matters about which you wrote in the Pidyon Nefesh.

Enclosed is an excerpt from the sicha of Shabbos Mevarchim Sivan, the content of which is truly relevant all year round, since the giving of the Torah—and consequently, the receiving of the Torah—is a daily occurrence, as per the phrasing of the blessing, "**gives** the Torah," in the present tense. It is appropriate to publicize its content in the widest possible circles in a suitable manner.

With blessing.

## 2145

2145

B"H, 24 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Through the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and dedicated communal worker, Rabbi Shmuel Dovid Halevi Raitshik, a shaliach, I received your regards. Rabbi Raitshik also writes to me that your son, [name], may he live, is currently in military service.

It is surely unnecessary to remind you to awaken your son, may he live, and explain to him the observance of Torah and mitzvos in general, to the extent that it is absolutely necessary for every Jew, and especially for one who finds himself in military service. It is especially and unconditionally necessary to maintain the putting on of tefillin every weekday, for at least a few minutes, at any time during the day until sunset. This is a segulah for one who is in military service to return home whole and in good health, as we have heard this many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. And thank G-d, all those who were in the military during the previous war and followed the instructions of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding putting on tefillin, returned home whole and in good health. As a general rule, when one observes Torah and mitzvos, one is not doing a favor for Hashem Yisbarach, but rather for oneself, one's family, and one's entire surroundings. I hope that you will find the appropriate words to explain this to your son, may he live, and also to influence him for his own good. May Hashem Yisbarach help that this should come easily to you and that you will be able to report back to me with good news regarding this.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
The Secretary

P.S. Enclosed is a message that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, wrote at the time, specifically for those who were in the army.

## 2146

B"H, 25 Sivan, 5713

## 2147

B"H, 25 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, refined, and involved in communal needs, etc.,
R' Yirmiyah, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

...Surely by the time you receive this letter, you will have already received a detailed report from here via the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, refined, and involved in communal needs, etc., R' Yosef, may he live, Halevi Weinberg, the shaliach. It is certainly unnecessary to ask you to assist him with all your ability and in all the necessary ways. However, based on the ruling in the Sifri on Parshas Tzav that "one only encourages those who are already diligent," I am writing these lines to further encourage and expedite the matter. Just as with Talmud Torah, where one is obligated in every single moment, and consequently, when even a small amount of time is not utilized, it is an irretrievable loss—for even if one fills the subsequent hours, they only fulfill their own obligation—so too is it regarding matters of tzedakah connected with Talmud Torah. Since, after all, the heart of a Yid is awake to Torah and mitzvos, the sooner one encourages the donor to complete their contribution, the sooner the possibility arises for the donor to add to their previous contribution.

And great is the merit of your participation in the "Tree [of Life]," for those who hold fast to it and support it are "blessed" (*me'ushar*).

May it be the will of Hashem that the interpretation of the Zohar (Zohar Vol. III, 153b) be fulfilled in you and your household, may they live: "Do not read it as *me'ushar* (blessed), but as *me'rosho* (from his head)." This means that from his head, all blessings and successes will be drawn down. And since the body follows the head, certainly, in a manner of *davar m'shulav* (intertwined), all of the above will be drawn down into other matters as well. And according to what is explained in the Zohar (Zohar Vol. I, 220a) that the head of the family is like the head of the body, then from the "head"—the matters pertaining to the husband—blessings will also be drawn down regarding his wife and household, may they live, with whatever each one specifically requires.

With blessings for appropriate arrangements for you and your household, may they live, in both material and spiritual matters alike, awaiting good news.

## 2148

B"H, 25 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and meticulous in his communal work, etc.,
R' Avraham, may he live.

Peace and Blessing!

...2) I was pleased to hear that you are in contact with the esteemed, etc., a branch of the tree of the forefathers, Mr. Shazar, may he live. My hope is strong that this will be to the benefit of both of you together.

3) Regarding what you wrote about the economic crisis in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established: when I am at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will read your *pidyon nefesh* regarding this. On the other hand, however, I am repeatedly astonished at *anash*. For they see with their own eyes how my father-in-law, the Rebbe, prepared the cure in advance and established various ventures there from which many of *anash* could find their livelihood... I am referring, quite simply, to the vocational school, the agricultural school, the farms in the village, the expansion of the *Reshet* (network of schools) and the rescue from the missionary influence, and the most recent initiative of shipping books from here, from the Kehot Publication Society, to Eretz Yisrael. If they would look at this with an open eye, they would see that in addition to the incomparable spiritual livelihood, all of the above would provide a livelihood in the physical sense, quite literally. Even if one were to take on some role or position in these ventures, it would provide him with various connections in offices throughout the country, and consequently, it would eventually lead to a source of livelihood for one person after another, and so on. And although it is explained in Chassidus that in the worlds of *Beriah, Yetzirah,* and *Asiyah*, the world is [perceived as] simple and Elokus is [perceived as] a novelty—meaning that one needs many proofs and explanations for this—all the aforementioned matters have been clothed in the simplest of garments so as not to give room for the *Yetzer Hara* to blind the eyes of the wise. Consequently, there is no room to distort the words of the *tzaddikim*, for "your people are all *tzaddikim*..."

5) It is a great wonder that, since the Rav A.B.G., may he live, surely explained the extreme urgency required in the matter of bringing the shipment of Kehot books from here as soon as possible, the matter has nevertheless not yet been put into practice.

With blessings for proper health and for success in communal matters and in his own private matters and those of his household, may they live.
