## 2149

B"H, 27 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I have just received your letter of 24 Sivan (and in due time, your letters of 4 Iyar and 11 Sivan were also received), in which you write about the dream you had.

My advice to you is: steer clear of this path. Stop dwelling on dreams. As is explained in many sefarim, for people whose every detail of life is conducted according to Torah and mitzvos, even a dream—over which one has little control—may have some significance and cannot be entirely without meaning (though even in such a case, our Sages of blessed memory say, "There is no dream without nonsense"). However, for people of our generation, in whose lives there are many idle words, and certainly idle thoughts—devoid of content, and certainly devoid of the content of Torah and mitzvos—for such people, dreams are nothing more than just dreams. Sometimes, this is also a tactic of the Yetzer Hara to distract a person from matters of truth. Therefore, I repeat once again: do not allow yourself to dwell on thoughts about dreams.

It would be appropriate for you to have the mezuzos checked in the rooms where you sleep, as well as your tefillin, and to act with the proper energy regarding a shidduch and regarding business. Regarding the former, as I have already written to you, do not be overly selective. You may rely on the elders of Anash, may they live long. Since they are older, as the verse says, "Length of days shall teach wisdom," and especially since they can view the matter objectively, whereas one who is inside the situation may sometimes think subjectively. If you follow all of this—naturally, in addition to your regular shiurim of learning, as I wrote to you in my previous letter—Hashem Yisbarach will help you so that you will have success in both material and spiritual matters. You will be able to report good news, that you have begun to follow this, and you will see even with your physical eyes that it is worthwhile.

When I am at the Tziyun HaKadosh of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, ztzkllh"h, nbgm"y, zy"a, I will mention you for success in your affairs.

With blessings.

## 250

28 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Rabbi Ben-Zion Meir Chai Uziel, may he live and be well,
Rishon LeZion, Chief Rabbi.

May the peace of your honor increase.

I received your letter with pleasure, along with the two maamarim enclosed. I had been waiting from day to day to receive your book, *Hegyonot Uziel*, Part I, as you mentioned in your letter, and this is the reason for the delay in my response until now. I ask for your honor’s full forgiveness and pardon.

Thank you very much for this gift, and especially for the aforementioned book; the contents are worthy of their author. However, based on the words of our Sages (Bava Metzia 84a), "He would raise twenty-four difficulties for me, and I would provide twenty-four resolutions, and the subject matter would thereby become clear," I will take the liberty of offering a general observation regarding your book.

By way of introduction, based on the words of our Sages: "Whatever an experienced student is destined to innovate" (as the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya, transcribed in *Kuntres Acharon* there, 159b; and so it is in the introduction of the Shach to the Torah, *Torat HaOlah* Part II, Ch. 55, and in *Metivot* Section 2, Vayikra Ch. 22) "was already told to Moshe at Sinai." I am referring to the hidden Torah, the Torah of Chassidus. For until the experienced student reveals the matter, it is incumbent upon every individual to seek their own path and explanation regarding it, since none of us knows who the experienced student is who will reveal what was told to Moshe at Sinai. But once the matter has emerged from concealment to revelation through an experienced student, and it has become publicized and accepted among many of the Jewish people—and especially when reality itself has proven that this is indeed the truth—then it is no longer possible to say, "We have no business with hidden matters." Rather, everyone must take into account and respond in an appropriate manner to the innovation of this experienced student.

Now, most of the issues that your honor discusses in your book, which are among the foundations of our Torah, are issues deeply connected to the hidden Torah and the inner dimension of the Torah. Before the hidden Torah became the revealed possession of every ben Torah, it was possible to deliberate and discuss these problems from the perspective of secular philosophy and the like. This is because, as the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, writes in his *Iggeret HaKodesh* (Section 21), the *Zohar* and the entire wisdom of Kabbalah were "hidden in their days and concealed from all Torah scholars, except for a select few, and even then, only in private and not in public." This is not the case in these days, where, according to the directive of the Arizal, in these final generations it is permitted and a mitzvah to reveal this wisdom. Therefore, seemingly (see *Sdei Chemed*, *Pe'at HaSadeh* 16:8), there is no place for a comprehensive discussion of these problems without bringing and explaining the statements and rulings of the hidden Torah, the Torah of Kabbalah, and the Torah of Chassidus regarding these questions.

- Based on the above, it is understood that there is no contradiction at all in the fact that the Rav Saadia Gaon, the Rambam, the author of the *Ikkarim*, and so on—among the greatest Jewish thinkers who were faithful to Hashem and His Torah—discussed these questions without citing the perspective of the Torah of Kabbalah, even though, according to some opinions, it was known to them. This is because, as stated above, the experienced student had not yet come and innovated it in a way that it was publicized to all and the hidden Torah became revealed. -

Undoubtedly, your honor is familiar with the books of Kabbalah and Chassidus that discuss these questions. As is known, from time immemorial, a special affection has been held by the Sefardic sages and their rabbis for the hidden Torah. In these days, as mentioned above from the Arizal, not only is there no need to conceal these matters, but on the contrary, it is a mitzvah to reveal them.

I hope that your honor will not take offense at this observation and will judge me favorably, especially in light of what is known from the *Iggeret HaBaal Shem Tov*—the response of Melech HaMashiach that the coming of Mashiach depends on the spreading of the wellsprings (the wellsprings of the hidden Torah and the Torah of Chassidus) outward. The precision in the word **"outward"** is also well known.

With great respect and honor, and with blessings.

Following the above, I am sending your honor in a separate package the book ***Taamei HaMitzvos*** by the Admur, the author of the *Tzemach Tzedek*, in which several of the matters that your honor discusses in your book are also explained, as marked in the index of subjects there.

A minor note, yet a grave one due to the wayward among our people: I noticed that your honor cites in your letter the book *Moreh Nevuchei HaZman*, *Sefer HaTekufah*, etc. Even though there is good in everything in this world, not every mind can bear to discard the shell and search for and find the good, and eat only that.

Since your honor quotes these books in your book, even if you disagree with them, for many of the readers this will serve as an endorsement. In a simple sense, it implies that these books should also be found in their homes—at a time when, for the inhabitants of Russia and Poland in particular, the great destruction caused by these books and their like is well known. May Hashem save us.

## 2,151

B"H, 28 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Asher Zelig, may he live, Shochet and Bodek

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter and the enclosed sum—the remainder of the funds for the repair of the Sefer Torah, which each of the congregants donated according to their ability for the sake of the repair—

I was pleased to learn that there was more than enough, as this is a sign of the quality of their interest and affection.

Since in every matter one must seek a point and a way to strengthen through it the feeling of Yiras Shamayim that exists within the inner being of every Jewish man and woman, it would be appropriate for you to explain to each of the aforementioned participants what is explained in the sefarim: that there are 600,000 letters in the Torah, corresponding to the 600,000 souls of Israel, which constitute Klal Yisrael. From this, it is understood that each person must know that the matter depends upon them—to rectify Klal Yisrael by performing what is incumbent upon them in Torah and mitzvos with greater intensity and strength. Just as the kashrus of a Sefer Torah depends on every one of its letters being kosher, and the beauty of a Sefer Torah depends on every letter within it being beautiful.

The path to this is a paved road: living according to Torah and mitzvos—simply, as it sounds, in day-to-day life.

Enclosed here is a passage from a sicha of Shabbos Mevarchim Sivan, as well as a collection of letters from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, which includes a letter regarding the Hachnosas Sefer Torah into a Beis Medrash. It is surely a matter in its proper time, even though in the present case it is a repair of a Sefer Torah. It is understood that through this, you will bring merit to the many.

With blessings and regards to all the aforementioned participants, may they live.

P.S. Since these are funds belonging to the repair of a Sefer Torah, and it is known what is written in Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah (Siman 270, Seif 2) that in these days, study books are akin to a Sefer Torah in their times, I have transferred the money to the fund from which holy books are sent for Chadorim and Yeshivos.

## 2152

B"H, 28 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch,

Peace and blessing!

I received with pleasure your letter of 3 Sivan, along with the enclosures, the report on the students' studies in the daytime divisions. It is surprising that the continuation—as you mention in your letter—regarding the students who study in the afternoon has not yet been received.

It is surely superfluous to remark upon the absolute necessity of utilizing the summer days, when the students are free from their other studies, for additional hisorerus and strengthening, especially in yiras shamayim for all the students. Even though there is a ready-made excuse for this—that the students are tired from their studies throughout the year, that they travel out of town, and that the heat is difficult to bear, which generally affects the energy of the students and the administration, etc., etc.—I do not wish to repeat everything said above once again. I will only emphasize that this is nothing more than an excuse. The proof is that in all the places where they decided to actually utilize the summer days, they succeeded, despite all the aforementioned claims. And they succeeded to such an extent that for the following year, there was no need for me to prompt them again, because they themselves saw that it is beneficial even in gashmius.

With a blessing for success in your holy work, and that this may bring added blessing and success to each one of you in your personal matters as well.

## 2,554

B"H, 29 Sivan, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...I was extremely surprised by the tone of your letter... [regarding] the individual mentioned, as if these are his own private affairs and he is doing a favor by dealing with them. I am astonished that a *tamim* who has been engaged in the work of *chinuch* for many years seemingly does not grasp this matter in its entirety. For the work of Chabad *chinuch* in general, and [your work] in particular, is the concern of the *Ribono shel Olam*, and His *shaliach* in this is our *Nasi*, *k'vod kedushas* my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukul-l-h-h n-b-g-m z-y-a*. Consequently, those who are *mekushar* to *k'vod kedushas* my revered father-in-law, and even those who are merely connected to him, must—according to what is brought in *Tanya*—receive all their matters through their *Nasi*, especially since the *Nasi* is also the *Nasi* of the generation, *k'vod kedushas* my revered father-in-law.

It is just that this *hashpaah* can come in different ways, whether in a manner of *panim* (openly) or otherwise. Those whom Hashem has privileged, and whom *k'vod kedushas* my revered father-in-law has chosen so that their influence should be a conduit—the purpose of which is to draw the hearts of the sons and daughters of Yisrael to their Father in Heaven and to draw into them the light of Torah, which is the *Torah* of *Chassidus*—fortunate is their portion that they have merited that their spiritual and material influence should proceed in a manner of "face to face," and in a way that even the circumstances themselves are channels of *hashpaah* for those engaged in this work. And if there was someone who acted as the intermediary and agent in this, one is obligated to thank, praise, and laud him for having placed them upon the beautiful and good portion, both for himself and for his family, *shichyu*, in both spirituality and materiality together. And I am surprised, time and again, that even to someone like you, it is necessary to explain all of this...

With blessings for success in your holy work and in the private affairs of yourself and your family, *shichyu*.

## 2157

B”H, 2nd of Rosh Chodesh Tammuz, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Blessings and peace!

...On this occasion, I would also like to emphasize and draw attention to the story recounted in the parsha we have just read in the Torah—Parshas Korach. It is a story that should serve as a moral lesson for every Jew in general, for women in particular, and especially for the women of Nshei U’Bnos Chabad, from whom the holy Rebbes demand that they conduct themselves *lifnim mishuras hadin* in their *ahavas Hashem*, *ahavas haTorah*, and *ahavas Yisrael*, and for which they grant them the *kochos* to do so.

The story and the moral lesson are as follows:

Korach was among the most distinguished of the Jewish people; he descended from one of the finest families, was a great *lamdan*, one of the wealthiest men in the world, a very wise man, and a close associate of Moshe Rabbeinu and Aharon HaKohen. In contrast, regarding On ben Peles, one of his cohorts, we find no particular distinction: not in wisdom, not in lineage, nor in other matters.

How did their lives turn out?

The exact opposite of what one might have expected.

Korach met a devastating end, and he dragged hundreds and hundreds of Jews down with him into that misfortune.

On ben Peles, by contrast, was saved along with his entire family. He was the **one and only** person among all those who were in Korach’s congregation who did not suffer.

What was the reason for such an unexpectedly terrible end for Korach and a good end for On ben Peles?

**The influence and conduct of their wives!**

The wife of On ben Peles, in those final hours, managed to save her husband and their entire family. She was the true *akeres habayis*.

Korach’s wife, on the other hand, contributed through her words and conduct to her husband’s downfall, and to the downfall of his entire congregation. Instead of being the *akeres habayis*—the foundation of the home—she was the *okeires habayis*, the one who uprooted the home.

In the *Gemara* (Sanhedrin 109b) and in the *Midrashim*, this is recounted in detail.

All of this must, again and again, bring each and every one of us to deeply contemplate the tremendous responsibility of a woman, and the highly significant role she plays in the goodness and well-being of her husband and family.

As Shlomo HaMelech says (Mishlei 14:1): *Chachmas nashim*—the wise conduct of women—*bansa beisah*—builds the well-being of her home; in the opposite case, *rachmana litzlan*, it is as the verse says further on regarding that matter.

With blessings to each of you, and with wishes for success in your work and in your personal affairs.

## 2157

B"H, 2 Tammuz, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the congregants of Beis HaKnesses Rodef Shalom Anshei Kiev,
Toronto, may they live.

As we have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, every Jew keeps the memory of their parents and the "old country" fresh and alive. Since it is evident that you are from the Anshei Kiev of the old country, I hope that the conduct of your parents and grandparents from the old country—which was permeated with warmth and attachment to Torah and mitzvos—remains fresh in your memory and stands before your eyes. This must be maintained by every Jew, at all times and in every place, wherever they may be. For just as Hashem is eternal, so too are Torah and mitzvos eternal. Likewise, the Jewish people as a whole, and every individual Jew in particular, become united with the Holy One, blessed be He, by holding fast to Torah and mitzvos, such that "Yisrael, the Torah, and the Holy One, blessed be He, are all one."

With blessings for success to each of the congregants and their families, may they live.

## 2158

B"H, 2 Tammuz, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from this past Erev Shabbos: Regarding what you wrote concerning your wife, *tichyeh*, the language used was "that she should not publicize it." Regarding your question about a special *hanhagah* (practice), I believe I have already written to you some time ago that I have not heard of anything specific in this regard. Rather, in general, one should check the *mezuzos* in their home, and also give a few coins to *tzedakah* every morning on weekdays—this is, of course, in addition to what she surely already practices, giving *tzedakah* before lighting the candles for *Shabbos* and *Yom Tov*.

Regarding your question about the woman... who heals without medicine, etc.: on the face of it, it is not understood why one needs to resort to methods that are not understood, given that the Torah has granted permission for a physician to heal.

Enclosed is the *kuntres* that was published for the upcoming *Chag HaGeulah*, 12-13 Tammuz. Surely you will merit to share its contents with the many.

Regarding what I wrote previously about the difficulties in educating children in the *Talmud Torah*—the **general** point (because in specifics, it **varies** according to the location and the **student**) is to work at this without tiring, and through ways of pleasantness, and in the end, one succeeds.

With blessings for success in your holy work and for proper health for you and your wife, *shichyu*.

## 2160

B"H, 2 Tammuz, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and refined, involved in communal needs, R' Dovid Nosson, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter of 27 Sivan with pleasure. As you requested, when I visit the Ohel of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention those about whom you wrote.

2) In response to your question: I do not have in my possession any manuscript written by the scribe of the Baal Shem Tov.

3) Regarding your proposal to print an alphabet of the letters with their tagin (crowns) exactly as they are written in the Torah: I do not see the necessity or the benefit in this. Since such things are liable not to be treated with the proper care, it is better to limit their distribution. This does not pertain to the education of children—for in matters pertaining to education, the words of our Sages in Shir HaShirim Rabbah on the verse "and his banner over me was love" are well known. However, in areas that do not pertain to the aforementioned, our Sages have spoken at length in many places regarding the sanctity of the Ashuri script. The response of the Rambam on this matter is also well known; see also Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah, end of section 284.

4) And last but not least, I conclude my letter with a blessing of Mazal Tov, Mazal Tov, on the occasion of the marriage of your brother's daughter, may she live. May it be the will of Hashem that they build a home in Israel, an everlasting edifice, upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos as they are illuminated by the "light of the Torah"—which is the Torah of Chassidus.

With blessing.

## 2162

## 2163

B"H, 8 Tammuz, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, refined, and dedicated to communal needs,
Rabbi Refael Nachman, may he live and be well, HaKohen

Shalom u’Bracha!

After a long hiatus, I have received with pleasure the continuation of your notes. It is surprising, however, that you did not include at least a word regarding the state of your health and that of your wife, may they live. May it be G-d’s will that this is a good sign that all is well. Nevertheless, in the future, please write also regarding the aforementioned, as well as regarding your success at the Yeshivas Achei Temimim in Tel Aviv. Thank you in advance.

Regarding what you wrote in your notes about the *Chacham* (the author of the *Sdei Chemed*), it seems there is some error here. The *Sdei Chemed* came to Crimea from Constantinople (not from Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt speedily in our days) in the year 5627, and he returned to the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily in our days, in the year 5659. Thus, his stay in Crimea was 32 years, not 42. Furthermore, regarding his battle against the Alliance schools, this took place in Chevron after his return from Crimea; it is not known from any other source that this also occurred in Jerusalem. Especially since when the *Chacham* left Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt speedily in our days, he was approximately 18–20 years old, and it is unreasonable to suggest that among all the rabbis of Jerusalem, he was the one fighting against the aforementioned.

Enclosed is the *kuntres* published for the upcoming *Chag HaGeulah*, 12–13 Tammuz. Surely you will merit to share its content with the many.

With blessings for proper health for you and your household, may they live, and for success in all your endeavors.

**M. Schneerson**

## 2,164

B"H, 8 Tammuz, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote, that due to your preoccupations you are unable to participate in the aforementioned matter, etc.—I am surprised by this, for the opposite is surely the case. To what can this be compared? To a person who has become physically weak, and is told to increase his eating and drinking, but he replies that since he is weak, he lacks the strength to eat and drink, and that once he recovers, he will then increase his eating and drinking.

The same applies here: when one sees that he is preoccupied with matters that are distracting and detrimental, and which yield no satisfaction, one of the ways to be rid of this is to become preoccupied with matters that strengthen Torah and Yiddishkeit—for "one breath expels another." Especially regarding Torah, it is well known from our Sages that whoever fulfills the Torah out of poverty will eventually fulfill it out of wealth. And poverty and wealth refer not only to silver and money, but also to time, etc.

With blessings and regards to all Anash, may they live.

## 265

B"H, 9 Tammuz, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Regarding what you noted in your letter concerning a *mechitzah* in the *beis knesses*: A *maamar* on this subject was published some time ago in the monthly journal *HaMaor*, which is published in Brooklyn (Tevet 5711), by Rabbi Avraham Weinfield of New York. He cites the *Rambam* (Chapter 8 of *Hilchos Lulav* and Chapter 5 of *Hilchos Beis HaBechirah*), the *Peirush HaMishnayos* on *Sukkah*, and the *Tosafos Yom Tov*. These sources indicate that the *mechitzah* must be constructed in such a way that one cannot see through it. He also points to *Shu"t Maharam Schick* (Orach Chaim, Siman 77), where he stirred the world against those who wish to construct a *mechitzah* using pillars in a way that allows for visibility. He concludes that it is obvious that all of this applies even if all the women are careful to cover their hair and keep only a *tefach* exposed; how much more so, *a fortiori*, if they go with uncovered hair and exposed arms, where there is a double prohibition. See *Orach Chaim*, Siman 75; this is simple. The aforementioned journal from the months of Iyar-Sivan 5713 also discusses this matter.

#### ***265***

**Regarding a *mechitzah*:** See also below, Letter 284.

## 266

B"H, 9 Tammuz, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I have just received your prompt letter from the beginning of the month of Tammuz, and because of the importance of the matter, I am hastening to answer it out of the regular order of correspondence. The main purpose of my letter is to express my appreciation and commend your strength in Torah, for you have taken upon yourself to do according to your ability to raise the banner of... It is known that the Ribono shel Olam says, "When I ask, I only ask according to their strength." On the other hand, it is known that our Sages have ruled, "Whoever adds, they add to him." Since you have approached your holy work with desire and energy, from time to time they will surely grant you additional strength from Above to increase Torah and make it glorious. Fortunate is your lot, and further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

Regarding what you wrote in your letter:

1) How to conduct yourself with a student who is feared to have a negative influence on his peers—whether to distance him from the walls of the yeshiva even though this will cause him harm, or not. It is obvious that when faced with the harm of an individual versus the harm of the collective, one must be more cautious regarding the harm of the collective. However, in cases where it is possible to influence the student not to cause damage (which is only impossible in very rare instances), and through ways of drawing him near, usually one can change the student’s behavior—first so that he does not spoil others, and subsequently, that he may also rectify himself.

2) Whether you should strive to draw more avreichim and youths to enter the yeshiva, or whether you should devote yourself only to the current students of the yeshiva. The necessity of the first matter—increasing the number of students—is simple. However, you should delegate the work of drawing them near and bringing them in to the other avreichim of anash, and also to the members of anash who are always in the city. May the Ribono shel Olam grant them success, and you should assist them only from time to time as needed.

3) Your personal question regarding the fact that you possess Rabbeinu Tam tefillin and whether you should begin wearing them. If you are careful with *tevilas Ezra*—*bli neder*—and you daven according to the *nusach* of the Ari, and the tefillin have been checked, you should do as mentioned above. This is especially true now that you have begun additional work in spreading *pnimiyus haTorah*, which is also one of the distinctions in the inner dimension of things between Rashi tefillin and Rabbeinu Tam tefillin. In the language of Kabbalah, Rashi tefillin are *mochin d'Imma* and relate more to understanding and comprehension, which is the *nigleh* of Torah. Rabbeinu Tam tefillin, in the language of Kabbalah, are *mochin d'Abba* and relate more to the matters of Torah that are "implanted in the soul"—*aplayg*—and not so much to understanding and comprehension, which is *pnimiyus haTorah*. See also *Torah Or*, Parshas Shemos 52, bottom of the second column.

Enclosed is the *kuntres* and the *reshima* that were published for the upcoming *Chag HaGeulah*, 12-13 Tammuz. I am certain you will merit to utilize their content in a way that is appropriate for the students of the yeshiva and all those connected to this. May the Ribono shel Olam grant you success in all the above.

With blessings for success.

## 2167

B"H, 9 Tammuz, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter, written promptly on Erev Shabbos, in which you write that you are finally seeing positive results from your stay in your city. It is surely unnecessary to point out to you that if this much is visible to the physical eye, there is certainly much more that exists in reality which is not yet visible. May Hashem grant you success so that this, too, will be revealed.

2) Regarding what you wrote about your livelihood being difficult (and you surely have not forgotten the words of our Sages that a person’s sustenance is as difficult as the splitting of the Yam Suf), it is surprising that you did not write the details of what the final outcome was regarding the search for a suitable place for a Talmud Torah, and in time, for a shul in the other part of your city. You will surely fill me in on this when you come here.

3) Regarding what you asked me some time ago about whether it is our custom to say Tachanun on the day of a Tzaddik’s passing:

You are surely aware that even on 10 Shevat we say Tachanun. I once asked my father-in-law, the Rebbe, about this, and he answered me: "When is there a better time to beseech [Hashem] than on these days?"

4) Regarding sections 2 and 3 of your letter: since you are coming here next week, we will continue this discussion when you arrive.

5) I do not know the nature of those whom you have influenced in your city, but in general, you should explain to them the concept of the Ohel of the Tzaddik of the generation. This is also alluded to in the Gemara, in the words of our Sages that Calev prostrated himself on the graves of the Patriarchs, from which it is understood that through this he was saved from the counsel of [the spies], and on the contrary, he even inherited their portion. Therefore, they too should empower you and give you *peteklach* and the like, since they are unable to visit the holy Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, himself. You will surely find the appropriate words to explain this to them. See also Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 28, and its explanation.

6) Enclosed is the Kuntres and the Reshima published for the upcoming Chag HaGeulah, 12-13 Tammuz, as well as a copy of my general letter to Agudas N'shei U'Bnos Chabad. You will surely publicize their contents in the widest possible circles and in an appropriate manner.

With blessings for success.

## 2168

B”H, 10 Tammuz, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, R’ Avraham Sender and his wife, Mrs. Sheina Sarah, may they live:

Shalom u’Bracha!

...May it be the will of Hashem that, as per the saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, you should have a healthy and happy summer.

Based on the words of our Sages in Sotah 10a, that Shimshon was named after Hashem, as it is written, “For Hashem G-d is a sun and a shield”—which is also the allusion to the fact that in the future, Hashem will take the sun out of its sheath—and the sun in its strength in the physical sense is during the summer months, this serves as an instruction that it is the same in the spiritual sense, as physical things evolve from spiritual sources. Therefore, it is explained in Chassidus that the avodah of Hashem during the summer months is easier than during the winter months.

May you have a healthy and happy summer, both physically and spiritually, and may you be blessed to see your son and his family, may they live, and your son-in-law and his family, may they live, in peace.

With blessings for long life and good years, with all the interpretations.

P.S. I was pleased to hear that you are endeavoring to inspire others regarding the necessity of the *kav ha’avodah* (line of service). Even though you did not receive a written response to your letter, surely every matter of holiness—and certainly words of inspiration—is guaranteed to have an effect, whether it is visible to the physical eye or remains hidden for a time. See the *Kuntres Eitz Chaim* by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory, Addition 3, which states that in our time, the primary effort of the *yetzer hara* is to prevent Bnei Yisrael from the *kav ha’avodah*, and from this itself, the great necessity of this is understood.

Enclosed are the *kuntres* and the *reshima* that were published in connection with the upcoming *Chag HaGeulah*, 12–13 Tammuz, as well as a copy of my general letter to the Agudas N’shei U’Bnos Chabad, the content of which is truly relevant to all daughters of Israel. I am certain you will utilize these materials in the places you visit in an appropriate manner.

## 270

B"H, 16 Tammuz, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from 11 Tammuz, and thank you for it. Regarding the second point therein: your suggestion that he should completely abandon the matter of college—it is well known what is explained in many places, that breaking another person in matters of *reshus* (i.e., matters that are, for the other person, a matter of choice) is not desirable, especially when there is a risk that he will not comply, which would inevitably lead to a test—either breaking [the relationship] or resulting in the opposite effect. Rather, I spoke with the aforementioned individual regarding increasing his studies, both in *nigleh* and in *Chassidus*, and he generally understood from me that I find the length of his studies in college somewhat surprising. I also urged him to get into the habit of repeating *Chassidus* in public...

2) By the way, I am surprised... that for some time now, the practice of repeating *Divrei Elokus Chassidus* in synagogues by the senior students of the yeshiva has ceased. It is a great wonder, and the damage caused by this cancellation is understood. I have requested the aforementioned individual to convey to all those who were involved in this that they should continue even now. Perhaps it would be worthwhile—in order for them to have more interest and an opportunity to distinguish themselves—that they do this through their own *is'arusa* (initiative), just as is done here, where the students themselves, of their own accord, chose the *avreichim* who go to the synagogues, etc. However, it is understood that there must be supervision, in a way that they do not feel it, and instructions should also be given in such a manner; and a judge has only what his eyes see on the spot.

With blessings for proper health for you and all your household members, may they live.

Just consider: if one is so preoccupied with the expenses of the *chuppah* and its accessories—which is only a matter of one day, and most of the expense is due to the desire to find favor in the eyes of others—then how much more preoccupied should one be with the spiritual preparations, which concern the young couple for the duration of their entire lives? Further elaboration on this is surely unnecessary...

## 274

B"H, 23 Tammuz, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...It is surely known to you that regarding women, according to our Sages of blessed memory (Bechoros 45a), they have 252 limbs. Therefore, the custom is to write, **"for all** her limbs and 365 sinews," and for those who are not particular about this—we are not particular either. And all is well.

274

B.H., 23 Tammuz, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hope that your journey from Denmark went well, and that by the time this letter arrives, you will already be in our Holy Land—may it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu speedily in our days, Amen—in accordance with your planned schedule. I hope that you also utilized your travels to Eretz Yisrael to strengthen Yiddishkeit in the places where you stopped, as circumstances allowed.

In continuation of the conversation we had before your departure, I would like to reiterate my words briefly here, as well as supplement a few points, after a short preface:

It is a well-known principle in our holy Torah that every matter is by *Hashgacha Pratis*, and according to the well-known statement of our Sages, everything that Hashem does is for the good. *Hashgacha Pratis* is especially noticeable in something that happens unexpectedly or in an unusual manner. Our meeting in the days before your departure occurred at an unplanned time, and therefore I view it as a clear matter of *Hashgacha Pratis*, which you and I must strive to utilize to the greatest extent for the true good, especially in a matter that concerns the public.

It is certainly unnecessary to elaborate on the difficult financial situation of the *yeshivos hakedoshos* in our Holy Land. While *yeshivos* throughout the world struggle with their material situation—as you know well, even regarding the *yeshivos* in New York—the material condition of the *yeshivos* in Eretz Yisrael is far sharper and more difficult, due to various reasons. The situation is even more distressing when one sees that from time to time, the state of the *yeshivos* not only fails to improve, but new obstacles arise that hinder the improvement of their material situation. It is also self-evident that the difficult material situation of the *yeshivos* affects the number of *yeshiva bochurim*, regardless of the sense of *mesiras nefesh* among Jews, and especially among the youth. To a certain extent, even if small, it deters a number of parents from sending their children to the *yeshivos* in our Holy Land. For the aforementioned reasons, every *yeshiva bochur* in the *yeshivos* in Eretz Yisrael has greater value, and one must apply all means to prevent the number of *yeshiva bochurim* from decreasing, and to ensure that their numbers increase.

One of the means to this end is to improve the material situation of the *yeshivos*. It is therefore clear that one must not permit anything that could reduce the number of *yeshiva bochurim*, and even when such a possibility is merely a *safek*, one must combat it even from the perspective of a *safek*. For unfortunately, it has become evident that wherever the fate of the *yeshivos* was touched upon, all such *sfeikos* in recent times have proven to be justified.

It is therefore unnecessary to emphasize how great is the *mitzvah* and obligation of every Jew to stand on guard to protect the *yeshivos hakedoshos* in our Holy Land at this critical time. The responsibility is especially great for those who have influence over a larger circle, and even more so for those who occupy a prominent place in Jewish society and are among the pillars of *yeshiva* life.

After this preface, I come to the point regarding the project... which is intended to serve as an institution where they will teach *limudei kodesh*, such as *Gemara*, *Tosafos*, etc., and also—*lehavdil*—*limudei chol* in order to train professionals, such as engineers, doctors, lawyers, etc.

Without entering into the question itself of how advisable it is and to what extent one may create such a mixed institution—the opinion of the *Gedolei Yisrael* against this is well-known from many generations—and looking at the entire matter solely from the standpoint of the *yeshivos* in our Holy Land, there can be no doubt that the very idea of such an institution will cause *bochurim* to be drawn away from the *yeshivos*... and will generally weaken the state of the *yeshivos*, with which—and with which alone—the existence of our people is bound.

I take the full liberty to state the above so sharply because I have had the opportunity to see up close how similar institutions have affected the Jewish youth, having been in Russia, and later in Poland, Germany, France, and America. My precise knowledge from various sources regarding the different circles of youth in Eretz Yisrael confirms my opinion that such an institution for religious youth in Eretz Yisrael... will bring damage and destruction, *r"l*, incomparably more than a similar institution elsewhere, such as in America, where the circumstances, due to many reasons, are entirely different.

With blessings.

## 2176

B"H, 24 Tammuz, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs,
R' Shmuel Tzvi, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter of 17 Tammuz (may it soon be transformed into joy and gladness), in which you write that through the efforts of the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, R' Yona Eidelkopf, a Talmud Torah has been established in his growing city. According to your knowledge as a resident of the place, there is great potential for the Talmud Torah to develop to fame and glory, as there are enough parents and activists interested in an education of *yiras shamayim*, and funds, too, will not be lacking.

As is apparent from your letter, all of the above exists to a certain extent only in potential, and it must be brought from potential into actuality. As our Sages of blessed memory said, "The reader of the letter should be the messenger." I am certain that you will exert the greatest energy, and will also involve your friends and acquaintances so that all of this may be brought from potential into actuality. Surely, there will then be no shortage of G-d-fearing *melamdim* who will take upon themselves the primary work—namely, the education of the boys and girls in the spirit of *Yisrael Saba*. It is obvious that you will be a *talmid chacham* from the outset if you write regarding the implementation of all the above in the appropriate detail.

Regarding your concluding remark that you are in need of a *melamdim*, etc.: First and foremost, you should arrange for the *melamed* who is already available in the appropriate manner, as this in itself will serve as a drawing force for additional *melamdim*.

At the beginning of your letter, you write that your father was, in his early years, attached to Chabad, and was also one of the *roshei yeshiva* at the Chabad yeshiva in Chevron. Therefore, it is surprising that you do not elaborate on your *kvius itim* (fixed times) for the study of Chabad *Torah*. If in these days this is an obligatory duty for every Jew, then how much more so for the "son who is the leg of his father," who was one of the Chassidim of Chabad. Further elaboration on this is surely unnecessary.

With blessings.

## 2127

2127

B"H, 25 Tammuz, 5713
Brooklyn.

Blessings and peace!

I have received your letter regarding your son... noting that it has been several years since your son’s wedding and they do not yet have any children.

The first thing that must be ascertained is whether his wife, your daughter-in-law, conducts herself like all Jewish daughters in observing Taharas HaMishpacha. When one observes Taharas HaMishpacha, Hashem Yisbarach blesses them with healthy children—healthy physically and healthy spiritually. It is possible—if she is not currently observing Taharas HaMishpacha—that it is actually a kindness from Hashem that they do not have children yet, because Hashem wishes to bless them with children who are healthy both physically and spiritually. It is not a question that one sees people who, G-d forbid, do not observe Taharas HaMishpacha, and they have—**or so it appears**—healthy children. This is only because one does not know exactly what is happening with others. The pain that parents feel from the injustice they have committed against their own children in such cases is something they are ashamed to share; they hide the inner suffering and pain through various means and methods. If one could recount the facts that most parents share privately—the feelings of regret over not having observed Taharas HaMishpacha and the consequences that their children suffer as a result—it would save much need for discussion regarding the importance of observing Taharas HaMishpacha.

I do not wish to cause you pain, but as a mother and a woman, you should exert your efforts to ensure that Taharas HaMishpacha is observed by your son and his wife, as well as by your other children. By doing so, one is not doing a favor for Hashem Yisbarach; rather, one is doing a favor for oneself, to be spared from tragedies, Heaven forbid, regarding children and grandchildren.

With a wish that you will report good news that you have begun to take action in this matter, and with success.

**On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,**

**The Secretary**

## 2178

B"H, 26 Tammuz, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Finally—after your long silence—your letter of 15 Tammuz has been received, in which you write regarding your visit to the doctor and what he told you.

It is well known how precious the health of a Yiddishe body is in the eyes of Hashem. We have heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that once his father, the Rebbe, revealed to him: "See the great value of the body, for whose sake so much Torah and mitzvos have been poured." Consequently, it is simple that one must guard the health of one's body. Since this is one of the matters that the Torah has entrusted to the doctor to prescribe the regimen for eating, drinking, etc., one must follow their instructions. It is therefore incomprehensible that you write that because of this you cannot engage in the avodah of tefillah. If you mean that you are not eating or tasting anything before tefillah, it is well known among the Acharonim, and so have our holy Nesi'im ruled, that where it is necessary for the health of the body, it is permitted to eat before tefillah. On the contrary, it is a mitzvah and an obligation. This is especially true according to the saying of the Tzemach Tzedek, that it is better to eat for the sake of tefillah than to daven for the sake of eating. Regarding the specifics of your diet, speak with your mashpia and act according to his guidance, in accordance with the doctors' instructions.

The same applies to what you write regarding feelings of sadness. Surely this, too, can be corrected easily by taking frequent walks and the like. Most importantly, this is achieved through complete bitachon in Hashem, who leads each and every one of us—and you are included—on the path ascending to the House of Hashem. However, one must strengthen one's connection to Hashem and His Torah through ahavas Hashem, ahavas haTorah, and ahavas Yisrael. Stay away from the matter of melancholy, as it is a tactic of the yetzer hara to distract you from Torah and avodah, and primarily from the concept of "In all your ways, know Him."

I await good news and bless you with success and proper health, both physical and spiritual.

Great is the merit of your involvement in this, which will draw down for you an added measure of blessing and success in your personal affairs as well.

## 280

B”H, 26 Tammuz, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding what you write, that you perceive a decline in your spiritual state: There is no doubt that the words of our Sages are true. Since they have ruled—and it is a matter of Mishnah—that "a mitzvah draws another mitzvah," it is clear that involvement in proper chinuch, which draws the hearts of the children of Yisrael to our Father in Heaven, must necessarily draw after it more mitzvos, and not, Heaven forbid, diminish the spiritual state of the one engaged in it. This is understood with even greater force and intensity based on what is explained in Torah Or at the beginning, regarding the concept that "charity elevates a nation," and in the words of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, that one’s mind and heart become refined "a thousand times over." This is literally a thousand times over, as is proven by the language of the Midrash—that a thousand enter for Scripture, one hundred [for Mishnah], etc., and one emerges for instruction—which is explained in Likutei Torah at the beginning of the three parshiyos. However, from this very expression—that his mind and heart become refined—it is understood that, at the very least, a fixed time for Torah study must be maintained. Then, one succeeds in one hour in what would otherwise require a thousand hours. I am confident that the thousandth part of the time you used to set aside for Torah before your involvement in proper chinuch can be set aside now as well, and even more than that; and there is nothing that can stand before the will.

I was very pleased by what you wrote, that your wife maintains a connection with her former students. This will certainly bring benefit to the students in many respects. And according to the words of our Sages, that "the poor person does more for the householder than the householder does for the poor person," this will certainly also bring benefit to your wife, she should live and be well, and to her entire household.

With blessings for success in your holy work and in the personal matters of yourself and all your family members, may they live and be well.

## 2181

B"H, 26 Tammuz, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the brilliant Rabbi, the chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, whose work is the work of Heaven, etc., Moreinu HaRav Moshe Dober, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

On Monday evening, I received your two letters at once. It is a pity that you did not tell the chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, who is occupied with communal needs, etc., Moreinu HaRav Chaim Avraham, may he live, Chadakov, that you wished to come in for a yechidus since you are traveling to a place of rest, for in cases such as these, I am not stringent...

I will conclude with wishes—in the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—for a healthy summer and a happy summer, for you and for your entire household, may they live.

With blessing.

Regarding what you wrote about the discomfort in the sole of your foot: The concept of the foot and the heel has already been explained in Chassidus, specifically in their spiritual sense. When there is an increase of strength in them in the spiritual realm, an improvement will naturally be drawn down into the physical as well—see Torah Or at the beginning, and Likkutei Torah for the festivals, in the maamar beginning "Ein HaKadosh Baruch Hu ba b'trunya," and in many other places. (Based on this, one can explain the opinion [Berachos 25b] that in the heel, the verse "All my bones shall say [**'praising'** and thanking]" does not apply, for its essence is kabbalas ol and mesiras nefesh). And note the Tanchuma cited in Rashi (Devarim 2:5): "the sole of the foot," and "His feet shall stand on that day."

## 2182

B”H, 26 Tammuz, 5713
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings,

I received your letter from Monday, Parshas Pinchas, with pleasure—following your long silence—and I was happy to read that you are continuing to teach the study of Chassidus in public. Surely you will increase in this, in accordance with the ruling of our Sages, "We increase in matters of holiness." Regarding what you write about those who opposed this study, this was surely nothing more than a test—to see if you would be ashamed before those who mock, as required by our holy Torah at the beginning of Orach Chaim (both in the Tur and in the Rema, the leader of the Diaspora). Despite the concealment, you must spread the light of this Torah—which is the Torah of Chassidus—and fortunate is your portion that you stood the test. This will certainly serve as an example to others as well: that if they truly desire it, Hashem’s will shall succeed in their hands to bring the light, vitality, and warmth of Chassidus to the sons and daughters of Yisrael, wherever they may be.

Regarding your question: until now you were careful to daven at sunrise, but from here on you wish to daven with a bit more length, and also to prepare for davening through immersion in a mikveh and contemplation prior to davening.

It is already well-known that the ruling is to "prepare to meet your G-d, O Yisrael," especially regarding the matter of davening, which is the "service of the heart," and the matter depends entirely on kavanah (as fits the ruling that if the primary kavanah of the davening is missing, it is a void davening*). The manner of kavanah is not the same for all people and at all times, for "according to the camel is the burden." Since you have been stirred by the aforementioned pure thought, you certainly must act upon it. To add further strength and intensity, you should recite the short Krias Shema at sunrise, and also perform *hataras nedarim* (annulment of vows) before three people. Even though, as mentioned, this is only for added strength, it is in accordance with the nature of davening, for "the Merciful One desires the heart," and davening is a plea for mercy...

With blessings for proper health—health in physicality and health in spirituality.

## 2183

[26 Tammuz, 5713]

...And thank you for what you write regarding the farbrengen that you held on the yahrtzeit of Dovid Hamelech. Surely, in the future as well, you will utilize days of respite to gather for a Chassidishe farbrengen, to awaken ahavas Hashem, ahavas haTorah, and ahavas Yisroel. And the main thing is to commit yourselves with a firm resolution that the time has truly arrived to emerge from your limited "four amos" and to spread out, in an appropriate manner, among other circles of Bnei Yisroel to disseminate the wellsprings—the wellsprings of Chassidus, the general teachings of Chassidus, and the teachings of Chabad Chassidus. There are many ways to achieve this, and one of the ways is through public farbrengens and by making an effort to involve people—especially the youth—from various circles. Surely this will fulfill the desire and will of the Alter Rebbe, that Chabad should not be a matter of a "party," but rather that the entirety of the Jewish people should live by it.

#### 2183

## 2184

B”H, 1 Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive in due time your letter sent via the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, a man of stature and accomplishment, engaged in communal affairs, Rabbi Eli Simpson. He also spoke to me of your good works and the influence you exert in your surroundings for the sake of raising the pride of Israel and strengthening the spirit of Yiddishkeit. If in all places and at all times a good deed by a Jew is precious, then how much more so in our current time, when the concealments and obstructions that hinder everything holy and pure have intensified. According to the principle brought in the letter of the Ramban, "that which is holier than its fellow is more desolate than its fellow," it is all the more imperative to cherish every good deed and to utilize every opportunity, whether in action or speech, to strengthen Torah and Yiddishkeit. This is certainly true, and a fortiori, for those of the tribe and portion of the tribe whom Hashem has chosen to be Kohanim before Him and to serve in the Sanctuary, whose words and deeds in all the above are of manifold greater significance.

It is known that all the details of a person’s life are by Divine Providence from Him, may He be blessed. Since the matter of the *mechitzah* in the *beis knesses* has come to your attention, it is surely by way of special Divine Providence that it is in your power to act upon it. To elaborate on the great value of a *mechitzah* in a *beis knesses* is surely superfluous. If in the *Beis HaMikdash* in Eretz Yisrael, where they witnessed miracles tangibly—as the *Mishnah* states, "Ten miracles were performed for our forefathers in the *Beis HaMikdash*"—they were nonetheless required to have a *mechitzah* between men and women, as recounted in *Maseches Sukkah* and in the *Hilchos Beis HaBechirah* of the Rambam, then how much more so after the destruction of the *Beis HaMikdash*—may it be rebuilt speedily in our days—in the Diaspora, and in a *beis knesses* which is merely a *mikdash me'at* (a miniature sanctuary). This is especially true in our orphaned generation, where the matter of a *mechitzah* in the *beis knesses* is more necessary than ever. We have seen tangibly that in those *batei knesses* where they abolished the *mechitzah* or made it too small, it was nothing but the beginning of a departure and a descent from one level to a lower one, *r”l*. Afterward, they also installed a microphone on *Shabbos* and *Yom Tov*, which is an *issur d’oraisa*, and their hand remains outstretched to descend many more rungs backward. I do not wish to dwell on the shortcomings of the children of Israel, and my hope—based on the saying of our Sages that "one only encourages those who are already diligent"—is that you will employ all means and methods to nullify this evil thought of abolishing the *mechitzah* in the *beis knesses*. Explain to them—even though it is a simple matter—that when one comes before even a minor minister of flesh and blood to request even a small favor, it is a matter of etiquette, and understandable by simple logic, that one should not do things during that time that are contrary to the minister’s will, for that is in contradiction and opposition to the request. How much more so when one comes before the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He, and prays for life, children, and sustenance; it is forbidden and a grave sin to perform, at that very time, acts that defy the word of Hashem, the G-d of the world. It is known that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, would say: "It is a certainty that *ta'amulah* (propaganda/outreach) does not return empty." May Hashem grant you success, so that with ease and in pleasant ways, you may fulfill the mission of the Omnipresent, may He be blessed, that the *beis knesses* remain a house of prayer to Hashem, in which the prayers of Israel will be accepted.

With respect and blessings for success.

## 285

B"H, 1 Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and refined, engaged in communal needs, etc.,
R' Shalom, may he live.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the 25th of Tammuz, in which you write regarding the rationale for organizing a continuation of the classes of Yeshivas Achei Temimim in the summer camp, in addition to those that exist now, which, according to your estimation, might hinder some students currently in the higher classes from continuing their studies at the Yeshiva in the future; and you ask if it would be possible to send 6-7 students from here, along with a Rosh Yeshiva, to the summer camp in order to supervise the aforementioned students.

Now, certainly, adding higher classes is very, very correct (see *Likutei Torah, Shelach 38c*).

Regarding the matter of sending students from here, this must be discussed with the administration of the Yeshiva here. But on the face of it, there are several difficulties with this. The main point is that, seemingly, the parents of the aforementioned students would not agree to this, as it is contrary to the usual path—for people travel from a small city to a large city, and from a small Yeshiva to a larger Yeshiva, and not the reverse. You surely also remember the attempt in... regarding this, which did not succeed, even though not all the conditions were the same. This is in contrast to if you were to bolster your efforts regarding the boys and bochurim in your city, which is likely much easier. In any case, I am not ruling out the matter, and as mentioned, you should discuss it with the Yeshiva administration.

With blessings for success.

## 286

B”H, 2 Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned man, a man of knowledge who engages in communal needs, etc., Rabbi Shimshon Raphael, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I recently received the annual booklet of "Young Israel" along with the President’s report. It was surely sent at your suggestion, and I thank you for bringing it to my attention. I was pleased to see in several places the stance of "Young Israel" regarding religious matters—for instance, in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt, regarding education in general and the conscription of girls, and in our country regarding the obligation to maintain boundaries from the Conservatives. The blurring of lines in this regard is even worse than the damage caused by their mere opposition. And although, given the seriousness of these matters, the stance of "Young Israel" should have been emphasized even more and with greater sharpness—especially since, given the current climate, it is an opportune time to voice firm and clear positions that are ready to be accepted, and furthermore, since it is the nature of American youth to view compromise as a complete "bluff"—it is my hope that in practice, their stance will not lack the necessary firmness and sharpness, and that their actions in this regard will be carried out with the appropriate vigor.

I will take the liberty of adding one brief remark, even though I went through the booklet quickly due to a lack of time: while it is necessary to take into account the achievements attained during the past year’s work, as this serves as spiritual encouragement for the continuation of the work, on the other hand, one must be careful that this satisfaction does not lead to saying in one’s heart—and perhaps even with one’s mouth—"I have already done enough, and I will be content with my lot." Simultaneously with the enumeration of accomplishments, one must also address what has not yet been done and the shortcomings in the work (for all human endeavors are inherently lacking in perfection).

I see from what is written explicitly, and even more so between the lines, that you have played a major role in maintaining the appropriate approach, in the spirit of Torah and tradition, toward several important issues. It was pleasant for me to see in several places in the report that the leadership of Young Israel also recognizes this, and not only does it not "frighten" them, but on the contrary...

On this occasion, I wish to express my gratitude—in addition to what I conveyed through the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned man who engages in communal needs, etc., Rabbi Chaim Mordechai Aizik Hodakov, may he live—for your gift: the book *Likutei Torah* on the Book of Devarim, the first edition. And since the *Sefer HaMitzvos* by the Tzemach Tzedek has just been published in a new edition with additions, I have requested that it be sent to you in a separate package. There is no doubt that you will be able to utilize the *maamarim* in this book and their content in your own sermons and discourses.

With blessings for success in your work and in your personal affairs.

#### ***286***

## 2187

B"H, 7 Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, involved in communal needs, etc.,
R' Avraham, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from Motzaei Shabbos Chukas, the 26th of Tammuz, and Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av.

Regarding your observation as to why the teachings of Chassidus are called **Chassidus** (a name used by our Rebbe HaZaken himself, as is known from the *Iggeres HaKodesh* regarding the matter and order of *avodah* in the study of Chassidus, printed in *Ginzei Nistaros*, p. 45) rather than being named after the Rebbes, etc.:

It is similar to why the Torah of Hashem in its entirety is called "Torah"—named for its function, which is a language of instruction (*hora'ah*) for daily life for the soul as it is bound within the body. This is also the case with Chassidus; the name indicates the purpose. As is known from the statement of our Rebbe HaZaken when he was asked what Chassidus is: he replied, "To become someone who is not particular about his own loss, provided that he helps another," based on the teaching of our Sages in *Niddah* (17a).

It causes me great distress—as I have written many times—regarding the delay in sending the books of Kehot Publication Society to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt speedily. Especially since the months of Elul and Tishrei are fast approaching, and arrangements should have been made so that the books, particularly the books of Chassidus, would already be there by then, so that they could be distributed at an affordable price.

Enclosed is the *kuntres* that was published recently.

With blessings for success in all your affairs.

## 290

B"H, 7 Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, R' Avraham Yaakov, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I trust you have received my letter—a response to yours. Since it has been a long time since I have received any news from you, and although the general presumption (*chazakah*) is that when one does not write, it is a sign that all is well, it is well known that the *Shulchan Aruch* (Yoreh Deah, at the beginning) rules that in a place where it is possible to verify, one does not rely on a *chazakah*. Therefore, I am certain you will also inform me explicitly.

Enclosed is a *kuntres* that discusses the concept of "remembrance"—both that which Hashem requests of Yisrael and that which Yisrael requests of Hashem—as explained therein. The attribute of Hashem is "measure for measure": when one remembers his fellow for good and for blessing at all times, his reward from Heaven is doubled, for through this, Hashem remembers both the one who remembers and the one who is remembered, to fulfill the needs of each. This can be extended to the matter of "a person should not take leave of his fellow except through a matter of *halacha*," for through this, one remembers him. In this, too, the aforementioned three aspects are present, serving as a *segulah* that one will remember his fellow, and that the remembrance will be bound up with a matter of *halacha*—the "walking" (*halichah*) of Hashem, for "the ways (*halichos*) of the world are His" (Chavakuk 3:6). This is based on the *Midrash* that Hashem "walked" a journey of 500 years to acquire a name for Himself (Koheles Rabbah 7:1), and this is achieved through Torah. Further elaboration for one such as you is unnecessary.

With the blessing that Hashem should transform these days into joy and gladness, speedily in our days, and with honor.

***

**290**

**R' Avraham Yaakov:** Neimark. Additional letters to him appear above, Vol. 6, 1515.

**Kuntres:** *Zachor Hashem* (Sefer HaMaamarim 5713, p. 554; Sefer HaMaamarim of the Rebbe Shlita, Likkutim, p. 483).

## 291

B"H, 7 Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter informing me of the good news that the members of your congregation have decided to provide a significant increase to your salary. What I found particularly gratifying in this is that it serves as a sign that they value the role of a Rav and a guide in the path of Torah and mitzvos. Surely you are familiar with the adage of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that one must be wary of the feeling of self-satisfaction. For the most part, the Yetzer Hara uses this to convince a person that he has already done enough—the proof being that even others acknowledge it, and furthermore, express their appreciation publicly. This then leads to a situation where, in terms of character development, it is an undesirable state; it hinders one’s avodah as it should be from this point forward, and who is to say that one will increase their avodah as the needs of the hour demand?

On the contrary, with every such event, one must conduct a personal accounting: if one has acted in a measure that has earned him gratitude and his efforts are recognized, then had he truly fulfilled his role in the fullest sense of the word, it would have been done many times over. Therefore, one must cherish every moment and opportunity from here on to fill in what is lacking. Further elaboration on this is surely unnecessary, just as it is unnecessary to add that in Lubavitch, there is no custom of preaching mussar. The intention in speech or writing is only because of the strong confidence that it will lead to action, and consequently, this is not mussar, but rather a preparation for a mitzvah (which is performed by others).

It causes me distress that you do not bring good news regarding your true settling down, specifically concerning a good shidduch. Even though it is known from our Sages that it is as difficult as [the splitting of the Red Sea], the remedy is also found in the Shas: "According to the camel is the load." Consequently, the possibility is given to every person that if he only follows the instruction of our Sages—to follow the path of a man, to return, etc.—he will find a wife, find goodness, and draw favor from Hashem, the Good. Here, too, as mentioned above, my intention is not mussar, but rather for the sake of action. Although I have already written to you about this many times, I am writing again, and surely you will not take offense, for my intention is only for your benefit.

Enclosed is the Kuntres that was just published, and surely you will merit to share its contents with the many. May the Almighty turn these days into gladness and joy, speedily in our time.

With blessings.

## 292

B"H, 7 Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod,
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters dated the 19th, 24th, and 25th of Tammuz, along with their enclosures...

Regarding the printing of a booklet containing *chiddushei Torah* from the *ramim* and, primarily, from the students: generally, in booklets of this nature, the focus is on the students' *chiddushei Torah*, and only in isolated cases do the *ramim* also participate with some of their own *chiddushim*... It is a worthwhile endeavor to publish such a booklet.

However, it is essential that every single booklet include a *maamar Chassidus* and a *sicha* (specifically those *maamarim* and *sichos* that are most relevant to *yeshiva* students). After all, one must not forget what my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe (Rashab), *n.e.*, wrote regarding the purpose of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim; see *Kuntres Eitz HaChaim*, Chapter 22, and the addition there. [See also] the *sicha* "Kol HaYotzei L'Milchemes Beis David." Regarding what you wrote—that such a booklet has not yet appeared in Eretz Yisrael—I believe one does appear, and it is called *HaNe'eman*. In any case, it is worthwhile to prepare material for the aforementioned booklet.

When the matter is closer to fruition, it will be possible to decide whether to unite it with [...] a similar project from Yeshivas Toras Emes, and perhaps also from the *yeshiva* here. But it is still too early to decide on this. Consequently, if you wish to proceed with this discreetly, for the reason you mentioned, you may do so; it is possible that your *yeshiva* could first publish a booklet independently, and later join it with other booklets.

With blessings for success in your holy work,

**M. Schneerson**

## 2193

B"H, 7 Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, involved in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Yitzchak, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

Regarding your observation on Rashi in Shabbos 55a, where he begins with the middle letters and afterwards [discusses] the first and last: this can be explained in two ways: 
a) The novelty here is that the *Mem* is the middle letter, which is only [the case] in the combination of the letters *Man-Tzaph-Chach*. 
b) According to the verse, "I am the first and I am the last," etc. "I am the first" refers to before the creation of the world, and "I am the last" refers to when they [the worlds] will be nullified; thus, the "middle" letters represent the present state, and from this he brings proof regarding "I am the first and I am the last." This is similar to what you wrote, that it is akin to *Melech, Malach, Yimloch*—where *Melech* (King) is in the present tense, and from this we also know *Malach* (was King) in the past, and *Yimloch* (will be King) forever and ever (see the Tzemach Tzedek’s commentary on *Yehi Kavod*).

Regarding what you wrote about *Ana B'Koach* and *Kiddush Levanah*—see *Shaar HaKollel*. Regarding *Sefiras HaOmer*—see the *Siddur* of the Arizal and *Sefer Derech Mitzvosecha*, p. 54, that it is called *tenufah* (waving).

***

**Rabbi Yitzchak:** Dubov. Additional letters to him—see above 1898, and the references in the notes there.

**Regarding Ana B'Koach:** It is explained in *Shoresh Mitzvos HaTefillah* (122b) that wherever one requires the level of the soul’s ascent, one recites *Ana B'Koach*. Based on this, [one can understand] why we recite *Ana B'Koach* after *Sefiras HaOmer* and after *Kiddush Levanah*.

## 294

B"H, 7 Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Although I have not received any letters from you personally, I am nonetheless pleased to receive regards from you from time to time through good friends. May Hashem help that you should always be able to report good news about yourself, both in material and spiritual matters.

I hear that there are certain branches of commerce that are not currently going as the merchants had hoped. Surely, one must view this as a test (*nisayon*) through which Hashem wishes to try Yidden. Even though He, blessed be He, knows that a Yiddishe heart is always open and responsive to Torah and mitzvos, nevertheless, in order to satisfy the *Beis Din* of angels who do not wish to believe that a Yid will withstand the *nisayon*, Hashem shows them: "See, even though the *yetzer hara* can convince a Yid that he must reduce his *tzedakah* because business is not as it was before, Yidden are quite wise. They understand that this is only intended to test them." When one withstands the *nisayon* and understands the true intent behind it, not only will business become as good as it was before, but on the contrary, it will become even better than before. For a father appreciates when his son understands the true intent (*kavanah*) behind the father’s actions, and the more the child demonstrates his wisdom in this, the greater the gifts he receives from the father.

Merchants say that the older one gets, the more one understands the nature of commerce. Therefore, having been in business for a long time, you will understand Hashem’s intent in the aforementioned situation. Just as with a good investment—whether it is a hotel or a business—not only should one not reduce Hashem’s share in it, but on the contrary, one should allocate an even larger account to His share. In that case, Hashem fulfills His promise in the Torah, "Tithe so that you may become wealthy" (*aser bishvil shetis'asher*), granting His partner an even greater income than before.

I hope that your state of health is better than when you were in New York, and that you will also be able to report good news regarding your sister, Mrs. ..., *tichyeh*.

With blessings,

## 295

B”H, 8 Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...I was pleased to hear that you view the mosdos in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) with a favorable eye, and that you inform me of their positive qualities. May it be that, in time, these will be intrinsic virtues, and not merely because you are comparing them to the shortcomings of the mosdos abroad. It is a well-known saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, regarding how careful one must be with the feeling of satisfaction. For the most part, the yetzer hara uses this to lull one to sleep and to awaken a sense of self-importance and ego, etc., which, as a result, spoils even what has been accomplished until now. In truth, I am willing to overlook even this concern, provided that there is something to be satisfied with, in a measure appropriate to the will of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the founder and director of these mosdos...

Enclosed is the Kuntres that was just published, and surely you will merit to bring merit to the many through its content. May Hashem turn these days into gladness and joy, speedily in our time.

With blessings, and looking forward to good news.

## 296

B"H, 10 Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Your letter has just been received, in which you request a blessing for your father, who is involved in a dispute regarding an inheritance. When I am at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nebg"m, zya*, the Nasi of Yisrael, I will mention your father, *shiya*, for livelihood in abundance. It is surprising that you did not write your father’s name along with his mother’s name—which I am sure you will provide at the next opportunity.

It is also surprising that you do not write anything regarding your own studies, both in the revealed Torah and in Chassidus. According to our Sages, "a son brings merit to his father," and it is understood that if you are exerting yourself for your father's success in the aforementioned matter and in other areas by writing a letter to me, then all the more so must you do everything in your power to assist him. This is accomplished by elevating your own *avodah* in the three pillars upon which the world (and this includes the "small world," which is man) stands: Torah, *avodah* (tefillah), and *gemilus chasadim* (good *midos*).

Specifically, since this matter concerns an inheritance, you should strive in the areas regarding which we say every day in our *tefillah*, "How beautiful is our inheritance." You are surely aware that this primarily refers to the matter of *emunah* and the hidden love—which also includes *dichilu* (awe)—that we possess as an inheritance from our forefathers, as is explained at length in the Tanya.

May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant you success, that you may strengthen yourself and increase your courage in *ahavas Yisrael*, love of Torah, and love of Hashem, and that you may ascend in your *avodah* each and every day.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

**The Secretary**

## 2197

B"H, 10 Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter of 4 Menachem Av with pleasure, as well as the one preceding it. Although you do not write details in your second letter, since its content is that from now on peace will prevail between you and all of anash—may they live—I was very pleased by this. May it be His will that it be for long days and good years, both materially and spiritually.

I have already said that since in this month the damage was caused by baseless hatred, the rectification must be measure for measure—baseless love. Moreover, since the measure of good is greater, the love must be many times over. And if this is true for the general public, then how much more so within the ranks of anash, who have been educated and follow in the ways of the Nesi’im of Chabad and the Nesi’im of Chassidus in general, headed by the Baal Shem Tov, whose well-known adage is that love of a fellow Jew and love of Hashem are one and the same.

With blessings for proper health and for things to be arranged appropriately, both materially and spiritually.
