## 2198

B"H, 12 Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was distressed to learn that you are again suffering from your leg and that a doctor is treating you. Surely, even while you follow the doctor’s instructions, you should not let it weigh heavily on your heart. As is well known, the Tzemach Tzedek explained the Sages' teaching that "the Torah granted permission to the physician to heal"—this means that permission and power were given to heal, but not to make things heavy on the heart. I look forward to hearing good news from you, and I thank you in advance.

Enclosed is the Kuntres that was recently published. I have already written that in this month, when the destruction came about through Kamtza and Bar Kamtza—baseless hatred—the remedy is to grasp the opposite extreme (in accordance with what the Rambam writes in Hilchos De'os, Chapter 2), which is Ahavas Yisrael, baseless love (baseless according to human intellect, for according to Torah, one must love every single Jew, as explained in Tanya, Chapter 32, and in the Sefer HaMitzvos of the Tzemach Tzedek regarding the mitzvah of Ahavas Yisrael, etc.). Then, Hashem will show us favor and take us out of this Galus, for "you were sold for nothing [chinam]," and consequently, "you shall be redeemed without money."

With blessings for a complete recovery.

## 299

B"H, 12 Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn

To the Organization of N'shei U’Bnos Chabad in London,
May Hashem grant you life,

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 3 Menachem Av, in which you write about your future work plans. It is surely unnecessary to point out to you that you must draw more members into the organization. N’shei Chabad are not only those who were born into a Chabad family or who have found themselves in a Chabad environment, but also *al shem ha’asid* (with an eye toward the future), as through an appropriate approach, they too will become closer to the *raayon* (idea) of Chabad. You surely know the *ptagam* (saying) of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the name of our Rebbe HaZaken—*ztzukulleh"h nbg"m zi"a*—that Chassidus Chabad is not only for a portion of the Jewish people, but for the entire *Klal Yisrael*. The words of the *Tzaddik*, our *Nasi*, will certainly be fulfilled, but it takes time, and the speed of this fulfillment depends on the energy of the work, through which one reaches the goal all the sooner.

Regarding your question on how to study Chumash and the other subjects: this should be adapted according to what is better for the members and what they prefer. It is also necessary to study the *dinim* that arise in daily life. You should consult with the *zikeinei Anash* of your city, who will indicate to you the *sefarim* from which one can learn the necessary *dinim*. Hopefully, you have the *sichos* from several years that have been published by Merkas L'Inyonei Chinuch, in which there is a wealth of material for all the weeks of the year.

With blessings that the *Ribono shel Olam* grant success to each and every one of the members, along with all their family members, in all that they require, and that you may always be able to share good news.

In certain cases, it is much easier to accomplish this in summer locations, where women are free from household chores and have a greater inclination to listen to new ideas, especially if one presents them in a suitable manner. It is a well-known saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that "one only accomplishes if one acts."

I was especially pleased to read in your letter that you are working on involving children during the summer months and connecting them with Beis Rivkah. Beyond the benefit of this in itself, it is also certain that it will leave a lasting impression on them, both regarding the children themselves and regarding their influence in their parents' homes.

May Hashem grant success to each one of you in whatever you yourselves and your entire families are in need of.

With blessings for success,

## 203

203

B.H., 23 Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Surely you are aware that it is not the Lubavitcher approach to preach morality, and I have no intention of changing this approach. Furthermore, it is not the Lubavitcher way to do things merely so that one can say afterward, "And what have I said? I have saved my own soul." Nevertheless, I am writing this letter because I hope it will lead to a prompt change in your conduct regarding the institution. And this change should come not only from a place of *kabalas ol* (accepting the yoke), but because you yourself will recognize that this is not the way. After this introduction, I approach the matter itself:

One must always remember that *K'vod K'dushat* my father-in-law, the Rebbe, entrusted you with the administration of the Yeshiva... From this, we know two things: a) That you **have** the capability to lead the institution **according** to the will and intent of *K'vod K'dushat* my father-in-law, the Rebbe; and b) That this will be demanded **of you**, and not of others, or the *baalei batim* of... And when one wishes to divert their attention from this, it does **not** change the reality itself. For, as has been said, *K'vod K'dushat* my father-in-law, the Rebbe, did not give anyone a task that was not according to their strength, nor did he demand it **of** them; rather, he connected it to the fact that this should be **their** conduit through which they have blessing and success in all **their** affairs—both in what they were given to do and also in the personal matters of themselves and their families, *shichyu*. However, knowing at the same time that one can sometimes forget this, *K'vod K'dushat* my father-in-law, the Rebbe, showed them blessing and success so that it would be easier for them to pass through the *he'lem* and *hester* (concealments). And when you and your wife, *tichye*, reflect well upon the past few years, since the *histalkus* of *K'vod K'dushat* my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and—honestly—you will see many instances of *hashgacha pratis* and success...

It goes without saying that one cannot demand from the *baalei batim* of... the same level of understanding as one can demand of you, into whom *K'vod K'dushat* my father-in-law, the Rebbe, poured [his influence] year after year, and through that, prepared him for the position upon which **he** placed him.

Surely you know the saying of *K'vod K'dushat* my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that "our *ziburis* (inferior) is better than their *idit* (superior)." And this is said not only regarding the fact that it is so in *Olam HaAtzilus*, but also in this physical *Olam HaZeh*, and especially in the institutions of *K'vod K'dushat* my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for which he *moser nefesh* (sacrificed himself) and promised *hatzlacha muflaga* (extraordinary success), provided that one strengthens oneself to walk in this path and fulfills his intent, which is the *kavana elyonah* (the supreme intent).

And after reflecting on all of this, I want to say only briefly what I would do if I were in your place and standing in such a position, and in which I see, without doubt, success in both material and spiritual matters. And that is:

Exert **all** your strength so that all the teachers are those to whom *K'vod K'dushat* my father-in-law, the Rebbe, gave strength. And even if it seems that in certain details they have a shortcoming, it is without a doubt that every teacher, whoever he may be, is not free of shortcomings. But only those educated by *K'vod K'dushat* my father-in-law, the Rebbe, have this blessing and success to raise students who are *yirei Shamayim* (G-d-fearing), who will consequently be what a student of his Yeshiva needs to be... And it is **certainly** understandable that in such a Yeshiva, a teacher must not be someone who is not a Jew, or someone who is not a *shomer Torah u'mitzvos*. And I am not saying this only regarding whether one is permitted to hire such people according to *Shulchan Aruch*; rather, I am speaking for the sake of the success and benefit of the institution, and for the sake of the success and benefit of the people who are connected with this institution...

With the blessing that you will reflect upon this as is fitting, and act accordingly, and immediately.

## 204

B"H, 23 Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to hear that you have accepted my words regarding the privilege of your work in the institutions of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. However, I must also clarify a point, as it seems one aspect of my letter was not sufficiently clear: in accordance with the magnitude of the privilege and the work in the institutions of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, which serves as the conduit for all that is needed—both materially and spiritually—for those who participate in this work, it is a simple matter that the more the institution’s benefit, development, and success grow, so too will the success and blessing bestowed upon those who work in these institutions grow. And for the institutions to succeed, they must be aligned with the will and intent of my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

It is unnecessary to elaborate on how much my father-in-law, the Rebbe, insisted that every matter be conducted with order internally, and certainly regarding matters directed outward. Therefore, in all the various institutions, he established a central point from which guidance would emanate to all branches (even if the nature of that guidance—whether it is only general or also specific and detailed—varies according to the place and the individuals). It is understood that this does not in the least diminish or belittle anyone’s stature; it concerns only external matters—that is, the methods by which the work can be carried out without friction and with a unified front toward the outside. For it is understood that those on the outside watch with seven eyes to find a flaw or a shortcoming, and it is inevitable that they will seek ways and pretexts to create contradictions between one and another, etc. And although there are no actual conflicts, until the matter is clarified through *ratzo v'shov*, there can be significant damage.

I will repeat once more that this is not a diminution of anyone’s stature, Heaven forbid, but for the organization of the work, it is necessary that there be one conduit, and that all other institutions receive [guidance] through this conduit, even if at many times it serves only as a passage and not as an *hitlabshut*. I hope that my words above are sufficient to explain the entire course, order, and *hishtalshelus* of the work.

The students in the list you sent—I mentioned them while at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and surely he will arouse Divine mercy for each of them in whatever they require.

I believe I wrote last year that if the custom of the students traveling home for the month of Tishrei is unavoidable, then they must be given spiritual provisions for the journey—that is, instructions in conduct and easily understood *maamarim* that they can study while they are in their respective locations, and especially that they be able to speak in public or teach them to others. But as mentioned, this is only if it is an absolute necessity; the effort should be to the contrary—that is, during the *Yomim Nora'im*, the *Aseres Yemei Teshuvah*, and the Holy Day [Yom Kippur], they should be together in the same institution through which they receive guidance in *yiras shamayim*. The magnitude of the benefit in this, and the impact of publicizing such conduct, is immeasurable—both for the students themselves and even more so for their surroundings. And although one should not interfere with their customs, which they have received as a tradition from generations, surely one can find several Chabad customs that they can uphold without interfering with the aforementioned.

I was pleased with what you wrote regarding the celebration of the *Chag HaGeulah*. It is surprising that there is no effort to have such matters printed in the newspapers that appear in the area and the country. Even if caution is needed "not to draw attention," surely a middle path can be found.

Enclosed is a *kuntres* that was published recently; surely you will merit the public with it, primarily the students, may they live.

With blessings for success in your holy work and in your personal affairs.

## 225

B"H, 23 Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...I am writing to him regarding the fact that the students travel to their homes for the entire month of Tishrei. This practice is contrary to reason and contrary to the intent of guidance in yiras shamayim. If such guidance is necessary throughout the entire year, then there is no more opportune time and no greater eis ratzon for this than during the days of Selichos, the Yomim Nora'im, and so on. If this practice cannot be changed, they must at least be equipped with spiritual provisions, both for their own sake and for the sake of the places to which they are traveling. And if it is possible to hold back at least the older students in the yeshiva for Rosh Hashanah, Aseres Yemei Teshuvah, and the Yom HaKadosh, this time should be utilized to bring them closer to the customs of Chassidim and their guidance. Even though one **should not** interfere with their own good customs that they have received from generation to generation, there are nevertheless Chabad customs that they should be made aware of, so that they may conduct themselves accordingly without interfering with the customs of the Sephardim.

## 208

B"H, 23 Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding what you conclude in your letter, that I should not be upset that your son, may he live, did not travel on the shlichus of the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch: I am not upset about this, but I am saddened. For these trips, even though "externally" it is said that they are on behalf of the Merkos, in truth, the matter is part of the program for the chinuch of the avreichim and brings them great benefit in several respects. According to my assessment of your son's, may he live, soul-character, the benefit for him would have been in several ways even greater than for the other avreichim hatmimim. This is not only for the reason that an avreich yeshiva should not conduct himself differently than his peers, but—and this is the main point—because such a trip on shlichus would have given him a great deal. However, one does not cry over the past.

Enclosed is the Kuntres that was recently published, which I am sure will interest you, may he live.

With respect and blessings, and for proper health for you and all your family, may they live.

## 210

B"H, 24 Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your *pidyon nefesh*, and I will read it at an auspicious time at the holy resting place of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. It seems I have already written to you that you must be more careful regarding the preservation of your physical health in the literal, material sense. Consequently, you must follow the instructions of the doctors in this regard and not play games with it, for this too is a part of the holy Torah, just like all other *mitzvos*. The explanation of our Alter Rebbe is well-known (transcribed in *Hayom Yom*, Erev Rosh Hashanah): "One has absolutely no grasp of how precious a Jewish body is to Hashem." This is a well-known concept in *Chassidus* and requires no proof. As for those who say that they are being *mehader* (scrupulous in observance) and therefore do not take care of their physical health, this is actually the opposite of *hiddur*, and so on. You should conduct yourself in the manner described above, and may Hashem grant you true health, both physically and spiritually...

## 211

B"H, 24 Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter in which you ask regarding what is written in the maamar *Lecha Amar Libi* of 18 Elul (Kuntres 81), that a person must beseech Hashem to find good understanding in *Elokus*—you find it difficult to understand why he does not say this regarding the comprehension of Torah as well.

The explanation for this is that within the study of Torah itself there are several levels, and their order is from below to above: 
a) One who studies Torah solely in order to know the practical *mitzvah* to perform—meaning, he makes the Torah secondary to another matter. 
b) One who studies Torah in order to know it, to understand it, and to comprehend it. 
c) One who studies Torah while knowing that this is the wisdom and will of the *Ribono shel Olam*, and since He and His wisdom are one, through this, the Yisrael who studies becomes—by means of the *Oraisah* (Torah) that he studies—one with *Kudsha Brich Hu*. 

According to what is explained in many places, and also in the books of the Maharal of Prague (see *Netzach Yisrael*, Chapter 3) regarding the concept that the *Ribono shel Olam* is the Knowledge, the Knower, and the Known, the person who studies then becomes a *mashpia* (influencer) upon the Torah, for he connects it with the Giver of the Torah. As is known, this is the meaning of the two parables brought in *Chazal*: sometimes Yisrael is called the bride, and their influence is through the Torah—as *Chazal* say, "On the day of His wedding," this refers to the giving of the Torah—and sometimes Yisrael is called the groom and the Torah the bride, meaning that Yisrael is the *mashpia* and the Torah is the *mekabel* (recipient). It is obvious that in the third type of study, he attains in the Torah not only the logic and wisdom contained therein, but also the *Elokus* within the Torah. This is the meaning of the statement in the maamar that one must beseech Hashem regarding the matter of *Elokus* comprehension, for this is also the ultimate purpose of Torah study.

2) Regarding your question that you pray regularly in a *minyan* that uses our *nusach*, and you are concerned about the *tekios*—whether they are as meticulous as possible:

*Chazal* have said, "Whoever **establishes** a place for his prayer, the G-d of Avraham is his help." Therefore, it does not seem right to me that you wish to change your physical location, especially since the *nusach* there is different from the one you pray with. Furthermore, according to *nigleh*, it is not advisable to do so during the *Yomim Nora'im*, because the *shaliach tzibbur* recites *piyutim* in the middle of the *brachos* of *Krias Shema*, and for us, this is not the accepted practice due to the *hefsek* (interruption) in the *bracha*. Why should you join a congregation where that would be your *shaliach tzibbur*, given that until now you did not hold that this is permissible? 

Furthermore, there is an additional matter if you pray in the *beis medrash* where you have been until now: since you have some concern regarding the manner of the *tekios*, you can *oivarnen dos* (warn/caution them about this), and in doing so, you will be among those who "merit the masses." May the *Ribono shel Olam* bless you with proper health—(since you are concerned, according to your words, regarding the voice, and the days of *Tekios* are approaching, it is worthwhile that you study the *drushim* for *Rosh Hashanah*, especially those in the *Siddur* and in the book *Ateres Rosh*, where the source of the voice and the manner of its expansion are discussed. When you complete your knowledge of the spiritual aspect of the matter, the *Ribono shel Olam* will surely fulfill its corresponding physical aspects. It is understood that you must also have a hold on the ways of nature, which is by following the instructions of the doctor).

With blessings for proper health in both physicality and spirituality together.

## 2112

B"H, 24 Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim
in Montreal,
May Hashem preserve them and grant them life.

Peace and Blessing!

...I have explained many times that the principle of "we elevate in matters of holiness and do not lower" [ftnref_X_Y] is a ruling of our Sages, and it applies to all matters of holiness. This is all the more true regarding an institution connected to chinuch, as the very essence of chinuch is like the matter of sowing and planting, where it is an absolute necessity that it must constantly grow and progress. Regarding our situation, although your institution is called a "Yeshiva," it appears that for the time being, it is merely a matter of Talmud Torah, or at most, a Yeshiva Ketana. Even though in the early years there was apparently an opinion among some of the board members that, eventually, it must become a [full] Yeshiva, from year to year the matter has stagnated. Furthermore, they find reason after reason—"it doesn't read well"—and since the will influences the intellect, reasons sprout one after another as to why the thing is impossible.

Through Hashgacha Pratis, you have received ready-made students from the children of Anash who came from overseas, as well as potential students from the G-d-fearing refugees who came to live in your country. Hashem also provided you with Roshei Yeshiva suitable for the aforementioned, and this, too, without any effort on your part.

...I told them calmly and repeatedly that this is the success of their institution, and consequently, one must seize the opportunity and, as soon as possible, do everything possible to transform their institution into a [full] Yeshiva. I hoped, having already seen many miracles beyond the natural order that were brought about by the arousal of Rachamim from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisrael, that in this matter, too, he would arouse Rachamim upon them so that they would see and understand the situation, and that this is their happiness and success—both for the institution and for the members of the administration, they and their families, may they live.

With a blessing for success in your holy work, in accordance with the intent of our Nasi, my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

## 2113

B"H, 28 Menachem Av, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and meticulous in his communal work,
Rabbi Yosef, may he live, HaLevi

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 17th of Menachem Av. I was pleased to hear that you intend to visit additional countries in Africa that you did not visit previously. We have discussed this many times: it is essential for all our institutions to fulfill the ruling of our Sages to "always increase in matters of holiness," for the success of our endeavors depends upon this. As the saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, goes: in our times, it is like one climbing a very steep mountain. On level ground, a traveler can stop for a time to rest, but on a steep incline, if one stands still, it is—to use a common expression—a retreat; he slides further and further down, G-d forbid. I am certain you will investigate the possibility of increasing the number of places you visit, as this will surely be of benefit not only in material matters but in spiritual ones as well.

It is surely unnecessary to remind you of what we have discussed many times: that in the places you visit, you should inquire whether there are shuls, or even individuals, who possess seforim they no longer need, which are not available here. In places where they are needed, you should tell them that they can exchange them for the seforim we have printed here, especially those that are accessible to everyone, such as the volumes of sichos, etc. I am certain you will make an effort in this regard as well, and I rely on your understanding to handle each situation in the appropriate manner.

Please convey my regards to anash, and especially to the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and meticulous in his communal work, Rabbi Yirmiyah, may he live. May there be blessings for success in "gathering material and sowing spiritual," and I await good news.

## 214

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Elul, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who occupies himself with communal needs, R' Chaim Menachem, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter in due time. When I was at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I mentioned you, your wife, your mother, and your entire household, may they all live, for whatever they are in need of. May it be the will of Hashem that your move to a new residence brings a change of place that brings a change of fortune for the good and for blessing, both materially and spiritually.

Surely, in connection with this, you will also add strength to the matter of the "residence" in a spiritual sense, which is the study of Torah. This is understood according to the *maamar* based on the verse "A psalm, a song for the dedication of the house" in *Likutei Torah*, and at the end of the *hemshech* *Mayim Rabim* 5636. It is also alluded to in the *Gemara* regarding the Beis Hamikdash—which is the residence of the *Ribono shel Olam*, as it is written, "And they shall make Me a sanctuary and I will dwell among them"—that since its destruction, the *Ribono shel Olam* has only the "four cubits of *halacha*." In the context of Torah study, this requires "a *kav* of salt," and in the Torah itself, this refers to the inwardness of the Torah: the study of *Chassidus*. See *Likutei Torah* at the end of *Parshas Vayikra*. There is nothing that can stand before the will; just as one should not believe if someone says "I labored and did not find," one should also not believe if someone says "I did not labor and I found." Moreover, one succeeds in a manner that transcends nature...

With the blessing of *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year.

## 216

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Elul, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, man of action, etc.,
Rabbi Yehoshua, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I was distressed to read your letter regarding the tragedy that has befallen you with the passing of your wife, may she rest in peace. May it be the will of Hashem that from now on you know no further sorrow or distress, Heaven forbid.

Perhaps you have already heard the story of the elder Chabad Chassidim: When the Rebbetzin, wife of the Tzemach Tzedek, passed away, he was in a state of deep despondency and repeatedly quoted the statement from the Zohar: "A King without a Queen is not a King" (Zohar III, 5a). His son, Admur Maharil, entered and said to him, "Father, we heard explicitly from you that 'See life with the wife whom you love' (Koheles 9:9) refers to Torah" (Kiddushin 30b). His father, the Tzemach Tzedek, replied, "My son, you have revived me."

It is a common saying among Chassidim that this is difficult to understand: surely this is a well-known teaching of our Sages that the Tzemach Tzedek was already aware of, so what did his son, Admur Maharil, reveal to him? The explanation is that one must draw the concept down from the world of thought and contemplation into the world of speech and action, for that is where the body is found, and there the significance of the body—and consequently the deficiency caused by the absence of its vitality—is felt. The resolution of that deficiency must also take place in this world itself—namely, through speech, which is a minor act, especially when it leads to action. And according to the teaching of our Sages that "a prisoner cannot free himself," this drawing down must be done by another, provided it is someone close to him, for then it is a powerful speech that draws the influence down into action and fills the void to a great extent. This is what the son said to the father: that he (the father) himself, as a *posek*, had already ruled on this very matter, using the language of the Gemara that this is "Torah," and Torah governs nature and reality, even retroactively (Yerushalmi, Kesuvos 1:2). Consequently, there is no longer a deficiency.

May it be the will of Hashem that you, may you live, find at least a partial filling of this void through an increase of strength in the study of Torah, and specifically in the study of Chassidus, and may you increase your efforts for Torah—to make it great and glorious—Torah permeated with fear of Heaven.

I read the note you enclosed with your letter at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

With blessings for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah* for a good year.

## B'riz

*[1st of Elul, 5713]*

...We find in the mitzvah of Milah something that is not present in all other mitzvos. By way of introduction: The fact that minors are not obligated in mitzvos can, on the face of it, be explained in two ways: 1) That the Torah and mitzvos are not relevant to them at all, as they were given specifically to adults. 2) That the Torah and mitzvos were given to all of Yisrael, but minors are not subject to obligation or punishment because they lack *da'as*.

There is a practical difference between these two approaches: According to the first, a minor (specifically, for adults are warned in many places regarding the conduct of minors) does not commit a transgression by performing one of the mitzvos of Hashem that one is forbidden to do, because it is not relevant to him at all; it is permitted, and consequently, there is no matter of *teshuvah* or atonement involved (though this requires further study; see *Yevamos* 48b, and see the *Yaavetz* and *Ahavas Eisan* there). This is not the case according to the second approach.

And if so—the ruling that an adult does well to take upon himself some measure of *teshuvah* and atonement for what he did during his minority (*Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim*, end of 343)—even in places where there is no specific instruction regarding this, such as in *Rambam, Hilchos Issurei Biah* 3:17, *Hilchos Nedarim* 11:4, and elsewhere—and see the *Rishonim* in *Kiddushin* 19a—proves the second approach.

Furthermore, regarding the mitzvah of *Talmud Torah*: It is not only that it is relevant to minors, as with all other mitzvos, but the Torah has obligated (the father, the sage, and through the principle of *kum v'aseh*) that minors be taught Torah. Moreover, the obligation of *Talmud Torah* in its entirety is bound up with this, as our Sages said (*Kiddushin* 29b): "Anyone whom others are commanded to teach, is commanded to teach himself." (This can be explained as not merely a sign, but a reason or cause; and based on this, *Talmud Torah* in general is not only connected to, but also dependent upon, "And you shall teach them to your children.")

There is an additional, unique aspect to the mitzvah of Milah: It is not only that it is relevant to minors and the Torah has obligated that the mitzvah be fulfilled in minors—as is the case with the mitzvah of *Talmud Torah*—but beyond that:

Whereas in the mitzvah of *Talmud Torah*, the obligation of minors is only for when they grow up—at least to some extent—and the mitzvah can be fulfilled even without minors (for "And you shall teach them to your children" includes adult children as well, since "teach them" refers to the entire Torah, and a fifteen-year-old is ready for Gemara), this is not the case with the mitzvah of Milah. Its essence is in the minor, and in the minor in the ultimate sense, immediately upon his arrival into the world, as per the question of our Sages (*Niddah* 31b): "Why did the Torah command Milah for the eighth day (and not before)?"

The reason for these distinctions can be explained as follows: Since the moment one becomes an adult, he is obligated in all mitzvos, it is necessary that prior to this he engage in study, which leads to action. Preparation for the state of adulthood is relevant only to one who has grown somewhat. And since this necessity exists only because of the matter of action, the mitzvah of *Talmud Torah* can be fulfilled in its entirety by adults alone as well.

This is not the case with the matter of the mitzvah of Milah. It is a *bris* with Hashem, a weakening of the material and the desire (*Moreh Nevuchim*, Part 3, end of ch. 47; quoted in *Rabbeinu Bachya*, end of *Parshas Lech Lecha*), and the beginning of the entry of the *neshamah* of holiness (*Shulchan Aruch Admur HaZaken*, *Mahadura Basra*, end of ch. 4). This is so that he may be able to stand against the *nefesh habehamis*—the "foolish king"—which arrives the moment he is stirred to emerge from his mother's womb. Therefore, the matter of adulthood is not relevant here. On the contrary, it provides him with a "folly of holiness" against the "spirit of folly" that leads one to commit a transgression, similar to what the *Rambam* writes in *Hilchos Deos* 2:2 (see also *Kuntres U'Maayan*, pp. 26-27). It must be in close proximity to the time he is stirred to emerge from his mother's womb, as is understood (see *Moreh Nevuchim* there: "And it is as if he is still in the womb until the end of the seven days, and then he is counted as one who sees the light of the world," end of quote. See also *Zohar* Vol. 3, 43b; *Devarim Rabbah*, beginning of ch. 6).

This is also the *avodah* of the month of Elul—the acronym for *U'mal Hashem Es Levavcha* (And Hashem will circumcise your heart) (*Baal HaTurim, Devarim* 30:6)—an *avodah* that is above *taam v'daas*. Through this, "My heart said to You, 'Seek My face'—Your face, Hashem, I will seek"—a *bris* with Hashem.

## 208

B.H., 1 Elul, 5713
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your two letters, in which you write regarding your state of mind, your manner of study in general and in Sifrei Chassidus in particular, and some of the ideas that have occurred to you regarding the statements of our Sages.

It appears from your letters that you are specifically seeking new paths and original innovations of your own—meaning, not merely an innovation in the interpretation of a subject, but an innovation in finding the path itself. Even if we assume that you will not err in your search and will find the true point and the correct path in general, and for yourself in particular, there is no doubt that you will lose a great deal of time and effort. According to the statement of our Sages, "A person does not fully grasp the words of Torah unless he has first stumbled in them." In your case, the stumbling will be in the path itself, not just in a specific subject or a specific halachah. It is self-understood that since all Jews are "believers, the children of believers," we know **simply** that nothing in the world was created in vain. Especially regarding a Jewish person, all our days are numbered according to the measure of the avodah in Torah and mitzvos that one must fulfill. Every day and hour that one spends on a matter that has already been paved by our predecessors—who were like angels—even if we say it is a mitzvah and one will receive reward for it, on the other hand, he is **not** doing **his own avodah**. Consequently, he is wasting time on matters that are not his, and in the final analysis, he will **lack** in the matters that he is actually required to do.

This can be compared to a person who wants to study the Mishnah and says he does not want to look at the commentaries on the Mishnah, but rather will exert himself until he can arrive at the pilpul brought in the Gemara, Rashi, Tosafos, and so on. If you would listen to my opinion, turn away from this path. Study the Sifrei Chassidus, in which our Rebbes have **clearly** shown us the path in which we should walk—both in the study of the revealed Torah and in the Torah of Chassidus, and in the manner of fulfilling mitzvos with joy and hiddur. Then, you will see that many of the matters that are currently in doubt for you have already been clarified by our predecessors long ago, and regarding many matters for which you say you have already found the solution, you will see that this is not the explanation and this is not the path in which you should walk.

One of the tests to know whether one is walking on the correct path is to examine the **practical outcome** regarding hiddur in the fulfillment of mitzvos, consistency in the study of Torah, and warmth in Ahavas Yisrael. You should take into account your conduct in all the above for yourself, and contemplate whether the engagement in the studies you write about in your letter has brought about an increase in all these, or, on the contrary, a weakening. Further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

The conclusion from all the above: divert your attention—for several hours a day—from your own talents and essence, and study the halachos that one needs to know for daily life, and study **Toras HaChassidus**, Tanya, Derech Mitzvosecha, and the like. For Siyata Dishmaya, give a few coins to tzedakah every weekday before davening, and after davening—every day, including Shabbos and Yom Tov—recite the portion of Tehillim as divided for the days of the month. May Hashem grant you the merit and success to stand on the "King's Highway" and not to search for side paths and detours, and it will be good for you, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year, and success in Torah and Yiras Shamayim.

## 218

B"H, 1 Elul, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from Erev Shabbos Parshas Re'eh. I see in it a contradiction between the beginning and the end: you begin by writing about the groups and the shiurim you are teaching, yet you conclude that in terms of your spirituality, your essence is diminishing. It is well known according to our Sages of blessed memory the great value of one who teaches Torah to his fellow’s son, and especially one who teaches Torah to the son of an am ha'aretz. If so, it is impossible that through this your own standing should be diminished. Surely this, too, is a tactic of the yetzer hara to weaken you in your aforementioned avodah, perhaps even to bring you to a feeling of despair—reasoning that since the situation is not as it should be, what is the point, how can one possibly succeed, and is the effort to improve the situation even worthwhile? (This, too, is the opposite of what our Sages said: "If one says, 'I have labored and not found,' do not believe him.")

I have already told you many times that in this time, it is a necessity for every individual to involve themselves in some matter of communal needs. For those who are suited for it, the matters of proper chinuch take precedence over everything. Along with this—and specifically for the sake of this—it is essential that you have a fixed time for learning the sefarim of Chassidus Chabad, and you should also strive to serve Hashem specifically out of simcha.

Regarding what you wrote, that you began learning a little Tanya and found it very difficult because you are not accustomed to it: since you yourself write the reason, it is in your hands to nullify it and to accustom yourself to this study. The rule of our Sages is well known: "If one says, 'I have not labored and found,' do not believe him." As is evident from your letter itself, you have not yet **begun** to study with labor. If the yetzer hara is not comfortable with the study of Torah in any form, then all the more so regarding study that leads—in the language of the Rambam in Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah—to the love and awe of Hashem. What is the benefit of debating this? Begin to learn, and in the course of time, you will see success in it.

With blessings,

## 2220

2220

B”H, 2 Elul, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, R’ Moshe Hakohen, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Tuesday, Parshas Shoftim, albeit very brief, and I have enclosed the receipt as you requested.

As we are entering the month of Elul, the month of mercy, I am enclosing a sicha from Shabbos Mevarchim Elul. Although it was not delivered this year, its message is relevant to every year, throughout the year, and especially during the days of Elul. The acronym for Elul (א-ל-ו-ל) corresponds to: "And Hashem your G-d will circumcise your heart (א-ת ל-ב-ב-ך) and the heart of your offspring" — Teshuvah; "I am to my beloved and my beloved is to me" (א-נ-י ל-ד-ו-ד-י ו-ד-ו-ד-י ל-י) — Tefillah; "And G-d brought him to the place (א-נ-ה ל-י-ד-ו ו-ש-מ-ת-י ל-ך) where he shall flee" — Torah; and "Sending portions to one another (א-י-ש ל-ר-ע-ה-ו ו-מ-ת-נ-ו-ת ל-א-ב-י-ו-נ-י-ם) and gifts to the poor" — Tzedakah. This is explained in my introduction to the Kuntres of Chai Elul 5710, and surely you will merit to share its content with the public in an appropriate manner.

With blessings for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah* for a good year for you and your wife, may she live, and it is obvious that this includes the proper fear of Heaven.

## 221

B"H, 2 Elul, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Your letter informing me of your successful journey to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, reached me today. Since the ship you are traveling on has already left New York, I must send this letter via my office in Paris to hasten and alert you that the ship "Jerusalem," on which you intend to travel from Marseille, is a Jewish ship and the crew members are Jewish. There is a prohibition against traveling on it on Shabbos, or even being on it on the day of Shabbos and benefiting from the work performed on that day.

Since, according to the information I have received, the aforementioned ship will leave Marseille this coming Thursday or Friday and will only arrive in Haifa after Shabbos, the journey involves the desecration of Shabbos. If you have no alternative option for travel to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, perhaps it is possible and necessary for you to travel in a different manner—by train or airplane to Naples for Shabbos, and from there continue the journey on that same ship, "Jerusalem," which I understand leaves Naples on Sunday.

Surely you will not suffice with saving yourself and your wife, may she live, from the desecration of Shabbos; perhaps you will inform other G-d-fearing people of this as well, who, only due to a lack of knowledge, might G-d forbid desecrate Shabbos.

With blessings for a *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah*.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 2223

B"H, 6 Elul, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 29 Menachem Av, in which you write regarding the matter of *machshavos zaros* (alien thoughts) that distract you from time to time, and especially during *davening*.

You should *daven* from the *Siddur*, and even when you need to engage in *hisbonenus* (contemplation), the *Siddur* should remain open before you. When you feel your thoughts beginning to wander, look into the *Siddur*; it is known from our Sages that the letters themselves illuminate. You should also have certain concepts from *Toras HaChassidus* engraved in your memory, word for word—among them the *maamar* "Ve'hadarta Pnei Zaken" at the end of *Parshas Kedoshim* in *Likutei Torah*. Furthermore, before *davening* each morning—on weekdays—give a few coins to *tzedakah* from time to time, and arrange to have your *tefillin* checked. May Hashem grant you success in your *avodah* and in your study of the revealed Torah and *Toras HaChassidus*. Do not seek out great and wondrous things; the explanation of "one who serves Hashem" is known—that it requires *avodah* and difficult exertion, as explained in *Tanya* and in the *maamarim* of *Chassidus*.

With blessings for a *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

**The Secretary**

## 2224

B"H, 6 Elul, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and refined, R' Avraham Moshe, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write that for some twenty-five years you have served as the Baal Koreh, Baal Tokeah, and Shliach Tzibbur for Shacharis on Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur, and since this year falls within the twelve months of mourning for your mother, a"h, you are asking my opinion as to whether you should lead the davening.

The ruling on this matter is explained in many places: one who has been established in this practice for several years should lead the davening, even on Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur. You may consult the commentaries on the Shulchan Aruch, in Aruch HaShulchan, subsections 46-47, and the sources cited there; Mateh Efraim and its commentaries, Siman 581. This is especially true given that you write in your letter that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, ztzkllh"h, nbgm, zy"a, already ruled on this as a practical matter during his own days of mourning for his father, a"h.

You are surely aware of the instructions of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, for one who leads the davening on Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur: to review the meaning of the words—at the very least according to their simple interpretation—both of the tefillah and the piyutim, in the days leading up to them.

With blessings for a *ksivah v'chasimah tovah*, and that you should be a good shaliach for those who sent you, to be blessed with a good and sweet year, in all that you need.

***

**R' Avraham Moshe:** Kirschenbaum, Jerusalem.

**Instruction:** See also above, Vol. 6, letters 1812, 1829.

## 230

B"H, 16 Elul, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 10 Elul, in which you write about your manner of study until now and your fulfillment of mitzvos, as well as the apprehensions you have regarding the study of Toras HaChassidus.

You should have no apprehension whatsoever, for this is not the study of Kabbalah, but the study of Toras HaChassidus. Even though matters from Kabbalah are sometimes mentioned, their explanation according to Toras HaChassidus leaves no room for the concerns mentioned in your letter. It is essential that you study the *Kuntres Eitz Chaim* and *Kuntres U’Maayan* by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, and the introduction to *Kuntres Eitz Chaim* by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. You will then see how baseless your concerns are; they are nothing but a tactic of the yetzer hara to prevent you from gaining knowledge of a great portion of our holy Torah—a portion that our generation, the *ikvesa d’meshicha*, has specifically merited to have revealed to the masses. If, through Divine Providence, you have also merited to learn of this, you must seize this opportunity with all your heart and soul, without entering into any debate with your yetzer hara, which is stirring these concerns within you. If a little light pushes away much darkness, then how much more so does a great deal of light. One should not raise the question of what happened in earlier generations before Toras HaChassidus was revealed, for this question is similar to those who ask what happened in the time of the Mishnah before there was a Gemara, or in the time of the Gemara before there were the works of the Rishonim, etc. To elaborate on this is unnecessary. Study the aforementioned *Kuntres Eitz Chaim*, and you will find it pleasant and relieving. May Hashem grant you success in increasing your strength in both the revealed Torah and Toras HaChassidus together, with success.

With blessings for a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah*.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

**The Secretary**

## 231

B.H., 16 Elul, 5713
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, R' Elchanan HaKohen, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 24 August, in which you write regarding our friend, that he told you he is feeling somewhat better. One must hope that he will continue to do what depends on him, and in that case, Hashem will surely do many times more.

Hopefully, the check he is sending is not a one-time payment. As far as I recall, I emphasized that the amount is not as important here as the fact that one should give something to tzedakah every single day. Just as one cannot be satisfied today with a large meal eaten a week ago, so too it is with the nourishment of the soul. While there are things that can be done once and suffice for a longer period—which is generally the **analogy** in human life, such as a house or clothing—eating, however, must be done every day, and one cannot fulfill the obligation of one day with the food of another.

So too in the matters of Torah and mitzvos: there are mitzvos that one performs once, and that suffices for a longer period, such as the mitzvah of tekias shofar, which, according to the explanation of our Sages, is the act of crowning Hakadosh Baruch Hu as King, and this suffices for the entire year. However, learning Torah and giving tzedakah—at least in smaller amounts—must be done every day. Although there are differences even in this—for instance, before Rosh Hashanah, or in a time of distress (G-d forbid), or when one encounters a very needy person, one should increase the quantity—even that does not exempt one from giving smaller amounts, bli neder, day in and day out.

You will excuse me for writing about such simple matters, but I believe psychologically that when a thought is written down or spoken, the matter becomes clearer to oneself as well. I hope that our friend, too, notwithstanding that he likely does not have the patience for this, will nevertheless set aside some amount for tzedakah every day, and not content himself with the fact that he will give a larger sum later.

When Dr. Nissan Mindel returns from vacation, I will with pleasure write a mazal tov regarding the tana'im of his son, may he live, and a heartfelt thank you to you for your note to do so. However, as mentioned, I wish to write this in English.

With the blessing of Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah.

## 2,134

[21 Elul, 5713]

...Regarding what you wrote, that the status of the Yeshiva is still unclear, etc., etc.: In my opinion, this is not the case. It has been clear for some time that the Torah of the Baal Shem Tov and its objectives must be fulfilled through the principle of *yifutzu maynotecha chutza* (spreading the wellsprings outward). Consequently, it is impossible for there to be any corner of the globe where members of *Bnei Yisrael* are found that this Torah will not reach—and specifically in accordance with the will of the Baal Shem Tov and his successors, the *Nesi'ei Chabad*, that Torah and life should be one, meaning in day-to-day life.

Since we have heard many times from my revered father-in-law, the *Admur*, that we are in the *ikvesa d'Meshicha*—that he is standing behind our wall, waiting for the clarification of the few remaining *hefochim* (opposites)—it is therefore imperative that the study of *Chassidus* take place in [the location mentioned] as well. This applies not only among *Anash* from Russia who were sent there, but that it should penetrate the inhabitants of the land—that is, the *Bnei Yisrael* who are residents of [the location]. And since this is a necessity, all that is required for it will surely be found.

It is surely superfluous to note that since the Yeshiva building makes a good impression, efforts should be made for it to serve generally as a center for *Chabad* affairs—a place for Torah, a place for *tefillah*, and a place for *farbrengens*, meetings, etc. It is understood that all of the above is stated with the proviso that it does not contradict the studies, but there is certainly room and time for all these matters in this building. Experience has already shown that having these other matters there will certainly serve as an aid to the affairs of the Yeshiva...

But we are "workers of the day," as the Tzemach Tzedek said—we are working to bring light, and we require concrete actions. And so that one does not fool oneself, one should take a piece of paper and write down what one has actually done, and what one could have accomplished...

Surely you are aware that the connection between the Jewish people and Hashem is through the Torah—both the revealed and the hidden aspects of Torah—as is brought in the Zohar (Vol. III, 73a). Likewise, the connection of one Jew to another is also, in its essence, through the Torah, for the 600,000 letters of the Torah correspond to the 600,000 souls that comprise the totality of the Jewish people. Since you are sending me a *pidyon nefesh*, it is certain that you are already studying, or at the very least will immediately begin to study, the Chassidus of Chabad—the hidden aspect of Torah—the revelation of which we have merited specifically in these generations. ## 2238

2238

B"H, First Day of Selichos, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To our brothers and sisters, the sons and daughters of Israel,
In every place and location,
May Hashem keep them alive!

Peace and blessing!

As the new year approaches for us and for all of Israel for the good, I hereby express my blessing to all our brothers and sisters, the sons and daughters of Israel wherever they may be, for a good and sweet year.

Rosh Hashanah, the beginning of a new year—5714 since the creation of the world—is not the first day of the creation of the world, but rather the day when Adam HaRishon, the first human, was created—the sixth day of the work of creation. The world of *domem* (inanimate objects, minerals, etc.), *tzomei'ach* (vegetation), and *chai* (living creatures) was created earlier, as the Torah tells us.

Nevertheless, Rosh Hashanah is celebrated on the day when man was created. And it is precisely from this day that the new year begins for the **entire world**—including *chai*, *tzomei'ach*, and *domem*. On this day we say, **"This is the day of the beginning of Your works"**—this is the day of the **beginning** of Your works!

Herein lies a deep lesson and moral, which everyone must contemplate, especially in these current days of *cheshbon hanefesh*:

The world, and all parts of the world, only became what they were intended to be when man was created, for he is the *tachlis habriah* (the purpose of creation).

Man is an "olam katan" (a microcosm); the entire creation is reflected within him. Just as in the totality of creation, so too in man specifically, there exist all the levels of creation. In the course of his life's journey, a person passes through a time when he lives like a *domem*, a time when he is like a *tzomei'ach*, then like a *chai*, and then like a *medaber* (a speaker). But even when a person reaches human intellect and spirit, these levels exist within his life and deeds: at certain times of the day, it may be that a person does not distinguish himself from a *domem*; at other times he is on the level of a *tzomei'ach* or a *chai*; and there are times of deeds and activities that bear witness that he is an *adam*—a rational and spiritual being.

The moral of Rosh Hashanah for every person is:

The beginning, Rosh Hashanah, is only when man was created. The entire preceding creation of *domem*, *tzomei'ach*, and *chai* does not yet justify the celebration of the creation of the world. Only when Adam HaRishon was created and called to the entire creation, "Come, let us bow down and kneel, let us bless before Hashem our Maker" (*Zohar*, Vol. I, 221b; *Pirkei DeRabbi Eliezer*, Chapter 11), and ensured that this was so—that he connected the creation with the Creator and made the world a *mishkan* and a *mikdash* for the Divine *Shechinah*—only then is the intent and purpose of the entire creation and every part of it fulfilled, and only then is it Rosh Hashanah, a new time.

So too with every person, both in the course of life in general and every day in particular: the *pnimiyus* and *atzmiyus* (inner essence) of a person consists of the *chelek adam* (the human part) that is within him influencing and permeating his *chelek chai*, his *chelek tzomei'ach*, and his *chelek domem*. Only then is the name "Adam" correctly applied. And only then, when the parts of his life and activities in which he equates himself with a *chai*, *tzomei'ach*, and even *domem* are refined, elevated, and permeated with the loftiness of the *medaber*, so that the **entire** *adam*—body and soul—carries out the call, "Come, let us bow down and kneel, let us bless before Hashem our Maker!"—this can only be achieved by leading a life according to the instructions of the Creator, a life *al pi Torah u'mitzvah* of Hashem our Maker.

Standing on the threshold of the new year, beginning a new year and a new era in life, every person must once again contemplate and engrave in his memory that "This is the day of the beginning of Your works." This is the beginning, the foundation, and the purpose of the entire creation—*kabbalas ol malchus shamayim*—when the entire creation cries out, "Hashem is King, Hashem was King, Hashem will be King forever and ever."

With blessings for a good and sweet year in both material and spiritual matters.

## 239

B"H, First day of Selichos, 5713
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To our brothers and sisters, the sons and daughters of Yisroel,
Wherever they may be,
May Hashem grant them life!

Peace and blessing!

As we approach the New Year, which comes upon us and upon all Yisroel for good and for blessing, I hereby extend my blessing to all our brothers and sisters, the sons and daughters of Yisroel wherever they are, with the blessing of *Kesivah v'chasimah tovah*.

Rosh Hashanah—the head and beginning of the new year, the year 5714 from the creation of the world—is, as is known, not set on the first day of the six days of creation, but rather on the day that Hashem created man upon the earth. And although all parts of creation—the inanimate, the vegetative, and the living—preceded man, as recounted in the Torah, we nonetheless commemorate the creation specifically on the day of man's creation. It is on this day that a new era begins for the entire universe—the living, the vegetative, and the inanimate alike—and on this day we declare: "This is the day, the beginning of Your works!"

From this, there is a lesson and a moral for each and every one of us to contemplate and observe, especially during these days of *cheshbon hanefesh*:

The heavens and the earth and all their hosts only reach their purpose and their true state when man, the purpose of creation, is created.

Man is a *olam katan* (a microcosm). Just as in the totality of creation, so too within man himself there exist all the levels—inanimate, vegetative, living, and speaking. Throughout the days of his life, a person passes from level to level. At first, he is at the level of the inanimate; then, at the level of the vegetative; then, at the level of the living; and finally, when he attains his intellect and his spiritual maturity, he reaches the level of man. But even then, when he reaches the stature of man, his lifestyle and actions still contain all these levels. A portion of his time is spent in a state comparable to the inanimate; several hours a day, his activities are like those of the vegetative and the living. Yet, a portion of his deeds testifies to the stature of man—a rational and spiritual creature, a body and a *neshamah* which is a part of Hashem from above, literally.

Rosh Hashanah teaches us: The head and beginning of all creation is man. Only when the first man was created—who, immediately upon his creation, announced and proclaimed to all: "Come, let us bow down and kneel, let us bend the knee before Hashem our Maker," and who inspired this in them, and through this made the world and all that fills it a sanctuary and a dwelling place for His *Shechinah*—only then was the intent and purpose of creation fulfilled, and only then is it Rosh Hashanah, the head of a new era.

And so it is in the life of each and every person: The essence of man is expressed only when the "man" within him influences and permeates his "living" part, his "vegetative" part, and his "inanimate" part. Furthermore: only when he refines, elevates, and sanctifies even those parts of his life and actions in which he is comparable to the living, the vegetative, and even the inanimate, until they too are permeated with spirituality and holiness—only then is he truly a man. He becomes a creature who entirely declares: "Come, let us bow down and kneel, let us bend the knee before Hashem our Maker," through a lifestyle following the path of Torah and *mitzvos* that Hashem our Maker has given us. It is within his power, and it is the purpose of his creation, to bring about a state where the entire creation proclaims: "Hashem is King, Hashem was King, Hashem will be King forever and ever!"

With the blessing of *Kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

## 240

240

B"H, 27 Elul, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the Shabbos of Parshas Ki Savo, along with the *pidyon nefesh*. Regarding the latter, you should explain to your son-in-law, *shiya*, that this is not the proper way to conduct oneself with the *Ribono shel Olam*. It is not right that when his daughter was—heaven forbid—not well, he made a commitment, yet afterward he became lax in that commitment, waiting until, heaven forbid, a new ailment arises and he remembers the promise. It is understood that these words must be explained to him in a pleasant and calm manner, etc., and may the *Ribono shel Olam* grant you success in finding the appropriate words, so that your son-in-law, *shiya*, will have "open ears" to hear them.

With blessings.

#### ***240***

Published in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 16, p. 587.

## 251

[27 Elul, 5713]

...When I am at the holy resting place of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention him for a speedy recovery. He must strengthen his trust in Hashem, the Healer of all flesh who performs wonders, that He will restore his health. May he and his wife, long may they live, raise their children, long may they live, to Torah, the chuppah, and good deeds, in health and with peace of mind. However, they must strengthen their connection to the Healer of all flesh who performs wonders by living a life consistent with His will, which is also a way of life that brings both physical and spiritual happiness. They must remain firm in their resolve to raise their children in the way of Torah and good deeds...

#### ***251***

Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 11, p. 294.

## 2742

2742

B"H, 27 Elul, 5713
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Kfar Chabad in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily!
May they live!

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter, which was begun on the evening following Shabbos, the auspicious day of Chai Elul. I trust that in the meantime, you have also received my letter from here.

Regarding the content of your letter, I am somewhat surprised, for in your previous letter you wrote that you have seen good fruit from your labor this year, whereas in this letter you describe the entire situation in dark colors. May it be the will of Hashem that from now on you bring only good tidings, both in material and spiritual matters.

Regarding your general question: although it is against my desire and contrary to my nature, I have no choice but to write as I see the situation, just as I have hinted in several of my letters since then. It is as follows:

It is clear to me that the village is a conduit and a vessel for your livelihood, not only in spiritual matters but also in material ones. On the other hand, one must view this matter in its true light: it is a **collective** of Anash, and not a situation where every single individual is an entity unto himself who needs to protect only his own interests and view the others—or at least some of them—as competitors. Even if there might have been room for such an interpretation when you were in our country [Russia] in the past—when the only thing that connected you were spiritual matters, the spiritual of the spiritual, namely, study sessions in Nigleh and Chassidus, the avodah of tefillah, and tzedakah, etc.—it is different now. For the thing that unites you (and not, Heaven forbid, separates you) is also your material interests—namely, the concept of a Chassidic village in the Holy Land, which in time will serve as a center from which more Chassidic settlements will spread throughout the Holy Land, etc. It is understood that there cannot be a common endeavor when one looks at his fellow "as a competitor." If everyone cooperates together, then it is beyond any doubt that not only will there be no deficiencies in your livelihood, but on the contrary, blessing and success will be added, in accordance with the ruling of our Sages that peace is the vessel that holds blessing—the blessing of the Holy One, Blessed be He, which is without limit. If the people of the village could bring this about themselves, so that all of this would "take root within them," then the relationships would change completely, and the actions themselves would be of a different nature and essence.

Based on the above, it is also understood that even if in your previous places of residence, communal matters were only a matter of the World to Come—for "there is no reward for a mitzvah in this world"—in your current situation, this is also a vessel for your livelihood and the livelihood of your families, may they live. This is why I have been crying out for several months now that this is for the benefit of the people of the village (in addition to the benefit of establishing the stature of Chabad in the Holy Land as a whole): that the village should develop as quickly as possible, like all other settlements and even more so. This is to be achieved through the construction of an agricultural school and a vocational school, and by increasing the number of settlers, etc. The sooner you advance in this, the sooner the benefit will be seen even with physical eyes.

Mr. Geshtenkorn visited me a few times. One of the topics of our conversation was the development of Bnei Brak. I became convinced that it is neither wondrous nor far-fetched that the village could also develop in this direction. The only deficiency is that in Bnei Brak there was one will, and that will was for development—whereas in Kfar Chabad, every person is a "full world" with his own will, fulfilling the saying of our Sages that "their opinions are not the same," and sometimes they even pride themselves on this.

I was pleased to learn that Anash have conducted a collection at my request and have contributed 200 Lira to the temporary maintenance of the Village Committee, 300 Lira to the temporary maintenance of Beis Rivkah and the kindergarten, and 200 Lira to the maintenance of the Talmud Torah in the village. May Hashem grant that you bring me good news in all matters.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the *Mehadrin*: I am surprised, for all the offices in the Holy Land know that the time for plowing and sowing is approaching, and consequently, the situation must be clarified as soon as possible. Likewise, regarding the construction of the vocational and agricultural school, the Youth Aliyah office and the Joint, etc., are also interested in such institutions, especially in recent times. Consequently, one can hope that the representatives of these offices will cooperate with you in your efforts regarding this, and I will await good news.

Regarding the agricultural school: based on my conversation with Mr. Moshe Kol when he was here, it is also his firm opinion that you should strive to ensure that the building you erect is not made of shacks, but is a proper building. Especially since this—the proposal—comes from Mr. Kol, you must, for your part, strengthen him in this, especially given my hope for the development of the village as mentioned above.

It goes without saying that I do not see it as being within their possibilities to provide a loan of several thousand Lira immediately. But on the other hand, my hope is strong that Mr. Kol will "find a way." And it is obvious that my commitment to pay off half the sum over the course of several years stands firm, even if they build the building for fifty thousand Lira or even sixty thousand Lira. And all the more so.

May it be the will of Hashem that the saying of the Tzemach Tzedek, which the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, related—that he once said "Aleph-Beis" (A-B) stands for *Achdus* (unity) - *Bracha* (blessing)—will be fulfilled in you.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and upon all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to your families, may they live: a blessing of *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

With the blessing of success in fear of Heaven and in the development of Kfar Chabad, I await and look forward to good news.

## 2243

27 Elul, 5713
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings,

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 21 Elul, along with the two *pidyonos nefesh* enclosed therein. By now, you have surely received my letter of response to the village administration, which also contains a reply to your letter. I must reiterate once again: even if you are entirely correct in all the excuses and justifications you provide for the lack of action, these excuses and justifications do not take the place of actual deeds. Furthermore, even in matters that serve as channels for livelihood, there is a very significant weakness—and perhaps even a total lack of action. I do not understand what the ultimate goal of this will be. It is my hope that these days, which are days of *hisorerus*—of bringing the Source of Light closer to the spark, and consequently bringing the spark closer to the Source of Light—will see these matters rectified, at least in a significant part. It is surely unnecessary to point out that if one lets the time of the month of Tishrei pass by regarding *ta'amulah* (outreach/propaganda), one will have to wait a long time until such an opportune moment arises again. Further elaboration on this is superfluous.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of *Klal Yisrael* for good and for blessing, I hereby wish to convey my blessing to you and your family—may they live—a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually...

With blessings,

## 244

B"H, 27 Elul, 5713
Brooklyn.

The Administration of the Yeshiva and Talmud Torah in Kfar Chabad
Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established
May Hashem keep them and grant them life!

Peace and Blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 23 Elul. I was pleased to read that despite the difficulties that stood in your way, your spirits have not fallen and you are continuing your holy work. There is no doubt that if you only make the effort, you will succeed with great success.

On the other hand, I was alarmed to read in your letter that two of your teachers were removed in connection with the state education system. I am also puzzled, as there was an explicit declaration that the dismissals were merely a formal and technical matter. As is known from the attitude of the Poalei Agudas Yisrael kibbutzim and the like, they will not interfere from the outside regarding the hiring of teachers, etc., provided that, officially, they accept the requirements they demand. Consequently, it is understood that on their part, too, they should not permit outside interference to dictate the dismissal of teachers in whom there is trust, etc.

Although it is also understood that it is healthier for the entire matter to be arranged without commotion and in a simple manner—as it is a necessity that the education in the village, which has a specific character, be conducted by teachers appropriate to that character. I am firmly confident that if you handle this diplomatically and quietly, it will be carried out in pleasant ways and in a simple manner. Especially since you already have a *chazakah* from several years, there is room for special concessions for you for several reasons, and the wise will understand.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express to you and your families, may they live, my blessing: a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

## 2745

[5713]

1) Regarding your uncertainty concerning the Rambam’s ruling on the law of *shelo k’sidran* (writing out of order) in *tefillin* and *mezuzos*—it is clear that he rules it invalid, as he writes in *Hilchos Tefillin*, Chapter 1, Halacha 12. See there the *nosei keilim* (commentaries) on the Rambam, *Tzafnas Paneach* there, *Be’er HaGolah* to *Shulchan Aruch*, section 32, subsection 23, and elsewhere. It is unnecessary to struggle in your letter to find the reasoning for the Rambam there, because:

2) It is obvious that the Rambam includes in his *Yad* (Mishneh Torah) laws from the Yerushalmi, Mechilta, etc., even if they are not brought in the Bavli, provided the Bavli does not disagree with them.

3) For the source of the invalidity of *shelo k’sidran* in *tefillin* and *mezuzos*, see also *Responsa Tzemach Tzedek*, *Shaar HaMiluim*, section 3.

4) As to whether it is invalid *min haTorah* (by Torah law) or *miderabanan* (by Rabbinic law), see *Responsa Radbaz*, Vol. 1, section 310; *Mishbetzos Zahav*, beginning of section 32 and beginning of section 34; *Tzemach Tzedek* and *Tzafnas Paneach* there; *Keshes HaSofer*, section 9; *Os Chaim* (by the author of *Minchas Ani*), beginning of section 32; and the books cited in *Sefer Measef Lechol HaMachanos* there.

5) The name "Shabbos Berachos"—**after** the *Kuntres HaAvodah* was published, I became aware that this is what it is called in many places in Poland, etc.

And last but not least, a blessing for all times: May it be the will of Hashem that he and his wife, *shichyu*, raise their son Mordechai, *shichyei*, along with their other children, *shichyu*, for Torah, *chuppah*, and *maasim tovim*, in true health and true prosperity.

#### ***2745***

**The name "Shabbos Berachos":** See also above, Vol. 3, Letter 731, section 7.

**Kuntres HaAvodah:** See page 6 in the note of the Rebbe, *shlita*, there: "The meaning of this word requires study." See also what Y. Mondshine wrote regarding this in *Kovetz He'aros U'Biurim*, issue 439, page 7.
